CHAPTER 1: QUESTIONS OF BHARGAVA
    
ॐ नमः कारणानन्दरुपिणी परचिन्मयि । विराजते जगच्चित्रचित्रदर्पणरूपिणी ॥ १ ॥

श्रुतं कच्चिन्नारदैतत् सावधानेन चेतसा । माहात्म्यं त्रिपुराख्याया यच्छ्रुतिः परसाधनम्‌ ॥ २ ॥

अथ ते कथयाम्यद्य ज्ञानखण्डं महा महाद्भुतम्‌ । यच्छ्रुत्वा न पुनः क्वापि मनुष्यः शोकमृच्छति ॥ ३ ॥

वैदिकं वैष्णवं दौवं शाक्तं पाशुपतं तथा । विज्ञानं सम्यगालोच्य यदेतत्‌ प्रविनिश्चितम्‌ ॥ ४ ॥

नैतद्विज्ञानसदृशमन्यद्‌ मानसमारुहेत्‌ । श्या श्रोदत्तगुरुणा भार्गवाय निरूपितम्‌ ॥ ५ ॥

उपप्त्तयुपलब्धिभ्यां समेतं बहु चित्रितम्‌ । अत्रोक्तेनापि नो वेद यदि करिचद्विमूढधीः ॥ ६ ॥

स॒ केवलं दैवहतः स्थाणुरेव न संशयः । न तस्य स्यादपि ज्ञानं साक्षाच्छिवनिरूपितम्‌ ॥ ७ ॥

तत्ते शृणु समाख्यास्ये ज्ञानखण्डात्मना स्थितम्‌ । अहो सतामद्भुतं हि वृत्तं सवेगुणोत्तरम्‌ ॥ ८ ॥

यन्मत्तोऽप्येष देवर्षिः शुश्रूषत्यपि किञ्चन । अनुग्राहकता चैषा सतां सहजसम्भवा ॥ ९ ॥

​​यथा घ्राणोल्लासकता मृगनाभेः स्वतः स्थिता । एवं दत्तात्रेयमुखाच्छ्रुत्वा माहात्म्यवैभवम्‌ ॥ १० ॥

रामः सर्वजनारामो जामदग्न्यः शुभाशयः । भक्त्यापहृतसच्चित्तस्तुष्णीं किञ्चिद्‌ बभूव ह ॥ ११ ॥

अथासाद्य बहिर्वृत्ति भरितानन्दलोचनः । रोमाञ्चपीवरवपुः स्वान्तरानन्दनिर्भरः ॥ १२ ॥

हर्षोऽमायन्‌ रोमकूपविभेदान्निर्गमन्निव । प्रणनाम दत्तगुरुं दण्डवच्चरणान्तिके ॥ १३ ॥

उत्थाय हर्षभरितः प्राह गद्गदसुस्वरः । धन्योऽहं कृतकृत्योऽहं श्रीगुरो त्वत्प्रसादतः ॥ १४ ॥

यस्य मे करुणासिन्धुस्तुष्टः साक्षाद्‌ गुरुः शिवः । यस्मिस्तुष्टे ब्रह्मपदमपि स्यात्‌ तृणसम्मितम्‌ ॥ १५ ॥

मृत्युरप्यात्मतां याति यस्मात्तुष्टाद्‌ गुरोर्ननु । ममाकाण्डादेव गुरुः सोऽद्य तुष्टो महेश्वरः ॥ १६ ॥

मन्ये सर्वं मया प्राप्तमित्येव कृपया गुरोः । नाथ माहात्म्यमखिलं श्रुतं त्वत्कृपयाधुन ॥ १७ ॥

तामुपासितुमिच्छामि त्रिपुरां परमेश्वरीम्‌ । तदुपास्तिक्रमं ब्रूहि मह्यं सुकृपया गुरो ॥ १८ ॥

इति संप्रार्थितो दत्तगुरुरालक्ष्य भार्गवे । योग्यतां त्रिपुरोपास्तौ सच्छ्रद्धाभक्तिबृंहिताम्‌ ॥ १९ ॥

क्रमेण दीक्षयामास त्रिपुरोपास्तिहेतवे । जामदग्न्योऽपि संप्राप्य त्रैपुरं दीक्षणं शुभम्‌ ॥ २० ॥

सर्वदीक्षासमधिकं पूर्णतत्तवप्रबोधनम्‌ । मन्त्रयन्त्रवासनाभिरन्वितं निखिलं क्रमम्‌ ॥ २१ ॥

प्राप्य श्रीगुरुवक्त्राब्जाद्रसं मधुकरो यथा । तृप्तान्तरङ्ग आनन्दमादितो भार्गवस्तदा ॥ २२ ॥

श्रीनाथेनाभ्यनुज्ञातस्त्रिपुरासाधनोद्यतः । परिक्रम्य गुरु नत्वा महेन्द्राद्रिमुपाययौ ॥ २३ ॥

तत्र निर्माय वसति शुभामतिसुखावहाम्‌ । अभूदुपासनपरो वर्षद्वादशकं तदा ॥ २४ ॥

नित्यनैमित्तिकपरः पूजाजपपरायणः । सदा श्रीत्रिपुरेशान्या मूर्त्तिध्यानैकतत्परः ॥ २५ ॥

एवं तस्यात्यगात्‌ कालो द्वादशाब्दो निमेषवत्‌ । अथैकदा सुखासीनो जामदग्न्योऽनुचिन्तयत्‌ ॥ २६ ॥

पुरा यत्प्राह संवर्तो मया स्वभ्यर्थितः पथि । तन्मया नैव विदितमंशेनापि तदा ननु ॥ २७ ॥

विस्मृतं च मया यस्मात्‌ प्राडन पृष्टं गुरुं प्रति । माहात्म्यं त्रिपुराशक्तेः श्रुतं श्रीगुरुवक्त्रतः ॥ २८ ॥

परन्तु तन्न विदितं यत्संवर्तः पुराऽब्रवीत्‌ । मया सृष्टिप्रसङ्गेन पृष्टं किञ्चिद्‌ गुरुं प्रति ॥ २९ ॥

तदा कटकृदाख्यानं वर्णयित्वा च मे गुरुः । नाब्रवीदप्रकृततस्तन्मे तत्तादृशं स्थितम्‌ ॥ ३० ॥

लोकस्य गतिमेतां तु न जानाम्यपि लेशतः । कस्मादिदं समुदितं जगदाडम्बरं महत्‌ ॥ ३१ ॥

कुत्र वा गच्छति पुनः कुत्र संस्थानमृच्छति । अस्थिरं तु प्रपश्यामि सर्वं सर्वत्र किञ्चन ॥ ३२ ॥

व्यवहारः स्थिरप्रायः कस्मादेतदपीदृशम्‌ । चित्रां जगद्वयवह्रतिं प्रपश्याम्यविमर्शिनीम्‌ ॥ ३३ ॥

अहो यथान्धानुगतो ह्यन्धश्चेष्टति तादृशः । लोकस्य व्यवहारो वै सर्वस्याप्यभिलक्षितः ॥ ३४ ॥

निदर्शनं ह्यात्मकृतिरत्र मे सर्वथा भवेत्‌ । नूनं मम शैशवे किं जातं तन्मे न भावितम्‌ ॥ ३५ ॥

कौमारे चान्यथा वृत्तं तारुण्येऽपि ततोऽन्यथा । इदानीमन्यथैव्रास्ति व्यापारो मम सर्वथा ॥ ३६ ॥

किमभूत्‌ फलमेतेषां तन्न वेद्मि कथञ्चन । यद्यत्काले यच्च यच्च क्रियते येन येन वै ॥ ३७ ॥

सम्यगेवेति तदबुद्ध्वा फलावष्टम्भपूर्वकम् । फलं किं तत्र संप्राप्तं केन वा सुखमात्मनः ॥ ३८ ॥

यच्चापि लोके फलवदविमृश्य फलं हि तत्‌ । न फलं तदहं मन्ये पुनर्यस्मात् करोति सः ॥ ३९ ॥

प्राप्ते फले फलेच्छावान्‌ पुनर्भूयात् कथं वद । यस्मान्नित्यं करोत्येव जनः सर्वः फलेहया ॥ ४० ॥

फलं तदेव संप्रोक्तं दुःखहानिः सुखं च वा । कर्तव्यशेषे नो दुःखनाशो वा सुखमेव वा ॥ ४१ ॥

कर्तव्यतैव दुःखानां परमं दुःखमुच्यते । तत्सत्त्वे तु कथं ते स्तो दुःखाभावः सूखं च वा ॥ ४२ ॥

यथा दग्धाखिलाङ्गस्य पादे पाटीरलेपनम्‌ । तथा कर्तव्यशेषस्य सुखलाभ इहोच्यते ॥ ४३ ॥

यथा शराविद्धहृदः परिष्वङ्गोऽप्सरोगणैः । तथा कर्तव्यशेषस्य सुखलाभ इहोच्यते ॥ ४४ ॥

यथा क्षयामयाविष्टनरस्य गीतसंश्रुतिः । तथा कर्तव्यशेषस्य सुखलाभ इहोच्यते ॥ ४५ ॥

सुखिनस्ते हि लोकेषु येऽकर्तव्यतया स्थिताः । पर्णाशया महात्मानः सर्वदेहसुशीतलाः ॥ ४६ ॥

यदि कर्तव्यशेषेऽपि सुखं स्यात्‌ केनचित्‌ क्वचित्‌ । शूलप्रोतेऽपि च नरे स्यात्‌ सुखं गन्धमाल्यजम्‌ ॥ ४७ ॥

अहो महच्चित्रमेतत्‌ कर्तव्यशतसंकुले । सुखमस्तीह यस्यार्थे करोत्येव सदा जनः ॥ ४८ ॥

अहो विचारमाहात्म्यं किं वदामि नृणामहम्‌ । अनन्तकर्तव्यशैलाक्रान्ताः सौख्यं लभन्ति च ॥ ४९ ॥

यथा सौख्याय यतते सार्वभौमस्तु सर्वदा । तथैव यतते नित्यमपि भिक्षाटने रतः ॥ ५० ॥

पृथक्‌ तौ प्राप्नुतः सौख्यं मन्येते कृतकृत्यताम्‌ । तद्येन यान्ति सर्वेऽपि याम्यहं ताननुक्रमात्‌ ॥ ५१ ॥

अनालोच्य फलं चापि यथान्धोऽन्धानुगस्तथा । तदलं मेधयानेन भूयो गत्वा दयानिधिम्‌ ॥ ५२ ॥

विजिज्ञासितजिज्ञास्यो विचिकित्साम्बुधेः परम्‌ । पारं प्रपत्स्ये सुशुभं गुरुवाक्प्लवमाश्रितः ॥ ५३ ॥

इति व्यवस्य सहसा जामदग्न्यः शुभाशयः । प्रतस्थे तद्गिरिवराद्‌ गुरुदर्शनकाङ्क्षया ॥ ५४ ॥

गन्धमादनशैलेन्द्रं प्राप्य शीघ्रमपश्यत । गुरुं पद्मासनासीनं भूभास्वन्तमिव स्थितम्‌ ॥ ५५ ॥

प्रणनाम पादपीठपुरतो भुवि दण्डवत्‌ । शिरसाऽपीडयत्‌ पादपद्मं निजकराश्रितम् ॥ ५६ ॥

अथैवं प्रणतं रामं दत्तात्रेयः प्रसन्नधीः । आशीर्भिर्योजयामास समुत्थापयदादरात्‌ ॥ ५७ ॥

वत्सोत्तिष्ठ चिरादद्य त्वां पश्यामि समागतम्‌ । ब्रूहि स्वात्मभवं वृत्तं निरामयतया स्थितम्‌ ॥ ५८ ॥

अथोत्थाय गुरूक्त्या स गुर्वादिष्टाम्यविष्टरः । उपविश्य प्रसन्नात्मा बद्धाञ्जलिपुटोऽब्रवीत्‌ ॥ ५९ ॥

श्रीगुरो करुणासिन्धो तवत्कृपामृत आप्लुतः । कथं स॒ परिभूयेत विधिसृष्टैरथामयैः ॥ ६० ॥

त्वत्कृपात्मामृतकरमण्डलान्तः स्थितं तु माम्‌ । सन्तापयेत्‌ कथं व्याधिश्चण्डांशुरतिभीषणः ॥ ६१ ॥

आन्तरं बाह्यमपि ते कृपयानन्दितं मम । सदा स्थितं किन्तु भवत्पादाब्जवियुति विना ॥ ६२ ॥

नान्यद्रुजवाहं किञ्चिदासीन्मे लेशतः क्वचित्‌ । तद्भवच्चरणाम्भोजदर्शनादद्य वे पुनः ॥ ६३ ॥

संपूर्णता समापन्ना सर्वथा श्रीगुरो ननु । तत्‌ किञ्चिच्चिरसंवृत्तं हृदि मे परिवर्तते ॥ ६४ ॥

तत्प्रष्टुं त्वाभिवाञ्छामि चिरसंशयितान्तरः । आज्ञप्तो भवताद्याहं पृच्छामि विचिकित्सितम्‌ ॥ ६५ ॥

संश्रुत्यैवं भार्गवोक्तिं दत्तात्रेयो दयानिधिः । सम्प्रहृष्टमना राममूचे प्रीत्याथ भार्गवम् ॥ ६६ ॥

पृच्छ भार्गव यत्तेऽद्य प्रष्टव्यं चिरसम्भृतम्‌ । तव भक्त्या प्रसन्नोऽस्मि प्रब्रवीमि तवेप्सितम्‌ ॥ ६७ ॥

इति श्रीमदितिहासोत्तमे त्रिपुरारहस्ये ज्ञानखण्डे भार्गवप्रश्ने प्रथमोऽध्यायः ॥

CHAPTER 2: GREATNESS OF CONTEMPLATION
   Verse 1
   इत्याज्ञप्तो जामदग्न्यः प्रणम्याऽत्रिसुतं मुनिम्‌ ।
   प्रश्रयावनतो भूत्वा संप्रष्टुमुपचक्रमे ॥ १ ॥
   ityājñapto jāmadagnyaḥ praṇamyā'trisutaṁ munim ।
   praśrayāvanato bhūtvā saṁpraṣṭumupacakrame ॥ 1 ॥
   iti — thus; ājñaptaḥ — instructed; jāmadagnyaḥ — son of Jamadagni; praṇamya — having bowed; atrisutaṁ — son of Atri; munim — sage; praśraya — humility; avanataḥ — bent; bhūtvā — having become; saṁpraṣṭum — to ask; upacakrame — began
   Following the sage's instructions, the son of Jamadagni bowed humbly to the son of Atri, and with reverence, began to ask his questions.
   
   Verse 2
   भगवन्‌ गुरुनाथार्य सर्वज्ञ करुणानिधे ।
   पुरा मे नुपवंशेषु क्रोधः कारणतो ह्यभूत्‌ ॥ २ ॥
   bhagavan gurunāthārya sarvajña karuṇānidhe ।
   purā me nupavaṁśeṣu krodhaḥ kāraṇato hyabhūt ॥ 2 ॥
   bhagavan — O Lord; gurunātha — revered Guru; ārya — noble one; sarvajña — all-knowing; karuṇānidhe — ocean of compassion; purā — before; me — my; nupavaṁśeṣu — in the line of kings; krodhaḥ — anger; kāraṇataḥ — due to reasons; hi — indeed; abhūt — arose
   O Lord, revered Guru, noble and all-knowing, ocean of compassion! In the past, anger arose within me due to my ancestral lineage.
   
   Verse 3
   तद्भूयो निहितं क्षात्रं सगर्भ सस्तनन्धयम्‌ ।
   मया त्रिःसप्तकृत्वो वै क्षत्रासृग्भरिते हृदे ॥ ३ ॥
   tadbhūyo nihitaṁ kṣātraṁ sagarbha sastanandhayam ।
   mayā triḥsaptakṛtvo vai kṣatrāsṛgbharite hṛde ॥ 3 ॥
   tat — that; bhūyaḥ — again; nihitaṁ — placed; kṣātraṁ — warrior caste; sagarbha — with pregnant women; sastanandhayam — with infants; mayā — by me; triḥsaptakṛtvaḥ — twenty-one times; vai — indeed; kṣatrāsṛgbharite — filled with the blood of warriors; hṛde — heart
   Furthermore, deep within lies the warrior's lineage, hidden like an embryo in the womb. Indeed, my heart has borne the burden of warriors twenty-one times.
   
   Verse 4
   सन्तर्पिताः पितृगणास्तुष्टा मद्भक्तिगौरवात्‌ ।
   मत्क्रोधं शामयामासुः शान्तः पित्राज्ञयाप्यहम्‌ ॥ ४ ॥
   santarpitāḥ pitṛgaṇāstuṣṭā madbhaktigauravāt ।
   matkrodhaṁ śāmayāmāsuḥ śāntaḥ pitrājñayāpyaham ॥ 4 ॥
   santarpitāḥ — satisfied; pitṛgaṇāḥ — groups of ancestors; tuṣṭāḥ — pleased; madbhaktigauravāt — by the respect of my devotion; matkrodhaṁ — my anger; śāmayāmāsuḥ — they calmed; śāntaḥ — pacified; pitṛājñayā — by the command of ancestors; api — also; aham — I
   The groups of ancestors, satisfied and pleased by my respectful devotion, calmed my anger, despite the initial command given by them.
   
   Verse 5
   सम्प्रत्ययोध्यामध्यास्ते यः श्रीरामो हरिः स्वयम्‌ ।
   क्रोधान्धस्तेन भूयोऽहं सङ्गतो बलदर्पितः ॥ ५ ॥
   sampratyayodhyāmadhyāste yaḥ śrīrāmo hariḥ svayam ।
   krodhāndhastena bhūyo'haṁ saṅgato baladarpitaḥ ॥ 5 ॥
   samprati — now; ayodhyām — in Ayodhya; adhyāste — dwells; yaḥ — who; śrīrāmaḥ — Shri Rama; hariḥ — Hari; svayam — himself; krodha — anger; andhaḥ — blind; tena — by him; bhūyaḥ — again; ahaṁ — I; saṅgataḥ — associated; baladarpitaḥ — overcome by power and pride
   Now, in Ayodhya, resides Shri Rama, Hari himself. Blinded by anger, I was once again overcome by power and pride against him, leading me astray.
   
   Verse 6
   तेन दर्पाद्भगवता च्यावितश्च पराजितः ।
   जीवन्‌ कथञ्चिन्निर्यातो ब्रह्मण्येनानुकम्पिना ॥ ६ ॥
   tena darpādbhagavatā cyāvitaśca parājitaḥ ।
   jīvan kathaṁcin niryāto brahmaṇyenānukampinā ॥ 6 ॥
   tena — by him; darpāt — from pride; bhagavatā — by the Lord; cyāvitaḥ — expelled; ca — and; parājitaḥ — defeated; jīvan — alive; kathaṁcit — somehow; niryātaḥ — escaped; brahmaṇyena — by a Brahmin; anukampinā — compassionate
   By him, stripped of pride and defeated by the Lord, I somehow escaped alive through the compassion of the Supreme Brahman.
   
   Verse 7
   अथ मामुपसंप्राप्तो निर्वेदः परिभावितम्‌ ।
   ततोऽत्यन्तं पथि मया बहुधा परिदेवितम्‌ ॥ ७ ॥
   atha mām upasaṁprāpto nirvedaḥ paribhāvitaṁ ।
   tato'tyantaṁ pathi mayā bahudhā paridevitam ॥ 7 ॥
   atha — then; mām — to me; upasaṁprāptaḥ — approached; nirvedaḥ — dejection; paribhāvitaṁ — influenced; tataḥ — then; atyantaṁ — extensively; pathi — on the path; mayā — by me; bahudhā — many times; paridevitam — lamented
   Then, profound dejection overwhelmed me. I wandered extensively on the path and lamented many times.
   
   Verse 8
   संवर्तमवधूतेन्द्रं मार्गेऽकस्मात्‌ समासदम्‌ ।
   भस्मच्छन्नाग्निवद्‌ गूढं कथञ्चिदविदं तदा ॥ ८ ॥
   saṁvartam avadhūtendraṁ mārge'kasmāt samāsadam ।
   bhasmacchannāgnivad gūḍhaṁ kathaṁcidavidaṁ tadā ॥ 8 ॥
   saṁvartam — Samvarta; avadhūta — ascetic; indraṁ — leader; mārge — on the path; akasmāt — suddenly; samāsadam — I met; bhasmacchanna — covered with ashes; agnivad — like fire; gūḍhaṁ — hidden; kathaṁcid — somehow; avidaṁ — I recognized; tadā — then
   I suddenly encountered Samvarta, the leader of ascetics, on the path. Covered with ashes, like hidden fire, I recognized him somehow then.
   
   Verse 9
   सन्तप्त इव नीहारं तं सर्वाङ्गसुशीतलम्‌ ।
   सङ्गम्यैवातिशिशिरभावमासादयं तदा ॥ ९ ॥
   santapta iva nīhāraṁ taṁ sarvāṅgasuśītalam ।
   saṅgamyaivātiśiśirabhāvam āsādayaṁ tadā ॥ 9 ॥
   santaptaḥ — heated; iva — like; nīhāram — mist; taṁ — him; sarvāṅgasuśītalam — cool all over; saṅgamya — upon meeting; eva — indeed; atiśiśira — very cool; bhāvam — state; āsādayaṁ — I attained; tadā — then
   Like heated mist, he exuded coolness all over. Meeting him, I indeed found myself in a state of profound coolness.
   
   Verse 10
   मया स्वस्थितिमापृष्टः प्राहामृतसुपेशलम्‌ ।
   सुसारपिण्डवत्‌ सर्वं निष्कृष्य प्रत्यपादयत्‌ ॥ १० ॥
   mayā svasthitim āpṛṣṭaḥ prāhāmṛtasupēśalam ।
   susārapiṇḍavat sarvaṁ niṣkṛṣya pratyapādayat ॥ 10 ॥
   mayā — by me; svasthitim — his state; āpṛṣṭaḥ — asked; prāha — spoke; amṛtasupēśalam — sweet as nectar; susārapiṇḍavat — like an expertly crafted ball; sarvaṁ — everything; niṣkṛṣya — extracting; pratyapādayat — he presented
   When I inquired about his state, he spoke with the sweetness of nectar. He extracted and imparted all the essence, just like drawing the sap from a stalk.
   
   Verse 11
   नाहं तदशकं स्प्रष्टुं रङ्को राज्ञीं यथा तथा ।
   भूयः संप्रार्थितः सोऽथ भवन्तं मे विनिर्दिशत् ॥ ११ ॥
   nāhaṁ tadaśakaṁ spraṣṭuṁ raṅko rājñīṁ yathā tathā ।
   bhūyaḥ saṁprārthitaḥ so'tha bhavantaṁ me vinirdiśat ॥ 11 ॥
   na — not; aham — I; tad — that; aśakaṁ — capable; spraṣṭuṁ — to touch; raṅkaḥ — a beggar; rājñīṁ — queen; yathā — just as; tathā — likewise; bhūyaḥ — again; saṁprārthitaḥ — entreated; saḥ — he; atha — then; bhavantaṁ — you; me — to me; vinirdiśat — directed
   I couldn't touch it, like a beggar reaching for a queen. Pleading once more, he then directed me to you.
   
   Verse 12
   तद्भवच्चरणद्वन्द्वं तत आसादितं मया ।
   अन्धो जनसमायोगमिवात्यन्तसुखावहम्‌ ॥ १२ ॥
   tadbhavaccaraṇadvandvaṁ tata āsāditaṁ mayā ।
   andho janasamāyogamivātyantasukhāvaham ॥ 12 ॥
   tat — that; bhavat — your; caraṇa — feet; dvandvaṁ — pair; tata — then; āsāditaṁ — reached; mayā — by me; andhaḥ — blind man; jana — people; samāyogam — union; iva — like; atyanta — extremely; sukhāvaham — blissful
   Then, reaching your feet was like a blind man finding companionship — extremely blissful.
   
   Verse 13
   तन्मे न विदितं किञ्चित्‌ संवर्तमुनिराह यत्‌ ।
   श्रुतं माहात्म्यमखिलं त्रिपुराभक्तिकारकम्‌ ॥ १३ ॥
   tanme na viditaṁ kiñcit saṁvartamunirāha yat ।
   śrutaṁ māhātmyamakhilaṁ tripurābhaktikārakam ॥ 13 ॥
   tat — that; me — to me; na — not; viditaṁ — known; kiñcit — anything; saṁvarta — Samvarta; munirāha — the sage said; yat — what; śrutaṁ — heard; māhātmyaṁ — greatness; akhilaṁ — entire; tripurābhaktikārakam — inspiring devotion to Tripura
   That which the sage Samvarta said is not known to me. I have heard the complete greatness that fosters devotion to Tripura.
   
   Verse 14
   सा भवद्रूपिणी देवी हृदि नित्यं समाहिता ।
   एवं मे वर्तमानस्य किं फलं समवाप्यते ॥ १४ ॥
   sā bhavadrūpiṇī devī hṛdi nityaṁ samāhitā ।
   evaṁ me vartamānasya kiṁ phalaṁ samavāpyate ॥ 14 ॥
   sā — she; bhavadrūpiṇī — in your form; devī — the goddess; hṛdi — in the heart; nityaṁ — always; samāhitā — established; evaṁ — thus; me — my; vartamānasya — existing; kiṁ — what; phalaṁ — result; samavāpyate — is attained
   The goddess, in your form, is always established in my heart. Thus, what is the result of my existence?
   
   Verse 15
   भगवन्‌ कृपया ब्रूहि यत्संवर्तः पुरावदत्‌ ।
   अविदित्वा च तन्नास्ति क्वचिच्च कृतकृत्यता ॥ १५ ॥
   bhagavan kṛpayā brūhi yatsaṁvartaḥ purāvadat ।
   aviditvā ca tannāsti kvacicca kṛtakṛtyatā ॥ 15 ॥
   bhagavan — O Lord; kṛpayā — kindly; brūhi — tell; yat — what; saṁvartaḥ — Samvarta; purā — previously; avadat — said; aviditvā — without knowing; ca — and; tat — that; na — not; asti — is; kvacit — anywhere; ca — and; kṛtakṛtyatā — fulfillment
   O Lord, please share what Samvarta previously said. Without that knowledge, I find no fulfillment anywhere.
   
   Verse 16
   तदुक्तमविदित्वा तु यद्यच्च क्रियते मया ।
   तद्बालक्रीडनमिव प्रतिभाति समन्ततः ॥ १६ ॥
   taduktamaviditvā tu yadyacca kriyate mayā ।
   tadbālakrīḍanamiva pratibhāti samantataḥ ॥ 16 ॥
   tat — that; uktam — said; aviditvā — without knowing; tu — but; yat — what; yat — what; ca — and; kriyate — is done; mayā — by me; tat — that; bālakrīḍanam — child's play; iva — like; pratibhāti — appears; samantataḥ — entirely
   Without knowing what was said, everything I do feels futile, like a child's play.
   
   Verse 17
   पुरा मया हि बहुशः क्रतुभिर्दक्षिणोच्छ्रयैः ।
   प्रभूतान्नगणैरिष्टा देवाः शक्रमुखा ननु ॥ १७ ॥
   purā mayā hi bahuśaḥ kratubhir dakṣiṇocchrayaiḥ ।
   prabhūtānna gaṇair iṣṭā devāḥ śakramukhā nanu ॥ 17 ॥
   purā — previously; mayā — by me; hi — indeed; bahuśaḥ — many times; kratubhiḥ — by sacrifices; dakṣiṇa — with gifts; ucchrayaḥ — profuse; prabhūta — abundant; anna — food; gaṇaiḥ — with groups; iṣṭāḥ — worshipped; devāḥ — gods; śakramukhā — led by Indra; nanu — indeed
   Previously, many times, through sacrifices with generous gifts and abundant food, I worshipped the gods led by Indra.
   
   Verse 18
   तदल्पफलमेवेति श्रुतं संवर्तवक्त्रतः ।
   मन्ये तदहमल्पं यद्‌ दुःखमेवेति सर्वथा ॥ १८ ॥
   tadalpaphalameveti śrutaṁ saṁvartavakrataḥ ।
   manye tadaham alpaṁ yad duḥkham eveti sarvathā ॥ 18 ॥
   tat — that; alpa — small; phalam — result; eva — indeed; iti — thus; śrutaṁ — heard; saṁvarta — Samvarta; vaktrataḥ — from the mouth; manye — I consider; tat — that; aham — I; alpaṁ — small; yat — what; duḥkham — sorrow; eva — indeed; iti — thus; sarvathā — in every way
   That fruit, indeed, is a small result. As heard from the mouth of Samvarta, I consider that small, which is indeed sorrow in every way.
   
   Verse 19
   असुखं नहि दुःखं स्याद्‌ दुःखमल्पं सुखं स्मृतम्‌ ।
   यतः सुखात्यये दुःखं भवेद्‌ गुरुतरं किल ॥ १९ ॥
   asukhna na hi duḥkhaṁ syād duḥkham alpaṁ sukhaṁ smṛtam ।
   yataḥ sukhātyaye duḥkhaṁ bhaved gurutaraṁ kila ॥ 19 ॥
   asukhna — not happiness; na — not; hi — indeed; duḥkhaṁ — sorrow; syāt — would be; duḥkham — sorrow; alpaṁ — small; sukhaṁ — happiness; smṛtam — considered; yataḥ — because; sukhātyaye — in the absence of happiness; duḥkhaṁ — sorrow; bhaved — would be; gurutaram — heavier; kila — indeed
   Without happiness, indeed, sorrow would be greater. A little sorrow is considered happiness because, in the absence of happiness, sorrow would indeed be heavier.
   
   Verse 20
   नैतावदेव चैतस्मादधिकं चास्ति वैभवम्‌ ।
   मृत्यूपयोगो यद्भूयो न तन्न स्यात्‌ कदाचन ॥ २० ॥
   naitāvadeva caitasmād adhikaṁ cāsti vaibhavam ।
   mṛtyūpayoho yad bhūyo na tanna syāt kadācana ॥ 20 ॥
   na — not; etāvat — this much; eva — indeed; ca — and; etasmāt — than this; adhikam — more; ca — and; asti — is; vaibhavam — glory; mṛtyūpayoho — use of death; yad — which; bhūyo — again; na — not; tat — that; na — not; syāt — would be; kadācana — ever
   Not only this, indeed, but more than this is the glory; the final embrace of death. There never will be anything worse than that.
   
   Verse 21
   एवमेव भवेद्यन्मे क्रियते त्रिपुराविधौ ।
   बालक्रीडेव मे भाति सर्व तन्मानसं यतः ॥ २१ ॥
   evameva bhaved yan me kriyate tripurāvidhau ।
   bālakrīḍeva me bhāti sarva tanmānasaṁ yataḥ ॥ 21 ॥
   evam — thus; eva — indeed; bhaved — would be; yat — whatever; me — my; kriyate — is done; tripurāvidhau — in the worship of Tripura; bālakrīḍa — child's play; iva — like; me — to me; bhāti — appears; sarva — everything; tat — that; mānasaṁ — mental; yataḥ — because
   Indeed, whatever I do in the worship of Tripura seems to me like child’s play, as everything resides in the mind.
   
   Verse 22
   एतद्यदुक्तं भवता कर्तुं तत्‌ स्यादितोऽन्यथा ।
   नियतं चाप्यन्यथा तद्‌ वचोभेदसमाश्रयात्‌ ॥ २२ ॥
   etad yad uktaṁ bhavatā kartuṁ tat syād ito'nyathā ।
   niyataṁ cāpyanyathā tad vacobhedasamāśrayāt ॥ 22 ॥
   etat — this; yat — what; uktam — said; bhavatā — by you; kartum — to do; tat — that; syāt — would be; itaḥ — hence; anyathā — otherwise; niyatam — fixed; ca — and; api — also; anyathā — otherwise; tat — that; vacobheda — difference of words; samāśrayāt — from dependence
   What you instruct to be done should be followed accordingly; otherwise, the outcome will differ. Depending on the variation in words, the duty may also change.
   
   Verse 23
   आलम्बभेदततश्चापि विविधं प्रतिपद्यते ।
   कथमेतत्‌ क्रतुसममसत्यफलसम्मितम्‌ ॥ २३ ॥
   ālambabhedatataś cāpi vividhaṁ pratipadyate ।
   katham etat kratusamamasatyaphalasammitam ॥ 23 ॥
   ālamba — support; bheda — difference; tataḥ — hence; ca — and; api — also; vividham — variously; pratipadyate — behaves; katham — how; etat — this; kratu — sacrifice; samam — equal; asatyaphala — false result; sammitam — considered
   Various supports and diverse practices are perceived in their own ways. How can this be compared to a ritual that truly yields fruit?
   
   Verse 24
   अप्यसत्यात्मकं यस्मात्‌ कथं सत्यसमं भवेत्‌ ।
   अथापि नित्यं कर्तव्यमेतन्नास्यावधिः क्वचित्‌ ॥ २४ ॥
   apyasatyātmakaṁ yasmāt kathaṁ satyasamaṁ bhavet ।
   athāpi nityaṁ kartavyam etannāsyāvadhiḥ kvacit ॥ 24 ॥
   api — also; asatyātmakaṁ — untrue self; yasmāt — from which; katham — how; satyasamaṁ — equal to truth; bhavet — would be; atha — then; api — also; nityam — always; kartavyam — duty; etat — this; na — not; asya — its; avadhiḥ — limit; kvacit — anywhere
   Since it is based on an untrue self, how can it become like the truth? Nevertheless, one must always perform their duties; there is no limit for them at any time.
   
   Verse 25
   लक्षितो मे स भगवान्‌ संवर्तः सर्वशीतलः ।
   कर्तव्यलेशविषमविषज्वालाविनिर्गतः ॥ २५ ॥
   lakṣito me sa bhagavān saṁvartaḥ sarvaśītalaḥ ।
   kartavyaleśaviṣamaviṣajvālāvinirgataḥ ॥ 25 ॥
   lakṣitaḥ — observed; me — by me; saḥ — he; bhagavān — divine; saṁvartaḥ — Samvarta; sarvaśītalaḥ — entirely cool; kartavya — duty; leśa — trace; viṣama — poison; viṣajvālā — poison fire; vinirgataḥ — free from
   Observed by me, the divine Samvarta, entirely cool, free from the poison fire of the trace of duty.
   
   Verse 26
   हसन्निव लोकतन्त्रमभयं मार्गमाश्रितः ।
   वने दावाग्निसङ्कीर्णे हिमाम्बुस्थगजोपमः ॥ २६ ॥
   hasanniva lokatantram abhayaṁ mārgam āśritaḥ ।
   vane dāvāgnisaṅkīrṇe himāmbusthagajopamaḥ ॥ 26 ॥
   hasan — smiling; iva — as if; loka — world; tantram — system; abhayaṁ — fearless; mārgam — path; āśritaḥ — taken refuge; vane — in the forest; dāvāgni — forest fire; saṅkīrṇe — mixed; hima — cold; ambu — water; stha — residing; gaja — elephant; upamaḥ — like
   Smiling, as if he had taken refuge in the fearless path of the world system, he was like an elephant residing in cold water amidst a forest mixed with fire.
   
   Verse 27
   सर्वकर्तव्यवैकल्यामृतसंस्वादनन्दितः ।
   कथमेतां दशां प्राप्तो यच्च मामाह तत्पुरा ॥ २७ ॥
   Sarvakartavyavaikalyāmṛtasaṁsvādananditaḥ ।
   katham etāṁ daśāṁ prāpto yac ca mām āha tatpurā ॥ 27 ॥
   sarva — all; kartavya — duties; vaikalyā — lack; amṛta — nectar; saṁsvāda — taste; ānanditaḥ — delighted; katham — how; etāṁ — this; daśām — state; prāptaḥ — attained; yat — what; ca — and; mām — to me; āha — said; tatpurā — then
   Delighted by the taste of the nectar of being free from all duties, how did he attain this state, which he had described to me?
   
   Verse 28
   सर्वमेतत् सुकृपया गुरो मे वक्तुमर्हसि ।
   कर्तव्यकालभुजगनिगीर्णं मां विमोचय ॥ २८ ॥
   sarvametat sukripayā guro me vaktum arhasi ।
   kartavyakālabhujaganigīrṇaṁ māṁ vimocaya ॥ 28 ॥
   sarvam — all; etat — this; sukripayā — with kindness; guro — O Guru; me — to me; vaktum — to speak; arhasi — you should; kartavya — duty; kāla — time; bhujaga — serpent; nigīrṇaṁ — swallowed; māṁ — me; vimocaya — liberate
   O Guru, with kindness, you should tell me all of this. Liberate me, as I am swallowed by the serpent of duty and time.
   
   Verse 29
   इत्युक्त्वा चरणौ मूर्ध्ना गृहीत्वा दण्डवन्नतः ।
   अथ दृष्ट्वा तथाभूतं भार्गवं मुक्तिभाजनम्‌ ॥ २९ ॥
   ityuktvā caraṇau mūrdhnā gṛhītvā daṇḍavannataḥ ।
   atha dṛṣṭvā tathābhūtaṁ bhārgavaṁ muktibhājanam ॥ 29 ॥
   iti — thus; uktvā — having said; caraṇau — feet; mūrdhnā — with head; gṛhītvā — holding; daṇḍavat — like a stick; nataḥ — bowed; atha — then; dṛṣṭvā — seeing; tathābhūtaṁ — in that state; bhārgavaṁ — Bhargava, muktibhājanam — worthy of liberation
   Thus, having spoken, he bowed like a stick, holding the feet with his head. Then, seeing Bhargava in that state, worthy of liberation.
   
   Verse 30
   दयमानस्वभावोऽथ दत्तो वक्तुमुपाक्रमत्‌ ।
   वत्स भार्गव धन्योऽसि यस्य ते बुद्धिरीदृशी ॥ ३० ॥
   dayamānasvabhāvo'tha datto vaktumupākramat ।
   vatsa bhārgava dhanyo'si yasya te buddhirīdṛśī ॥ 30 ॥
   dayamāna — compassionate; svabhāvaḥ — nature; atha — then; datto — Dattatreya; vaktum — to speak, upākramat — began; vatsa — my dear; bhārgava — Bhargava; dhanyaḥ — blessed; asi — you are; yasya — whose; te — your; buddhiḥ — intellect; īdṛśī — such
   With a compassionate nature, Dattatreya then began to speak. "My dear Bhargava, you are blessed, whose intellect is such."
   
   Verse 31
   अब्धौ निमज्जतो नौकासम्प्राप्तिरिव सङ्गता ।
   एतावदेव सुकृतिः क्रियाभिरुपसङ्गतः ॥ ३१ ॥
   abdhau nimajjato naukāsamprāptiriva saṅgatā ।
   etāvadeva sukṛtiḥ kriyābhirupasaṅgataḥ ॥ 31 ॥
   abdhau — in the ocean; nimajjataḥ — drowning; naukā — boat; samprāptiḥ — arrival; iva — like; saṅgatā — association; etāvat — this much; eva — indeed; sukṛtiḥ — virtuous; kriyābhiḥ — by actions; upasaṅgataḥ — attained
   Just like a boat’s arrival to one drowning in the ocean, this association is indeed attained by virtuous actions.
   
   Verse 32
   स्वात्मानमारोहयति पदे परमपावने ।
   सा देवी त्रिपुरा सर्वह्रदयाकाशरूपिणी ॥ ३२ ॥
   svātmānamārohāyati pade paramapāvane ।
   sā devī tripurā sarvahṛdayākāśarūpiṇī ॥ 32 ॥
   svātmānam — oneself; ārohāyati — ascends; pade — to the state; parama — supreme; pāvane — pure; sā — she; devī — goddess; tripurā — Tripura; sarvahṛdaya — all hearts; ākāśarūpiṇī — of the form of space
   One ascends to the supreme pure state. She, the goddess Tripura, is of the form of space in all hearts.
   
   Verse 33
   अनन्यशरणं भक्तं प्रत्येवंरूपिणी द्रुतम्‌ ।
   ह्रदयान्तः परिणता मोचयेद्‌ मृत्युजालतः ॥ ३३ ॥
   ananyaśaraṇaṁ bhaktaṁ pratyevaṁrūpiṇī drutam ।
   hṛdayāntaḥ pariṇatā mocayed mṛtyujālataḥ ॥ 33 ॥
   ananyaśaraṇaṁ — without any other refuge; bhaktaṁ — devotee; prati — towards; evaṁrūpiṇī — in this form; drutam — quickly; hṛdayāntaḥ — within the heart; pariṇatā — transformed; mocayed — would liberate; mṛtyujālataḥ — from the net of death
   Without any other refuge, the devotee, devoted to this form, is quickly transformed within the heart and liberated from the net of death.
   
   Verse 34
   यावत्‌ कर्तव्यवेतालान्न बिभेति दृढं नरः ।
   न तावत्‌ सुखमाप्नोति वेतालाविष्टवत्‌ सदा ॥ ३४ ॥
   yāvat kartavyavetālānna bibheti dṛḍhaṁ naraḥ ।
   na tāvat sukhamāpnoti vetālāviṣṭavat sadā ॥ 34 ॥
   yāvat — as long as; kartavya — duty; vetālān — ghosts; na — not; bibheti — fears; dṛḍhaṁ — firmly; naraḥ — man; na — not; tāvat — then; sukham — happiness; āpnoti — attains; vetāla — possessed; āviṣṭa — like; vat — always; sadā — always
   As long as a man does not firmly fear the ghosts of duties, he does not attain happiness and remains like one possessed.
   
   Verse 35
   नृणां कर्तव्यकालाहिसन्दष्टानां कथं शुभम्‌ ।
   करालगरलज्वालाक्रान्ताङ्गानामिव क्वचित्‌ ॥ ३५ ॥
   nṛṇāṁ kartavyakālāhisaṁdaṣṭānāṁ kathaṁ śubham ।
   karālagaralajvālākrāntāṅgānāmiva kvacit ॥ 35 ॥
   nṛṇāṁ — of men; kartavya — duty; kāla — time; ahi — serpent; saṁdaṣṭānāṁ — bitten; kathaṁ — how; śubham — auspiciousness; karāla — terrible; garala — poison; jvālā — flames; ākrānta — scorched; aṅgānām — bodies; iva — like; kvacit — anywhere
   What auspiciousness can there be for men bitten by the serpent of duty and time? They are like bodies scorched by the terrible poison flames.
   
   Verse 36
   कर्तव्यविषसंसर्गमूर्च्छितं पश्य वै जगत्‌ ।
   अन्धीभूतं न जानाति क्रियां स्वस्य हितात्मिकाम्‌ ॥ ३६ ॥
   kartavyaviṣasaṁsargamūrchitaṁ paśya vai jagat ।
   andhībhūtaṁ na jānāti kriyāṁ svasya hitātmikām ॥ 36 ॥
   kartavya — duty; viṣa — poison; saṁsarga — association; mūrchitaṁ — unconscious; paśya — see; vai — indeed; jagat — world; andhībhūtaṁ — blinded; na — not; jānāti — knows; kriyāṁ — action; svasya — own; hita — beneficial; ātmikām — nature
   Indeed, observe the world, unconscious due to the poison of duty, blinded, not knowing what actions are truly beneficial for them.
   
   Verse 37
   अन्यथा चेष्टते भूयो मोहमापद्यते पुनः ।
   एवंविधो हि लोकोऽयं कर्तव्यविषमूर्च्छितः ॥ ३७ ॥
   anyathā ceṣṭate bhūyo mohamāpadyate punaḥ ।
   evaṁvidho hi loko'yaṁ kartavyaviṣamūrchitaḥ ॥ 37 ॥
   anyathā — otherwise; ceṣṭate — acts; bhūyaḥ — again; moham — delusion; āpadyate — falls into; punaḥ — again; evaṁvidhaḥ — such; hi — indeed; lokaḥ — world; ayam — this; kartavya — duty; viṣa — poison; mūrchitaḥ — unconscious
   Otherwise, one acts again, falls into delusion once more. Indeed, this world is such, unconscious due to the poison of duty.
   
   Verse 38
   अनादिकालतो भीमे पच्यते विषसागरे ।
   यथा हि केचित्‌ पथिकाः प्राप्ता विन्ध्यमहानगम्‌ ॥ ३८ ॥
   anādikālato bhīme pacyate viṣasāgare ।
   yathā hi kecit pathikāḥ prāptā vindhyamahānagam ॥ 38 ॥
   anādi — from time immemorial; kālataḥ — from time; bhīme — terrible; pacyate — cooked; viṣasāgare — in the ocean of poison; yathā — as; hi — indeed; kecit — some; pathikāḥ — travelers; prāptāḥ — reached; vindhya — Vindhya; mahān — great; agam — mountain
   Since time immemorial, cooked in the terrible ocean of poison, just as some travelers reached the great Vindhya mountain.
   
   Verse 39
   क्षुधाभरसमाक्रान्ताः फलानि ददृशुर्वने ।
   विषमुष्टिफलान्याशु तिन्दुकस्य फलेहया ॥ ३९ ॥
   kṣudhābharasamākrāntāḥ phalāni dadṛśurvane ।
   viṣamuṣṭiphalānyāśu tindukasya phalehayā ॥ 39 ॥
   kṣudhā — hunger; bhara — burden; samākrāntāḥ — overwhelmed; phalāni — fruits; dadṛśuḥ — saw; vane — in the forest; viṣamuṣṭiphalāni — poisonous berries; āśu — quickly; tindukasya — of Tinduka; phalehayā — desiring fruits
   Overwhelmed by hunger, they saw fruits in the forest and, desiring them quickly, ate the poisonous berries of Tinduka.
   
   Verse 40
   भक्षयामासुरत्यन्तक्षुधानष्टरसेन्द्रियाः ।
   अथ ते तद्विषज्वा​​लाज्वलिताङ्गाः सुपीडिताः ॥ ४० ॥
   bhakṣayāmāsuratyanta kṣudhānaṣṭarasaindriyāḥ ।
   atha te tadviṣajvālājvalitāṅgāḥ supīḍitāḥ ॥ 40 ॥
   bhakṣayāmāsuḥ — they ate; atyanta — extremely; kṣudhānaṣṭa — destroyed by hunger; rasa — taste; indriyāḥ — senses; atha — then; te — they; tad — that; viṣa — poison; jvālā — flame; jvalita — burned; aṅgāḥ — bodies; supīḍitāḥ — greatly distressed
   Overwhelmed by extreme hunger, they ate, losing their senses and taste. Greatly distressed, their bodies were burned by the poison flames.
   
   Verse 41
   अन्धीभूता विचिन्वन्तस्तद्विषोष्णप्रशान्तये ।
   अविदित्वा मुष्टिफलं तिन्दूफलनिषेवणात्‌ ॥ ४१ ॥
   andhībhūtā vicinvantas tadviṣoṣṇapraśāntaye ।
   aviditvā muṣṭiphalaṁ tindūphalaṇiṣevaṇāt ॥ 41 ॥
   andhībhūtāḥ — blinded; vicinvantaḥ — searching; tat — that; viṣa — poison; uṣṇa — heat; praśāntaye — to calm; aviditvā — not knowing; muṣṭiphalaṁ — poisonous fruit; tindūphalaṇiṣevaṇāt — from consuming Tinduka fruit
   Blinded and seeking to calm the heat from the Tinduka fruit, which they had consumed, not knowing it was poisonous.
   
   Verse 42
   मत्वा ज्वालां निजे देहे धत्तूरफलमासदुः ।
   भ्रान्त्या जम्बीरबुद्धया तत्‌ सर्वैरासीत्‌ सुभक्षितम्‌ ॥ ४२ ॥
   matvā jvālāṁ nije dehe dhattūraphalamāsaduḥ ।
   bhrāntyā jambīrabuddhayā tat sarvairāsīt subhakṣitam ॥ 42 ॥
   matvā — thinking; jvālāṁ — flame; nije — own; dehe — in the body; dhattūraphalam — Datura fruit; āsaduḥ — took; bhrāntyā — in delusion; jambīrabuddhayā — mistaking for lemon; tat — that; sarvaiḥ — by all; āsīt — was; subhakṣitam — well eaten
   Thinking of the flames in their own bodies, they took the Datura fruit in their delusion, mistaking it for a lemon, and it was eagerly consumed by all.
   
   Verse 43
   उन्मत्ताश्च ततोऽभूवन्‌ मार्गाद्‌ भ्रष्टाश्च ते तदा ।
   अन्धीभूतातिगहने पतन्तो निम्नभूमिषु ॥ ४३ ॥
   unmattāś ca tato'bhūvan mārgād bhraṣṭāś ca te tadā ।
   andhībhūtātigahane patanto nimnabhūmiṣu ॥ 43 ॥
   unmattāḥ — insane; ca — and; tataḥ — then; abhūvan — became; mārgāt — from the path; bhraṣṭāḥ — fallen; ca — and; te — they; tadā — then; andhībhūtātigahane — in the dense blindness; patantaḥ — falling; nimnabhūmiṣu — into the low grounds
   Then, they became insane and strayed from the path, falling into deep blindness and sinking into low grounds.
   
   Verse 44
   कण्टकैश्छिन्न सर्वाङ्गा भग्नबाहूरुपादकाः ।
   अधिक्षिपन्तश्चान्योन्यं कलह चक्रुरुच्चकैः ॥ ४४ ॥
   kaṇṭakaiś chinna sarvāṅgā bhagnabāhūrupādakāḥ ।
   adhikṣipantaś cānyonyaṁ kalaha cakruruccakaiḥ ॥ 44 ॥
   kaṇṭakaiḥ — by thorns; chinna — cut; sarvāṅgā — all over the body; bhagna — broken; bāhūru — arms and thighs; pādakāḥ — feet; adhikṣipantaḥ — insulting; ca — and; anyonyaṁ — each other; kalaha — quarrel; cakruḥ — did; uccakaiḥ — loudly
   Cut all over the body by thorns, with broken arms, thighs, and feet, they insulted each other and quarreled loudly.
   
   Verse 45
   मुष्टिभिश्च शिलाभिश्च काष्ठर्जध्नुः परस्परम्‌ ।
   अथ ते दीर्णसर्वाङ्गाः पुरं कञ्चित्‌ समासदुः ॥ ४५ ॥
   muṣṭibhiś ca śilābhiś ca kāṣṭhārjadhnuḥ parasparam ।
   atha te dīrṇasarvāṅgāḥ puraṁ kañcit samāsaduḥ ॥ 45 ॥
   muṣṭibhiḥ — with fists; ca — and; śilābhiḥ — with stones; ca — and; kāṣṭhaiḥ — with sticks; ajadhnuḥ — struck; parasparam — each other; atha — then; te — they; dīrṇa — torn; sarvāṅgāḥ — all over the body; puraṁ — city; kañcit — some; samāsaduḥ — reached
   With fists, stones, and sticks, they struck each other. Torn all over the body, they finally reached a city.
   
   Verse 46
   निशीथे दैववशतः पुरद्वारमुपाययुः ।
   पुरद्वाराधिपालैस्ते प्रतिरुद्धाः प्रवेशने ॥ ४६ ॥
   niśīthe daivavaśataḥ puradvāramupāyayuḥ ।
   puradvārādhipālais te pratiruddhāḥ praveśane ॥ 46 ॥
   niśīthe — at midnight; daivavaśataḥ — by fate; puradvāram — city gate; upāyayuḥ — approached; puradvāra — city gate; adhipālaiḥ — by the guards; te — they; pratiruddhāḥ — blocked; praveśane — in entering
   At midnight, by fate, they approached the city gate, only to be blocked by the guards at the entrance.
   
   Verse 47
   देशकालानभिज्ञानात्‌ कलहं चक्रुरुच्चकैः ।
   अथ ते प्रहृता द्वारपालैरतितरां यदा ॥ ४७ ॥
   deśakālānabhiñānāt kalahaṁ cakruruccakaiḥ ।
   atha te prahṛtā dvārapālairatitarāṁ yadā ॥ 47 ॥
   deśakāla — place and time; anabhiñānāt — without knowledge; kalahaṁ — quarrel; cakruḥ — did; uccakaiḥ — loudly; atha — then; te — they; prahṛtāḥ — struck; dvārapālaiḥ — by the gatekeepers; atitarām — excessively; yadā — when
   Without knowledge of place and time, they quarreled loudly. Then, excessively struck by the gatekeepers.
   
   Verse 48
   तदा पलायनपरा बभूवुः परितस्तु ते ।
   पतिताः परिखे केचिद्‌ भक्षिता मकरादिभिः ॥ ४८ ॥
   tadā palāyanaparā babhūvuḥ paritastu te ।
   patitāḥ parikhe kecid bhakṣitā makarādibhiḥ ॥ 48 ॥
   tadā — then; palāyana — fleeing; parā — intent; babhūvuḥ — became; paritas — around; tu — indeed; te — they; patitāḥ — fell; parikhe — in the ditch; kecid — some; bhakṣitāḥ — devoured; makarādibhiḥ — by crocodiles and others
   Intent on fleeing, they scattered. Some fell into ditches, while others were devoured by crocodiles and other creatures.
   
   Verse 49
   केचित्‌ खातेषु कूपेषु पतिताः प्राणमुत्सृजुः ।
   अपरे तैर्विनिहताः केचिज्जीवग्रहं गताः ॥ ४९ ॥
   kecit khāteṣu kūpeṣu patitāḥ prāṇamutsṛjuḥ ।
   apare tairvinihatāḥ kecijjīvagrahaṁ gatāḥ ॥ 49 ॥
   kecit — some; khāteṣu — in pits; kūpeṣu — in wells; patitāḥ — fell; prāṇam — life; utsṛjuḥ — gave up; apare — others; taiḥ — by them; vinihatāḥ — killed; kecit — some; jīvagrahaṁ — captivity; gatāḥ — went
   Some fell into pits and wells, giving up their lives. Others were killed by the guards, and some were taken into captivity.
   
   Verse 50
   ​​एवं जना हितेच्छाभिः कर्तव्यविषमूर्च्छिताः ।
   अहो विनाशं यान्त्युच्चैर्मोहेनान्धीकृताः खलु ॥ ५० ॥
   evaṁ janā hitecchābhiḥ kartavyaviṣamūrchitāḥ ।
   aho vināśaṁ yānty uccairmohenāndhīkṛtāḥ khalu ॥ 50 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; janāḥ — people; hitecchābhiḥ — with desire for welfare; kartavya — duty; viṣa — poison; mūrchitāḥ — unconscious; aho — alas; vināśaṁ — destruction; yānti — go; uccaiḥ — greatly; mohenāndhīkṛtāḥ — blinded by delusion; khalu — indeed
   Thus, people with desires for welfare, unconscious from the poison of duty, alas, go to great destruction, greatly blinded by delusion.
   
   Verse 51
   धन्योऽसि भार्गवं त्वं तु यस्मादभ्युदयं गतः ।
   विचारः सर्वमूलं हि सोपानं प्रथमं भवेत्‌ ॥ ५१ ॥
   dhanyo'si bhārgavaṁ tvaṁ tu yasmād abhyudayaṁ gataḥ ।
   vicāraḥ sarvamūlaṁ hi sopānaṁ prathamaṁ bhavet ॥ 51 ॥
   dhanyaḥ — blessed; asi — are; bhārgavaṁ — Bhargava; tvaṁ — you; tu — indeed; yasmāt — because; abhyudayaṁ — prosperity; gataḥ — reached; vicāraḥ — contemplation; sarvamūlaṁ — the root of all; hi — indeed; sopānaṁ — step; prathamaṁ — first; bhavet — would be
   You are blessed, Bhargava, for you have achieved prosperity. Contemplation is indeed the root of all and the first step.
   
   Verse 52
   परश्रेयोमहासौधप्राप्तौ जानीहि सर्वथा ।
   सुविचारमृते क्षेमप्राप्तिः कस्य कथं भवेत्‌ ॥ ५२ ॥
   paraśreyo mahāsaudha prāptau jānīhi sarvathā ।
   suvicāramṛte kṣemaprāptiḥ kasya kathaṁ bhavet ॥ 52 ॥
   paraśreyaḥ — highest good; mahāsaudha — great mansion; prāptau — in attaining; jānīhi — know; sarvathā — in every way; suvicāra — good contemplation; mṛte — without; kṣemaprāptiḥ — attainment of welfare; kasya — whose; kathaṁ — how; bhavet — would be
   To achieve the highest good, the great mansion, understand that without proper contemplation, attaining welfare in every way would be impossible.
   
   Verse 53
   अविचारः परो मृत्युरविचारहता जनाः ।
   विमृश्यकारी जयति सर्वत्राभीष्टसङ्गमात्‌ ॥ ५३ ॥
   avichāraḥ paro mṛtyuravichārahataḥ janāḥ ।
   vimṛśyakārī jayati sarvatrābhīṣṭasaṅgamāt ॥ 53 ॥
   avichāraḥ — lack of contemplation; paro — supreme; mṛtyuḥ — death; avichārahataḥ — those destroyed by lack of contemplation; janāḥ — people; vimṛśyakārī — one who contemplates; jayati — conquers; sarvatra — everywhere; abhīṣṭasaṅgamāt — by desirable associations
   Lack of contemplation is the ultimate death; people perish due to lack of contemplation. One who contemplates triumphs everywhere through favorable associations.
   
   Verse 54
   अविचारहता दैत्या यातुधानाश्च सर्वशः ।
   विचारपरमा देवाः सर्वतः सुखभागिनः ॥ ५४ ॥
   avicārahata daityā yātudhānāś ca sarvaśaḥ ।
   vicāraparamā devāḥ sarvataḥ sukhabhāginaḥ ॥ 54 ॥
   avicāra — without contemplation; hata — destroyed; daityāḥ — demons; yātudhānāḥ — ogres; ca — and; sarvaśaḥ — in every way; vicāraparamāḥ — full of contemplation; devāḥ — gods; sarvataḥ — in every way; sukhabhāginaḥ — enjoy happiness
   Without contemplation, demons and ogres are utterly destroyed. Conversely, gods, brimming with contemplation, enjoy happiness in all aspects.
   
   Verse 55
   विचारद्विष्णुमाश्रित्य जयन्ति प्रत्यरीन्‌ सदा ।
   विचारः सुखवृक्षस्य बिजमङ्कुरशक्तिकम्‌ ॥ ५५ ॥
   vicāra-dviṣṇumāśritya jayanti pratyarīn sadā ।
   vicāraḥ sukhavṛkṣasya bija-maṅkuraśaktikam ॥ 55 ॥
   vicāra — contemplation; dviṣṇumāśritya — relying on Vishnu; jayanti — conquer; pratyarīn — enemies; sadā — always; vicāraḥ — contemplation; sukhavṛkṣasya — of the tree of happiness; bija — seed; maṅkura — sprout; śaktikam — energy
   By relying on Vishnu through contemplation, they consistently overcome their enemies. Contemplation serves as the seed and nurturing energy of the tree of happiness.
   
   Verse 56
   विराजते विचारेण पुरुषः सर्वतोऽधिकः ।
   विचाराद्विधिरुत्कृष्टो विचारात्‌ पृज्यते हरिः ॥ ५६ ॥
   virājate vicāreṇa puruṣaḥ sarvato'dhikaḥ ।
   vicārādvidhirutkṛṣṭo vicārāt pṛjyate hariḥ ॥ 56 ॥
   virājate — shines; vicāreṇa — by contemplation; puruṣaḥ — man; sarvataḥ — in every way; adhikaḥ — greater; vicārāt — by contemplation; vidhiḥ — order; utkṛṣṭaḥ — excellent; vicārāt — by contemplation; pṛjyate — is worshipped; hariḥ — Vishnu
   A man excels through contemplation, becoming greater in every way. Through contemplation, order is maintained excellently. Through contemplation, Vishnu is worshipped.
   
   Verse 57
   सर्वज्ञस्तु विचारेण शिव आसीन्महेश्वरः ।
   अविचारान्मृगासक्तो रामो बुद्धिमतांवरः ॥ ५७ ॥
   sarvajñastu vicāreṇa śiva āsīn maheśvaraḥ ।
   avicārān mṛgāsakto rāmo buddhimatāṁ varaḥ ॥ 57 ॥
   sarvajñaḥ — all-knowing; tu — indeed; vicāreṇa — by contemplation; śivaḥ — Shiva; āsīt — was; maheśvaraḥ — the great Lord; avicārāt — without contemplation; mṛgāsaktaḥ — attached to the deer; rāmaḥ — Rama; buddhimatāṁ varaḥ — the best among the wise
   Indeed, through contemplation, Shiva, the great Lord, became all-knowing. Without contemplation, even Rama, the best among the wise, was captivated by the deer.
   
   Verse 58
   परमामापदं प्राप्तो विचारादथ वारिधिम्‌ ।
   बद्ध्वा लङ्कपुरीं रक्षोगणाकीर्णां समाक्रमत्‌ ॥ ५८ ॥
   paramām āpadaṁ prāpto vicārād atha vāridhim ।
   baddhvā laṅkapurīṁ rakṣogaṇākīrṇāṁ samākramat ॥ 58 ॥
   paramām — great; āpadaṁ — distress; prāptaḥ — attained; vicārāt — by contemplation; atha — then; vāridhim — ocean; baddhvā — building a bridge; laṅkapurīṁ — the city of Lanka; rakṣogaṇākīrṇām — filled with demons; samākramat — attacked
   In great distress, Rama, through contemplation, constructed a bridge over the ocean and launched an attack on the city of Lanka, which was filled with demons.
   
   Verse 59
   अविचाराद्विधिरपि मूढो भूत्वाऽभिमानतः ।
   शिरश्छेदं समगमदिति संश्रृतमेव ते ॥ ५९ ॥
   avicārād vidhir api mūḍho bhūtvā'bhimānataḥ ।
   śiraśchedaṁ samagamad iti saṁśṛtameva te ॥ 59 ॥
   avicārāt — without contemplation; vidhiḥ — Brahma; api — even; mūḍhaḥ — foolish; bhūtvā — becoming; abhimānataḥ — due to pride; śiraḥchedam — beheading; samagamat — attained; iti — thus; saṁśṛtam — it is heard; eva — indeed; te — by you
   Without contemplation, even Brahma became foolish due to pride and faced beheading. Thus, you have indeed heard.
   
   Verse 60
   महादेवोऽविचारेण वरं दत्वाऽसुराय वै ।
   भस्मीभावात्‌ स्वस्य भीतः पलायनपरोऽभवत्‌ ॥ ६० ॥
   mahādevo'vicāreṇa varaṁ datvā'surāya vai ।
   bhasmībhāvāt svasya bhītaḥ palāyanaparo'bhavat ॥ 60 ॥
   mahādevaḥ — great god; avicāreṇa — without contemplation; varam — boon; datvā — giving; asurāya — to the demon; vai — indeed; bhasmībhāvāt — turning to ashes; svasya — of himself; bhītaḥ — afraid; palāyanaparaḥ — intent on fleeing; abhavat — became
   Without contemplation, the great god Shiva, upon granting a boon to a demon, feared turning to ashes himself and resorted to fleeing.
   
   Verse 61
   अविचाराद्धरिः पूर्वं भृगुपत्नों निहत्य तु ।
   शापेन परमं दुःखमाप्तमवापा त्यन्तदुःसहम्‌ ॥ ६१ ॥
   avicārāddhariḥ pūrvaṁ bhṛgupatnōṁ nihatya tu ।
   śāpena paramaṁ duḥkham āptam avāpātyantaduḥsaham ॥ 61 ॥
   avicārāt — without contemplation; hariḥ — Vishnu; pūrvam — previously; bhṛgupatnōṁ — Bhrigu's wife; nihatya — killing; tu — indeed; śāpena — by the curse; paramam — great; duḥkham — sorrow; āptam — attained; avāpa — suffered; atyantaduḥsaham — extremely unbearable
   Without contemplation, Vishnu once killed Bhrigu’s wife. As a result of the curse, he endured immense sorrow and suffered extremely unbearable distress.
   
   Verse 62
   एवमन्ये सुरा देवा यातुधाना नरा मृगाः ।
   अविचारवशादेव विपदं प्राप्नुवन्ति हि ॥ ६२ ॥
   evamanye surā devā yātudhānā narā mṛgāḥ ।
   avicāravaśādeva vipadaṁ prāpnuvanti hi ॥ 62 ॥
   evam — thus; anye — others; surā — gods; devāḥ — deities; yātudhānāḥ — demons; narāḥ — men; mṛgāḥ — animals; avicāravaśāt — due to lack of contemplation; eva — indeed; vipadaṁ — distress; prāpnuvanti — attain; hi — indeed
   Thus, without contemplation, gods, deities, demons, humans, and animals all inevitably experience distress.
   
   Verse 63
   महाभागास्ते हि धीरा यान्‌ कुत्रापि च भार्गव । ​​
   विजहाति विचारो नो नमस्तेभ्यो निरन्तरम्‌ ॥ ६३ ॥
   mahābhāgāste hi dhīrā yān kutrāpi ca bhārgava ।
   ​​vijahāti vicāro no namastebhyo nirantaram ॥ 63 ॥
   mahābhāgāḥ — greatly fortunate; te — they; hi — indeed; dhīrāḥ — wise; yān — who; kutrāpi — anywhere; ca — and; bhārgava — O Bhargava; vijahāti — abandons; vicāraḥ — contemplation; no — not; namastebhyo — salutations to them; nirantaram — continually
   O Bhargava, those wise ones who are never abandoned by contemplation are greatly fortunate. Salutations to them continually.
   
   Verse 64
   कर्तव्यमविचारेण प्राप्य मुह्यन्ति सर्वतः ।
   विचार्य कृत्वा सर्वेभ्यो मुच्यतेऽपारसङ्कटैः ॥ ६४ ॥
   kartavyamavicāreṇa prāpya muhyanti sarvataḥ ।
   vicārya kṛtvā sarvebhyo mucyate'pārasaṅkaṭaiḥ ॥ 64 ॥
   kartavyam — duty; avicāreṇa — without contemplation; prāpya — attaining; muhyanti — become deluded; sarvataḥ — everywhere; vicārya — contemplating; kṛtvā — doing; sarvebhyaḥ — from all; mucyate — is freed; apārasaṅkaṭaiḥ — from boundless distress
   Attaining duty without contemplation leads to delusion everywhere. By contemplating and acting, one is freed from all boundless distress.
   
   Verse 65
   एवं लोकांश्चिरादेषोऽविचारः सङ्गतोऽभवत्‌ ।
   यस्याविचारो यावत्‌ स्यात्‌ कुतस्तावद्विमर्शनम् ॥ ६५ ॥
   evaṁ lokāṁścirādeṣo'vicāraḥ saṅgato'bhavat ।
   yasyāvicāro yāvat syāt kutastāvadvimarśanam ॥ 65 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; lokān — people; cirāt — for a long time; eṣaḥ — this; avicāraḥ — lack of contemplation; saṅgataḥ — associated; abhavat — became; yasya — whose; avicāraḥ — lack of contemplation; yāvat — as long as; syāt — would be; kutaḥ — where; tāvat — then; vimarśanam — reflection
   Thus, for a long time, people have been associated with a lack of contemplation. As long as contemplation is absent, where can reflection be found?
   
   Verse 66
   ग्रीष्मभीष्मकरातप्ते मरौ क्व शिशिरं जलम्‌ ।
   एवं चिराविचाराग्निज्वालामालापरीवृते ॥ ६६ ॥
   grīṣmabhīṣmakarātapte marau kva śiśiraṁ jalam ।
   evaṁ cirāvicārāgnijvālāmalāparīvṛte ॥ 66 ॥
   grīṣma — summer; bhīṣma — intense; kara — rays, ātapte — heated; marau — in the desert; kva — where; śiśiraṁ — cool; jalam — water; evaṁ — thus; cirāvicārāgni — long-lasting fire of lack of contemplation; jvālā — flames; malā — impurities; parīvṛte — surrounded
   In the summer, in a desert scorched by intense rays, where is cool water found? Similarly, one is engulfed by the enduring flames of lack of contemplation and impurities.
   
   Verse 67
   विचारशीतलस्पर्शः कथं स्यात्‌ साधनं विना ।
   साधनं त्वेकमेवात्र परमं सर्वतोऽधिकम्‌ ॥ ६७ ॥
   vicāraśītalasparśaḥ kathaṁ syāt sādhanam vinā ।
   sādhanaṁ tvekamevātra paramaṁ sarvato'dhikam ॥ 67 ॥
   vicāra — contemplation; śītala — cool; sparśaḥ — touch; kathaṁ — how; syāt — would be; sādhanam — means; vinā — without; sādhanaṁ — means; tu — but; ekam — one; eva — indeed; atra — here; paramaṁ — supreme; sarvataḥ — in every way; adhikam — greater
   Without the means, how would the cool touch of contemplation be experienced? Indeed, the means here is singular, supreme, and superior in every way.
   
   Verse 68
   सर्वहृत्पद्मनिलयदेवतायाः परा कृपा ।
   तां विना स्यात्‌ कथं कस्य महाश्रेयः सुसाधनः ॥ ६८ ॥
   sarvahṛtpadmanilayadevatāyāḥ parā kṛpā ।
   tāṁ vinā syāt kathaṁ kasya mahāśreyaḥ susādhanaḥ ॥ 68 ॥
   sarvahṛt — all hearts; padma — lotus; nilaya — residing; devatāyāḥ — of the deity; parā — supreme; kṛpā — grace; tāṁ — that; vinā — without; syāt — would be; kathaṁ — how; kasya — whose; mahāśreyaḥ — great welfare; susādhanaḥ — easy attainment
   Without the supreme grace of the deity residing in the lotus of all hearts, how would anyone easily attain great welfare?
   
   Verse 69
   विचारार्कोऽविचारान्धमहाध्वान्तनिबर्हणः ।
   तत्र मूलं भवेद्भक्त्या देवतापरिराधनम्‌ ॥ ६९ ॥
   vicārārko'vicārāndhamahādhvāntanibarhaṇaḥ ।
   tatra mūlaṁ bhavedbhaktyā devatāparirādhanam ॥ 69 ॥
   vicāra — contemplation; arkaḥ — sun; avicāra — lack of contemplation; andha — blind; mahādhvānta — great darkness; nibarhaṇaḥ — dispeller; tatra — there; mūlaṁ — root; bhavet — would be; bhaktyā — with devotion; devatā — deity; parirādhanam — worship
   The sun of contemplation dispels the great darkness of non-contemplation. There, the foundation lies in the devoted worship of the deity.
   
   Verse 70
   राधिता परमा देवी सम्यक्‌ तुष्टा सती तदा ।
   विचाररूपतां याति चित्ताकाशे रविर्यथा ॥ ७० ॥
   rādhitā paramā devī samyak tuṣṭā satī tadā ।
   vicārarūpatāṁ yāti cittākāśe raviryathā ॥ 70 ॥
   rādhitā — worshipped; parama — supreme; devī — goddess; samyak — completely; tuṣṭā — pleased; satī — being; tadā — then; vicārarūpatāṁ — form of contemplation; yāti — attains; cittākāśe — in the sky of the mind; raviḥ — sun; yathā — like
   When the supreme goddess is completely worshipped and pleased, she assumes the form of contemplation, like the sun illuminating the sky of the mind.
   
   Verse 71
   तस्मान्निजात्मरुपां तां त्रिपुरां परमेश्वरीम्‌ ।
   सर्वान्तरनिकेतां श्रीमहेशीं चिन्मयीं शिवाम्‌ ॥ ७१ ॥
   tasmān nijātmarupāṁ tāṁ tripurāṁ parameśvarīm ।
   sarvāntaraniketāṁ śrīmahēśīṁ cinmayīṁ śivām ॥ 71 ॥
   tasmāt — therefore; nijātmarupāṁ — of one's own form; tāṁ — that; tripurāṁ — Tripura; parameśvarīm — supreme goddess; sarvāntara — all within; niketāṁ — dwelling; śrīmahēśīṁ — great goddess; cinmayīṁ — of consciousness; śivām — auspicious
   Therefore, worship Tripura, the supreme goddess, dwelling within all, the great and auspicious goddess of consciousness.
   
   Verse 72
   आराधयेदकापटयात्‌ सद्गुरुद्वारतः क्रमात्‌ ।
   आराधनेऽपि मूलं स्याद्भक्तिः श्रद्धा च निर्मला ॥ ७२ ॥
   ārādhayedakāpaṭayāt sadgurudvārataḥ kramāt ।
   ārādhane'pi mūlaṁ syād bhaktiḥ śraddhā ca nirmalā ॥ 72 ॥
   ārādhayet — worship; akāpaṭayāt — without deceit; sadguru — true guru; dvārataḥ — through; kramāt — gradually; ārādhane — in worship; api — also; mūlaṁ — root; syāt — would be; bhaktiḥ — devotion; śraddhā — faith; ca — and; nirmalā — pure
   Worship gradually without deceit through the true guru. In worship, the root is devotion and pure faith.
   
   Verse 73
   तत्रापि मूलं माहात्म्यश्रवणं परिकीर्तितम्‌ ।
   अतस्ते प्रथमं राम माहात्म्यं सम्प्रवर्तितम्‌ ॥ ७३ ॥
   tatrāpi mūlaṁ māhātmyāśravaṇaṁ parikīrtitam ।
   ataste prathamaṁ rāma māhātmyaṁ sampravartitam ॥ 73 ॥
   tatra — there; api — also; mūlaṁ — root; māhātmya — greatness; śravaṇam — hearing; parikīrtitam — praised; ataḥ — therefore; te — to you; prathamaṁ — first; rāma — Rama; māhātmyaṁ — greatness; sampravartitam — has been told
   There too, the root is praised by hearing its greatness. Therefore, Rama, the greatness has been told to you first.
   
   Verse 74
   तेन श्रुतेनाधुना त्वं प्राप्तवानसि मङ्गलम्‌ ।
   विचारः श्रयसो मूलं यस्मात्ते नहि भीरितः ॥ ७४ ॥
   tena śrutenādhunā tvaṁ prāptavān asi maṅgalam ।
   vicāraḥ śrayaso mūlaṁ yasmāt te nahi bhīritaḥ ॥ 74 ॥
   tena — by that; śrutena — hearing; adhunā — now; tvaṁ — you; prāptavān — attained; asi — are; maṅgalam — auspiciousness; vicāraḥ — contemplation; śrayasaḥ — prosperity; mūlaṁ — root; yasmāt — because; te — to you; nahi — not; bhīritaḥ — afraid
   By hearing that, you have now attained auspiciousness. Contemplation is the root of prosperity because you are without fear.
   
   Verse 75
   विचारोदयपर्यन्तं भयमस्ति महत्तरम्‌ ।
   अविचारात्मदोषेण ग्रस्तस्य प्रतिवासरम्‌ ॥ ७५ ॥
   vicārodayaparyantaṁ bhayamasti mahattaram ।
   avicārātmadoṣeṇa grastasya prativasaram ॥ 75 ॥
   vicāra — contemplation; udaya — rise; paryantam — until; bhayam — fear; asti — is; mahattaram — great; avicāra — lack of contemplation; ātma — self; doṣeṇa — defect; grastasya — affected; prativasaram — daily
   Until the rise of contemplation, there is great fear, daily affected by the flaw of a lack of contemplation.
   
   Verse 76
   यथा हि सन्निपातेन ग्रस्तस्यौषधसेवनात्‌ ।
   अपि तावद्भवेद् भीतिर्यावद्धातोरशुद्धता ॥ ७६ ॥
   yathā hi sannipātena grastasya auṣadhasevanāt ।
   api tāvad bhaved bhītir yāvad dhātor aśuddhatā ॥ 76 ॥
   yathā — as; hi — indeed; sannipātena — by disorder; grastasya — affected; auṣadhasevanāt — by taking medicine; api — also; tāvat — until; bhavet — would be; bhītiḥ — fear; yāvat — until; dhātoḥ — element; aśuddhatā — impurity
   Just as taking medicine affects disorder, so too would fear persist until the impurity of the element is removed.
   
   Verse 77
   प्राप्ते विचारे परमे फलितं जीवितं नृणाम्‌ ।
   यावत्सु जन्मसु नृणां विचारो न भवेत्‌ परः ॥ ७७ ॥
   prāpte vicāre parame phalitaṁ jīvitaṁ nṛṇām ।
   yāvatsu janmasu nṛṇāṁ vicāro na bhavet paraḥ ॥ 77 ॥
   prāpte — attaining; vicāre — contemplation; parame — supreme; phalitaṁ — fruitful; jīvitaṁ — life; nṛṇām — of men; yāvatsu — in all; janmasu — births; nṛṇāṁ — of men; vicāraḥ — contemplation; na — not; bhavet — would be; paraḥ — supreme
   Life becomes fruitful for men upon attaining supreme contemplation, but in all births of men, supreme contemplation must be achieved.
   
   Verse 78
   तावन्तो जन्मतरवो वन्ध्या विफलहेतुतः ।
   स एव सफलो जन्मवृक्षो यत्र विमर्शनम्‌ ॥ ७८ ॥ ​​
   tāvanto janmataravo vandhyā vipalahetutaḥ ।
   sa eva saphalo janmavṛkṣo yatra vimarśanam ॥ 78 ॥
   tāvantaḥ — so many; janmataravaḥ — trees of birth; vandhyāḥ — barren; vipalahetutaḥ — for the cause of fruitlessness; saḥ — that; eva — indeed; saphalaḥ — fruitful; janmavṛkṣaḥ — tree of birth; yatra — where; vimarśanam — contemplation
   Many trees of birth are barren due to fruitlessness. That tree of birth becomes fruitful where there is contemplation.
   
   Verse 79
   कूपमण्डूकसदृशा ये नरा निर्विमर्शनाः ।
   यथा कूपे समुत्पन्नो भेको नो वेद किञ्चन ॥ ७९ ॥
   kūpamaṇḍūkasadṛśā ye narā nirvimarśanāḥ ।
   yathā kūpe samutpanno bheko no veda kiñcana ॥ 79 ॥
   kūpamaṇḍūka — well-frog; sadṛśāḥ — like; ye — who; narāḥ — men; nirvimarśanāḥ — without contemplation; yathā — as; kūpe — in a well; samutpannaḥ — born; bhekaḥ — frog; na — not; veda — knows; kiñcana — anything
   Men are like well-frogs without contemplation, much like a frog born in a well knows nothing beyond it.
   
   Verse 80
   शुभं वाप्यशुभं वापि कूपे एव विनश्यति ।
   तथा जना अपि वृथोत्पन्ना ब्रह्माण्डकूपके ॥ ८० ॥
   śubhaṁ vāpy aśubhaṁ vāpi kūpe eva vinaśyati ।
   tathā janā api vṛthotpannā brahmāṇḍakūpake ॥ 80 ॥
   śubham — good; vā — or; api — also; aśubham — bad; vā — or; api — also; kūpe — in the well; eva — indeed; vinaśyati — perishes; tathā — likewise; janāḥ — people; api — also; vṛtha — in vain; utpannāḥ — born; brahmāṇḍakūpake — in the well of the universe
   Good or bad, it perishes in the well. Similarly, people are born in vain in the well of the universe.
   
   Verse 81
   शुभं वाप्यशुभं वापि न विदुः स्वात्मनः क्वचित्‌ ।
   उत्पद्योत्पद्य नश्यन्ति न जानन्ति स्वकं हितम्‌ ॥ ८१ ॥
   śubhaṁ vāpy aśubhaṁ vāpi na viduḥ svātmanaḥ kvacit ।
   utpadyotpadyanaśyanti na jānanti svakaṁ hitam ॥ 81 ॥
   śubham — good; vā — or; api — also; aśubham — bad; vā — or; api — also; na — not; viduḥ — know; svātmanaḥ — of themselves; kvacit — anywhere; utpadyotpadyanaśyanti — arising again and perish again; na — not; jānanti — know; svakam — own; hitam — benefit
   Good or bad, they do not recognize themselves anywhere. Arising again and again, they perish, unaware of their own benefit.
   
   Verse 82
   सुखबुद्धिं च दुःखेषु सुखे दुःखविनिश्चयम्‌ ।
   प्राप्याविचारमाहात्म्यात्‌ पच्यन्ते सृतिपावके ॥ ८२ ॥
   sukhabuddhiṁ ca duḥkheṣu sukhe duḥkhaviniścayam ।
   prāpyāvicāramāhātmyāt pacyante sṛtipāvake ॥ 82 ॥
   sukha — happiness; buddhiṁ — understanding; ca — and; duḥkheṣu — in sorrow; sukhe — in happiness; duḥkhaviniścayam — determined as sorrow; prāpya — obtaining; avicāramāhātmyāt — due to the greatness of lack of contemplation; pacyante — are cooked; sṛti — in the fire; pāvake — of transmigration
   Recognizing happiness in sorrow and sorrow in happiness, due to the profound impact of a lack of contemplation, they are consumed in the fire of transmigration (cycle of birth and death).
   
   Verse 83
   दुःखेन क्लिश्यमानाश्च न कथञ्चित् त्यजन्ति तत्‌ ।
   यथा पादशताघातैस्ताडितोऽपि महाखरः ॥ ८३ ॥
   duḥkhena kliśyamānāśca na kathañcit tyajanti tat ।
   yathā pādaśatāghātaistāḍito'pi mahākharaḥ ॥ 83 ॥
   duḥkhena — by sorrow; kliśyamānāḥ — afflicted; ca — and; na — not; kathañcit — in any way; tyajanti — abandon; tat — that; yathā — as; pāda — foot; śata — hundred; āghātaiḥ — by blows; tāḍitaḥ — struck; api — even; mahākharaḥ — great donkey
   Afflicted by sorrow and unable to abandon it in any way, just like a stubborn donkey, even when struck by a hundred blows.
   
   Verse 84
   रासभीमनुयात्येव तथा संसरणं जनः ।
   त्वं तु राम विचारात्मा पारं दुःखस्य सङ्गतः ॥ ८४ ॥
   rāsabhīmanuyātyeva tathā saṁsaraṇaṁ janaḥ ।
   tvaṁ tu rāma vicārātmā pāraṁ duḥkhasya saṅgataḥ ॥ 84 ॥
   rāsabhīmanuyāti — follows like a donkey; eva — indeed; tathā — thus; saṁsaraṇam — cycle of transmigration; janaḥ — people; tvaṁ — you; tu — but; rāma — O Rama; vicārātmā — one with contemplation; pāraṁ — beyond; duḥkhasya — of sorrow; saṅgataḥ — reached
   People indeed follow the cycle of transmigration like donkeys. But you, O Rama, with contemplation, have transcended sorrow.



   इति श्रीत्रिपुरारहस्ये ज्ञानखण्डे विचारमाहात्म्ये  दितीयोऽध्यायः ॥
   
   Thus ends the second chapter on the “Greatness of Contemplation” in the Knowledge Section of the revered Tripura Rahasya.
   

3. GREATNESS OF ASSOCIATION WITH THE GOOD
   Verse 1
   दत्तात्रेयप्रोक्तवचः श्रुत्वाऽ्त्यन्तसुकौतुकी ।
   जामदग्न्यः पुनरपि पप्रच्छ विनयान्वितः ॥ १ ॥
   dattātreyaprokta—vacaḥ śrutvā'tyanta-sukautukī ।
   jāmadagnyaḥ punarapi papraccha vinayānvitaḥ ॥ 1 ॥
   dattātreya — by Dattatreya; prokta — spoken; vacaḥ — words; śrutvā — hearing; atyanta — extremely; sukautukī — curious; jāmadagnyaḥ — Jamadagni's son (Parashurama); punaḥ — again; api — also; papraccha — asked; vinayānvitaḥ — with humility
   Intrigued by the words of Dattatreya, Jamadagni's son (Parashurama) humbly asked again, full of curiosity.
   
   Verse 2
   भगवन्‌ गुरुनाथोक्तं भवता य त्तथैव तत्‌ ।
   अविचारात्‌ परो नाशः संप्राप्तः सव॑था जनैः ॥ २ ॥
   bhagavan gurunāthoktaṁ bhavatā yat tathāiva tat ।
   avicārāt paro nāśaḥ saṁprāptaḥ savathā janaiḥ ॥ 2 ॥
   bhagavan — O Lord; gurunāthoktaṁ — spoken by the Guru; bhavatā — by you; yat — that; tathāiva — exactly; tat — that; avicārāt — without contemplation; paraḥ — great; nāśaḥ — destruction; saṁprāptaḥ — has been attained; savathā — entirely; janaiḥ — by people
   O Lord, what you have spoken is indeed true. Without contemplation, people have brought about their own great destruction.
   
   Verse 3
   विचारेण भवेच्छ्रेयस्तन्निदानमपि श्रुतम्‌ ।
   माहात्म्यश्रुतिरित्येवं तत्र मे संशयो महान्‌ ॥ ३ ॥
   vicāreṇa bhavecchreyas tanni-dānamapi śrutam ।
   māhātmyāśrutirityevaṁ tatra me saṁśayo mahān ॥ 3 ॥
   vicāreṇa — by contemplation; bhavet — would be; śreyas — prosperity; tan-nidānam — its cause; api — also; śrutam — heard; māhātmyā-śrutiḥ — hearing of greatness; iti — thus; evaṁ — so; tatra — there; me — my; saṁśayaḥ — doubt; mahān — great
   By contemplation, prosperity would indeed be attained, and its cause is also heard. Hearing of this greatness is clearly indicated here, yet a great doubt persists.
   
   Verse 4
   कथं वा तदपि प्राप्यं साधनं तत्र किं भवेत्‌ ।
   स्वाभाविकं तद्यदि स्यात्तत्सर्वैर्न कुतः श्रुतम्‌ ॥ ४ ॥
   kathaṁ vā tadapi prāpyaṁ sādhanam tatra kiṁ bhavet ।
   svābhāvikaṁ tadyadi syāt tat sarvairna kutaḥ śrutam ॥ 4 ॥
   kathaṁ — how; vā — or; tat api — that also; prāpyaṁ — to be obtained; sādhanam — means; tatra — there; kiṁ — what; bhavet — would be; svābhāvikaṁ — natural; tat — that; yadi — if; syāt — would be; tat — that; sarvaiḥ — by all; na — not; kutaḥ — from where; śrutam — heard
   How can it be obtained, and what are the means? If it is natural, why is it not known to everyone?
   
   Verse 5
   अहं वाद्यावधि कुतः प्रवृतिं नाप्तवानिह ।
   दुःखं मत्तोऽधिकं प्राप्ता विहताश्च पदे पदे ॥ ५ ॥
   ahaṁ vādyāvadhi kutaḥ pravṛtiṁ nāptavāniha ।
   duḥkhaṁ matto'dhikaṁ prāptā vihatāśca pade pade ॥ 5 ॥
   ahaṁ — I; vā — or; adya — today; avadhi — until; kutaḥ — from where; pravṛtiṁ — direction; na — not; āptavān — have attained; iha — here; duḥkhaṁ — sorrow; mattaḥ — from me; adhikaṁ — more; prāptā — obtained; vihatāḥ — defeated; ca — and; pade pade — at every step
   Until today, I have not found direction here. I have encountered more sorrow and have been defeated at every step.
   
   Verse 6
   न कुतः साधनं प्राप्ता एतन्मे कृपया वद ।
   इत्यापृष्टः प्राह भूयो हृष्टो दत्तो दयानिधिः ॥ ६ ॥
   na kutaḥ sādhanam prāptā etanme kṛpayā vada ।
   ityāpṛṣṭaḥ prāha bhūyo hṛṣṭo datto dayānidhiḥ ॥ 6 ॥
   na — not; kutaḥ — from where; sādhanam — means; prāptā — obtained; etat — this; me — to me; kṛpayā — kindly; vada — tell; iti — thus; āpṛṣṭaḥ — asked; prāha — spoke; bhūyo — again; hṛṣṭaḥ — pleased; datto — Dattatreya; dayānidhiḥ — ocean of compassion
   I have not found the means from anywhere; please tell me this. Thus asked, Dattatreya, the ocean of compassion, spoke again, pleased.
   
   Verse 7
   शुणु राम प्रवक्ष्यामि निदानं श्रेयसः परम्‌ ।
   सद्भिः सङ्गः परं मूलं सर्वदुःखनिबर्हणम्‌ ॥ ७ ॥
   śuṇu rāma pravakṣyāmi nidānaṁ śreyasaḥ param ।
   sadbhih saṅgaḥ paraṁ mūlaṁ sarvaduḥkhanibarhaṇam ॥ 7 ॥
   śuṇu — listen; rāma — O Rama; pravakṣyāmi — I will tell; nidānam — cause; śreyasaḥ — of prosperity; param — supreme; sadbhih — with the good; saṅgaḥ — association; paraṁ — supreme; mūlaṁ — root; sarva — all; duḥkha — sorrow; nibarhaṇam — removal
   Listen, O Rama, I will explain the ultimate cause of prosperity. The association with virtuous people is the fundamental root, leading to the elimination of all sorrow.
   
   Verse 8
   परमार्थफलप्राप्तौ बीजं सत्सङ्गं उच्यते ।
   त्वं चापि तेन हि सता संवर्तेन महात्मना ॥ ८ ॥
   paramārthaphalaprāptau bījaṁ satsaṅgaṁ ucyate ।
   tvaṁ cāpi tena hi satā saṁvartena mahātmanā ॥ 8 ॥
   paramārtha — ultimate goal; phala — fruit; prāptau — attainment; bījam — seed; satsaṅgam — association with the good; ucyate — is said; tvaṁ — you; ca — and; api — also; tena — by him; hi — indeed; satā — by the good; saṁvartena — by Samvarta; mahātmanā — the great soul
   In achieving the ultimate goal, the seed is believed to be the company of the virtuous. You too, through the association with the noble Samvarta, the great soul.
   
   Verse 9
   सङ्गतः सन्निमां प्राप्तो दशा श्रेयःफलोदयाम्‌ ।
   सन्त एव हि संयाता दिशन्ति परमं सुखम्‌ ॥ ९ ॥
   saṅgataḥ sannimāṁ prāpto daśā śreyaḥphalodayām ।
   santa eva hi saṁyātā diśanti paramaṁ sukham ॥ 9 ॥
   saṅgataḥ — associated; sannimām — this; prāptaḥ — attained; daśā — state; śreyaḥ — prosperity; phala — fruit; udayām — rise; santaḥ — the good; eva — indeed; hi — indeed; saṁyātāḥ — associated; diśanti — give; paramaṁ — supreme; sukham — happiness
   Through his association, you have reached this state, experiencing the fruit of prosperity. Truly, the virtuous, when connected with, bestow supreme happiness.
   
   Verse 10
   विना सत्सङ्गतः केन प्राप्त श्रेयः परं कदा ।
   लोकेऽपि यादृशं सङ्गं यो यः प्राप्नोति मानवः ॥ १० ॥
   vinā satsaṅgataḥ kena prāptaḥ śreyaḥ paraṁ kadā ।
   loke'pi yādṛśaṁ saṅgaṁ yo yaḥ prāpnoti mānavaḥ ॥ 10 ॥
   vinā — without; satsaṅgataḥ — association with the good; kena — by whom; prāptaḥ — attained; śreyaḥ — prosperity; paraṁ — supreme; kadā — when; loke — in the world; api — also; yādṛśaṁ — such; saṅgam — association; yaḥ — whoever; yaḥ — whoever; prāpnoti — attains; mānavaḥ — man
   Who has ever attained supreme prosperity without the association of the virtuous? In the world, a person becomes what they are through the associations they keep.
   
   Verse 11
   तत्फलं स समाप्नोति सर्वथा नहि संशयः ।
   अत्र ते कीर्तयिष्यामि शणु राम कथामिमाम्‌ ॥ ११ ॥
   tatphalaṁ sa samāpnoti sarvathā nahi saṁśayaḥ ।
   atra te kīrtayiṣyāmi śaṇu rāma kathāmimām ॥ 11 ॥
   tat — that; phalaṁ — fruit; saḥ — he; samāpnoti — attains; sarvathā — in every way; nahi — not; saṁśayaḥ — doubt; atra — here; te — to you; kīrtayiṣyāmi — I will narrate; śaṇu — listen; rāma — O Rama; kathām — story; imām — this
   In every way, he attains that result, without a doubt. Now, listen, O Rama, as I narrate this story to you.
   
   Verse 12
   पुरा दशार्णाधिपतिर्मुक्ताचूड इतीरितः ।
   तस्य पुत्रौ हेमचूडमणिचूडौ बभूवतुः ॥ १२ ॥
   purā daśārṇādhipatir muktācūḍa itīritaḥ ।
   tasya putrau hemacūḍamaṇicūḍau babhūvatuḥ ॥ 12 ॥
   purā — once; daśārṇādhipatiḥ — king of Dasharna; muktācūḍaḥ — Muktachuda; itīritaḥ — known as; tasya — his; putrau — sons; hemacūḍa — Hemachuda; maṇicūḍa — Manichuda; babhūvatuḥ — were born
   Once, there was a king of Dasharna known as Muktachuda. He had two sons, Hemachuda and Manichuda.
   
   Verse 13
   सुरुपौ सुगुणौ चोभौ सर्वविद्याविशारदौ ।
   कदाचिन्मृगयोत्साहात्‌ सेनाभिः परिवारितौ ॥ १३ ॥
   surupau suguṇau cobhau sarvavidyāviśāradau ।
   kadācin mṛgayotsāhāt senābhiḥ parivāritau ॥ 13 ॥
   surupau — handsome; suguṇau — virtuous; ca — and; ubhau — both; sarvavidyāviśāradau — skilled in all knowledge; kadācit — once; mṛgayotsāhāt — due to enthusiasm for hunting; senābhiḥ — with the army; parivāritau — surrounded
   Both were handsome and virtuous, skilled in all knowledge. Once, driven by enthusiasm for hunting, they set out, surrounded by the army.
   
   Verse 14
   सह्याचलवनं भीमं सिहव्याघ्रादिसङ्कुलम् ।
   महाबलौ विविशतुर्धनुबणिधरौ किल ॥ १४ ॥
   sahyācalavanaṁ bhīmaṁ siṁhavyāghrādisaṅkulam ।
   mahābalau viviśatur dhanubaṇidharau kila ॥ 14 ॥
   sahyācalavanaṁ — the forest of Sahya mountain; bhīmaṁ — terrible; siṁhavyāghrādisaṅkulam — filled with lions, tigers, etc.; mahābalau — very powerful; viviśatuḥ — entered; dhanubaṇidharau — carrying bows and arrows; kila — indeed
   They entered the formidable forest of the Sahya mountain, which was teeming with powerful lions, tigers, and other ferocious creatures, armed with bows and arrows.
   
   Verse 15
   अथ तत्र मृगान्‌ सिंहान्‌ वराहान्‌ महिषान्‌ वृकान्‌ ।
   जघ्नतुर्निशितैर्बाणैर्लाघवात् कार्मुकच्युतैः ॥ १५ ॥
   atha tatra mṛgān siṁhān varāhān mahiṣān vṛkān ।
   jaghnatur niśitair bāṇair lāghavāt kārmukacyutaiḥ ॥ 15 ॥
   atha — then; tatra — there; mṛgān — deer; siṁhān — lions; varāhān — boars; mahiṣān — buffaloes; vṛkān — wolves; jaghnatuḥ — they killed; niśitaiḥ — sharp; bāṇaiḥ — arrows; lāghavāt — swiftly; kārmukacyutaiḥ — released from the bow
   With their sharp arrows swiftly released from their bows, they killed deer, lions, boars, buffaloes, and wolves in that place.
   
   Verse 16
   एवं विनिध्नतोर्वन्यान्‌ मृगान्‌ राजकुमारयोः ।
   चण्डवायुः प्रादुरासीच्छर्कराश्मप्रवर्षणः ॥ १६ ॥
   evaṁ vinidhnator vanyān mṛgān rājakumārayoḥ ।
   caṇḍavāyuḥ prādurāsīc charkarāśmapravarṣaṇaḥ ॥ 16 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; vinidhnatoḥ — while killing; vanyān — wild; mṛgān — animals; rājakumārayoḥ — of the princes; caṇḍavāyuḥ — fierce wind; prādurāsīt — appeared; śarkarā — gravel; aśma — stones; pravarṣaṇaḥ — showering
   While the princes were engaged in killing wild animals, a fierce wind suddenly appeared, showering gravel and stones upon them.
   
   Verse 17
   पांशुभिर्नभ आक्रान्तमभूद्‌ दर्शनिशोपमम् ।
   न दृश्यते तत्र शिला वृक्षः पुरुष एव वा ॥ १७ ॥
   pāṁśubhir nabha ākrāntam abhūd darśaniśopamam ।
   na dṛśyate tatra śilā vṛkṣaḥ puruṣa eva vā ॥ 17 ॥
   pāṁśubhiḥ — with dust; nabha — sky; ākrāntam — covered; abhūt — became; darśaniśopamam — like night; na — not; dṛśyate — seen; tatra — there; śilā — rock; vṛkṣaḥ — tree; puruṣaḥ — person; eva — even; vā — or
   The sky was enveloped in dust, making it as dark as night. No rocks, trees, or people could be seen.
   
   Verse 18
   कुतो नीचोच्चतां पश्येदेवं ध्वान्तावृतो गिरिः ।
   निहता शर्करावर्षैः सेनात्यन्त पलायिता ॥ १८ ॥
   kuto nīcoccatāṁ paśyed evaṁ dhvāntāvṛto giriḥ ।
   nihatā śarkarāvarṣaiḥ senātyanta palāyitā ॥ 18 ॥
   kutaḥ — how; nīca — low; uccatāṁ — high; paśyet — see; evaṁ — thus; dhvāntāvṛtaḥ — covered in darkness; giriḥ — mountain; nihatā — struck; śarkarāvarṣaiḥ — by the shower of gravel; senā — army; atyanta — completely; palāyitā — fled
   With the mountain shrouded in darkness, how could one discern the heights from the depths? The army, struck by the shower of gravel, fled completely.
   
   Verse 19
   वृक्षान्‌ केचिच्छिलाः केचिद्‌ गुहाः केचिदुपासदुः ।
   अश्वारूढौ राजपुत्रावपि दूरं पलायितौ ॥ १९ ॥
   vṛkṣān kecic chilāḥ kecid guhāḥ kecid upāsaduḥ ।
   aśvārūḍhau rājakumārāv api dūraṁ palāyitau ॥ 19 ॥
   vṛkṣān — trees; kecit — some; chilāḥ — rocks; kecit — some; guhāḥ — caves; kecit — some; upāsaduḥ — took shelter; aśvārūḍhau — mounted on horses; rājakumārāv — princes; api — also; dūram — far; palāyitau — fled
   Some sought shelter by trees, others by rocks or caves. Mounted on horses, the princes also fled far.
   
   Verse 20
   हेमचूडः क्वचित्तत्र प्रपेदे तापसाश्रमम्‌ ।
   कदलीखर्ज्जूरवनैरक्रान्तमतिसुन्दरम्‌ ॥ २० ॥
   hemacūḍaḥ kvacit tatra prapede tāpasāśramam ।
   kadalīkharjjūravanair ākrāntam atisundaram ॥ 20 ॥
   hemacūḍaḥ — Hemachuda; kvacit — somewhere; tatra — there; prapede — reached; tāpasāśramam — hermitage of ascetics; kadalīkharjjūra — plantains and date palms; vanaiḥ — by groves; ākrāntam — surrounded; atisundaram — very beautiful
   Hemachuda eventually reached a hermitage of ascetics, surrounded by beautiful groves of plantains and date palms.
   
   Verse 21
   तत्रापश्यच्छुभां काञ्चित्‌ कन्यामग्निशिखामिव ।
   प्रद्योतमानां वपुषा तप्तहेमसुवर्चसाम्‌ ॥ २१ ॥
   tatrāpaśyac chubhāṁ kāñcit kanyām agniśikhām iva ।
   pradyotamānāṁ vapuṣā taptāhemasuvarcasām ॥ 21 ॥
   tatra — there; apaśyat — saw; śubhām — auspicious; kāñcit — some; kanyām — girl; agniśikhām iva — like a flame; pradyotamānām — shining; vapuṣā — with body; tapta — heated; hema — gold; suvarcasām — glowing
   There, he saw an auspicious girl, shining like a flame, her body glowing like heated gold.
   
   Verse 22
   तां दृष्ट्वा राजपुत्रोऽपि पद्मामिव सुरूपिणीम्‌ ।
   स्मयमान इवाऽपृच्छत्‌ का त्वं पद्मानने वने ॥ २२ ॥
   tāṁ dṛṣṭvā rājaputro'pi padmām iva surūpiṇīm ।
   smayamāna ivā'prācchat kā tvaṁ padmānane vane ॥ 22 ॥
   tāṁ — her; dṛṣṭvā — seeing; rājaputraḥ — prince; api — also; padmām iva — like a lotus; surūpiṇīm — beautiful; smayamāna iva — smiling; aprācchat — asked; kā — who; tvaṁ — you; padmānane — lotus-faced; vane — in the forest
   Seeing her, the prince smiled and asked, "Who are you, lotus-faced, in the forest?"
   
   Verse 23
   निर्जने भीतिजनने निर्भयेव समास्थिता ।
   कस्य त्वमपि केनात्र निवसस्येकला कथम्‌ ॥ २३ ॥
   nirjane bhītijanane nirbhayeva samāsthitā ।
   kasya tvamapi kenātra nivasasyekalā katham ॥ 23 ॥
   nirjane — in the desolate; bhītijanane — fear-inducing; nirbhayā — fearless; iva — as if; samāsthitā — residing; kasya — whose; tvam — you; api — also; kena — by whom; atra — here; nivasasi — live; ekalā — alone; katham — how
   Residing as if fearless in this desolate, fear-inducing place, to whom do you belong, and who has left you here alone? How is this possible?
   
   Verse 24
   पृष्टैवं प्राह सा कन्या राजपृत्रमनिन्दिता ।
   स्वागतं ते राजपुत्र विष्टरं प्रतिपद्यताम्‌ ॥ २४ ॥
   pṛṣṭaivaṁ prāha sā kanyā rājaputram aninditā ।
   svāgataṁ te rājaputra viṣṭaraṁ pratipadyatām ॥ 24 ॥
   pṛṣṭā — questioned; evaṁ — thus; prāha — spoke; sā — she; kanyā — girl; rājaputram — to the prince; aninditā — blameless; svāgatam — welcome; te — to you; rājaputra — prince; viṣṭaram — seat; pratipadyatām — take
   Questioned thus, the blameless girl spoke to the prince, "Welcome, prince, please take a seat."
   
   Verse 25
   तपस्विनामयं धर्मः पूजनं ह्यतिथेस्तु यत्‌ ।
   श्रान्तं त्वामभिपश्यामि व्यथितं चण्डवायुना ॥ २५ ॥
   tapasvinām ayaṁ dharmaḥ pūjanaṁ hyatithes tu yat ।
   śrāntaṁ tvām abhipaśyāmi vyathitaṁ caṇḍavāyunā ॥ 25 ॥
   tapasvinām — of ascetics; ayam — this; dharmaḥ — duty; pūjanam — worship; hi — indeed; atitheḥ — of a guest; tu — and; yat — that; śrāntam — tired; tvām — you; abhipaśyāmi — I see; vyathitam — distressed; caṇḍavāyunā — by the fierce wind
   This is the duty of ascetics, indeed, to worship a guest. I see you are tired and distressed by the fierce wind.
   
   Verse 26
   बध्वा खर्जूरवृक्षेऽश्वमत्रासीनो गतश्रमः ।
   मद्वृत्तमर्हसि श्रोतुमित्युक्तः स तथाऽकरोत्‌ ॥ २६ ॥
   badhvā kharjūravṛkṣe'śvam atrāsīno gataśramaḥ ।
   madvṛttam arhasi śrotum ityuktaḥ sa tathā'karot ॥ 26 ॥
   badhvā — tying, kharjūra — date palm, vṛkṣe — tree, aśvam — horse, atra — here, āsīnaḥ — sitting, gataśramaḥ — relieved of fatigue, madvṛttam — my story, arhasi — deserve, śrotum — to hear, iti — thus, uktaḥ — told, saḥ — he, tathā — thus, akarot — did
   Tying the horse to a date palm tree, he sat there, relieved of his fatigue, and said, ‘You deserve to hear my story.’
   
   Verse 27
   फलानि भोजयामास पाययामास सद्रसम्‌ ।
   एवं तं विश्रमं प्राप्तं राजपुत्रमनिन्दिता ॥ २७ ॥
   phalāni bhojayāmāsa pāyayāmāsa sadrasaṁ ।
   evaṁ taṁ viśramaṁ prāptaṁ rājaputram aninditā ॥ 27 ॥
   phalāni — fruits; bhojayāmāsa — made him eat; pāyayāmāsa — made him drink; sadrasaṁ — with juice; evaṁ — thus; tam — him; viśramam — rest; prāptam — obtained; rājaputram — prince; aninditā — blameless
   She gave him fruits to eat and juice to drink. Thus, the blameless girl helped the prince to rest.
   
   Verse 28
   प्राह सा मधुसंस्रावपेशलाकारया गिरा ।
   राजपुत्र व्याघ्रपादो मुनिः शिवपदाश्रयः ॥ २८ ॥
   prāha sā madhusaṁsrāvapeśalākārayā girā ।
   rājaputra vyāghrapādo muniḥ śivapadāśrayaḥ ॥ 28 ॥
   prāha — spoke; sā — she; madhusaṁsrāva — honey-flowing; peśalākārayā — sweet; girā — voice; rājaputra — prince; vyāghrapādaḥ — Vyaghrapada; muniḥ — sage; śivapadāśrayaḥ — follower of Shiva
   She spoke with a sweet, honey-flowing voice, "Prince, Vyaghrapada is the sage, a follower of Shiva."
   
   Verse 29
   येन लोकाः पुण्यतमा जिताः स्वतपसो बलात्‌ ।
   परावरज्ञो ह्यनिशं पूजितो मुनिनायकैः ॥ २९ ॥
   yena lokāḥ puṇyatamā jitāḥ svatapasobalāt ।
   parāvarajño hyaniśaṁ pūjito munināyakaiḥ ॥ 29 ॥
   yena — by whom; lokāḥ — worlds; puṇyatamāḥ — most virtuous; jitāḥ — conquered; svatapasobalāt — by the strength of his penance; parāvarajñaḥ — knower of the highest and lowest; hi — indeed; aniśam — always; pūjitaḥ — worshipped; munināyakaiḥ — by leaders of sages
   By whom the most virtuous worlds were conquered through the strength of his penance, the knower of the highest and lowest, always worshipped by the leaders of sages.
   
   Verse 30
   तस्याहं धर्मतः पुत्री हेमलेखेति विश्रुता ।
   विद्युत्प्रभाख्या विद्याध्री सा सर्वाङ्गमनोहरा ॥ ३० ॥
   tasyāhaṁ dharmataḥ putrī hemalekheti viśrutā ।
   vidyutprabhākhyā vidyādhrī sā sarvāṅgamanoharā ॥ 30 ॥
   tasya — his; ahaṁ — I; dharmataḥ — rightfully; putrī — daughter; hemalekha iti — named Hemalekha; viśrutā — known; vidyutprabhā — Vidyutprabha; khyā — named; vidyādhrī — virtue; sā — she; sarvāṅgamanoharā — enchanting in all parts
   I am rightly his daughter, known as Hemalekha, born of the virtuous Vidyutprabha, enchanting in all aspects.
   
   Verse 31
   इमां वेणामनु नदीं स्नातुमभ्याययौ क्वचित्‌ ।
   तदा तत्राजगामार्थात्‌ सुषेणो वङ्गभूपतिः ॥ ३१ ॥
   imāṁ veṇāmanu nadīṁ snātum abhyāyayau kvacit ।
   tadā tatrājagāmārthāt suṣeṇo vaṅgabhūpatiḥ ॥ 31 ॥
   imāṁ — this; veṇāmanu — along the Vena river; nadīṁ — river; snātum — to bathe; abhyāyayau — came; kvacit — once; tadā — then; tatra — there; ājagāma — came; arthāt — consequently; suṣeṇaḥ — Sushena; vaṅgabhūpatiḥ — king of Vanga
   Once, while along the Vena river, she came to bathe. Consequently, Sushena, the king of Vanga, arrived there.
   
   Verse 32
   स ददर्श विगाहन्तीं नदीं तां लोकसुन्दरीम्‌ ।
   क्लिन्नांशुकान्तरत्यन्तव्यक्तपोनकुचद्वयोम् ॥ ३२ ॥
   sa dadarśa vigāhantīṁ nadīṁ tāṁ lokasundarīm ।
   klinnāṁśukāntaratyaṁta-vyaktapōnakucadvayom ॥ 32 ॥
   saḥ — he; dadarśa — saw; vigāhantīm — bathing; nadīṁ — in the river; tāṁ — her; lokasundarīm — world beauty; klinnāṁśuka — wet cloth; antaratyaṁta — very; vyaktapōna — clearly visible; kucadvayom — pair of breasts
   He saw her, a beauty of the world, bathing in the river, her pair of breasts clearly outlined through the wet cloth.
   
   Verse 33
   कामबाणहतस्तत्र तां प्रार्थयदथापि सा ।
   सौन्दर्यमोहिता तस्य तदुक्ति सममंसत ॥ ३३ ॥
   kāmabāṇahatas tatra tāṁ prārthayad athāpi sā ।
   saundaryamohitā tasya tadukti samamaṁsata ॥ 33 ॥
   kāmabāṇa — love's arrow; hataḥ — struck; tatra — there; tāṁ — her; prārthayad — desired; athāpi — then; sā — she; saundaryamohitā — enchanted by beauty; tasya — his; tadukti — those words; samamaṁsata — accepted
   Struck by love’s arrow, he desired her then and there; she, captivated by his words, accepted.
   
   Verse 34
   सङ्गम्याथ तया राजा ययौ स्वनगरं प्रति ।
   दधार सापि विद्याध्री गर्भं राजर्षिवीर्यतः ॥ ३४ ॥
   saṅgamyātha tayā rājā yayau svanagaraṁ prati ।
   dadhāra sāpi vidyādhrī garbhaṁ rājarṣivīryataḥ ॥ 34 ॥
   saṅgamya — uniting; atha — then; tayā — with her; rājā — king; yayau — went; svanagaraṁ — to his city; prati — towards; dadhāra — bore; sā — she; api — also; vidyādhrī — the fairy; garbhaṁ — pregnancy; rājarṣivīryataḥ — from the Rajarishi’s strength
   United with her, the king returned to his city. The virtuous one, bearing the strength of the rajarishi, also conceived.
   
   Verse 35
   भीताऽपचारात्‌ पत्युः सा गर्भं त्यक्त्वात्र संययौ ।
   अमोघवीर्याद्‌ राजर्षेर्जाताहं कन्यका ततः ॥ ३५ ॥
   bhītā'pacārāt patyuḥ sā garbhaṁ tyaktvātra saṁyayau ।
   amoghavīryād rājarṣer jātāhaṁ kanyakā tataḥ ॥ 35 ॥
   bhītā — afraid; apacārāt — of offense; patyuḥ — of husband; sā — she; garbhaṁ — pregnancy; tyaktvā — abandoning; atra — here; saṁyayau — came; amoghavīryāt — of unfailing strength; rājarṣeḥ — of the royal sage; jātā — born; ahaṁ — I; kanyakā — girl; tataḥ — then
   Fearing she might offend her husband, she came here and abandoned the pregnancy. Born of the rajarishi’s unfailing strength, I am the girl from then.
   
   Verse 36
   मां ददर्श व्याघ्रपादः सन्ध्योपास्त्यर्थमागतः ।
   दयया मामुपादायाऽपालयज्जननी यथा ॥ ३६ ॥
   māṁ dadarśa vyāghrapādaḥ sandhyopāstyartham āgataḥ ।
   dayayā mām upādāyā'pālayaj jananī yathā ॥ 36 ॥
   mām — me; dadarśa — saw; vyāghrapādaḥ — Vyaghrapada; sandhyopāstyartham — for evening worship; āgataḥ — came; dayayā — with compassion; mām — me; upādāya — taking up; apālayat — protected; jananī — mother; yathā — like
   Vyaghrapada saw me during the evening worship, and with compassion, he took me in and protected me like a mother.
   
   Verse 37
   धर्मेण यः पालयिता प्रोच्यते हि पितैव सः ।
   अहं तस्य धर्मपुत्री पितृसेवापरायणा ॥ ३७ ॥
   dharmeṇa yaḥ pālayitā procyate hi pitaiva saḥ ।
   ahaṁ tasya dharmaputrī pitṛsevāparāyaṇā ॥ 37 ॥
   dharmeṇa — by duty; yaḥ — who; pālayitā — protector; procyate — is called; hi — indeed; pitaiva — like a father; saḥ — he; ahaṁ — I; tasya — his; dharmaputrī — rightful daughter; pitṛsevāparāyaṇā — devoted to serving father
   By duty, he who is called a protector, indeed like a father. I am his rightful daughter, devoted to serving him.
   
   Verse 38
   तस्य माहात्म्यतो मेऽत्र भयं नास्त्येव कुत्रचित्‌ ।
   नायं सुरासुरैर्वापि कदाचिद्‌ दुष्टबुद्धिभिः ॥ ३८ ॥
   tasya māhātmyato me'tra bhayaṁ nāstyeva kutracit ।
   nāyaṁ surāsurairvāpi kadācid duṣṭabuddhibhiḥ ॥ 38 ॥
   tasya — his; māhātmyataḥ — by greatness; me — my; atra — here; bhayaṁ — fear; na asti — not; eva — indeed; kutracit — anywhere; nāyam — this; surāsuraiḥ — by gods or demons; vā — or; api — also; kadācit — ever; duṣṭabuddhibhiḥ — by evil minds
   By his greatness, I have no fear here or anywhere. This place is never invaded by gods, demons, or evil minds.
   
   Verse 39
   परवेष्टुमाश्रमोऽर्हः स्यात्‌ प्रविशत्राशमाप्नुयात्‌ ।
   एतन्मेऽभिहितं वृत्तं तिष्ठ किञ्चिन्नुपात्मज ॥ ३९ ॥
   paraveṣṭumāśramo'rhaḥ syāt praviśatrāśamāpnuyāt ।
   etanme'bhihitaṁ vṛttaṁ tiṣṭha kiñcin nupātmaja ॥ 39 ॥
   paraveṣṭum — to invade; āśramaḥ — hermitage; arhaḥ — worthy; syāt — may be; praviśat — entering; rāśam — fear; āpnuyāt — may attain; etat — this; me — my; abhihitaṁ — stated; vṛttam — story; tiṣṭha — stay; kiñcit — a little; nupātmaja — prince
   You may be worthy to enter the hermitage, but upon entering, you will attain no fear. This is my story stated. Stay a little, prince.
   
   Verse 40
