   आयास्यति स भगवान्‌ पिता मे तं निशामय ।
   प्रणम्य तं प्राप्य चेष्टं ततः कल्ये प्रयास्यसि ॥ ४० ॥
   āyāsyati sa bhagavān pitā me taṁ niśāmaya ।
   praṇamya taṁ prāpya ceṣṭaṁ tataḥ kalye prayāsyasi ॥ 40 ॥
   āyāsyati — will come; saḥ — he; bhagavān — the venerable; pitā — father; me — my; taṁ — him; niśāmaya — behold; praṇamya — bowing; taṁ — him; prāpya — having received; ceṣṭam — wishes; tataḥ — then; kalye — in the morning; prayāsyasi — you may leave
   The venerable father will arrive; behold him. Bow to him, receive his blessings, and then you may depart in the morning.
   
   Verse 41
   हेमलेखावचः श्रुत्वा तत्सौन्दर्येण मोहितः ।
   भीतः किञ्चित् प्रववतुं तां विमना इव चाभवत्‌ ॥४१॥
   hemalekhāvacaḥ śrutvā tatsaundaryeṇa mohitaḥ ।
   bhītaḥ kiñcit pravavatuṁ tāṁ vimanā iva cābhavat ॥41॥
   hemalekhā — Hemalekha; vacaḥ — words; śrutvā — having heard; tat — that; saundaryeṇa — by beauty; mohitaḥ — fascinated; bhītaḥ — fearful; kiñcit — a little; pravavatuṁ — to proceed; tāṁ — her; vimanā — disturbed; iva — as if; ca — and; abhavat — became
   Hearing Hemalekha’s words and captivated by her beauty, he became somewhat fearful and appeared uneasy, as if hesitant to proceed further.
   
   Verse 42
   अथालक्ष्य राजपुत्रं कामस्य वशमागतम्‌ ।
   प्राह सा विदुषी भूयो राजपुत्र धृतिं भज ॥ ४२ ॥
   athālakṣya rājaputraṁ kāmasya vaśamāgatam ।
   prāha sā viduṣī bhūyo rājaputra dhṛtiṁ bhaja ॥ 42 ॥
   atha — then; ālakṣya — noticing; rājaputram — prince; kāmasya — of desire; vaśamāgatam — under control; prāha — spoke; sā — she; viduṣī — wise; bhūyaḥ — again; rājaputra — prince; dhṛtim — composure; bhaja — take
   Then, observing the prince under the sway of desire, the wise girl spoke again, ‘Prince, regain your composure.’
   
   Verse 43
   आगच्छति पिता सद्यस्ततोऽभिलषितं भज ।
   एवं वदन्त्यां तस्यां स व्याघ्रपादो महामुनिः ॥ ४३ ॥
   āgacchati pitā sadyas tato'bhilaṣitaṁ bhaja ।
   evaṁ vadantyāṁ tasyāṁ sa vyāghrapādo mahāmuniḥ ॥ 43 ॥
   āgacchati — is coming; pitā — father; sadyaḥ — soon; tataḥ — then; abhilāṣitam — desired; bhaja — seek; evaṁ — thus; vadantyām — while she was speaking; tasyām — she; saḥ — he; vyāghrapādaḥ — Vyaghrapada; mahāmuniḥ — great sage
   "Father is coming soon; then seek what you desire." As she was speaking, the great sage Vyaghrapada arrived.
   
   Verse 44
   आजगाम वनात्‌ पत्रपुष्पादेः कृतसञ्चयः ।
   मुनिं समागतं दृष्ट्वा राजपुत्रः समुत्थितः ॥ ४४ ॥
   ājagāma vanāt patrapuṣpādeḥ kṛtasañcayaḥ ।
   muniṁ samāgataṁ dṛṣṭvā rājaputraḥ samutthitaḥ ॥ 44 ॥
   ājagāma — arrived; vanāt — from the forest; patra — leaves; puṣpa — flowers; ādeḥ — etc.; kṛtasañcayaḥ — gathering; muniṁ — sage; samāgatam — arriving; dṛṣṭvā — seeing; rājaputraḥ — prince; samutthitaḥ — stood up
   He arrived from the forest, gathering leaves and flowers. Seeing the sage approaching, the prince stood up.
   
   Verse 45
   प्रणम्य नाम संश्राव्योपविष्टस्तेन देशितः ।
   अथ दृष्ट्वा राजपुत्रं कामेन विकृताकृतिम्‌ ॥ ४५ ॥
   praṇamya nāma saṁśrāvyopaviṣṭas tena deśitaḥ ।
   atha dṛṣṭvā rājaputraṁ kāmena vikṛtākṛtim ॥ 45 ॥
   praṇamya — bowing; nāma — name; saṁśrāvya — announcing; upaviṣṭaḥ — sat down; tena — by him; deśitaḥ — instructed; atha — then; dṛṣṭvā — seeing; rājaputram — prince; kāmena — by desire; vikṛtākṛtim — distorted appearance
   Bowing and announcing his name, he sat down as instructed. Then, noticing the prince’s appearance distorted by desire.
   
   Verse 46
   ज्ञात्वा योगदृशा सर्वं मत्वा युक्तं च तत्तदा ।
   दारक्रियार्थं तस्मै तां हेमलेखां ददौ मुनिः ॥ ४६ ॥
   jñātvā yogadṛśā sarvaṁ matvā yuktaṁ ca tattadā ।
   dārakriyārthaṁ tasmai tāṁ hemalekhāṁ dadau muniḥ ॥ 46 ॥
   jñātvā — knowing; yogadṛśā — with yogic vision; sarvaṁ — everything; matvā — considering; yuktaṁ — appropriate; ca — and; tat — that; tadā — then; dārakriyārthaṁ — for marriage; tasmai — to him; tāṁ — her; hemalekhāṁ — Hemalekha; dadau — gave; muniḥ — sage
   Perceiving everything with his yogic vision and deeming it appropriate, the sage gave Hemalekha to him in marriage.
   
   Verse 47
   तुष्टो राजकुमारोऽपि तामादाय पुरं ययौ ।
   मुक्ताचूडोऽतिसन्तुष्टो महोत्सवविधानतः ॥ ४७ ॥
   tuṣṭo rājakumāro'pi tāmādāya puraṁ yayau ।
   muktācūḍo'tisantuṣṭo mahotsavavidhānataḥ ॥ 47 ॥
   tuṣṭaḥ — pleased; rājakumāraḥ — prince; api — also; tām — her; ādāya — taking; puraṁ — to the city; yayau — went; muktācūḍaḥ — Muktachuda; ati—santuṣṭaḥ — very pleased; mahotsava-vidhānataḥ — with great celebration
   The delighted prince, taking her with him, returned to the city. Muktachuda, filled with joy, celebrated their union with great festivity.
   
   Verse 48
   विवाहमकरोत्तस्य विधानेन क्षितीश्वरः ।
   अथ राजकुमारोऽपि तया क्रीडापरः सदा ॥ ४८ ॥
   vivāham akarot tasya vidhānena kṣitīśvaraḥ ।
   atha rājakumāro'pi tayā krīḍāparaḥ sadā ॥ 48 ॥
   vivāham — marriage; akarot — performed; tasya — his; vidhānena — according to rules; kṣitīśvaraḥ — king; atha — then; rājakumāraḥ — prince; api — also; tayā — with her; krīḍāparaḥ — engaged in play; sadā — always
   The king performed the marriage ceremony according to the customs. Subsequently, the prince was always engaged in playful activities with her.
   
   Verse 49
   सौधेषु वनराजीषु पुलिनादिषु संबभौ ।
   हेमलेखां राजपुत्रो भोगेष्वनतिकामिनीम्‌ ॥ ४९ ॥
   sādheṣu vanarājīṣu pulinādiṣu saṁbabhau ।
   hemalekhāṁ rājaputro bhogeṣvanatikāminīm ॥ 49 ॥
   sādheṣu — in palaces; vanarājīṣu — in forests; pulinādiṣu — on riverbanks; saṁbabhau — spent time; hemalekhāṁ — Hemalekha; rājaputraḥ — prince; bhogeṣu — in enjoyments; anatikāminīm — not very desirous
   In palaces, forests, and riverbanks, the prince spent time with Hemalekha, who was not particularly desirous of worldly pleasures.
   
   Verse 50
   उदासीनां सदा दुष्ट्वा पप्रच्छ रहसि क्वचित्‌ ।
   किं प्रिये नानुरक्तासि प्रिये मय्यनुरागिणि ॥ ५० ॥
   udāsīnāṁ sadā dṛṣṭvā papraccha rahasi kvacit ।
   kiṁ priye nānuraktāsi priye mayy anurāgiṇi ॥ 50 ॥
   udāsīnām — indifferent; sadā — always; dṛṣṭvā — seeing; papraccha — asked; rahasi — in private; kvacit — somewhere; kiṁ — why; priye — dear; na — not; anuraktāsi — affectionate; priye — dear; mayi — in me; anurāgiṇi — who is affectionate
   Seeing her always indifferent, he asked privately, ‘Dear, why are you not affectionate towards me when I am so affectionate to you?’
   
   Verse 51
   कुतो भोगेषु नात्यन्तमासक्तासि शुचिस्मिते ।
   किं भोगास्ते मनोयोग्या न सन्त्यत्र कुतस्त्विदम्‌ ॥ ५१ ॥
   kuto bhogeṣu nātyantam āsaktāsi śucismite ।
   kiṁ bhogāste manoyogyā na santyatra kutastvidam ॥ 51 ॥
   kutaḥ — why; bhogeṣu — in enjoyments; na — not; atyantam — extremely; āsaktāsi — attached; śucismite — dear with a pure smile; kiṁ — what; bhogāḥ — enjoyments; te — your; manoyogyā — appealing; na — not; santi — are; atra — here; kutaḥ — why; idam — this
   My dear, with a pure smile, why are you not extremely attached to enjoyments? Are the enjoyments not appealing to you here? Why is this?
   
   Verse 52
   अत्युत्तमेषु भोगेषु नासक्तेव विभासि मे ।
   त्वय्यासक्तिविहीनायां कथं मे सुखदा रतिः ॥ ५२ ॥
   atyuttameṣu bhogeṣu nāsakteva vibhāsi me ।
   tvayy āsaktivihīnāyāṁ kathaṁ me sukhadā ratiḥ ॥ 52 ॥
   atyuttameṣu — in excellent; bhogeṣu — enjoyments; na — not; āsakteva — as if attached; vibhāsi — you seem; me — to me; tvayi — in you; āsaktivihīnāyām — lacking attachment; kathaṁ — how; me — my; sukhadā — pleasing; ratiḥ — love
   In these excellent enjoyments, you seem not to be attached to me. Without your attachment, how can my love be pleasing?
   
   Verse 53
   आसक्ते मयि चापि त्वं भास्यन्यगतमानसा ।
   भाषितापि मया भूयो न शृणोष्येव किञ्चन ॥ ५३ ॥
   āsakte mayi cāpi tvaṁ bhāsy anyagatamānasā ।
   bhāṣitāpi mayā bhūyo na śṛṇoṣyeva kiñcana ॥ 53 ॥
   āsakte — attached; mayi — in me; ca — and; api — also; tvaṁ — you; bhāsi — appear; anyagatamānasā — mind elsewhere; bhāṣitā — spoken; api — also; mayā — by me; bhūyaḥ — repeatedly; na — not; śṛṇoṣi — you hear; eva — indeed; kiñcana — anything
   Though I am attached to you, your mind seems to be elsewhere. Even when I speak repeatedly, you appear not to hear anything.
   
   Verse 54
   आगतं कण्ठसंलग्नं चिरादपि विभाव्य च ।
   कदा नाथागतं चेति पृच्छस्यविदिता यथा ॥ ५४ ॥
   āgataṁ kaṇṭhasaṁlagnaṁ cirādapi vibhāvya ca ।
   kadā nāthāgataṁ ceti pṛcchasy aviditā yathā ॥ 54 ॥
   āgatam — arriving; kaṇṭhasaṁlagnaṁ — embracing the neck; cirādapi — after a long time; vibhāvya — considering; ca — and; kadā — when; nātha — lord; āgatam — come; ca — and; iti — thus; pṛcchasi — you ask; aviditā — as if unaware; yathā — how
   Even after a long time, when I arrive and embrace your neck, you ask, 'When did you come, my lord?' as if unaware.
   
   Verse 55
   पेशलेषूपभोगेषु दुर्लभेषु क्वचिन्न ते ।
   मन आसज्जते कस्मान्न किञ्चिदनुमोदसि ॥ ५५ ॥
   peśaleṣu upabhogeṣu durlabheṣu kvacin na te ।
   mana āsajjate kasmān na kiñcid anumodasi ॥ 55 ॥
   peśaleṣu — in pleasing; upabhogeṣu — enjoyments; durlabheṣu — rare; kvacit — at all; na — not; te — your; manaḥ — mind; āsajjate — attached; kasmāt — why; na — not; kiñcit — anything; anumodasi — you approve
   In these rare and pleasing enjoyments, your mind is not attached at all. Why do you not approve of anything?
   
   Verse 56
   मया विरहितां त्वां वै निमील्य नयने स्थिताम्‌ ।
   यदा यदोपगच्छामि पश्यामि च तदा तदा ॥ ५६ ॥
   mayā virahitāṁ tvāṁ vai nimīlya nayane sthitām ।
   yadā yadopagacchāmi paśyāmi ca tadā tadā ॥ 56 ॥
   mayā — by me; virahitām — without; tvāṁ — you; vai — indeed; nimīlya — closing; nayane — eyes; sthitām — staying; yadā — when; yadā — when; upagacchāmi — I approach; paśyāmi — I see; ca — and; tadā — then; tadā — then
   In these moments when I approach and find you alone, with closed eyes, it feels as if you are dwelling in a different world, far from me.
   
   Verse 57
   विमुख्यां त्वयि भोगेषु विषयेषु सुखं मम ।
   कथं भवेद्दारुयोषासङ्गतस्येव तद्वद ॥ ५७ ॥
   vimukhyāṁ tvayi bhogeṣu viṣayeṣu sukhaṁ mama ।
   kathaṁ bhaved dāruyoṣāsaṅgatasyeva tadvad ॥ 57 ॥
   vimukhyām — indifferent; tvayi — you; bhogeṣu — in enjoyments; viṣayeṣu — in objects; sukham — happiness; mama — my; kathaṁ — how; bhavet — would be; dāruyoṣā — wooden doll; saṅgatasya — associated; iva — like; tadvat — similarly
   Indifferent to enjoyments and objects, how can my happiness flourish, as if I were connected to a lifeless wooden doll?
   
   Verse 58
   न तवाभिमतं त्यक्त्वा किञ्चिन्मम समीहितम्‌ ।
   सर्वथा त्वामनुगतो ज्योत्स्नां कुमुदवत्‌ किल ॥ ५८ ॥
   na tavābhimataṁ tyaktvā kiñcin mama samīhitam ।
   sarvathā tvām anugato jyotsnāṁ kumudavat kila ॥ 58 ॥
   na — not; tava — your; abhimatam — wish; tyaktvā — abandoning; kiñcit — anything; mama — my; samīhitam — intention; sarvathā — entirely; tvām — you; anugataḥ — following; jyotsnām — moonlight; kumudavat — like the lotus; kila — indeed
   Not abandoning your wish, my own intention holds no significance. I follow you entirely, just as the lotus follows the moonlight.
   
   Verse 59
   तदेवं ते कुतश्चित्तं ब्रूहि प्राणाधिकप्रिये ।
   येन शुद्धयेत्तु मच्चित्तं शापितासि मया प्रिये ॥ ५९ ॥
   tadevaṁ te kutaś cittaṁ brūhi prāṇādhikapriye ।
   yena śuddhayet tu maccittaṁ śāpitāsi mayā priye ॥ 59 ॥
   tad — thus; evaṁ — this; te — your; kutaḥ — from where; cittam — mind; brūhi — tell; prāṇādhikapriye — dearer than life; yena — by which; śuddhayet — would be purified; tu — indeed; maccittaṁ — my mind; śāpitāsi — you are requested; mayā — by me; priye — dear
   Thus, please tell me where your mind dwells, my dear, for whom you are dearer than life. By understanding this, my own mind may be purified. I earnestly request you, my beloved.

   
   इति श्रीत्रिपुरारहस्ये ज्ञानखण्डे सत्सङ्गमाहात्म्ये तृतीयोऽध्यायः ॥
   
   Thus ends the third chapter on the “Greatness of Association with the Good” in the Knowledge Section of the revered Tripura Rahasya.
   
   
4. FRUIT OF ASSOCIATION WITH THE GOOD
   Verse 1
   प्रियस्य कण्ठासक्तस्य निशम्यैवं वचो हि सा ।
   ईषत्स्मितानना प्राह राजपुत्रमनिन्दिता ॥ १ ॥
   priyasya kaṇṭhāsaktasya niśamyaivaṁ vaco hi sā ।
   īṣatsmitānanā prāha rājaputram aninditā ॥ 1 ॥
   priyasya — dear's; kaṇṭhāsaktasya — embracing the neck; niśamya — hearing; evaṁ — thus; vacaḥ — words; hi — indeed; sā — she; īṣat — slightly; smitānanā — with a smile; prāha — spoke; rājaputram — to the prince; aninditā — blameless
   Embracing his neck, she listened to her dear’s words and, with a slight smile, spoke to the prince, who was blameless.
   
   Verse 2
   बुबोधयिषती राजपुत्रं युक्त्याऽब्रवीदिदम्‌ ।
   राजपुत्र शृणु वचो नाहं त्वयि विरागिणी ॥ २ ॥
   bubodhayiṣatī rājaputraṁ yuktyā'bravīd idam ।
   rājaputra śṛṇu vaco nāhaṁ tvayi virāgiṇī ॥ 2 ॥
   bubodhayiṣatī — desiring to enlighten; rājaputram — the prince; yuktyā — with reason; abravīt — spoke; idam — this; rājaputra — prince; śṛṇu — listen; vacaḥ — words; na — not; ahaṁ — I; tvayi — in you; virāgiṇī — indifferent
   Desiring to enlighten the prince with reason, she said: “Prince, listen to my words, I am not indifferent to you.”
   
   Verse 3
   किं स्यात्‌ प्रियतमं लोके किन्नु स्यादप्रियं त्विति ।
   विचारपरमा नित्यं नान्तमेत्यत्र मे मतिः ॥ ३ ॥
   kiṁ syāt priyatamaṁ loke kinnu syād apriyaṁ tv iti ।
   vicāraparamā nityaṁ nāntam ety atra me matiḥ ॥ 3 ॥
   kiṁ — what; syāt — is; priyatamam — most dear; loke — in the world; kinnu — what; syāt — is; apriyam — not dear; tv — you; iti — thus; vicāraparamā — deep thinking; nityaṁ — always; na — not; antam — end; eti — reaches; atra — here; me — my; matiḥ — thought
   What is most dear in the world and what is not? Deep thinking always falls short of reaching an end here; this is my thought.
   
   Verse 4
   ध्यायाम्येतच्चिरान्नित्यं स्त्रीस्वभाववशादहम्‌ ।
   नैतज्जानामि तत्त्वं मे वक्तुमर्हसि तत्त्वतः ॥ ४ ॥
   dhyāyāmy etac cirān nityaṁ strīsvabhāvavaśād aham ।
   naitaj jānāmi tattvaṁ me vaktum arhasi tattvataḥ ॥ 4 ॥
   dhyāyāmi — I contemplate; etac — this; cirāt — for a long time; nityaṁ — always; strīsvabhāvavaśāt — due to the nature of a woman; aham — I; na — not; etat — this; jānāmi — I know; tattvam — truth; me — to me; vaktum — to tell; arhasi — you should; tattvataḥ — truly
   I have contemplated this for a long time, always reflecting on it as a woman. I do not know this truth; please tell me sincerely.
   
   Verse 5
   एवं प्रोक्तो हेमचूडः प्रहस्य प्राह तां प्रियाम्‌ ।
   नूनं स्त्रियो मूढधिय इति सत्यं न संशयः ॥ ५ ॥
   evaṁ prokto hemacūḍaḥ prahasya prāha tāṁ priyām ।
   nūnaṁ striyo mūḍhadhiya iti satyaṁ na saṁśayaḥ ॥ 5 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; proktaḥ — spoken; hemacūḍaḥ — Hemachuda; prahasya — smiling; prāha — said; tāṁ — to her; priyām — dear; nūnam — indeed; striyaḥ — women; mūḍhadhiyaḥ — foolish; iti — thus; satyam — true; na — not; saṁśayaḥ — doubt
   Thus spoken, Hemachuda, smiling, said to his beloved, “Indeed, women are foolish; this is undoubtedly true.”
   
   Verse 6
   प्रियाप्रिये हि जानन्ति पशुपक्षिसरीसृपाः ।
   यतस्तेषां दृश्यते हि प्रियेष्वप्रियकेषु च ॥ ६ ॥
   priyāpriye hi jānanti paśupakṣisarīsṛpāḥ ।
   yataḥ teṣāṁ dṛśyate hi priyeṣv apriyakeṣu ca ॥ 6 ॥
   priyāpriye — what is dear and not dear; hi — indeed; jānanti — know; paśu — animals; pakṣi — birds; sarīsṛpāḥ — reptiles; yataḥ — because; teṣām — their; dṛśyate — is seen; hi — indeed; priyeṣu — in dear; apriyakeṣu — in not dear; ca — and
   Indeed, animals, birds, and reptiles understand what is dear and not dear, as evidenced by their behavior towards those things.
   
   Verse 7
   प्रवृत्तिश्च निवृत्तिश्च किमत्र बहु चिन्तनम्‌ ।
   सुखं यस्मात्‌ तत्‌ प्रियं स्यात्‌ दुःखं यस्मात्तदप्रियम्‌ ॥ ७ ॥
   pravṛttiśca nivṛttiśca kimatra bahu cintanam ।
   sukhaṁ yasmāt tat priyaṁ syāt duḥkhaṁ yasmāt tadapriyam
   ॥ 7 ॥
   pravṛttiḥ — engagement; ca — and; nivṛttiḥ — disengagement; ca — and; kim — what; atra — here; bahu — much; cintanam — thinking; sukham — happiness; yasmāt — from which; tat — that; priyam — dear; syāt — is; duḥkham — sorrow; yasmāt — from which; tat — that; apriyam — not dear
   Engagement and disengagement, what is there to think much about it? Happiness makes something dear, while sorrow makes it not dear.
   
   Verse 8
   किमत्र मुग्धभावेन नित्यं चिन्तयसि प्रिये ।
   श्रुत्वा प्रियवचः प्राह हेमलेखा पुनः प्रियम्‌ ॥ ८ ॥
   kimatra mugdhabhāvena nityaṁ cintayasi priye ।
   śrutvā priyavacaḥ prāha hemalekha punaḥ priyam ॥ 8 ॥
   kim — why; atra — here; mugdhabhāvena — with bewilderment; nityaṁ — always; cintayasi — you think; priye — dear; śrutvā — hearing; priyavacaḥ — dear words; prāha — said; hemalekha — Hemalekha; punaḥ — again; priyam — to dear
   Why do you always ponder in bewilderment, dear? Hearing these words, Hemalekha again spoke to her beloved.
   
   Verse 9
   सत्यं स्त्रियो मुग्धभावा नास्त्यासां सद्विमर्शनम् ।
   तथाप्यहं बोधनीया त्वया सम्यग्विमर्शिना ॥ ९ ॥
   satyaṁ striyo mugdhabhāvā nāstyāsāṁ sadvimarśanam ।
   tathāpy ahaṁ bodhanīyā tvayā samyagvimarśinā ॥ 9 ॥
   satyaṁ — true; striyaḥ — women; mugdhabhāvāḥ — bewildered; na asti — not; āsāṁ — their; sadvimarśanam — proper contemplation; tathā api — even so; ahaṁ — I; bodhanīyā — should be enlightened; tvayā — by you; samyagvimarśinā — with proper contemplation
   It is true that women often seem bewildered and lack proper contemplation. Yet, I should be enlightened by you with the right contemplation.
   
   Verse 10
   सुबोधिता त्वया चाह चिन्तामेतां विसृज्य तु ।
   त्वया भोगेषु सततं भवाम्यनुदिनं ततः ॥ १० ॥
   subodhitā tvayā cāha cintām etāṁ visṛjya tu ।
   tvayā bhogeṣu satataṁ bhavāmy anudinaṁ tataḥ ॥ 10 ॥
   subodhitā — well enlightened; tvayā — by you; ca — and; ahaṁ — I; cintām — worry; etām — this; visṛjya — leaving; tu — indeed; tvayā — by you; bhogeṣu — in enjoyments; satataṁ — always; bhavāmi — will be; anudinaṁ — daily; tataḥ — then
   Once well enlightened by you, I will leave this worry behind. With your guidance, I will find daily enjoyment thereafter.
   
   Verse 11
   राजन्‌ सुखञ्च दुःखञ्च याभ्यां भवति ते ननु ।
   प्रियाप्रिये विनिर्दिष्टे सुक्ष्मविमर्शिना ॥ ११ ॥
   rājan sukhaṁ ca duḥkhaṁ ca yābhyāṁ bhavati te nanu ।
   priyāpriye vinirdiṣṭe sukṣmavimarśinā ॥ 11 ॥
   rājan — O king; sukham — happiness; ca — and; duḥkham — sorrow; ca — and; yābhyām — by which; bhavati — becomes; te — your; nanu — indeed; priyāpriye — dear and not dear; vinirdiṣṭe — determined; sukṣmavimarśinā — by subtle contemplation
   O king, indeed, happiness and sorrow become yours through the discernment of what is dear and not dear by means of subtle contemplation.
   
   Verse 12
   एकमेव सुखं दुःखं कालदेशाकृतेर्भिदा ।
   जनयेदत्र तत्‌ कस्मात्‌ प्रतिष्ठाऽध्यवसायिनी ॥ १२ ॥
   ekam eva sukhaṁ duḥkhaṁ kāladeśākṛter bhidā ।
   janayed atra tat kasmāt pratiṣṭhādhyavasāyinī ॥ 12 ॥
   ekam — one; eva — indeed; sukham — happiness; duḥkham — sorrow; kāla — time; deśa — place; ākṛteḥ — form; bhidā — difference; janayet — creates; atra — here; tat — that; kasmāt — why; pratiṣṭhā — basis; adhyavasāyinī — determined
   Indeed, one’s happiness and sorrow are shaped by variations in time, place, and form. Why is that considered the basis here?
   
   Verse 13
   यतो वह्निः कालभेदात् पुथगेव फलप्रदः ।
   तथा देशविभेदेनाप्याकारस्य विभेदतः ॥ १३ ॥
   yato vahniḥ kālabhedāt puthageva phalapradaḥ ।
   tathā deśavibhedenāpy ākārasya vibhedataḥ ॥ 13 ॥
   yataḥ — because; vahniḥ — fire; kālabhedāt — due to difference in time; puthag eva — separately; phalapradaḥ — gives result; tathā — likewise; deśavibhedenā — due to difference in place; api — also; ākārasya — of form; vibhedataḥ — due to difference
   Because fire produces different results depending on time, it similarly varies based on place and form.
   
   Verse 14
   शीतकाले प्रियो वह्निरूष्मे त्वप्रिय एव हि ।
   हिमोष्णदेशभेदेन प्रियश्चाप्रिय एव च ॥ १४ ॥
   śītakāle priyo vahnir ūṣme tv apriya eva hi ।
   himoṣṇadeśabhedena priyaś cāpriya eva ca ॥ 14 ॥
   śītakāle — in cold time; priyaḥ — dear; vahniḥ — fire; ūṣme — in heat; tu — but; apriyaḥ — not dear; eva — indeed; hi — surely; hima — cold; uṣṇa — hot; deśa — place; bhedena — due to difference; priyaḥ — dear; ca — and; apriyaḥ — not dear; eva — indeed; ca — and
   In cold weather, fire is cherished, but in heat, it is certainly not. The same holds true in places with cold and hot climates; its value fluctuates accordingly.
   
   Verse 15
   शीतप्रकृतिजीवानां प्रियोऽन्येषां तथेतरः ।
   अथाप्यधिकभावेनाल्पभावेनैवमीरितः ॥ १५ ॥
   śītaprakṛtijīvānāṁ priyo'nyeṣāṁ tathetaraḥ ।
   athāpy adhikabhāvenālpabhāvenaivam īritaḥ ॥ 15 ॥
   śīta — cold; prakṛti — nature; jīvānāṁ — of beings; priyaḥ — dear; anyeṣāṁ — of others; tathā — likewise; itaraḥ — opposite; atha — thus; api — also; adhikabhāvena — with higher degree; alpabhāvena — with lesser degree; evam — thus; īritaḥ — indicated
   For beings of cold nature, fire is cherished, while for others, it is not. This illustrates that its value varies significantly, either increasing or decreasing in different degrees.
   
   Verse 16
   एवं शीतं धनं दाराः पुत्रा राज्यं तथेतरत्‌ ।
   अथाप्येवं महाराजो दारपुत्रधनैर्वृतः ॥ १६ ॥
   evaṁ śītaṁ dhanaṁ dārāḥ putrā rājyaṁ tathetarat ।
   athāpy evaṁ mahārājo dāraputradhanair vṛtaḥ ॥ 16 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; śītam — cold; dhanam — wealth; dārāḥ — wives; putrāḥ — sons; rājyaṁ — kingdom; tathā — likewise; itarat — others; atha — thus; api — also; evaṁ — thus; mahārājaḥ — great king; dāra — wives; putra — sons; dhanaiḥ — with wealth; vṛtaḥ — surrounded
   Similarly, wealth, wives, sons, kingdoms, and other possessions are cherished, even by a great king surrounded by such abundance.
   
   Verse 17
   शोचत्यनुदिनं कस्मान्न शोचन्तीतरे कुतः ।
   योऽयं भोगः सुखार्थोऽस्ति सोऽप्यनन्तो भवेन्ननु ॥ १७ ॥
   śocaty anudinaṁ kasmān na śocantītare kutaḥ ।
   yo'yaṁ bhogaḥ sukhārtho'sti so'py ananto bhaven nanu ॥ 17 ॥
   śocati — grieves; anudinaṁ — daily; kasmāt — why; na — not; śocanti — grieve; itare — others; kutaḥ — why; yaḥ — this; ayaṁ — this; bhogaḥ — enjoyment; sukha-arthaḥ — for happiness; asti — is; saḥ — it; api — also; anantaḥ — endless; bhavet — becomes; nanu — indeed
   Why does he grieve daily, while others do not? The pursuit of happiness through enjoyment is an endless endeavor.
   
   Verse 18
   न केनचित्तदखिलं प्राप्तं यस्मात्‌ सुखं भवेत्‌ ।
   यत्किञ्चिल्लाभतो यत्स्यात्‌ सुखं तत्रापि संशृणु ॥ १८ ॥
   na kenacit tad akhilaṁ prāptaṁ yasmāt sukhaṁ bhavet ।
   yat kiñcil lābhato yat syāt sukhaṁ tatrāpi saṁśṛṇu ॥ 18 ॥
   na — not; kenacit — by anyone; tat — that; akhilam — whole; prāptam — obtained; yasmāt — from which; sukham — happiness; bhavet — becomes; yat — whatever; kiñcit — little; lābhataḥ — from gain; yat — which; syāt — is; sukham — happiness; tatra — there; api — also; saṁśṛṇu — listen
   That complete happiness has not been attained by anyone. Even the small amount of happiness that is gained, listen about that as well.
   
   Verse 19
   न तत्‌ सुखं भवेन्नाथ यतो दुःखविमिश्रितम् ।
   दुःखं तु द्विविधं प्रोक्तं बाह्यमान्तरमित्यपि ॥ १९ ॥
   na tat sukhaṁ bhaven nātha yato duḥkha-vimiśritam ।
   duḥkhaṁ tu dvividhaṁ proktaṁ bāhyam āntaram ity api ॥ 19 ॥
   na — not; tat — that; sukham — happiness; bhavet — becomes; nātha — lord; yataḥ — from which; duḥkha — sorrow; vimiśritam — mixed; duḥkham — sorrow; tu — but; dvividham — twofold; proktam — said; bāhyam — external; āntaram — internal; iti — thus; api — also
   Happiness does not remain happiness, lord, when it is mixed with sorrow. Sorrow is said to be of two kinds: external and internal.
   
   Verse 20
   बाह्यं शरीरसम्भूतं धातुदोषादिसम्भवम्‌ ।
   आन्तरं मानसं प्रोक्त तच्च वाञ्छासमुद्भवम् ॥ २० ॥
   bāhyaṁ śarīra-sambhūtaṁ dhātu-doṣādi-sambhavam ।
   āntaraṁ mānasaṁ prokta tacca vāñchā-samudbhavam ॥ 20 ॥
   bāhyam — external; śarīra-sambhūtam — arising from the body; dhātu-doṣa — imbalance of elements; ādi — and so on; sambhavam — arising; āntaram — internal; mānasam — mental; proktam — said; tat — that; ca — and; vāñchā-samudbhavam — arising from desire
   External sorrow arises from the body due to an imbalance of elements and similar factors. Internal sorrow is said to be mental, originating from desires.
   
   Verse 21
   महत्तरं मानसं स्याद्येन ग्रस्तमिदं जगत्‌ ।
   वाञ्छैव दुःखविटपिबीजं सुदृढशक्तिकम् ॥ २१ ॥
   mahattanam mānasam syād yena grastam idaṁ jagat ।
   vāñchāiva duḥkhaviṭapibījaṁ sudṛḍhaśaktikam ॥ 21 ॥
   mahattanam — greater; mānasam — mental; syāt — is; yena — by which; grastam — grasped; idaṁ — this; jagat — world; vāñchā — desire; eva — indeed; duḥkhaviṭapibījam — seed of the tree of sorrow; sudṛḍhaśaktikam — with strong power
   The intense mental suffering that grips the world is indeed rooted in desire, which is the powerful seed of the tree of sorrow.
   
   Verse 22
   यया किङ्करतां प्राप्ताः कुर्वन्त्येव दिवानिशम् ।
   इनद्रादयोऽपि विबुधाः स्वर्निवासाः सदोदिताः ॥ २२ ॥
   yayā kiṅkaratāṁ prāptāḥ kurvantyeva divāniśam ।
   indrādayo'pi vibudhāḥ svanivāsāḥ sadoditāḥ ॥ 22 ॥
   yayā — by which; kiṅkaratām — servitude; prāptāḥ — have attained; kurvanti — do; eva — indeed; divāniśam — day and night; indrādayaḥ — Indra and others; api — also; vibudhāḥ — wise ones; svanivāsāḥ — dwelling in heaven; sadoditāḥ — always known
   By desire, they serve and attain, working day and night. This is well-known even for Indra and the wise ones dwelling in heaven.
   
   Verse 23
   सुखं वाञ्छावशेषेऽपि यदस्ति नृपसम्भव ।
   तद्‌ दुःखमेव जानीहि यत्‌ कृमिष्वपि सम्भवेत्‌ ॥ २३ ॥
   sukhaṁ vāñchāvaśeṣe'pi yad asti nṛpasambhava ।
   tad duḥkham eva jānīhi yat kṛmiṣv api sambhavet ॥ 23 ॥
   sukham — happiness; vāñchāvaśeṣe — in remaining desire; api — even; yat — which; asti — is; nṛpasambhava — O prince; tad — that; duḥkham — sorrow; eva — indeed; jānīhi — know; yat — which; kṛmiṣu — in worms; api — even; sambhavet — happens
   O prince, the happiness that remains even after the fulfillment of desire, recognize that as the sorrow that even worms experience.
   
   Verse 24
   वरं तिर्यक्कीटकृमिप्रभृतीनां सुखं तु यत्‌ ।
   स्वल्पवाञ्छासम्मिलितं नृणां किं स्यात्‌ सुखं वद ॥ २४ ॥
   varaṁ tiryak kīṭa kṛmi prabhṛtīnāṁ sukhaṁ tu yat ।
   svalpa vāñchā sammilitaṁ nṛṇāṁ kiṁ syāt sukhaṁ vada ॥ 24 ॥
   varaṁ — better; tiryak — animals; kīṭa — insects; kṛmi — worms; prabhṛtīnāṁ — and so on; sukham — happiness; tu — indeed; yat — which; svalpa — small; vāñchā — desire; sammilitam — combined; nṛṇām — of men; kim — what; syāt — is; sukham — happiness; vada — say
   The happiness of animals, insects, worms, and others, combined with small desires, is greater. Tell me, what is the happiness of men when they possess only small desires?
   
   Verse 25
   वाञ्छाशतसमाविष्टो यदि किञ्चिदुपेत्य तु ।
   सुखी भवेदिह तदा को हि न स्यात्‌ सुखी वद ॥ २५ ॥
   vāñchāśata samāviṣṭo yadi kiñcid upetya tu ।
   sukhī bhaved iha tadā ko hi na syāt sukhī vada ॥ 25 ॥
   vāñchā — desire; śata — hundreds; samāviṣṭaḥ — filled; yadi — if; kiñcit — something; upetya — achieving; tu — indeed; sukhī — happy; bhavet — becomes; iha — here; tadā — then; kaḥ — who; hi — indeed; na — not; syāt — would be; sukhī — happy; vada — say
   If someone filled with hundreds of desires achieves something, they might find happiness here, wouldn't you agree?
   
   Verse 26
   अखिलाङ्गे वह्निदग्धे सूक्ष्मपाटीरबिन्दुना ।
   यदि शीतलदेहः स्यात्तदा सोऽपि सुखी भवेत्‌ ॥ २६ ॥
   akhilāṅge vahnidagdhe sūkṣmapāṭīrabindunā ।
   yadi śītaladehaḥ syāt tadā so'pi sukhī bhavet ॥ 26 ॥
   akhila-aṅge — entire body; vahni — fire; dagdhe — burned; sūkṣma — small; pāṭīra — sandalwood paste; bindunā — drop; yadi — if; śītala — cool; dehaḥ — body; syāt — becomes; tadā — then; saḥ — he; api — also; sukhī — happy; bhavet — would be
   If an entire body is burned by fire, and a small drop of sandalwood paste cools it, then he would find happiness in that small relief.
   
   Verse 27
   प्रियायाः सम्परिष्वङ्गात्‌ सुखं प्राप्नोति वै नरः ।
   तत्रैवाङ्गस्य विषमबन्धाद्‌ दुःखं भवेन्ननु ॥ २७ ॥
   priyāyāḥ sampariṣvaṅgāt sukhaṁ prāpnoti vai naraḥ ।
   tatraivāṅgasya viṣamabandhād duḥkhaṁ bhaven nanu ॥ 27 ॥
   priyāyāḥ — of the beloved; sampariṣvaṅgāt — from embrace; sukham — happiness; prāpnoti — gets; vai — indeed; naraḥ — man; tatra — there; eva — indeed; aṅgasya — of the body; viṣama — awkward; bandhāt — from binding; duḥkham — sorrow; bhavet — would be; nanu — indeed
   A man finds true happiness in the embrace of his beloved. Yet, when separated, the physical disconnect brings inevitable sorrow due to the awkward detachment of their bodies.
   
   Verse 28
   रत्यावेशात् परिश्रान्तिः सर्वेषा जायते किल ।
   अनन्तरं भारवाहपशोरिव परिश्रमः ॥ २८ ॥
   ratyāveśāt pariśrāntiḥ sarveṣā jāyate kila ।
   anantaraṁ bhāravāhapaśor iva pariśramaḥ ॥ 28 ॥
   ratyāveśāt — from the intensity of pleasure; pariśrāntiḥ — exhaustion; sarveṣāṁ — of all; jāyate — arises; kila — indeed; anantaram — thereafter; bhāravāhapaśoḥ — of a beast of burden; iva — like; pariśramaḥ — fatigue
   From the intensity of pleasure, exhaustion arises in everyone. Subsequently, the fatigue is akin to that of a burdened beast.
   
   Verse 29
   कथं पश्यसि तत्‌ सौख्यं नाथैतन्मे समुच्यताम्‌ ।
   यावत्‌ सुखं प्रियासङ्गे नाडीसंघट्टसम्भवम्‌ ॥ २९ ॥
   kathaṁ paśyasi tat saukhyaṁ nātha itanme samucyatām ।
   yāvat sukhaṁ priyāsaṅge nāḍīsaṁghaṭṭasaṁbhavam ॥ 29 ॥
   kathaṁ — how; paśyasi — do you see; tat — that; saukhyam — happiness; nātha — lord; etat — this; me — my; samucyatām — be told; yāvat — as long as; sukham — happiness; priyāsaṅge — in the company of the beloved; nāḍīsaṁghaṭṭa — nerve friction; saṁbhavam — arising
   How can this be seen as happiness, lord? Explain it to me: as long as happiness arises from the beloved's company, merely through the friction of nerves.
   
   Verse 30
   तवास्ति तावन्न किमु शुनामस्तीह तद्वद ।
   यत्ततो ह्यतिरिक्तं ते दृष्टसौन्दर्यसम्भवम्‌ ॥ ३० ॥
   tavāsti tāvan na kimu śunām astīha tadvad ।
   yattato hy atiriktaṁ te dṛṣṭasaundaryasaṁbhavam ॥ 30 ॥
   tava — your; asti — is; tāvat — so much; na — not; kimu — why; śunām — of dogs; asti — is; iha — here; tadvad — similarly; yat — that; tataḥ — then; hi — indeed; atiriktaṁ — exceeding; te — your; dṛṣṭasaundaryasaṁbhavam — from perceived beauty
   Is your happiness not akin to that of dogs here? Then, indeed, your happiness from perceived beauty must be far greater.
   
   Verse 31
   तत्‌ केवलाभिमानोत्थं स्वाप्नस्त्रीसङ्गमे यथा ।
   पुरा कश्चिद्राजसुतो मन्मथाधिकसुन्दरः ॥ ३१ ॥
   tat kevalābhimānotthaṁ svāpnastrīsaṅgame yathā ।
   purā kaścid rājasuto manmathādhikasundaraḥ ॥ 31 ॥
   tat — that; kevala — only; abhimānottham — arising from ego; svāpna — dream; strīsaṅgame — union with a woman; yathā — as; purā — long ago; kaścit — some; rājasutaḥ — prince; manmatha — Cupid; adhikasundaraḥ — more beautiful
   That happiness arises only from ego, like in a dream where one unites with a woman. Long ago, there was a prince, more beautiful than Cupid.
   
   Verse 32
   काञ्चित्‌ सुरूपिणीं प्राप्तः स्त्रियं सर्वमनोहराम् ।
   अत्यन्तमनुरक्तः स तस्यां राजकुमारकः ॥ ३२ ॥
   kāñcit surūpiṇīṁ prāptaḥ striyaṁ sarvamanoharām ।
   atyantam anuraktaḥ sa tasyāṁ rājakumārakah ॥ 32 ॥
   kāñcit — some; surūpiṇīm — beautiful; prāptaḥ — attained; striyam — woman; sarva-manoharām — all-enchanting; atyantam — extremely; anuraktaḥ — attached; saḥ — he; tasyām — in her; rājkumārakaḥ — prince
   A prince, more beautiful than Cupid, obtained an all-enchanting woman and became extremely attached to her.
   
   Verse 33
   सा त्वन्यस्मिन्‌ राजसुत भृत्ये संसक्तमानसा ।
   स भृत्यो राजपुत्रं तं वञ्चयामास युक्तितः ॥ ३३ ॥
   sā tv anyasmin rājasuta bhṛtye saṁsaktamānasā ।
   sa bhṛtyo rājaputraṁ taṁ vañcayāmāsa yuktitaḥ ॥ 33 ॥
   sā — she; tu — indeed; anyasmin — in another; rājasuta — prince; bhṛtye — servant; saṁsaktamānasā — attached in mind; saḥ — he; bhṛtyaḥ — servant; rājaputram — prince; taṁ — him; vañcayāmāsa — deceived; yuktitaḥ — with trick
   Her mind, however, was attached to another—the prince's servant. The servant cunningly deceived the prince with a trick.
   
   Verse 34
   मदिरां मोहनार्थाय तस्मै दत्वातिमात्रकम्‌ ।
   ततो मदान्धाय चेटीं काञ्चित्‌ प्रेष्य कुरूपिणीम्‌ ॥ ३४ ॥
   madirāṁ mohanārthāya tasmai datvā'timātrakam ।
   tato madāndhāya ceṭīṁ kāñcit preṣya kurūpiṇīm ॥ 34 ॥
   madirām — wine; mohanārthāya — for enchanting; tasmai — to him; datvā — giving; atimātrakam — excessive; tataḥ — then; madāndhāya — to the intoxicated; ceṭīm — maidservant; kāñcit — some; preṣya — sending; kurūpiṇīm — ugly
   He gave the prince an excessive amount of wine to enchant him, and then sent an unattractive maidservant to the now-intoxicated prince.
   
   Verse 35
   बुभुजे तां तस्य पत्नीं सर्वलोकैकसुन्दरीम्‌ ।
   येवमेव चिरं तत्र मदान्धो नृपतेः सुतः ॥ ३५ ॥
   bubhuje tāṁ tasya patnīṁ sarvalokaikasundarīm ।
   evam eva ciraṁ tatra madāndho nṛpateḥ sutaḥ ॥ 35 ॥
   bubhuje — enjoyed; tāṁ — her; tasya — his; patnīm — wife; sarvalokaikasundarīm — world's most beautiful; evam — thus; eva — indeed; ciram — long; tatra — there; madāndhaḥ — blinded by intoxication; nṛpateḥ — king's; sutaḥ — son
   He enjoyed her, believing she was his wife, the most beautiful woman in the world. Blinded by intoxication, the prince lingered in this illusion for a long time.
   
   Verse 36
   प्रत्यहं चेटिकां गच्छन्‌ स्वात्मानं सममंसत ।
   धन्योऽहमीदृशीं लोकसुन्दरीं प्राणप्रेयसीम्‌ ॥ ३६ ॥
   pratyahaṁ ceṭikāṁ gacchan svātmānaṁ samamaṁsata ।
   dhanyo'ham īdṛśīṁ lokasundarīṁ prāṇapreyasīm ॥ 36 ॥
   pratyaham — every day; ceṭikām — maidservant; gacchan — approaching; svātmānam — himself; samamaṁsata — considered; dhanyaḥ — fortunate; aham — I; īdṛśīm — such; lokasundarīm — world's most beautiful; prāṇapreyasīm — beloved
   Each day, as he approached the maidservant, he considered himself fortunate, thinking, "I am blessed to have such a beautiful beloved in the world."
   
   Verse 37
   उपगच्छाम्यहं नित्यं न मेऽस्ति सदृशः क्वचित्‌ ।
   एवं वृत्ते चिरे काले कदाचिद्‌ दैवयोगतः ॥ ३७ ॥
   upagacchāmy ahaṁ nityaṁ na me'sti sadṛśaḥ kvacit ।
   evaṁ vṛtte cire kāle kadācit daivayogataḥ ॥ 37 ॥
   upagacchāmi — I approach; aham — I; nityam — always; na — not; me — my; asti — is; sadṛśaḥ — equal; kvacit — anywhere; evam — thus; vṛtte — in action; cire — long; kāle — time; kadācit — once; daivayogataḥ — by divine will
   "I approach her daily, I have no equal anywhere." One day, by divine intervention...
   
   Verse 38
   भृत्यो निधाय पानं स कार्ये चात्यन्तिके ययौ ।
   अथ राजकुमारस्तत्पानं नात्यन्तिकं पपौ ॥ ३८ ॥
   bhṛtyo nidhāya pānaṁ sa kārye cātyantike yayau ।
   atha rājkumāras tat pānaṁ nātyantikaṁ papau ॥ 38 ॥
   bhṛtyaḥ — servant; nidhāya — placing; pānam — drink; saḥ — he; kārye — in duty; ca — and; atyantike — urgent; yayau — went; atha — then; rājkumāraḥ — prince; tat — that; pānam — drink; na — not; atyantikam — excessive; papau — drank
   The servant placed the drink and hurried off to attend to an urgent matter. The prince drank the beverage, not excessively.
   
   Verse 39
   निमित्ततो ययौ शीध्रं रत्युत्सुकितमानसः ।
   शयनीयं मनःकान्तं सर्वभोगर्द्धिसंयुतम्‌ ॥ ३९ ॥
   nimittato yayau śīghraṁ ratyutsukitamānasaḥ ।
   śayanīyaṁ manaḥkāntaṁ sarvabhogarddhisaṁyutam ॥ 39 ॥
   nimittataḥ — for the reason; yayau — went; śīghram — quickly; ratyutsukita — eager for pleasure; mānasaḥ — mind; śayanīyam — bed; manaḥkāntam — mentally delightful; sarvabhoga — all enjoyments; riddhi — prosperity; saṁyutam — endowed
   Driven by his desire, he quickly went to the bed, his mind filled with pleasure and delight, enjoying the prosperity of his indulgences.
   
   Verse 40
   शचीगृहं देवपतिरिव नन्दनसंस्थितम्‌ ।
   पराद्धर्यपर्यङ्कगतां तां चेटीमुपसङ्गतः ॥ ४० ॥
   śacīgṛhaṁ devapatir iva nandanasaṁsthitam ।
   parāddharyaparyaṅkagatāṁ tāṁ ceṭīm upasaṅgataḥ ॥ 40 ॥
   śacīgṛham — palace; devapatiḥ — lord of gods; iva — like; nandanasaṁsthitam — situated in Nandana; parāddharya — attained; paryaṅka — bed; gatām — gone; tāṁ — her; ceṭīm — maidservant; upasaṅgataḥ — approached
   In a palace resembling the abode of the gods in Nandana, he approached the maidservant on the bed, mistaking her for the princess.
   
   Verse 41
   कामवेगेन विवशो बुभुजेऽत्यन्तहर्षतः ।
   उपलभ्याथ रत्यन्ते चेटीं तां विकृताकृतिम्‌ ॥ ४१ ॥
   kāmavegena vivaśo bubhuje'tyantaharṣataḥ ।
   upalabhyātha ratyante ceṭīṁ tāṁ vikṛtākṛtim ॥ 41 ॥
   kāma-vegena — by the force of desire; vivaśaḥ — overwhelmed; bubhuje — enjoyed; atyanta-harṣataḥ — with extreme pleasure; upalabhya — discovering; atha — then; raty-ante — at the end of the pleasure; ceṭīm — maidservant; tām — her; vikṛta-ākṛtim — with distorted appearance
   Overwhelmed by the force of desire, he indulged in extreme pleasure. At the end of this pleasure, he discovered that she was a maidservant with a distorted appearance.
   
   Verse 42
   शङ्कितोऽमर्षितश्चापि किमेतदिति चिन्तयन्‌ ।
   क्व सा मम प्रियतमेत्येवं तामन्वपृच्छत ॥ ४२ ॥
   śaṅkito'marṣitaś cāpi kim etad iti cintayan ।
   kva sā mama priyatamety evaṁ tām anvapṛcchat ॥ 42 ॥
   śaṅkitaḥ — suspicious; amārṣitaḥ — indignant; ca — and; api — also; kim — what; etat — this; iti — thus; cintayan — thinking; kva — where; sā — she; mama — my; priyatamā — beloved; iti — thus; evam — in this way; tām — her; anvapṛcchat — asked
   Suspicious and indignant, he thought, "What is this? Where is my beloved?" and questioned her in this manner.
   
   Verse 43
   पुष्टैवं तेन सा चेटी विमदं तं निशाम्य तु ।
   भीता न किञ्चित्तं प्राह वेपमाना तदा ततः ॥ ४३ ॥
   puṣṭaivaṁ tena sā ceṭī vimadaṁ taṁ niśāmya tu ।
   bhītā na kiñcit taṁ prāha vepamānā tadā tataḥ ॥ 43 ॥
   puṣṭā — being questioned; evaṁ — thus; tena — by him; sā — she; ceṭī — maidservant; vimadam — sober; tam — him; niśāmya — observing; tu — indeed; bhītā — frightened; na — not; kiñcit — anything; tam — to him; prāha — spoke; vepamānā — trembling; tadā — then; tataḥ — thereafter
   Being questioned by him, the maidservant, observing his sober state, was indeed frightened. Trembling and unable to speak, she remained silent.
   
   Verse 44
   आलक्ष्य राजपुत्रोऽपि वैषम्य चात्मवञ्चनम्‌ ।
   वामेन जग्राह कचे चेटीं क्रोधारुणेक्षणः ॥ ४४ ॥
   ālakṣya rājaputro'pi vaiṣamya cātmavañcanam ।
   vāmena jagrāha kace ceṭīṁ krodhāruṇekṣaṇaḥ ॥ 44 ॥
   ālakṣya — noticing; rājaputraḥ — prince; api — also; vaiṣamya — trouble; ca — and; ātma-vañcanam — self-deception; vāmena — with the left; jagrāha — grabbed; kace — hair; ceṭīm — maidservant; krodha-aruṇa-īkṣaṇaḥ — with red eyes of anger
   Noticing the trouble and self-deception, the prince, his eyes red with anger, grabbed the maidservant’s hair with his left hand.
   
   Verse 45
   कृपाणिमाददे दक्षहस्तेन नृपसम्भवः ।
   तर्जयंस्तां प्रत्युवाच वद वृत्त यथातथम्‌ ॥ ४५ ॥
   kṛpāṇim ādade dakṣahastena nṛpasambhavaḥ ।
   tarjayan tām pratyuvāca vada vṛtta yathātatham ॥ 45 ॥
   kṛpāṇim — sword; ādade — took; dakṣa-hastena — with the right hand; nṛpasambhavaḥ — prince; tarjayan — threatening; tām — her; pratyuvāca — said; vada — speak; vṛtta — event; yathā-tatham — as it happened
   Taking the sword in his right hand, the prince, threatening her, said, “Speak the truth of what happened.”
   
   Verse 46
   नो चेन्न स्याज्जीवित ते क्षणमात्रमपि द्रुतम्‌ ।
   सैवं निशम्य तद्वाक्यं भीता प्राणपरीप्सया ॥ ४६ ॥
   no cen na syāj jīvita te kṣaṇamātram api drutam ।
   saivaṁ niśamya tadvākyaṁ bhītā prāṇaparīpsayā ॥ 46 ॥
   na — not; cet — if; na — not; syāt — will be; jīvita — life; te — your; kṣaṇamātram — for a moment; api — even; drutam — quickly; saḥ — she; evaṁ — thus; niśamya — hearing; tad-vākyaṁ — his words; bhītā — frightened; prāṇaparīpsayā — with desire to save life
   "Otherwise, your life will not last even for a moment.” Frightened by his words and eager to save her life, she began to speak.
   
   Verse 47
   जगौ यथावत्तत्‌ सर्वं चिराद्‌ वृत्तं समास्थितम्‌ ।
   प्रादर्शयच्चापि तस्मै तां भृत्येन सुसङ्गताम् ॥ ४७ ॥
   jagau yathāvat tat sarvaṁ cirād vṛttaṁ samāsthitam ।
   prādarśayac cāpi tasmai tāṁ bhṛtyena susaṅgatām ॥ 47 ॥
   jagau — told; yathāvat — as it happened; tat — that; sarvam — everything; cirāt — for a long time; vṛttam — event; samāsthitam — occurred; prādarśayat — showed; ca — and; api — also; tasmai — to him; tām — her; bhṛtyena — with the servant; susaṅgatām — associated
   She recounted everything that had transpired over time and showed him his wife's association with the servant.
   
   Verse 48
   क्वचिद्‌भूमौ कटे भृत्यं कृष्णं पिङ्गललोचनम्‌ ।
   प्रांशुं मलिनसर्वाङ्गं रूक्षवक्त्रं जुगुप्सितम्‌ ॥ ४८ ॥
   kvacid bhūmau kaṭe bhṛtyaṁ kṛṣṇaṁ piṅgalalocanam ।
   prāṁśuṁ malinasarvāṅgaṁ rūkṣavaktraṁ jugupsitam ॥ 48 ॥
   kvacit — somewhere; bhūmau — on the ground; kaṭe — lying; bhṛtyam — servant; kṛṣṇam — dark; piṅgala-locanam — with brown eyes; prāṁśum — tall; malina-sarvāṅgam — with dirty limbs; rūkṣa-vaktram — with a harsh face; jugupsitam — disgusting
   On the ground lay the servant, dark with brown eyes, tall, with filthy limbs, and a harsh, disgusting face.
   
   Verse 49
   समाशिलष्य रतिश्रान्तां सर्वाङ्गैः प्रेमभावतः ।
   मृदुबाहुलतावृत्तग्रीवस्य वदने स्वकम्‌ ॥ ४९ ॥
   samāśilasya ratiśrāntāṁ sarvāṅgaiḥ premabhāvataḥ ।
   mṛdubāhulatāvṛttagrīvasya vadane svakam ॥ 49 ॥
   samāśilasya — embracing; ratiśrāntām — exhausted from pleasure; sarvāṅgaiḥ — with all limbs; premabhāvataḥ — with a feeling of love; mṛdubāhu-latāvṛtta-grīvasya — with a neck surrounded by soft arms; vadane — in the face; svakam — his own
   Embracing her, exhausted from pleasure, with all his limbs in a feeling of love, his neck encircled by her soft arms, lay his own wife.
   
   Verse 50
   निवेश्य वक्त्रकमलं पद्भयामाशिलष्य गाढतः ।
   तस्योरुयुग्मं तद्धस्तसंसक्तगुरुसुस्तनीम्‌ ॥ ५० ॥
   niveśya vaktrakamalaṁ padbhayām āśilasya gāḍhataḥ ।
   tasyoruyugmaṁ taddhasta-saṁsakta-gurusustanīm ॥ 50 ॥
   niveśya — placing; vaktrakamalam — face like a lotus; padbhayām — in the feet; āśilasya — embracing; gāḍhataḥ — tightly; tasya — his; uruyugmam — pair of thighs; tat — her; hasta — hand; saṁsakta — attached; gurusustanīm — heavy breasts
   Placing his face like a lotus at her feet, embracing her tightly, his hands clasping her thighs, and her heavy breasts pressing against him.
   
   Verse 51
   वासन्तिकामिव लतां वृतां कुसुमकोरकैः ।
   रोहिणीं राहुणोपेतामिवापश्यन्नृपात्मजः ॥ ५१ ॥
   vāsantikām iva latāṁ vṛtāṁ kusumakorakaiḥ ।
   rohiṇīṁ rāhuṇopetām ivāpaśyan nṛpātmajaḥ ॥ 51 ॥
   vāsantikām — spring; iva — like; latām — creeper; vṛtām — covered; kusumakorakaiḥ — with clusters of flowers; rohiṇīm — Rohini; rāhuṇā — by Rahu; upetām — attacked; iva — like; apaśyan — saw; nṛpātmajaḥ — prince
   The prince saw her like a spring creeper covered with clusters of flowers, reminiscent of Rohini being eclipsed by Rahu.
   
   Verse 52
   एवंविधां समालोक्य निद्रयाऽपगतस्मृतिम्‌ ।
   मोमुह्यमानश्चात्यन्तं क्षणं पश्चाद्‌ धृति भजन्‌ ॥ ५२ ॥
   evaṁvidhāṁ samālokya nidrayā'pagatasmṛtim ।
   mohamānaś cātyantaṁ kṣaṇaṁ paścād dhṛtiṁ bhajan ॥ 52 ॥
   evaṁvidhām — in this way; samālokya — seeing; nidrayā — by sleep; apagatasmṛtim — unconscious; mohamānaḥ — deluded; ca — and; atyantam — extremely; kṣaṇam — for a moment; paścāt — thereafter; dhṛtim — composure; bhajan — attaining
   Seeing her in this state, unconscious in sleep and profoundly deluded, the prince paused for a moment before regaining his composure.
   
   Verse 53
   यत्‌ प्राह राजतनयस्तन्मत्तः श्रूयतां ननु ।
   धिङ्मामनार्यमत्यन्तं मूढं मदविमोहितम्‌ ॥ ५३ ॥
   yat prāha rāja-tanayas tanmattaḥ śrūyatāṁ nanu ।
   dhiṅ mām anāryam atyantaṁ mūḍhaṁ madavimohitam ॥ 53 ॥
   yat — what; prāha — spoke; rāja-tanayaḥ — prince; tat — that; mattaḥ — from me; śrūyatām — be heard; nanu — indeed; dhiṅ — shame; mām — on me; anāryam — ignoble; atyantam — extremely; mūḍham — foolish; madavimohitam — intoxicated and deluded
   Hear what the prince spoke, indeed, "Shame on me, so utterly ignoble, foolish, intoxicated, and deluded."
   
   Verse 54
   धिग्‌ ये स्त्रीष्वभिसंप्रीता धिक्‌ तांश्च पुरुषाधमान्‌ ।
   न कामिन्यः कस्यचित्‌ स्युवृ क्षस्येव च शारिकाः ॥ ५४ ॥
   dhik ye strīṣv abhisaṁprītā dhik tāṁś ca puruṣādhamān ।
   na kāminyaḥ kasyacit syur vṛkṣasyaiva ca śārikāḥ ॥ 54 ॥
   dhik — shame; ye — those; strīṣu — in women; abhisaṁprītāḥ — deeply attached; dhik — shame; tān — them; ca — and; puruṣādhamān — the lowest of men; na — not; kāminyaḥ — women; kasyacit — anyone's; syuḥ — would be; vṛkṣasya — tree's; iva — like; śārikāḥ — starlings
   Shame on those deeply attached to women, shame on those lowest of men. Women are not anyone’s, like starlings on a tree.
   
   Verse 55
   किमहं मां प्रवक्ष्यामि मुग्धं महिषपोतवत्‌ ।
   जानन्तमेनां प्राणेभ्यः प्रेष्ठां सुचिरकालतः ॥ ५५ ॥
   kim ahaṁ māṁ pravakṣyāmi mugdhaṁ mahiṣapotavat ।
   jānantam enāṁ prāṇebhyaḥ preṣṭhāṁ sucirakālataḥ ॥ 55 ॥
   kim — what; ahaṁ — I; māṁ — myself; pravakṣyāmi — will say; mugdham — foolish; mahiṣapotavat — like a calf of a buffalo; jānantam — knowing; enām — her; prāṇebhyaḥ — dearer than life; preṣṭhām — beloved; sucirakālataḥ — for a long time
   What can I say about myself, foolish like a buffalo calf, believing her to be dearer than life, thinking she was my beloved for so long?
   
   Verse 56
   न स्त्रियः कस्यचिद्वा स्पुर्वेश्या इव विटस्य हि ।
   यः स्त्रोषु विश्रब्ध मनाः स एव वनगर्दभः ॥ ५६ ॥
   na striyaḥ kasyacid vā spurveśyā iva viṭasya hi ।
   yaḥ strīṣu viśrabdha-manāḥ sa eva vanagardabhaḥ ॥ 56 ॥
   na — not; striyaḥ — women; kasyacit — anyone's; vā — or; spur — prostitute; iva — like; viṭasya — of a rogue; hi — indeed; yaḥ — who; strīṣu — in women; viśrabdha-manāḥ — confident; saḥ — he; eva — indeed; vana-gardabhaḥ — wild donkey
   Women are like a prostitute to a rogue, belonging to no one. Indeed, a man who trusts women is like a wild donkey.
   
   Verse 57
   या स्थितिः शारदाभ्रस्य क्षणिका ह्यनवस्थिता ।
   ततोऽपि पेलवा स्त्रीणां स्थितिरत्यन्तचञ्चला ॥ ५७ ॥
   yā sthitiḥ śāradābhrasya kṣaṇikā hy anavasthitā ।
   tato'pi pelavā strīṇāṁ sthitir atyantacañcalā ॥ 57 ॥
   yā — what; sthitiḥ — state; śāradābhrasya — of autumn cloud; kṣaṇikā — momentary; hi — indeed; anavasthitā — unstable; tataḥ — than that; api — even; pelavā — flimsy; strīṇām — of women; sthitiḥ — state; atyantacañcalā — extremely fickle
   The state of an autumn cloud is momentary and unstable. Even more fleeting is the extremely fickle nature of women.
   
   Verse 58
   नाहमद्यावधि ह्येवं स्त्रीस्वभावमहोऽविदम्‌ ।
   यन्मां सर्वात्मनासक्तं त्यक्त्वा भृत्यमनुव्रता ॥ ५८ ॥
   nāham adyāvadhī hyevaṁ strīsvabhāvam aho'vidam ।
   yan māṁ sarvātmana āsaktaṁ tyaktvā bhṛtyam anuvratā ॥ 58 ॥
   na — not; aham — I; adyāvadhī — till today; hi — indeed; evaṁ — thus; strīsvabhāvam — nature of women; aho — alas; avidam — knew; yat — that; māṁ — me; sarvātmanaḥ — with whole soul; āsaktam — attached; tyaktvā — abandoning; bhṛtyam — servant; anuvratā — devoted
   Alas, until today, I did not understand the true nature of women. While I was completely devoted to her, she abandoned me and devoted herself to a mere servant.
   
   Verse 59
   अन्यासक्ता गृढभावा मयि छद्मानुरागिणी ।
   प्रदर्शयन्ती भक्ति स्वां नटीव विटमण्डले ॥ ५९ ॥
   anyāsaktā gṛḍhabhāvā mayi chadmānurāgiṇī ।
   pradarśayantī bhaktiṁ svāṁ naṭīva viṭamaṇḍale ॥ 59 ॥
   anyāsaktā — attached to another; gṛḍhabhāvā — greedy in mind; mayi — in me; chadmānurāgiṇī — insincere love; pradarśayantī — displaying; bhaktim — devotion; svām — her own; naṭīva — like an actress; viṭamaṇḍale — in an actor's troupe
   Attached to another, greedy in mind, showing insincere love for me, she displayed her devotion like an actress performing in an actor’s troupe.
   
   Verse 60
   नाविद लेशतोऽप्येनां मदिरामत्तमानसः ।
   छायेव मां सङ्गतेति मत्वा विश्रब्धमानसः ॥ ६० ॥
   nāvida leśato'py enāṁ madirāmattamānasaḥ ।
   chāyeva māṁ saṅgateti matvā viśrabdhamaṇasaḥ ॥ 60 ॥
   na — not; avid — knew; leśataḥ — even a bit; api — also; enām — her; madirāmattamānasaḥ — with mind intoxicated by wine; chāyeva — like a shadow; māṁ — me; saṅgataḥ — attached; iti — thus; matvā — thinking; viśrabdhamaṇasaḥ — confident in mind
   With my mind clouded by wine, I didn't truly know her, believing she was attached to me like a shadow, confidently trusting her in my heart.
   
   Verse 61
   अप्रेक्षणीयां चेटीं तां वञ्चितश्चिरसङ्गतः ।
   नूनं मत्तो मूढतमः को भवेज्जगतीतले ॥ ६१ ॥
   aprekṣaṇīyāṁ ceṭīṁ tāṁ vañcitaś cirasaṅgataḥ ।
   nūnaṁ matto mūḍhatamaḥ ko bhavej jagatītale ॥ 61 ॥
   aprekṣaṇīyām — unattractive; ceṭīm — maidservant; tām — her; vañcitaḥ — deceived; cirasaṅgataḥ — long-associated; nūnam — certainly; mattaḥ — than me; mūḍhatamaḥ — more foolish; kaḥ — who; bhavet — would be; jagatītale — on earth
   Who on earth could be more foolish than I, deceived and long-associated with that unattractive maidservant?
   
   Verse 62
   य एवं विस्त्रम्भपूर्वमनया चिरवञ्चितः ।
   अहोऽयं भृत्यहतकः सर्वाङ्गविकृताकृतिः ॥ ६२ ॥
   ya evaṁ vistrambhapūrvam anayā ciravañcitaḥ ।
   aho'yaṁ bhṛtyahatakaḥ sarvāṅgavikṛtākṛtiḥ ॥ 62 ॥
   yaḥ — who; evaṁ — thus; vistrambha-pūrvam — with confidence; anayā — by her; ciravañcitaḥ — long deceived; aho — alas; ayam — this; bhṛtya-hatakaḥ — wretched servant; sarvāṅga-vikṛtākṛtiḥ — with distorted form
   Who, with confidence, was long deceived by her? Alas, this wretched servant with a distorted form.
   
   Verse 63
   किमस्मिन्ननया दृष्टं सौन्दर्यं सर्वतोऽधिकम्‌ ।
   यतो मां निजसौन्दर्याहृतलोकावलोकनम्‌ ॥ ६३ ॥
   kim asminn anayā dṛṣṭaṁ saundaryaṁ sarvato'dhikam ।
   yato māṁ nijasaundaryāhṛtalokāvalokanam ॥ 63 ॥
   kim — what; asmin — in this; anayā — by her; dṛṣṭam — seen; saundaryam — beauty; sarvataḥ — everywhere; adhikam — more; yataḥ — since; mām — me; nija-saundarya — own beauty; āhṛta — taken; loka-avalokanam — world-watching
   What beauty did she see in this wretched servant, more than in anyone else, even if my own beauty was considered world-renowned?
   
   Verse 64
   अनुरक्तं सर्वथैव त्यक्त्वैनमुपसङ्गता ।
   एव प्रलप्य बहुधा निर्विण्णोऽतितरां तदा ॥ ६४ ॥
   anuraktaṁ sarvathaiva tyaktvainaṁ upasaṅgatā ।
   eva pralapya bahudhā nirviṇṇo'titarāṁ tadā ॥ 64 ॥
   anuraktam — attached; sarvathā — entirely; eva — indeed; tyaktvā — abandoning; enam — him; upasaṅgatā — approached; eva — thus; pralapya — lamenting; bahudhā — variously; nirviṇṇaḥ — disillusioned; atitarām — extremely; tadā — then
   Entirely attached to the servant, she abandoned me and approached him. Thus, lamenting in various ways, he became extremely disillusioned.
   
   Verse 65
   राजपुत्रो वनं प्रागात्‌ सर्वसङ्गविवर्जितः ।
   तस्माद्‌ राजकुमारैतत्‌ सौन्दर्यं मनसोत्थितम्‌ ॥ ६५ ॥
   rājaputro vanaṁ prāgāt sarvasaṅgavivarjitaḥ ।
   tasmād rājakumāraitat saundaryaṁ manasotthitam ॥ 65 ॥
   rājaputraḥ — the prince; vanam — to the forest; prāgāt — went; sarvasaṅga-vivarjitaḥ — free from all attachments; tasmāt — therefore; rājapumāra — O prince; etat — this; saundaryam — beauty; manasaḥ — of the mind; utthitam — arisen
   The prince went to the forest, free from all attachments. Therefore, O prince, understand that this beauty arises from the mind.
   
   Verse 66
   यथा त्वं मयि चात्यन्तसौभगेक्षणपूर्वकम् ।
   रतिं विन्दस्यतितरां तथा वा तद्विशेषतः ॥ ६६ ॥
   yathā tvaṁ mayi cātyanta-saubhagekṣaṇa-pūrvakam ।
   ratiṁ vindasy atitarāṁ tathā vā tad viśeṣataḥ ॥ 66 ॥
   yathā — as; tvam — you; mayi — in me; ca — and; atyanta-saubhaga — extreme beauty; īkṣaṇa — seeing; pūrvakam — formerly; ratim — pleasure; vindasi — you find; atitarām — extremely; tathā — likewise; vā — or; tat — that; viśeṣataḥ — especially
   Just as you once found extreme pleasure in me due to my exceptional beauty, so too, in the same manner,
   
   Verse 67
   विन्दन्ति रतिमत्यन्तं योषित्सु विकृतास्वपि ।
   अत्र ते प्रत्ययं वक्ष्ये शृणु प्रिय समाहितः ॥ ६७ ॥
   vindanti ratim atyantaṁ yoṣitsu vikṛtāsv api ।
   atra te pratyayaṁ vakṣye śṛṇu priya samāhitaḥ ॥ 67 ॥
   vindanti — many find; ratim — pleasure; atyantam — extremely; yoṣitsu — in women; vikṛtāsu — deformed; api — even; atra — here; te — your; pratyayam — assurance; vakṣye — I will tell; śṛṇu — listen; priya — dear; samāhitaḥ — attentively
   Many find extreme pleasure even in deformed women. Here, I will give you assurance. Listen attentively, dear.
   
   Verse 68
   विलोक्यते या हि योषित्‌ सा बहिः सुव्यवस्थिता ।
   या च तत्प्रतिबिम्बात्मरूपिणी चित्तसंश्रया ॥ ६८ ॥
   vilokyate yā hi yoṣit sā bahiḥ suvyavasthitā ।
   yā ca tatpratibimbātmarūpiṇī cittasaṁśrayā ॥ 68 ॥
   vilokyate — is seen; yā — who; hi — indeed; yoṣit — woman; sā — she; bahiḥ — externally; suvyavasthitā — well-formed; yā — who; ca — and; tat — that; pratibimba — reflection; ātma — self; rūpiṇī — form; citta—saṁśrayā — residing in the mind
   A woman is perceived as externally well-formed, but this appearance is merely a reflection of her own self-image residing in the mind.
   
   Verse 69
   सङ्कल्परुपिणी तस्याः सौष्ठवं मनसोल्लिखन् ।
   पौनःपुन्येन तदनु वाज्छामुपसमागतः ॥ ६९ ॥
   saṅkalparūpiṇī tasyāḥ sauṣṭhavaṁ manasollikhan ।
   paunaḥpunyena tadanu vācchām upasamāgataḥ ॥ 69 ॥
   saṅkalpa-rūpiṇī — in the form of desire; tasyāḥ — of her; sauṣṭhavam — beauty; manasaḥ — in the mind; ullikhan — drawn; paunaḥpunyena — repeatedly; tat-anu — after that; vācchām — desire; upasamāgataḥ — achieved
   Her beauty is repeatedly envisioned in the mind as a form of desire. Once that desire is achieved, it fulfills the mental image formed.
   
   Verse 70
   क्षुब्धेन्द्रियो नरस्तस्यां रतिमाप्नोति सर्वतः ।
   अक्षुब्धे त्विन्द्रिये न स्यात्‌ सुन्दर्यामपि वै रतिः ॥ ७० ॥
   kṣubdhendriyo naras tasyāṁ ratim āpnoti sarvataḥ ।
   akṣubdhe tv indriye na syāt sundaryām api vai ratiḥ ॥ 70 ॥
   kṣubdha-indriyaḥ — agitated senses; naraḥ — man; tasyām — in her; ratim — pleasure; āpnoti — obtains; sarvataḥ — everywhere; akṣubdhe — unagitated; tu — indeed; indriye — senses; na syāt — would not be; sundaryām — in beauty; api — even; vai — indeed; ratiḥ — pleasure
   A man with agitated senses finds pleasure in her everywhere. However, if his senses are calm, he would not derive pleasure even from her beauty.
   
   Verse 71
   तत्र मूल समुल्लेख: सौष्ठवस्य पुनः पुनः ।
   अतः क्षोभो नैव दृष्टो बालानां योगिनामपि ॥ ७१ ॥
   tatra mūla samullekhaḥ sauṣṭhavasya punaḥ punaḥ ।
   ataḥ kṣobho naiva dṛṣṭo bālānāṁ yoginām api ॥ 71 ॥
   tatra — there; mūla — root; samullekhaḥ — description; sauṣṭhavasya — of beauty; punaḥ punaḥ — again and again; ataḥ — therefore; kṣobhaḥ — agitation; na — not; eva — indeed; dṛṣṭaḥ — seen; bālānām — of children; yoginām — of yogis; api — even
   The constant reiteration of her beauty is the root cause of agitation. However, this agitation is not observed in children or even in yogis.
   
   Verse 72
   तथा च यो यो यस्यां तु रति विन्दति मानवः ।
   सुदर्यां वापि चान्यस्यां तत्र सौष्ठवमुल्लिखेत् ॥ ७२ ॥
   tathā ca yo yo yasyāṁ tu rati vindati mānavaḥ ।
   sundaryām vāpi cānyasyāṁ tatra sauṣṭhavam ullikhet ॥ 72 ॥
   tathā — similarly; ca — and; yaḥ yaḥ — whoever; yasyām — in whom; tu — indeed; rati — pleasure; vindati — finds; mānavaḥ — man; sundaryām — in a beautiful one; vā — or; api — also; ca — and; anyasyām — in another; tatra — there; sauṣṭhavam — beauty; ullikhet — describes
   Likewise, a man describes beauty wherever he finds pleasure, whether in a beautiful person or someone else.
   
   Verse 73
   दृश्यन्ते योषितोऽत्यन्तबीभत्साकारविग्रहाः ।
   तरुणैः संगतास्ताश्च दृश्यन्तेऽपत्यहेतुतुः ॥ ७३ ॥
   dṛśyante yoṣito'tyantabībhat-sākāravigrahāḥ ।
   taruṇaiḥ saṁgatās tāś ca dṛśyante'patyahetutaḥ ॥ 73 ॥
   dṛśyante — seen; yoṣitaḥ — women; atyanta — extremely; bībhat-sākāra-vigrahāḥ — ugly form; taruṇaiḥ — with young men; saṁgatāḥ — associated; tāḥ — they; ca — and; dṛśyante — seen; apatyahetutaḥ — for the sake of children
   Women with unattractive forms are often seen associated with young men for the sake of having children.
   
   Verse 74
   विरूपतोल्लेखनं वाप्यनुल्लेखस्तु सौष्ठवे ।
   यदि स्यात्तत्‌ कथं नृणां रतिस्तासु हि सम्भवेत्‌ ॥ ७४ ॥
   virūpatollikhanaṁ vāpy anullekhastu sauṣṭhave ।
   yadi syāt tat kathaṁ nṛṇāṁ ratistāsu hi sambhavet ॥ 74 ॥
   virūpatollikhanam — description of deformity; vā — or; api — also; anullekhaḥ — non-description; tu — indeed; sauṣṭhave — in beauty; yadi — if; syāt — would be; tat — that; katham — how; nṛṇām — of men; ratiḥ — pleasure; tāsu — in them; hi — indeed; sambhavet — would happen
   If there is an emphasis on deformity or a lack of praise for beauty, how could men find pleasure in either?
   
   Verse 75
   किं वक्तव्यमहो नृणां कामिनां क्षिप्तचेतसाम्‌ ।
   जघन्याङ्गेऽपि सौन्दर्य भासते सर्वतोऽधिकम्‌ ॥ ७५ ॥
   kiṁ vaktavyam aho nṛṇāṁ kāmināṁ kṣiptacetāsām ।
   jaghanyāṅge'pi saundarya bhāsate sarvato'dhikam ॥ 75 ॥
   kim — what; vaktavyam — to be said; aho — alas; nṛṇām — of men; kāminām — of lustful ones; kṣipta-cetāsām — of distracted minds; jaghanya-aṅge — even in inferior parts; api — also; saundarya — beauty; bhāsate — shines; sarvataḥ — everywhere; adhikam — more
   What can be said, alas, of men with lustful, distracted minds? Beauty seems to shine everywhere, even in the least attractive parts.
   
   Verse 76
   मलमूत्रपरिक्लिन्नं यदङ्गं तत्र सौभगम्‌ ।
   पश्येच्चेत् कुत्र नो पश्येत् सौन्दर्य तन्भमेरय ॥ ७६ ॥
   malamūtra-pariklinnam yadaṅgaṁ tatra saubhagam ।
   paśyec cet kutra no paśyet saundarya tanmaheraya ॥ 76 ॥
   mala-mūtra-pariklinnam — smeared with filth and urine; yat — which; aṅgam — part; tatra — there; saubhagam — beauty; paśyet — sees; cet — if; kutra — where; na — not; paśyet — sees; saundarya — beauty; tanmaheraya — shining there
   If someone finds beauty even in parts smeared with filth and urine, then where would beauty not shine?
   
   Verse 77
   तस्मात्‌ सौन्दर्यमेतद्वै राजपुत्र निशामय ।
   अभिमानमृते नैष सुखहैतुर्भवेत् क्वचित् ॥ ७७ ॥
   tasmāt saundaryam etad vai rājaputra niśāmaya ।
   abhimānamṛte naiṣa sukhahaitur bhavet kvacit ॥ 77 ॥
   tasmāt — therefore; saundaryam — beauty; etad — this; vai — indeed; rājaputra — O prince; niśāmaya — observe; abhimānamṛte — without pride; naiṣa — this; sukhahaituḥ — cause of happiness; bhavet — would be; kvacit — anywhere
   Therefore, observe this beauty, O prince. Without pride, it can never be the cause of happiness anywhere.
   
   Verse 78
   क्षौद्रमाधुर्यवद् देहे सौन्दर्यं सहयं यदि ।
   तद्बालानां कुमाराणां कुंतो नो भाति तद्वद ॥ ७८ ॥
   kṣaudramādhuryavad dehe saundaryaṁ sahayaṁ yadi ।
   tad bālānāṁ kumārāṇāṁ kuto no bhāti tadvad ॥ 78 ॥
   kṣaudra-mādhurya-vat — like the sweetness of honey; dehe — in the body; saundaryam — beauty; sahayam — with; yadi — if; tad — that; bālānām — of children; kumārāṇām — of boys; kuto — where; no — not; bhāti — shines; tadvad — like that
   If beauty in the body is like the sweetness of honey, then why does it not shine in children or boys in the same way?
   
   Verse 79
   देशभेदेषु दृश्यन्ते विविधाकृतयो नराः ।
   एकपादैकनयना लम्बकर्णा हयाननाः ॥ ७९ ॥
   deśabhedeṣu dṛśyante vividhākṛtayo narāḥ ।
   ekapādaikanayanā lambakarṇā hayānanāḥ ॥ 79 ॥
   deśa-bhedeṣu — in different regions; dṛśyante — are seen; vividha-ākṛtayaḥ — various forms; narāḥ — men; eka-pāda — one-legged; eka-nayanā — one-eyed; lamba-karṇā — long-eared; haya-ānanāḥ — horse-faced
   In different regions, men with various physical forms are observed: one-legged, one-eyed, long-eared, and horse-faced.
   
   Verse 80
   कर्णप्रावरणाः फालवक्त्रा निर्गतदंष्ट्रकाः ।
   विनसा दीर्घनासाश्च लोमच्छन्ना विलोमकाः ॥ ८० ॥
   karṇaprāvaraṇāḥ phālavaktrā nirgatadaṁṣṭrakāḥ ।
   vināsā dīrghanāsāś ca lomacchannā vilomakāḥ ॥ 80 ॥
   karṇa-prāvaraṇāḥ — ear-covered; phāla-vaktrā — forehead-faced; nirgatadaṁṣṭrakāḥ — protruding teeth; vināsā — without nose; dīrgha-nāsāḥ — long-nosed; ca — and; loma-cchannā — covered with hair; vilomakāḥ — reverse-haired
   Covered in hair, reverse-haired, with ears over the forehead, protruding teeth, without a nose, or with long noses.
   
   Verse 81
   पिङ्गकेशाः श्वेतकेशा विकेशाः स्थूलकेशकाः ।
   श्वित्रवर्णाः काकवर्णाः पिङ्गला लोहिताङ्गकाः ॥ ८१ ॥
   piṅgakeśāḥ śvetakeśā vikeśāḥ sthūlakeśakāḥ ।
   śvitravarṇāḥ kākavarṇāḥ piṅgalā lohitāṅgakāḥ ॥ 81 ॥
   piṅga-keśāḥ — with tawny hair; śveta-keśāḥ — with white hair; vikeśāḥ — disheveled hair; sthūla-keśakāḥ — thick-haired; śvitra-varṇāḥ — with leprosy spots; kākavarṇāḥ — crow-colored; piṅgalā — yellowish; lohitāṅgakāḥ — reddish-bodied
   With tawny hair, white hair, disheveled hair, thick hair, leprosy spots, crow-colored skin, yellowish, and reddish-bodied.
   
   Verse 82
   एवं बहुविधा मर्त्याः सजातिवनितासु ते ।
   रति विन्दन्ति त्वमिव राजपुत्र निशामय ॥ ८२ ॥
   evaṁ bahuvidhā martyāḥ sajātivanitāsu te ।
   rati vindanti tvam iva rājaputra niśāmaya ॥ 82 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; bahuvidhā — various; martyāḥ — mortals; sajāti — same species; vanitāsu — among women; te — they; rati — pleasure; vindanti — find; tvam — you; iva — like; rājaputra — O prince; niśāmaya — observe
   Thus, various mortals find pleasure among women of their own kind. Observe this, O prince.
   
   Verse 83
   सुखसाधनभूतेषु मुख्यं यत्‌ स्त्रीवपुः स्थितम्‌ ।
   सर्वप्रियं यत्र सर्वे मुह्यन्ति विबुधा अपि ॥ ८३ ॥
   sukhasādhanabhūteṣu mukhyaṁ yat strīvapuḥ sthitam ।
   sarvapriyaṁ yatra sarve muhyanti vibudhā api ॥ 83 ॥
   sukha-sādhana-bhūteṣu — in sources of pleasure; mukhyam — main; yat — which; strī-vapuḥ — female form; sthitam — established; sarvapriyam — dear to all; yatra — where; sarve — all; muhyanti — are deluded; vibudhāḥ — wise ones; api — even
   In sources of pleasure, the primary one is the female form, cherished by all, where even the wise are led astray.
   
   Verse 84
   पुंसां वपुस्तथा स्त्रीणां प्रियमत्यन्तसुन्दरम्‌ ।
   विमर्शय सुबुद्धया त्वं राजपुत्र यथास्थितम्‌ ॥ ८४ ॥
   puṁsāṁ vapuḥ tathā strīṇāṁ priyamatyantasundaram ।
   vimarśaya subuddhayā tvaṁ rājaputra yathāsthitam ॥ 84 ॥
   puṁsām — of men; vapuḥ — form; tathā — likewise; strīṇām — of women; priyam — dear; atyanta-sundaram — extremely beautiful; vimarśaya — consider; su-buddhayā — with good intellect; tvam — you; rājaputra — O prince; yathā-sthitam — as it is
   Likewise, consider the forms of men and women, immensely beautiful and cherished, endowed with good intellect, as they are, O prince.
   
   Verse 85
   मांसलिप्तमसृक्क्लिन्नं शिराबद्धं त्वगाततम् ।
   अस्थिपञ्जरकं लोमच्छन्नं पित्तकफाहितम्‌ ॥ ८५ ॥
   māṁsaliptam asṛkklinnaṁ śirābaddhaṁ tvagātatam ।
   asthi-pañjarakaṁ lomacchannaṁ pitta-kaphāhitam ॥ 85 ॥
   māṁsa-liptam — smeared with flesh; asṛk-klinnam — soaked in blood; śirā-baddham — bound by veins; tvak-ātatam — covered with skin; asthi-pañjarakam — skeleton; loma-channam — covered with hair; pitta-kapha-āhitam — filled with bile and phlegm
   Smeared with flesh, soaked in blood, bound by veins, covered with skin, a skeleton covered with hair, filled with bile and phlegm.
   
   Verse 86
   मलमूत्रकुसूलं तच्छुक्रशोणितसम्भवम्‌ ।
   मूत्रद्वारसमुद्भूतमहो प्रियमिहेष्यते ॥ ८६ ॥
   mala-mūtrakusūlaṁ tac-chukraśoṇitasambhavam ।
   mūtradvārasamudbhūtam aho priyam iheṣyate ॥ 86 ॥
   mala-mūtra-kusūlam — filled with filth and urine; tat — that; śukra-śoṇita-sambhavam — born of semen and blood; mūtra-dvāra-samudbhūtam — arising from the urinary passage; aho — alas; priyam — dear; iha — here; iṣyate — desired
   Filled with filth and urine, born of semen and blood, arising from the urinary passage—alas, this is what is desired here.
   
   Verse 87
   य एवमतिबीभत्से वितन्वन्ति रति नराः ।
   विट्कृमिभ्यः कुतस्तेषां भवेदन्तरमीरय ॥ ८७ ॥
   ya evam atibībhatse vitanvanti rati narāḥ ।
   viṭkṛmibhyaḥ kutas teṣāṁ bhaved antaram īraya ॥ 87 ॥
   yaḥ — who; evam — thus; ati-bībhatse — extremely repulsive; vitanvanti — indulge in; rati — pleasure; narāḥ — men; viṭ-kṛmibhyaḥ — from worms in excrement; kutaḥ — where; teṣām — their; bhavet — would be; antaram — difference; īraya — tell
   Men who indulge in pleasure under such extremely repulsive conditions—tell me, how are they different from worms in excrement?
   
   Verse 88
   राजपुत्र तनुरियं प्रिया हि नितरां तव ।
   विभावय विवेकेन धातूनां च पृथक्स्थितिम्‌ ॥ ८८ ॥
   rājaputra tanur iyaṁ priyā hi nitarāṁ tava ।
   vibhāvaya vivekena dhātūnāṁ ca pṛthaksthitim ॥ 88 ॥
   rājaputra — O prince; tanuḥ — body; iyam — this; priyā — dear; hi — indeed; nitarām — extremely; tava — to you; vibhāvaya — consider; vivekena — with discernment; dhātūnām — of the elements; ca — and; pṛthaksthitim — separate existence
   O prince, this body is extremely dear to you. Consider with discernment the separate existence of its elements.
   
   Verse 89
   एवमन्यत्रोपयोज्ये मधुराम्लादिषड्रसे ।
   परिणामस्वभावं तु सूक्ष्मदृष्ट्या विभावय ॥ ८९ ॥
   evam anyatro payojye madhurāmlādiṣaḍrase ।
   pariṇāmasvabhāvaṁ tu sūkṣmadṛṣṭyā vibhāvaya ॥ 89 ॥
   evam — thus; anyatra — elsewhere; upayojye — to be used; madhura-amla-ādi-ṣaṭ-rase — in sweet, sour, etc. six tastes; pariṇāma-svabhāvam — nature of transformation; tu — indeed; sūkṣma-dṛṣṭyā — with subtle vision; vibhāvaya — consider
   Thus, consider the nature of sweet, sour, and other tastes. Similarly, reflect on the six tastes elsewhere. Indeed, view them with a subtle vision.
   
   Verse 90
   भक्षितस्यापि सर्वश्य विड्भावः परिणामके ।
   सर्वथा नात्र सन्देहः सर्वैरेव विभावितः ॥ ९० ॥
   bhakṣitasyāpi sarvasya viḍbhāvaḥ pariṇāmake ।
   sarvathā nātra sandehaḥ sarvaireva vibhāvitaḥ ॥ 90 ॥
   bhakṣitasya — of what is eaten; api — even; sarvasya — of all; viḍ-bhāvaḥ — state of excrement; pariṇāmake — in transformation; sarvathā — in every way; na — not; atra — here; sandehaḥ — doubt; sarvaiḥ — by all; eva — indeed; vibhāvitaḥ — realized
   Even the food that is eaten, in every way, ultimately transforms into excrement, a truth known by all without doubt.
   
   Verse 91
   वदैवं संस्थिते लोके किं प्रियं स्यात् किमप्रियम्‌ ।
   इत्युक्तो हेमचूडोऽथ वैरस्यं विषये विदन्‌ ॥ ९१ ॥
   vadaivaṁ saṁsthite loke kiṁ priyaṁ syāt kim apriyam ।
   ity ukto hemacūḍo'tha vairasyaṁ viṣaye vidan ॥ 91 ॥
   vada — tell; evam — thus; saṁsthite — established; loke — in the world; kim — what; priyam — dear; syāt — would be; kim — what; apriyam — not dear; iti — thus; uktaḥ — spoken; hemacūḍaḥ — Hemacuda; atha — then; vairasyam — indifference; viṣaye — in the subject; vidan — realizing
   Tell me, thus established in the world, what would be dear and what not dear? Thus spoken, Hemachuda then realized indifference in the subject.
   
   Verse 92
   श्रुत्वाऽपूर्वं वाक्यजालं विस्मितोऽभवदञ्जसा ।
   विचार्यं भूयस्तत्सर्व यदुक्तं हेमलेखया ॥ ९२ ॥
   śrutvā'pūrvaṁ vākyajālaṁ vismito'bhavad añjasā ।
   vicāryaṁ bhūyas tat sarva yad uktaṁ hemalekhayā ॥ 92 ॥
   śrutvā — hearing; apūrvam — unprecedented; vākyajālam — speech; vismitaḥ — astonished; abhavat — became; añjasā — immediately; vicāryaṁ — reflecting; bhūyaḥ — again; tat — that; sarvam — all; yat — what; uktam — said; hemalekhayā — by Hemalekha
   Upon hearing the unprecedented speech, he was immediately astonished and reflected deeply on everything Hemalekha had said.
   
   Verse 93
   भोगेषु जातनिर्वेदः परं वैराग्यमाप्तवान्‌ ।
   अथ क्रमेण पृष्ट्वा तां प्रियां ज्ञात्वा च तत्पदम्‌ ॥ ९३ ॥
   bhogeṣu jāta-nirvedaḥ paraṁ vairāgyam āptavān ।
   atha krameṇa pṛṣṭvā tāṁ priyāṁ jñātvā ca tat padam ॥ 93 ॥
   bhogeṣu — in pleasures; jāta-nirvedaḥ — with arisen disinterest; param — supreme; vairāgyam — detachment; āptavān — attained; atha — then; krameṇa — gradually; pṛṣṭvā — asking; tām — her; priyām — beloved; jñātvā — knowing; ca — and; tat — that; padam — state
   With disinterest in pleasures now arisen, he attained supreme detachment. Then, gradually, he asked his beloved, seeking to understand that state.
   
   Verse 94
   केवला चितिमात्मस्थां त्रिपुरामात्मरूपिणीम्‌ ।
   बुध्वाऽभवद्‌ विमुक्तात्मा स्वात्मभूताखिलेक्षणः ॥ ९४ ॥
   kevalā citim ātmasthāṁ tripurām ātmarūpiṇīm ।
   budhvā'bhavad vimuktātmā svātmabhūtākhilekṣaṇaḥ ॥ 94 ॥
   kevalāṁ — alone; citim — consciousness; ātmasthām — established in the self; tripurām — Tripura; ātma-rūpiṇīm — in the form of the self; budhvā — realizing; abhavat — became; vimuktātmā — liberated soul; svātma-bhūta-akhilekṣaṇaḥ — seeing everything as self
   Realizing the consciousness established in the self, Tripura as the essence of the self, he became a liberated soul, perceiving everything as the self.
   
   Verse 95
   जीवन्मुक्तः समभवत्‌ ततस्तस्यानुजोऽपि हि ।
   मणिचूडोऽविदद्‌ भ्रातुर्मुक्ताचूडोऽपि पुत्रतः ॥ ९५ ॥
   jīvanmuktaḥ samabhavat tatas tasyānujo'pi hi ।
   maṇicūḍo'vidad bhrātur muktācūḍo'pi putrataḥ ॥ 95 ॥
   jīvanmuktaḥ — liberated while living; samabhavat — became; tataḥ — then; tasya — his; anujaḥ — younger brother; api — also; hi — indeed; maṇicūḍaḥ — Manicuda; avidad — realized; bhrātuḥ — of the brother; muktācūḍaḥ — Muktacuda; api — also; putrataḥ — from the son
   He attained liberation while living. Following him, his younger brother Manicuda also realized this truth through his brother's guidance. Subsequently, Muktacuda too realized it from his son.
   
   Verse 96
   मणिताचूडप्रिया चापि स्नुषया ज्ञानमासदत्‌ ।
   मन्त्रिणश्चापि पौराश्च बभूवुर्ज्ञानशालिनः ॥ ९६ ॥
   maṇitācūḍapriyā cāpi snuṣayā jñānam āsadat ।
   mantriṇaś cāpi paurāś ca babhūvur jñānaśālinaḥ ॥ 96 ॥
   maṇitācūḍa-priyā — Manicuda's beloved; ca — and; api — also; snuṣayā — by the daughter-in-law; jñānam — knowledge; āsadat — attained; mantriṇaḥ — ministers; ca — and; api — also; paurāḥ — citizens; ca — and; babhūvuḥ — became; jñānaśālinaḥ — full of knowledge
   Manicuda’s beloved also attained knowledge from the daughter-in-law. Ministers and citizens too became enlightened.
   
   Verse 97
   न तत्र नगरे कश्चिदविद्वान् समजायत ।
   आसीद्‌ ब्रह्मपुरप्रख्यं शान्तसंसृतिवासनम्‌ ॥ ९७ ॥
   na tatra nagare kaścid avidvān samajāyata ।
   āsīd brahmapuraprakhyaṁ śāntasaṁsṛtivāsanam ॥ 97 ॥
   na — not; tatra — there; nagare — in the city; kaścit — anyone; avidvān — ignorant; samajāyata — was born; āsīt — became; brahma-pura-prakhyam — known as Brahma's city; śānta-saṁsṛti-vāsanam — abode of peaceful cycles of birth and death
   No one in that city was born ignorant. It became known as Brahma’s city, an abode of peaceful cycles of birth and death.
   
   Verse 98
   विशालनगरं तच्च जगत्यत्युत्तम बभौ ।
   यत्र कीराः शारिकाश्च पञ्जरस्थाः पठन्ति वै ॥ ९८ ॥
   viśālanagaraṁ tacca jagaty atyuttama babhau ।
   yatra kīrāḥ śārikāś ca pañjarasthāḥ paṭhanti vai ॥ 98 ॥
   viśāla-nagaram — great city; tat — that; ca — and; jagati — in the world; atyuttama — very excellent; babhau — appeared; yatra — where; kīrāḥ — parrots; śārikāḥ — mynah birds; ca — and; pañjara-sthāḥ — in cages; paṭhanti — recite; vai — indeed
   That great city stood out brilliantly in the world, where even parrots and mynah birds recited scriptures from their cages.
   
   Verse 99
   चितिरूपं स्वमात्मानं भजध्वं चेत्यवर्जितम् ।
   नास्ति चेत्यं चितेरन्यद्‌ दर्पणप्रतिबिम्बवत्‌ ॥ ९९ ॥
   citirūpaṁ svamātmānaṁ bhajadhvaṁ cetyavarjitam ।
   nāsti cetyaṁ citer anyad darpaṇapratibimbavat ॥ 99 ॥
   citi-rūpam — form of consciousness; svam — own; ātmānam — self; bhajadhvam — worship; ceti — awareness; avarjitam — without; nāsti — there is not; cetyaṁ — awareness; citeḥ — of consciousness; anyat — other; darpaṇa-pratibimba-vat — like a mirror's reflection
   Worship your own self as the embodiment of consciousness, devoid of any external awareness. There is no awareness separate from consciousness, just as a reflection in a mirror is not separate from the mirror itself.
   
   Verse 100
   चितिश्चेत्यं चितिरहं चितिः सर्व चराचरम्‌ ।
   यतः सर्वं चितिमनु भाति सा तु स्वतन्त्रतः ॥ १०० ॥
   citiś cetyaṁ citir ahaṁ citiḥ sarva carācaram ।
   yataḥ sarvaṁ citim anu bhāti sā tu svatantrataḥ ॥ 100 ॥
   citiḥ — consciousness; cetyam — awareness; citiḥ — I am; citiḥ — consciousness; sarva — all; cara-acaram — moving and non-moving; yataḥ — since; sarvam — all; citim anu — follows consciousness; bhāti — shines; sā — it; tu — indeed; svatantrataḥ — independently
   I am consciousness, pure awareness. All moving and non-moving entities follow and are illuminated by consciousness, shining independently in its presence.
   
   Verse 101
   अतश्चितिं जनाः सर्वे भासिनीं सर्वसंश्रयाम्‌ ।
   भजध्वं भ्रान्तिमुत्सुज्य चितिमात्रसुदृष्टयः ॥ १०१ ॥
   ataś citiṁ janāḥ sarve bhāsinīṁ sarvasaṁśrayām ।
   bhajadhvaṁ bhrāntim utsṛjya citimātrasudṛṣṭayaḥ ॥ 101 ॥
   ataḥ — therefore; citiṁ — consciousness; janāḥ — people; sarve — all; bhāsinīm — shining; sarvasaṁśrayām — all-pervading; bhajadhvaṁ — worship; bhrāntim — delusion; utsṛjya — abandoning; citimātra — pure consciousness; sudṛṣṭayaḥ — with clear vision
   Therefore, people, abandon delusion and worship the all—encompassing, radiant consciousness with a clear vision of pure awareness.
   
   Verse 102
   कदाचिदेवं कीराणां श्रुत्वा वाक्यं महोदयम्‌ ।
   ब्राह्मणा वामदेवाद्या नामाचख्युः पुरस्य तु ॥ १०२ ॥
   kadācid evaṁ kīrāṇāṁ śrutvā vākyaṁ mahodayam ।
   brāhmaṇā vāmadevādya nāmācakhyuḥ purasya tu ॥ 102 ॥
   kadācit — once; evam — thus; kīrāṇām — of the parrots; śrutvā — hearing; vākyam — speech; mahodayam — magnificent; brāhmaṇāḥ — the Brahmins; vāmadeva-ādyā — starting with Vamadeva; nāma — name; ācakhyuḥ — announced; purasya — of the city; tu — indeed
   Once, upon hearing the magnificent speech of the parrots, the Brahmins, led by Vamadeva, proclaimed the name of the city.
   
   Verse 103
   यतोऽत्र विद्यां तिर्यञ्चोऽप्याहुस्तस्मादिदं पुरम्‌ ।
   प्रसिद्धविद्यानगरमिति नाम्ना प्रसिध्यतु ॥ १०३ ॥
   yato'tra vidyāṁ tiryañco'py āhus tasmād idaṁ puram ।
   prasiddhavidyānagaram iti nāmnā prasidhyatu ॥ 103 ॥
   yataḥ — because; atra — here; vidyām — knowledge; tiryañcaḥ — even the animals; āhuḥ — recite; tasmāt — therefore; idam — this; puram — city; prasiddhavidyānagaram — famous city of knowledge; iti — thus; nāmnā — by name; prasidhyatu — be renowned
   Since even the animals here recite knowledge, let this city be renowned as the 'Famous City of Knowledge.'
   
   Verse 104
   तदद्यापि च तेनैव नाम्ना तन्नगरं स्थितम्‌ ।
   राम तस्मात्तु सत्सङ्गो मूलं सर्वशुभोदये ॥ १०४ ॥
   tad adyāpi ca tenaiva nāmnā tan nagaraṁ sthitam ।
   rāma tasmāt tu satsango mūlaṁ sarvaśubhodaye ॥ 104 ॥
   tat — that; adyāpi — even today; ca — and; tenaiva — by that; nāmnā — name; tat — that; nagaram — city; sthitam — established; rāma — O Rama; tasmāt — therefore; tu — indeed; sat—saṅgaḥ — association with the good; mūlam — root; sarva-śubha-udaye — for all auspiciousness
   Even today, that city retains its name. O Rama, this is why association with the virtuous is indeed the foundation for all auspiciousness.
   
   Verse 105
   सङ्गेन हेमलेखायाः सर्वे विद्याविदोऽभवन्‌ ।
   तस्मात्‌ सङ्गः परं मूलं राम जानीहि श्रेयसः ॥ १०५ ॥
   saṅgena hemalekhāyāḥ sarve vidyāvido'bhavan ।
   tasmāt saṅgaḥ paraṁ mūlaṁ rāma jānīhi śreyasaḥ ॥ 105 ॥
   saṅgena — by the association; hemalekhāyāḥ — with Hemalekha; sarve — all; vidyāvidaḥ — knowledgeable; abhavan — became; tasmāt — therefore; saṅgaḥ — association; param — supreme; mūlam — root; rāma — O Rama; jānīhi — know; śreyasaḥ — for prosperity
   By associating with Hemalekha, everyone gained knowledge. Therefore, O Rama, understand that such association is the ultimate root of prosperity.



   इति श्रीत्रिपुरारहस्ये ज्ञानखण्डे हेमचूडोपाख्याने  सत्सङ्गफलं चतुर्थोऽध्यायः ॥
   
   Thus ends the fourth chapter on the “Fruit of Association with the Good” in the Story of Hemachuda in the Knowledge Section of the revered Tripura Rahasya.
   

5. STORY OF BONDAGE IN TALE OF HEMACHUDA
   Verse 1
   एवं सत्सङ्गमाहात्म्यं श्रुत्वाऽत्रिसुतभाषितम्‌ ।
   प्रहृष्टमानसो भूयः प्रष्टुमेवोपचक्रमे ॥ १ ॥
   evaṁ satsaṅgamāhātmyaṁ śrutvā'trisutabhāṣitam ।
   prahṛṣṭamānaso bhūyaḥ praṣṭum evopacakrame ॥ 1 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; sat-saṅga-māhātmyam — greatness of good company; śrutvā — hearing; atri-suta-bhāṣitam — spoken by the son of Atri; prahṛṣṭa-mānasaḥ — delighted in mind; bhūyaḥ — again; praṣṭum — to ask; eva — indeed; upacakrame — commenced
   Hearing about the greatness of good company from the son of Atri, Rama was delighted in mind and began to ask further questions.
   
   Verse 2
   सत्यं प्रोक्तमिदं नाथ भवता शुभकारणम्‌ ।
   सत्सङ्गरूपमेतच्च प्रत्यक्षेणैव भावितम्‌ ॥ २ ॥
   satyaṁ proktam idaṁ nātha bhavatā śubhakāraṇam ।
   satsaṅgarūpam etac ca pratyakṣeṇaiva bhāvitam ॥ 2 ॥
   satyaṁ — true; proktam — spoken; idam — this; nātha — O lord; bhavatā — by you; śubhakāraṇam — cause of auspiciousness; sat-saṅga-rūpam — in the form of good company; etat — this; ca — and; pratyakṣeṇa — by direct experience; eva — indeed; bhāvitam — realized
   What you say is true, O lord, as the cause of auspiciousness, this form of good company is indeed realized through direct experience.
   
   Verse 3
   यो यथा सङ्गमाप्नोति फलं तस्य तथा भवेत्‌ ।
   स्त्रियोऽपि हैमलेखायाः सङ्गात् सर्वे महाफलाः ॥ ३ ॥
   yo yathā saṅgam āpnoti phalaṁ tasya tathā bhavet ।
   striyo'pi haimalekhayāḥ saṅgāt sarve mahāphalāḥ ॥ 3 ॥
   yaḥ — who; yathā — as; saṅgam — association; āpnoti — obtains; phalam — fruit; tasya — of that; tathā — so; bhavet — would be; striyaḥ — women; api — also; haimalekhayāḥ — of Hemalekha; saṅgāt — by association; sarve — all; mahāphalāḥ — great fruits
   As one attains association, so would be the fruit of that. Women, through their association with Hemalekha, also obtained great benefits.
   
   Verse 4
   भूय इच्छाम्यहं श्रोतुं हेमचूडस्तया कथम्‌ ।
   बोधितस्तन्ममाचक्ष्व विस्तरेण दयानिधे ॥ ४ ॥
   bhūya icchāmy ahaṁ śrotuṁ hemacūḍas tayā katham ।
   bodhitas tan mamācakṣva vistareṇa dayānidhe ॥ 4 ॥
   bhūyaḥ — again; icchāmi — I desire; ahaṁ — I; śrotum — to hear; hemacūḍaḥ — Hemacuda; tayā — by her; katham — how; bodhitaḥ — enlightened; tat — that; mama — to me; ācakṣva — tell; vistareṇa — in detail; dayānidhe — O ocean of compassion
   Again, I desire to hear how Hemachuda was enlightened by her. Please tell me that in detail, O ocean of compassion.
   
   Verse 5
   एवं रामेणानुयुक्तो दत्तात्रेय उवाच तम्‌ ।
   शृणु भार्गव वक्ष्यामि कथां परमपावनीम्‌ ॥ ५ ॥
   evaṁ rāmeṇānuyukto dattātreya uvāca tam ।
   śṛṇu bhārgava vakṣyāmi kathāṁ paramapāvanīm ॥ 5 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; rāmeṇa — by Rama; anuyuktaḥ — questioned; dattātreyaḥ — Dattatreya; uvāca — spoke; tam — to him; śṛṇu — listen; bhārgava — O descendant of Bhrigu; vakṣyāmi — I will tell; kathām — story; paramapāvanīm — supremely purifying
   Thus questioned by Rama, Dattatreya spoke to him. "Listen, O descendant of Bhrigu, I will tell you the supremely purifying story."
   
   Verse 6
   एवं तस्या वचः श्रुत्वा विषयान्‌ विरसान्‌ विदन्‌ ।
   तेषु सञ्जातनिर्वेदो विमना इव संबभौ ॥ ६ ॥
   evaṁ tasyā vacaḥ śrutvā viṣayān virasān vidan ।
   teṣu sañjātanirvedo vimanā iva saṁbabhau ॥ 6 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; tasyāḥ — her; vacaḥ — words; śrutvā — hearing; viṣayān — objects; virasān — tasteless; vidan — knowing; teṣu — in them; sañjāta—nirvedaḥ — disinterested; vimanāḥ — disheartened; iva — as if; saṁbabhau — became
   Thus, hearing her words and realizing the objects to be devoid of real essence, he became disinterested and disheartened.
   
   Verse 7
   चिरस्थितविषयजवासनानां वशं गतः ।
   त्यक्तुं वा संग्रहीतुं वा नाशकत्‌ सहसा हि सः ॥ ७ ॥
   cirasthitaviṣayajavāsanānāṁ vaśaṁ gataḥ ।
   tyaktuṁ vā saṁgrahītuṁ vā nāśakat sahasā hi saḥ ॥ 7 ॥
