   Immersed in the ocean of bliss, she became that instantly. Thus, you too should control the bad conduct arising from your friend.
   
   Verse 142
   प्राप्य स्वमातरं नाथ सुखं नित्यं समाप्नुहि ।
   एतत्ते कथितं नाथ स्वानुभूतं सुखास्पदम्‌ ॥ १४२ ॥
   prāpya sva-mātaraṁ nātha sukhaṁ nityaṁ samāpnuhī ।
   etat te kathitaṁ nātha sva-anubhūtaṁ sukha-āspadam ॥ 142 ॥
   prāpya — obtaining; sva-mātaraṁ — your mother; nātha — lord; sukhaṁ — happiness; nityaṁ — always; samāpnuhī — obtain; etat — this; te — to you; kathitaṁ — told; nātha — lord; sva-anubhūtaṁ — self-experienced; sukha-āspadam — source of happiness
   By obtaining your mother, Lord, you will always find happiness. This is shared with you, Lord, as a source of happiness I have experienced myself.


   
   इति श्रीत्रिपुरारहस्ये ज्ञानखण्डे हेमचूडोपाख्याने बन्धाख्यायिका पञ्चमोऽध्यायः॥
   
   Thus ends the fifth chapter on the “Story of Bondage in the tale of Hemachuda” in the Knowledge Section of the revered Tripura Rahasya.
   

6. PRAISE OF FAITH
   Verse 1
   एवं प्रियावचः श्रुत्वा हेमचूडोऽतिविस्मितः ।
   हसन्‌ पप्रच्छ तां कान्तामविद्वान्‌ विदुषीं तदा ॥ १ ॥
   evaṁ priyā-vacaḥ śrutvā hemacūḍo 'ti-vismitaḥ ।
   hasan papraccha tāṁ kāntām avidvān viduṣīṁ tadā ॥ 1 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; priyā-vacaḥ — sweet words; śrutvā — hearing; hemacūḍaḥ — Hemachuda; ati-vismitaḥ — very surprised; hasan — laughing; papraccha — asked; tāṁ — her; kāntām — dear; avidvān — ignorant; viduṣīṁ — wise; tadā — then
   Hearing these sweet words, Hemachuda, very surprised and still ignorant, laughed and asked his dear and wise companion.
   
   Verse 2
   प्रिये प्रोक्तं यदेतत्ते खचित्रमिव भाति मे ।
   निरालम्बं वचस्तेऽद्य जानाम्येतदशेषतः ॥ २ ॥
   priye proktaṁ yad etat te khacitram iva bhāti me ।
   nirālambaṁ vacas te 'dya jānāmy etad aśeṣataḥ ॥ 2 ॥
   priye — dear; proktam — spoken; yat — which; etat — this; te — your; khacitram — strange; iva — like; bhāti — appears; me — to me; nirālambaṁ — unsupported; vacaḥ — words; te — your; adya — today; jānāmi — I understand; etad — this; aśeṣataḥ — completely
   Dear, what you have spoken seems strange to me and unsupported; today, I understand this completely.
   
   Verse 3
   नूनं त्वमप्सरोद्भूता ऋषिणा वर्द्धिता वने ।
   संस्पृष्टयौवनाद्यापि न तारुण्यमलं गता ॥ ३ ॥
   nūnaṁ tvam apsarodbhootā ṛṣiṇā vardhitā vane ।
   saṁspṛṣṭa-yauvanād yāpi na tāruṇyam alaṁ gatā ॥ 3 ॥
   nūnam — surely; tvam — you; apsara-udbhūtā — born of a nymph; ṛṣiṇā — by a sage; vardhitā — raised; vane — in the forest; saṁspṛṣṭa-yauvanāt — by budding youth; yā — who; api — even; na — not; tāruṇyam — adulthood; alaṁ — fully; gatā — reached
   Surely, you are born of a nymph and raised by a sage in the forest. You have not yet fully reached adulthood and are still in budding youth.
   
   Verse 4
   वक्ष्यस्यनेकसाहस्त्रवर्षाणामिव संस्थितिम्‌ ।
   भूतग्रस्तोक्तिसदृशवचसा तेऽतिमात्रतः ॥ ४ ॥
   vakṣyasy aneka-sāhastra-varṣāṇām iva saṁsthitim ।
   bhūta-grasta-ukti-sadṛśa-vacasā te 'timātrataḥ ॥ 4 ॥
   vakṣyasi — you speak; aneka-sāhastra-varṣāṇām — of many thousand years; iva — like; saṁsthitim — state; bhūta-grasta-ukti-sadṛśa — resembling a possessed being's speech; vacasā — words; te — your; ati-mātrataḥ — extremely
   You speak words that resemble the speech of a possessed being, claiming to have lived for many thousands of years.
   
   Verse 5
   असन्दर्भेण किमहं विबुद्धयामि यथार्थतः ।
   वद ते सा सखी क्वास्ते बद्धश्च सखिपुत्रकः ॥ ५ ॥
   asandarbheṇa kim ahaṁ vibuddhayāmi yathārthataḥ ।
   vada te sā sakhī kvāste baddhaś ca sakhi-putrakaḥ ॥ 5 ॥
   asandarbheṇa — without context; kim — what; ahaṁ — I; vibuddhayāmi — understand; yathārthataḥ — truly; vada — tell; te — your; sā — she; sakhī — friend; kva — where; āste — stays; baddhaḥ — bound; ca — and; sakhi-putrakaḥ — friend's son
   Without context, how can I truly understand this? Tell me, where is your friend, and where is the friend's son bound?
   
   Verse 6
   पुराणि तानि वा कुत्र संस्थितानि तदीरय ।
   अस्तु किं तेन वृत्तेन वद मे क्व च सा सखी ॥ ६ ॥
   purāṇi tāni vā kutra saṁsthitāni tad īraya ।
   astu kiṁ tena vṛttena vada me kva ca sā sakhī ॥ 6 ॥
   purāṇi — old; tāni — those; vā — or; kutra — where; saṁsthitāni — established; tad — that; īraya — tell; astu — be it; kiṁ — what; tena — by that; vṛttena — event; vada — tell; me — me; kva — where; ca — and; sā — she; sakhī — friend
   How old are they, and where are they established? Even so, what about that event? Tell me, where is that friend?
   
   Verse 7
   सखीं न प्राप्तवान्‌ मातुरहं तत्‌ प्रविचारय ।
   आर्यास्ति मेऽवरोधे स्वे पितुर्मेऽन्या नहि प्रिया ॥ ७ ॥
   sakhīṁ na prāptavān mātur ahaṁ tat pravicāraya ।
   āryāsti me 'varoḍhe sve pitur me 'nyā nahi priyā ॥ 7 ॥
   sakhīṁ — friend; na — not; prāptavān — obtained; mātur — mother's; ahaṁ — I; tat — that; pravicāraya — consider; āryā — noble lady; asti — is; me — my; avaroḍhe — in seclusion; sve — own; pitur — father's; me — my; anyā — other; nahi — not; priyā — dear
   I believe that I have not found any such friend of my mother, a noble lady in seclusion, nor my own, nor my father's, nor anyone else dear to me.
   
   Verse 8
   सा वा सखी मे कुत्रास्ते तत्पुत्रो वा वद द्रुतम्‌ ।
   मन्येऽहं ते वचो लोके वन्ध्यापुत्रसमाश्रयम्‌ ॥ ८ ॥
   sā vā sakhī me kutrāste tat-putro vā vada drutam ।
   manye 'haṁ te vaco loke vandhyā-putra-samāśrayam ॥ 8 ॥
   sā — she; vā — or; sakhī — friend; me — my; kutra — where; āste — stays; tat-putro — her son; vā — or; vada — tell; drutam — quickly; manye — I think; ahaṁ — I; te — your; vaco — words; loke — in the world; vandhyā-putra-samāśrayam — like a barren woman's son
   Where is my friend or her son? Tell me quickly. I think your words are like a barren woman's son—nonexistent in the world.
   
   Verse 9
   यथाह कश्चिचन्नटिको विदूषकवचोविधौ ।
   वन्ध्यापुत्रः समारूढः प्रतिबिम्बमहारथम्‌ ॥ ९ ॥
   yathāha kaścit naṭiko vidūṣaka-vaco-vidhau ।
   vandhyā-putraḥ samārūḍhaḥ pratibimba-mahāratham ॥ 9 ॥
   yathā — as; āha — said; kaścit — some; naṭiko — actor; vidūṣaka-vaco-vidhau — in jesting speech; vandhyā-putraḥ — barren woman's son; samārūḍhaḥ — mounted; pratibimba-mahāratham — on an illusory great chariot
   Your words are like an actor speaking in jest or like the son of a barren woman riding an illusory great chariot.
   
   Verse 10
   शुक्त्यारोपितहैरण्यभूषणैर्भूषिताङ्गकः ।
   आयुधैर्नरशृङ्गोत्थैर्युद्ध्वा गगनकानने ॥ १० ॥
   śukty-āropita-hairṇya-bhūṣaṇair bhūṣitāṅgakaḥ ।
   āyudhaiḥ nara-śṛṅga-utthair yuddhvā gagana-kānane ॥ 10 ॥
   śukty-āropita-hairṇya-bhūṣaṇaiḥ — with oyster shells made to look like golden ornaments; bhūṣita-aṅgakaḥ — adorned body; āyudhaiḥ — with weapons; nara-śṛṅga-utthaiḥ — made from human horns; yuddhvā — fighting; gagana-kānane — in the sky forest
   Or like adorning the body with oyster shells made to look like golden ornaments, or fighting with weapons made from human horns in the sky forest.
   
   Verse 11
   हत्वा भविष्यद्राजानं जित्वा गन्धर्वपत्तनम्‌ ।
   मरीचिस्रोतसि स्वाप्नकामिनीभिर्हि खेलति ॥ ११ ॥
   hatvā bhaviṣya-drājānaṁ jitvā gandharva-pattanam ।
   marīci-srotasi svāpna-kāminībhir hi khelati ॥ 11 ॥
   hatvā — having killed; bhaviṣya-drājānaṁ — future king; jitvā — having won; gandharva-pattanam — celestial city; marīci-srotasi — in the stream of illusion; svāpna-kāminībhir — with dream maidens; hi — indeed; khelati — plays
   Having killed the future king and won the celestial city, or indeed playing with dream maidens in the stream of illusion.
   
   Verse 12
   तथा तव वचो मन्ये सर्वथाऽसङ्गतं ननु ।
   श्रुत्वैवं प्रियवाक्यं सा चतुरा प्राह तं पुनः ॥ १२ ॥
   tathā tava vaco manye sarvathā 'saṅgataṁ nanu ।
   śrutvā evaṁ priya-vākyaṁ sā caturā prāha taṁ punaḥ ॥ 12 ॥
   tathā — thus; tava — your; vaco — words; manye — I think; sarvathā — entirely; asaṅgatam — unrelated; nanu — indeed; śrutvā — hearing; evaṁ — thus; priya-vākyaṁ — dear words; sā — she; caturā — clever; prāha — said; taṁ — to him; punaḥ — again
   Thus, I think your words are entirely unrelated. Hearing this, she cleverly responded to him again.
   
   Verse 13
   नाथ प्रोक्तं मया यत्ते तत्‌ कथं स्यादपार्थकम्‌ ।
   न मादृशानां वचनं निरालम्बं क्वचिद्भवेत्‌ ॥ १३ ॥
   nātha proktaṁ mayā yat te tat kathaṁ syād aparthakam ।
   na mādṛśānāṁ vacanaṁ nirālambaṁ kvacid bhavet ॥ 13 ॥
   nātha — lord; proktaṁ — spoken; mayā — by me; yat — which; te — to you; tat — that; kathaṁ — how; syāt — can be; aparthakam — meaningless; na — not; mādṛśānāṁ — of people like me; vacanaṁ — words; nirālambaṁ — unsupported; kvacit — anywhere; bhavet — be
   Lord, how can what I have spoken to you be meaningless? The words of people like me are never unsupported anywhere.
   
   Verse 14
   मृषा हि तपसां हन्त्री सत्यशीलेषु सा कुतः ।
   तपस्विनां कुले कस्माच्छवित्रे सौन्दर्यवद्भवेत्‌ ॥ १४ ॥
   mṛṣā hi tapasāṁ hantrī satya-śīleṣu sā kutaḥ ।
   tapasvināṁ kule kasmāc chavitre saundarya-vad bhavet ॥ 14 ॥
   mṛṣā — falsehood; hi — indeed; tapasāṁ — of ascetics; hantrī — destroyer; satya-śīleṣu — among those of truthful character; sā — she; kutaḥ — where; tapasvināṁ — of ascetics; kule — in the family; kasmāt — why; śavitre — like a corpse; saundarya-vat — with beauty; bhavet — be
   Falsehood is indeed the destroyer of ascetics; where is it among those of truthful character? Why would falsehood exist in the family of ascetics, akin to beauty in a corpse?
   
   Verse 15
   यो योजयति जिज्ञासुमन्यार्थेन ह्यसत्यतः ।
   तस्य नोद्र्ध्वं न चाधस्ताल्लोकोऽस्ति सुखसाधनम्‌ ॥ १५ ॥
   yo yojayati jijñāsum anyārthena hy asatyataḥ ।
   tasya nodr̥d hwaṁ na cādhas tāl loko 'sti sukha-sādhanam ॥ 15 ॥
   yo — who; yojayati — engages; jijñāsum — the inquisitive; anyārthena — for other purposes; hi — indeed; asatyataḥ — falsely; tasya — his; na — not; urdhvaṁ — upward; na — nor; ca — and; adhas — downward; tāl — there; loko — world; asti — is; sukha-sādhanam — means of happiness
   Whoever falsely engages the inquisitive for other purposes finds neither the upward nor the downward world as a means of happiness.
   
   Verse 16
   शृणु राजसुतोक्तिं मे लोके तैमिरिकः क्वचित्‌ ।
   समदृष्टिं नैति शीघ्रमञ्जनानां वचोगणैः ॥ १६ ॥
   śr̥ṇu rāja-sutoktiṁ me loke taimirikaḥ kvacit ।
   samadr̥ṣṭiṁ naiti śīghram añjanānāṁ vaco-gaṇaiḥ ॥ 16 ॥
   śr̥ṇu — listen; rāja-suta — prince; uktiṁ — words; me — my; loke — in the world; taimirikaḥ — blind; kvacit — sometimes; samadr̥ṣṭiṁ — even vision; naiti — does not attain; śīghram — quickly; añjanānāṁ — of medical eyewash; vaco-gaṇaiḥ — by words
   Listen, prince, to my words: sometimes in this world, a blind person does not quickly attain vision, even with the application of medicinal eyewash.
   
   Verse 17
   असत्यमेव जानाति हितप्रोक्तं च मूढधीः ।
   तत्त्वां प्रियाऽहं जिज्ञासुमसत्यैर्योजयामि किम्‌ ॥ १७ ॥
   asatyam eva jānāti hita-proktaṁ ca mūḍha-dhīḥ ।
   tattvāṁ priyā 'haṁ jijñāsum asatyair yojayāmi kim ॥ 17 ॥
   asatyam — falsehood; eva — only; jānāti — knows; hita-proktaṁ — beneficially spoken; ca — and; mūḍha-dhīḥ — foolish mind; tattvāṁ — you; priyā — dear; ahaṁ — I; jijñāsum — inquisitive; asatyaiḥ — by falsehoods; yojayāmi — engage; kim — why
   The foolish mind knows only falsehood and not beneficial words. Dear, why would I deceive you, the inquisitive, with falsehoods?
   
   Verse 18
   अप्यसत्यं मयोक्तं यत्तद्विमर्शय सद्धिया ।
   लोके हि कुशलो मर्त्यः सर्वव्यवहृतौ ननु ॥ १८ ॥
   apy asatyaṁ mayoktaṁ yat tad vimarśaya sad-dhiyā ।
   loke hi kuśalo martyaḥ sarva-vyavahr̥tau nanu ॥ 18 ॥
   api — even if; asatyam — falsehood; mayā — by me; uktaṁ — spoken; yat — which; tad — that; vimarśaya — consider; sad-dhiyā — with a sound mind; loke — in the world; hi — indeed; kuśalaḥ — skilled; martyaḥ — mortal; sarva-vyavahr̥tau — in all conduct; nanu — indeed
   Even if I have spoken falsehood, consider it with a sound mind. Indeed, in this world, a skilled mortal excels in all conduct.
   
   Verse 19
   परीक्ष्यैकांशतः सर्वामभिजानाति संस्थितिम्‌ ।
   निदर्शनं प्रदास्यामि तुभ्यमत्र समीक्षय ॥ १९ ॥
   parīkṣyaikaṁśataḥ sarvām abhijānāti saṁsthitim ।
   nidarśanaṁ pradāsyāmi tubhyam atra samīkṣaya ॥ 19 ॥
   parīkṣya — examining; ekaṁśataḥ — partially; sarvām — all; abhijānāti — understands; saṁsthitim — condition; nidarśanaṁ — example; pradāsyāmi — I will give; tubhyam — to you; atra — here; samīkṣaya — observe
   By examining a part, one can understand the whole. Let me give you an example; observe here.
   
   Verse 20
   यः पुरा विषयः सर्वो बभूवाभीष्टसाधनम्‌ ।
   चिरान्मद्वचनात्‌ सोऽद्य कुतो न सुखसाधनम्‌ ॥ २० ॥
   yaḥ purā viṣayaḥ sarvo babhūvābhīṣṭa-sādhanam ।
   cirān mad-vacanāt so 'dya kuto na sukha-sādhanam ॥ 20 ॥
   yaḥ — which; purā — formerly; viṣayaḥ — object; sarvaḥ — all; babhūva — became; abhīṣṭa-sādhanam — means to the desired; cirāt — for long; mad-vacanāt — by my words; saḥ — that; adya — today; kuto — how; na — not; sukha-sādhanam — means of happiness
   Which object was previously the means to the desired goal? For so long, it was my words. So how can they not be a means of happiness today?
   
   Verse 21
   स एवाद्य साधयति सुखमन्येषु वै कुतः ।
   एतन्निदर्शनेनैव स्वमतं वेत्तुमर्हसि ॥ २१ ॥
   sa evādya sādhayati sukhamanyeṣu vai kutaḥ ।
   etan nidarśanenaiva svamataṁ vettum arhasi ॥ 21 ॥
   saḥ — he; eva — indeed; adya — today; sādhayati — accomplishes; sukham — happiness; anyeṣu — in others; vai — indeed; kutaḥ — how; etat — this; nidarśanena — by example; eva — indeed; svamataṁ — your belief; vettum — to know; arhasi — you should
   How does he now accomplish happiness in others? You should understand your belief through this example.
   
   Verse 22
   शृणु राजन्‌ यद्ब्रवीमि ऋज्व्या निर्मलया धिया ।
   अनाश्वासो रिपुर्लोके भवेदाप्तोक्तिषु स्थिरः ॥ २२ ॥
   śṛṇu rājan yad bravīmi ṛjvyā nirmalayā dhiyā ।
   anāśvāso ripur loke bhaved āptoktiṣu sthiraḥ ॥ 22 ॥
   śṛṇu — listen; rājan — king; yad — what; bravīmi — I say; ṛjvyā — straightforward; nirmalayā — pure; dhiyā — with intellect; anāśvāsaḥ — distrustful; ripuḥ — enemy; loke — in the world; bhaved — becomes; āpta—uktiṣu — in trustworthy sayings; sthiraḥ — firm
   Listen, O king, to what I say with a straightforward and pure intellect. In this world, a distrustful enemy becomes firm through trustworthy sayings.
   
   Verse 23
   श्रद्धा माता प्रपन्नं सा वत्सलेव सुतं सदा ।
   रक्षति प्रौढभीतिभ्यः सर्वथा नहि संशयः ॥ २३ ॥
   śraddhā mātā prapannaṁ sā vatsaleva sutaṁ sadā ।
   rakṣati prauḍha-bhītibhyaḥ sarvathā nahi saṁśayaḥ ॥ 23 ॥
   śraddhā — faith; mātā — mother; prapannaṁ — surrendered one; sā — she; vatsalā iva — like a loving mother; sutaṁ — child; sadā — always; rakṣati — protects; prauḍha-bhītibhyaḥ — from great fears; sarvathā — in every way; nahi — indeed; saṁśayaḥ — doubt
   Faith, like a loving mother, always protects the surrendered one from great fears in every way; indeed, there is no doubt about this.
   
   Verse 24
   आप्तेष्वश्रद्धिनं मूढं जहाति श्रीः सुखं यशः ।
   स भवेत्‌ सर्वतो हीनो यः श्रद्धारहितो नरः ॥ २४ ॥
   āpteṣv aśraddhinaṁ mūḍhaṁ jahāti śrīḥ sukhaṁ yaśaḥ ।
   sa bhavet sarvato hīno yaḥ śraddhā-rahito naraḥ ॥ 24 ॥
   āpteṣu — in the trustworthy; aśraddhinam — faithless; mūḍham — foolish; jahāti — leaves; śrīḥ — prosperity; sukham — happiness; yaśaḥ — fame; saḥ — he; bhavet — becomes; sarvataḥ — entirely; hīnaḥ — devoid; yaḥ — who; śraddhā-rahitaḥ — without faith; naraḥ — man
   Prosperity, happiness, and fame abandon the foolish and faithless and favor those who are trustworthy. He who is without faith becomes entirely devoid of these.
   
   Verse 25
   श्रद्धा हि जगतां धात्री श्रद्धा सर्वस्य जीवनम्‌ ।
   अश्रद्धो मातृविषये बालो जीवेत्‌ कथं वद ॥ २५ ॥
   śraddhā hi jagatāṁ dhātrī śraddhā sarvasya jīvanam ।
   aśraddho mātṛ-viṣaye bālo jīvet kathaṁ vada ॥ 25 ॥
   śraddhā — faith; hi — indeed; jagatām — of the worlds; dhātrī — nourisher; śraddhā — faith; sarvasya — of all; jīvanam — life; aśraddhaḥ — faithless; mātṛ-viṣaye — in the matter of mother; bālaḥ — child; jīvet — lives; katham — how; vada — say
   Faith is indeed the nourisher of the worlds, faith is the life of all. Tell me, how can a faithless child live with the mother in this matter?
   
   Verse 26
   अश्रद्धस्तरुणः पत्न्यां कथं ससुखमेधते ।
   तथाऽपत्येषु स्थविरः कथमीयात्‌ सतीं गतिम्‌ ॥ २६ ॥
   aśraddhas taruṇaḥ patnyāṁ kathaṁ sasukham edhate ।
   tathā 'patyeṣu sthaviraḥ katham īyāt satīṁ gatim ॥ 26 ॥
   aśraddhaḥ — faithless; taruṇaḥ — young; patnyām — in wife; kathaṁ — how; sasukham — with happiness; edhate — flourishes; tathā — similarly; apaty-eṣu — in children; sthaviraḥ — old; katham — how; īyāt — goes; satīṁ — virtuous; gatim — path
   How can a faithless young man flourish with happiness with his wife? Similarly, how can an old man follow the virtuous path without faith in his children?
   
   Verse 27
   अश्रद्धो वा भुवं कस्माद्‌ विकर्षेत्‌ कर्षकः किल ।
   न प्रवृत्तिर्भवेत्‌ क्वापि त्यागे वा संग्रहेऽपि वा ॥ २७ ॥
   aśraddho vā bhuvaṁ kasmād vikarṣet karṣakaḥ kila ।
   na pravṛttir bhavet kvāpi tyāge vā saṁgrahe 'pi vā ॥ 27 ॥
   aśraddhaḥ — faithless; vā — or; bhuvam — earth; kasmāt — why; vikarṣet — plow; karṣakaḥ — farmer; kila — indeed; na — not; pravṛttiḥ — activity; bhavet — becomes; kvāpi — anywhere; tyāge — in renunciation; vā — or; saṁgrahe — in acquisition; api — also; vā — or
   Why would a faithless farmer plow the earth? Without faith, there would be no activity anywhere, neither in renunciation nor in acquisition.
   
   Verse 28
   श्रद्धावैधुर्ययोगेन विनश्येज्जगतां स्थितिः ।
   एकान्तग्रहणाल्लोकप्रवृत्तिरिति चेच्छृणु ॥ २८ ॥
   śraddhā-vaidhurya-yogena vinaśyed jagatāṁ sthitiḥ ।
   ekānta-grahaṇāl loka-pravṛttir iti cet śṛṇu ॥ 28 ॥
   śraddhā-vaidhurya-yogena — due to lack of faith; vinaśyet — would perish; jagatāṁ — of the worlds; sthitiḥ — existence; ekānta-grahaṇāt — from complete acceptance; loka-pravṛttiḥ — worldly activity; iti — thus; cet — if; śṛṇu — listen
   Without faith, the existence of the worlds would perish. Listen, if worldly activity arises from complete acceptance.
   
   Verse 29
   एकान्तग्रहणे वापि श्रद्धा कस्मात्‌ प्रतिष्ठिता ।
   तत्राप्येकान्तशरणः श्रद्धाशरण एव हि ॥ २९ ॥
   ekānta-grahaṇe vāpi śraddhā kasmāt pratiṣṭhitā ।
   tatrāpy ekānta-śaraṇaḥ śraddhā-śaraṇa eva hi ॥ 29 ॥
   ekānta-grahaṇe — in complete acceptance; vā — or; api — even; śraddhā — faith; kasmāt — why; pratiṣṭhitā — established; tatra api — there also; ekānta-śaraṇaḥ — sole refuge; śraddhā-śaraṇa — refuge in faith; eva — indeed; hi — indeed
   Even in complete acceptance, why is faith necessary? There too, the sole refuge is indeed faith itself.
   
   Verse 30
   तस्माच्छ्रद्धामृते लोकोऽवसीदेदश्वसन्‌ ध्रुवम्‌ ।
   तस्माच्छ्रद्धां दृढां प्राप्य सुखमात्यन्तिकं व्रज ॥ ३० ॥
   tasmāc chraddhāmṛte loko 'vasīd edaśvasan dhruvam ।
   tasmāc chraddhāṁ dṛḍhāṁ prāpya sukham ātyantikaṁ vraja ॥ 30 ॥
   tasmāt — therefore; śraddhāmṛte — without faith; lokaḥ — the world; avasīd et — would perish; aśvasan — without breathing; dhruvam — surely; tasmāt — therefore; śraddhāṁ — faith; dṛḍhām — firm; prāpya — obtaining; sukham — happiness; ātyantikam — ultimate; vraja — go
   Therefore, without faith, the world would surely perish, just like it would without breathing. So, obtain firm faith and seek ultimate happiness.
   
   Verse 31
   श्रद्धाऽवरे न कार्येति मन्यसे यदि तच्छृणु ।
   इयं च श्रद्धयैवास्ते प्रवृत्तिर्नुपतेः सुत ॥ ३१ ॥
   śraddhā 'vare na kāry eti manyase yadi tac chṛṇu ।
   iyaṁ ca śraddhayāiva 'ste pravṛttir nupateḥ sutaḥ ॥ 31 ॥
   śraddhā — faith; avare — in the lower; na kārya — not to be done; iti — thus; manyase — you think; yadi — if; tat — that; śṛṇu — listen; iyaṁ — this; ca — and; śraddhayā — by faith; eva — indeed; aste — exists; pravṛttiḥ — activity; nupateḥ sutaḥ — prince
   If you think faith should not be placed in the lowly, listen. Any activity indeed exists by faith, O prince.
   
   Verse 32
   तत्‌ कथं ते प्रवृत्तिः स्यादिति श्रुत्वा प्रियावचः ।
   हेमचूडः प्राह पुनः प्रियां कुशलभाषिणीम्‌ ॥ ३२ ॥
   tat kathaṁ te pravṛttiḥ syād iti śrutvā priyā-vacaḥ ।
   hemacūḍaḥ prāha punaḥ priyāṁ kuśala-bhāṣiṇīm ॥ 32 ॥
   tat — that; katham — how; te — your; pravṛttiḥ — activity; syāt — would be; iti — thus; śrutvā — having heard; priyā-vacaḥ — beloved's words; hemacūḍaḥ — Hemachuda; prāha — said; punaḥ — again; priyāṁ — beloved; kuśala-bhāṣiṇīm — skilled speaker
   Hearing his beloved's words, Hemachuda said again to the skilled speaker, "How would your activity be thus, my dear?"
   
   Verse 33
   नूनं प्रिये सर्वथैव श्रद्धातव्यं यदा भवेत्‌ ।
   श्रद्धा सत्सु विधातव्या यया श्रेयः समाप्नुयात्‌ ॥ ३३ ॥
   nūnaṁ priye sarvathaiva śraddhātavyaṁ yadā bhavet ।
   śraddhā satsu vidhātavyā yayā śreyaḥ samāpnuyāt ॥ 33 ॥
   nūnam — indeed; priye — dear; sarvathā — in every way; eva — indeed; śraddhātavyam — to be placed in faith; yadā — when; bhavet — becomes; śraddhā — faith; satsu — in the good; vidhātavyā — to be placed; yayā — by which; śreyaḥ — welfare; samāpnuyāt — would attain
   Indeed, dear, faith should be placed in every way when it is to be placed in faith. Faith should be placed in the good, by which welfare is attained.
   
   Verse 34
   असत्सु नो विधातव्या श्रद्धा श्रेयोऽभिवाञ्छिना ।
   अन्यथान्तः सुनिशिते कुटिले बडिशे यथा ॥ ३४ ॥
   asatsu no vidhātavyā śraddhā śreyo 'bhivāñchinā ।
   anyathāntaḥ suniśite kuṭile baḍiśe yathā ॥ 34 ॥
   asatsu — in the bad; no — not; vidhātavyā — to be placed; śraddhā — faith; śreyaḥ — welfare; abhivāñchinā — desirous of; anyathā — otherwise; antaḥ — inside; suniśite — sharp; kuṭile — crooked; baḍiśe — hook; yathā — like
   Faith should not be placed in the bad by one who desires welfare. Otherwise, it is like a sharp, crooked hook inside.
   
   Verse 35
   बहिःसमे सुपिष्टेन मीनानां नाशमाप्नुयात्‌ ।
   तस्मात्‌ सत्स्वेव कर्तव्या श्रद्धा नासत्यु कुत्रचित्‌ ॥ ३५ ॥
   bahiḥ same supiṣṭena mīnānāṁ nāśam āpnuyāt ।
   tasmāt satsv eva kartavyā śraddhā nāsatyu kutracit ॥ 35 ॥
   bahiḥ — outside; same — similar; supiṣṭena — well-ground; mīnānām — of fish; nāśam — destruction; āpnuyāt — attains; tasmāt — therefore; satsv — in the good; eva — indeed; kartavyā — to be placed; śraddhā — faith; na — not; asatyu — in the untruth; kutracit — anywhere
   Just as fish meet their destruction by well—ground bait outside, so should faith be placed in the good, not in untruth anywhere.
   
   Verse 36
   असत्सु कृत्वा श्रद्धां ये नाशमीयुः परेऽपि च ।
   सत्सु श्रेयोयुजः श्रद्धावशतस्ते निदर्शनम्‌ ॥ ३६ ॥
   asatsu kṛtvā śraddhāṁ ye nāśam īyuḥ pare 'pi ca ।
   satsu śreyo—yujaḥ śraddhāvaśatas te nidarśanam ॥ 36 ॥
   asatsu — in the bad; kṛtvā — having placed; śraddhām — faith; ye — who; nāśam — destruction; īyuḥ — attained; pare — others; api — also; ca — and; satsu — in the good; śreyaḥ-yujaḥ — those united with welfare; śraddhāvaśataḥ — due to faith; te — they; nidarśanam — example
   Those who placed faith in the bad met with destruction, as did others. Conversely, those who placed faith in the good attained welfare and prosperity.
   
   Verse 37
   अतः प्रतीत्यैव युक्ता कर्तुं श्रद्धा न चान्यथा ।
   तत्‌ कथं ते प्रवृत्तिः स्यादिति प्रश्नः कथं तव ॥ ३७ ॥
   ataḥ pratītyaiva yuktā kartuṁ śraddhā na cānyathā ।
   tat kathaṁ te pravṛttiḥ syād iti praśnaḥ kathaṁ tava ॥ 37 ॥
   ataḥ — therefore; pratītya — believing; eva — indeed; yuktā — proper; kartum — to do; śraddhā — faith; na — not; ca — and; anyathā — otherwise; tat — that; katham — how; te — your; pravṛttiḥ — activity; syāt — would be; iti — thus; praśnaḥ — question; katham — how; tava — your
   Therefore, placing faith properly is essential. Thus, you asked, "How would your activity be thus?"
   
   Verse 38
   इत्युक्ता हेमलेखा सा पुनराह पतिं प्रियम्‌ ।
   शृणु राजकुमारेदं प्रोच्यमानं मया वचः ॥ ३८ ॥
   ityuktā hemalekhā sā punar āha patiṁ priyam ।
   śṛṇu rāja-kumāredam procyamānaṁ mayā vacaḥ ॥ 38 ॥
   iti — thus; uktā — spoken; hemalekhā — Hemalekha; sā — she; punaḥ — again; āha — said; patiṁ — husband; priyam — dear; śṛṇu — listen; rāja-kumāra — prince; idam — this; procyamānaṁ — being said; mayā — by me; vacaḥ — words
   Thus spoken, Hemalekha said again to her dear husband, "Listen, O prince, to these words I am saying."
   
   Verse 39
   यदात्थ त्वं कथं प्रश्न इति तत्र ब्रवीमि ते ।
   अयं सन्‌ वा ह्यसन्‌ वायमिति ते निश्चयः कुतः ॥ ३९ ॥
   yadāttha tvaṁ kathaṁ praśna iti tatra bravīmi te ।
   ayaṁ san vā hy asan vāyam iti te niścayaḥ kutaḥ ॥ 39 ॥
   yadāttha — you said; tvaṁ — you; kathaṁ — how; praśna — question; iti — thus; tatra — there; bravīmi — I say; te — to you; ayam — this; san — being; vā — or; hi — indeed; asan — non-being; vā — or; ayam — this; iti — thus; te — your; niścayaḥ — certainty; kutaḥ — how
   You asked this question, "how." To that, I say to you, "How certain are you about this being or non-being?"
   
   Verse 40
   सत्यस्मिन्‌ निश्चये भूयाच्छुभं सच्छ्रद्धयेह वै ।
   सोऽपि लक्षणतः स्याच्चेच्छ्रद्धा लक्षणसङ्गता ॥ ४० ॥
   satyasmin niścaye bhūyāc chubhaṁ sa-cchraddhayeha vai ।
   so 'pi lakṣaṇataḥ syāc chec chraddhā lakṣaṇa-saṅgatā ॥ 40 ॥
   satyasmin — in truth; niścaye — certainty; bhūyāt — should become; śubham — good; sa-śraddhayā — with faith; iha — here; vai — indeed; saḥ — that; api — also; lakṣaṇataḥ — by characteristic; syāt — would be; cet — if; śraddhā — faith; lakṣaṇa-saṅgatā — associated with characteristics
   If there is certainty in the truth, it should indeed become good with faith here. That would also be characterized if faith is associated with characteristics.
   
   Verse 41
   प्रमाणाल्लक्षणज्ञानमिति चेत्तत्र संशृणु ।
   अश्रद्धस्य प्रमाणं कि भवेत्तत्‌ सुनिरूप्यताम्‌ ॥ ४१ ॥
   pramāṇāl lakṣaṇa-jñānam iti cet tatra saṃśṛṇu ।
   aśraddhasya pramāṇaṁ ki bhavet tat sunirūpyatām ॥ 41 ॥
   pramāṇāt — from evidence; lakṣaṇa-jñānam — knowledge of characteristics; iti — thus; cet — if; tatra — there; saṃśṛṇu — listen; aśraddhasya — of one who lacks faith; pramāṇam — evidence; ki — what; bhavet — would be; tat — that; sunirūpyatām — let it be well examined
   If knowledge of characteristics comes from evidence, then listen to this: What evidence is there for one who lacks faith? Let that be well examined.
   
   Verse 42
   अन्यथा हि प्रमाता नो विसंवाद्येत कुत्रचित्‌ ।
   तस्माच्छ्रद्धां समाश्रित्य लोकः सर्वः प्रवर्तते ॥ ४२ ॥
   anyathā hi pramātā no visaṃvādyeta kutracit ।
   tasmāc chraddhāṁ samāśritya lokaḥ sarvaḥ pravartate ॥ 42 ॥
   anyathā — otherwise; hi — indeed; pramātā — the knower; no — not; visaṃvādyeta — would be contradicted; kutracit — anywhere; tasmāt — therefore; śraddhām — faith; samāśritya — relying on; lokaḥ — the world; sarvaḥ — all; pravartate — operates
   Otherwise, the knower would not be contradicted anywhere. Therefore, the entire world operates by relying on faith.
   
   Verse 43
   तत्प्रकारं प्रवक्ष्यामि शृणु निश्चलचेतसा ।
   अनवस्थिततर्को वा ह्यतर्को वापि सर्वथा ॥ ४३ ॥
   tat prakāraṁ pravakṣyāmi śṛṇu niścalacetasa ।
   anavasthita-tarko vā hy atarko vāpi sarvathā ॥ 43 ॥
   tat — that; prakāram — method; pravakṣyāmi — I will explain; śṛṇu — listen; niścalacetasa — with a steady mind; anavasthita-tarkaḥ — unsettled reasoning; vā — or; hi — indeed; atarkaḥ — no reasoning; vā — or; api — also; sarvathā — in every way
   I will explain that method; listen with a steady mind. It concerns unsettled reasoning or the absence of reasoning altogether, in every way.
   
   Verse 44
   श्रेयो न प्राप्नुयाल्लोक इह वापि परत्र वा ।
   तत्रातर्कस्य कालेन भवेच्छ्रेयः कदाचन ॥ ४४ ॥
   śreyo na prāpnuyāl loka iha vāpi paratra vā ।
   tatrātarkasya kālena bhavec chreyaḥ kadācana ॥ 44 ॥
   śreyaḥ — welfare; na — not; prāpnuyāt — would attain; lokaḥ — the world; iha — here; vā — or; api — also; paratra — hereafter; vā — or; tatra — sometimes; atarkasya — without reasoning; kālena — by chance; bhavet — may come; śreyaḥ — welfare; kadācana — sometimes.
   The world would not attain welfare here or hereafter without reasoning. Sometimes, welfare may come by chance without reasoning.
   
   Verse 45
   अनवस्थिततर्कस्य न श्रेयः स्यात्‌ कथञ्चन ।
   पुरा सह्यगिरौ गोदावरीतीरे हि कौशिकः ॥ ४५ ॥
   anavasthita-tarkasya na śreyaḥ syāt kathaṃcana ।
   purā sahyagirau godāvarītīre hi kauśikaḥ ॥ 45 ॥
   anavasthita-tarkasya — for unsettled reasoning; na — not; śreyaḥ — welfare; syāt — would come; kathaṃcana — in any way; purā — once upon a time; sahyagirau — on the Sahya mountain; godāvarītīre — by the Godavari river; hi — indeed; kauśikaḥ — sage Kaushika.
   For unsettled reasoning, welfare would not come in any way. Once upon a time, on the Sahya mountain by the Godavari river, there was a sage named Kaushika.
   
   Verse 46
   न्यवसच्छान्तसुमतिर्ज्ञातलोकसतत्त्वकः ।
   तस्य शिष्यास्तु शतशः स्थिता गुरुसमाश्रयात्‌ ॥ ४६ ॥
   nyavasac chānta-sumatiḥ jñāta-loka-satattvakaḥ ।
   tasya śiṣyās tu śataśaḥ sthitā guru-samāśrayāt ॥ 46 ॥
   nyavasat — lived; śānta-sumatiḥ — with a calm mind; jñāta-loka-satattvakaḥ — knowing the true nature of the world; tasya — his; śiṣyāḥ — disciples; tu — indeed; śataśaḥ — hundreds; sthitāḥ — stayed; guru-samāśrayāt — by the guru’s guidance
   He lived with a calm mind, knowing the true nature of the world. Hundreds of his disciples stayed under the guru’s guidance.
   
   Verse 47
   त एकदा गुरुमनु गता लोकस्य संस्थितिम्‌ ।
   निर्णेतुं बुद्धयनुगुणं तदा प्रोचुः परस्परम्‌ ॥ ४७ ॥
   ta ekadā gurum anu gatā lokasya saṃsthitim ।
   nirṇetuṁ buddhi-anuguṇaṁ tadā procuḥ parasparam ॥ 47 ॥
   te — they; ekadā — one day; gurum — guru; anu — approached; gatāḥ — went; lokasya — the world’s; saṃsthitim — state; nirṇetum — to determine; buddhi-anuguṇam — according to their intellect; tadā — then; procuḥ — spoke; parasparam — to each other
   One day, they approached the guru to understand the state of the world according to their intellect, and then they spoke to each other.
   
   Verse 48
   तत्राजगाम शुङ्गाख्यो विप्रः कश्चिन्महाबुधः ।
   स सर्वेषां मतं प्रोक्तं दूषयद्बुद्धिकौशलात्‌ ॥ ४८ ॥
   tatrājagāma śuṅgākhyo vipraḥ kaścinmahābudhaḥ ।
   sa sarveṣāṁ mataṁ proktaṁ dūṣayad buddhi-kauśalāt ॥ 48 ॥
   tatra — there; ājagāma — came; śuṅga-ākhyāḥ — named Shunga; vipraḥ — brahmin; kaścit — some; mahā-budhaḥ — highly learned; saḥ — he; sarveṣām — of all; matam — opinions; proktam — stated; dūṣayat — refuting; buddhi-kauśalāt — by skill in reasoning
   A highly learned Brahmin named Shunga arrived. With his skill in reasoning, he refuted the stated opinions of all.
   
   Verse 49
   अश्रद्धया हतप्रज्ञो विवादनिपुणस्तदा ।
   प्रमाणात्‌ प्रमितं सत्यमित्युक्तेषु द्विजेष्वथ ॥ ४९ ॥
   aśraddhayā hata-prajño vivāda-nipuṇas tadā ।
   pramāṇāt pramitaṁ satyam ity ukteṣu dvijeṣv atha ॥ 49 ॥
   aśraddhayā — without faith; hata-prajñaḥ — having lost wisdom; vivāda-nipuṇaḥ — skillful in debate; tadā — then; pramāṇāt — from evidence; pramitaṁ — measured; satyam — truth; iti — thus; ukteṣu — said; dvijeṣu — among the brahmins; atha — then
   Then, without faith and having lost wisdom but still skillful in debate, he said among the Brahmins, "Truth is what is measured from evidence."
   
   Verse 50
   अनवस्थिततर्को वै प्राह तर्कैकसंश्रयः ।
   शुङ्गाख्य आक्षिपन्‌ सर्वान्‌ तत्र वादकथान्तरे ॥ ५० ॥
   anavasthita-tarko vai prāha tarkaika-saṃśrayaḥ ।
   śuṅgākhya ākṣipan sarvān tatra vādakathāntare ॥ 50 ॥
   anavasthita-tarkaḥ — unsettled reasoning; vai — indeed; prāha — said; tarka-eka-saṃśrayaḥ — relying only on reasoning; śuṅga-ākhyā — Shunga; ākṣipàn — refuting; sarvān — all; tatra — there; vāda-kathā-antare — in the debate
   Relying solely on unsettled reasoning, Shunga refuted everyone in the debate.
   
   Verse 51
   विप्राः शृणुध्वं मद्वाक्यं सत्यं न क्वापि सिध्यति ।
   प्रमितं यत्‌ प्रमाणेन तत्‌ सत्यमिति हीरितम्‌ ॥ ५१ ॥
   viprāḥ śṛṇudhvaṁ mad-vākyaṁ satyaṁ na kvāpi sidhyati ।
   pramitaṁ yat pramāṇena tat satyam iti hīritam ॥ 51 ॥
   viprāḥ — O brahmins; śṛṇudhvaṁ — listen; mad-vākyaṁ — my words; satyaṁ — truth; na kvāpi — nowhere; sidhyati — is established; pramitaṁ — measured; yat — what; pramāṇena — by evidence; tat — that; satyam — truth; iti — thus; hīritam — is said
   "O Brahmins, listen to my words. Truth is nowhere established. What is measured by evidence is said to be the truth."
   
   Verse 52
   तत्र तेन दोषयुजा भवेदप्रमितं ननु ।
   निश्चेतव्या ततस्त्वादौ प्रमाणानामदुष्टता ॥ ५२ ॥
   tatra tena doṣa-yujā bhaved apramitaṁ nanu ।
   niścetavyā tatas tvādau pramāṇānām aduṣṭatā ॥ 52 ॥
   tatra — there; tena — by that; doṣa-yujā — with defect; bhavet — would be; apramitaṁ — immeasurable; nanu — indeed; niścetavyā — should be ascertained; tataḥ — then; tvādau — first; pramāṇānām — of the evidence; aduṣṭatā — defectlessness
   There, indeed, due to that defect, it would be immeasurable. First, the flawlessness of the evidence should be ascertained.
   
   Verse 53
   सा प्रमाणान्तरकृता तत्राप्येवं विचिन्त्यताम्‌ ।
   इत्येवमनवस्थानाद्‌ न किञ्चित्‌ प्रमितं भवेत्‌ ॥ ५३ ॥
   sā pramāṇāntara-kṛtā tatrāpy evaṁ vicintyatām ।
   ity evam anavasthānād na kiñcit pramitaṁ bhavet ॥ 53 ॥
   sā — that; pramāṇa-antara-kṛtā — created by other evidence; tatra api — even there; evam — thus; vicintyatām — should be considered; iti evam — thus; anavasthānāt — from uncertainty; na kiñcit — nothing; pramitaṁ — measured; bhavet — would be
   Thus, even that created by other evidence should be considered. Therefore, from uncertainty, nothing can be measured.
   
   Verse 54
   अतः प्रमाता प्रमितं प्रमाणं वा न सिध्यति ।
   तस्माच्छून्याश्रयो ह्येष विकल्पो विविधः स्थितः ॥ ५४ ॥
   ataḥ pramātā pramitaṁ pramāṇaṁ vā na sidhyati ।
   tasmāc chūnyāśrayo hyeṣa vikalpo vividhaḥ sthitaḥ ॥ 54 ॥
   ataḥ — therefore; pramātā — the knower; pramitaṁ — measured; pramāṇaṁ — evidence; vā — or; na sidhyati — does not establish; tasmāt — therefore; śūnya—āśrayaḥ — based on emptiness; hi — indeed; eṣaḥ — this; vikalpaḥ — alternative; vividhaḥ — various; sthitaḥ — exists
   Therefore, the knower, the measured, and the evidence do not establish anything. Consequently, based on emptiness, various alternatives indeed exist.
   
   Verse 55
   सोऽपि शून्यात्मतां प्राप्तः प्रमाणाविषयत्वतः ।
   तस्माच्छून्यं न किञ्चित्‌ सदित्येष प्रविनिर्णयः ॥ ५५ ॥
   so 'pi śūnyātmatāṁ prāptaḥ pramāṇāviṣayatvataḥ ।
   tasmāc chūnyaṁ na kiñcit sad ity eṣa pravinirṇayaḥ ॥ 55 ॥
   saḥ api — even he; śūnya-ātmatām — state of emptiness; prāptaḥ — attained; pramāṇa-aviṣayatvataḥ — due to lack of evidence; tasmāt — therefore; śūnyam — emptiness; na kiñcit — nothing; sat — is real; iti — thus; eṣaḥ — this; pravinirṇayaḥ — conclusion
   Even he attained a state of emptiness due to the lack of evidence. Therefore, nothingness and emptiness are real; thus, this is the conclusion.
   
   Verse 56
   इति शुङ्गवचः श्रुत्वा तेषु केचिद्‌ द्विजाधमाः ।
   तं श्रिता निश्चयाभासं बभूवुः शून्यवादिनः ॥ ५६ ॥
   iti śuṅgavacaḥ śrutvā teṣu kecid dvijā-dhamāḥ ।
   taṁ śritā niścayābhāsaṁ babhūvuḥ śūnyavādinaḥ ॥ 56 ॥
   iti — thus; śuṅga-vacaḥ — Shunga's words; śrutvā — hearing; teṣu — among them; kecid — some; dvija-dhamāḥ — lowly brahmins; taṁ — him; śritāḥ — followed; niścaya-ābhāsaṁ — apparent certainty; babhūvuḥ — became; śūnya-vādinaḥ — proponents of emptiness
   Thus, hearing Shunga's words, some lowly Brahmins among them followed him, becoming proponents of emptiness with apparent certainty.
   
   Verse 57
   विनाशमीयुस्तन्निष्ठाः शून्यभावं परं गताः ।
   ये द्विजाः सारहृदयास्ते शुङ्गस्य प्रभाषितम्‌ ॥ ५७ ॥
   vināśam īyuḥ tan-niṣṭhāḥ śūnya-bhāvaṁ paraṁ gatāḥ ।
   ye dvijāḥ sāra-hṛdayās te śuṅgasya prabhāṣitam ॥ 57 ॥
   vināśam — destruction; īyuḥ — went; tat-niṣṭhāḥ — devoted to that; śūnya-bhāvaṁ — state of emptiness; paraṁ gatāḥ — attained; ye — those; dvijāḥ — brahmins; sāra-hṛdayāḥ — with strong hearts; te — they; śuṅgasya — Shunga's; prabhāṣitam — words
   Those devoted to that belief went to destruction, attaining a state of emptiness. The Brahmins with strong hearts rejected Shunga's words.
   
   Verse 58
   निरूप्य कौशिके तेन समाहितहृदोऽभवन्‌ ।
   तस्मात्‌ सर्वात्मना त्यक्त्वा तर्कं तमनवस्थितम्‌ ॥ ५८ ॥
   nirūpya kauśike tena samāhita-hṛdo 'bhavan ।
   tasmāt sarvātmanā tyaktvā tarkaṁ tam anavasthitam ॥ 58 ॥
   nirūpya — analyzing; kauśike — by Kaushika; tena — by him; samāhita-hṛdaḥ — with composed hearts; abhavan — became; tasmāt — therefore; sarvātmanā — completely; tyaktvā — abandoning; tarkaṁ — reasoning; tam — that; anavasthitam — unsettled
   By analyzing Kaushika's teachings, they became composed at heart, thereby completely abandoning that unsettled reasoning.
   
   Verse 59
   सदा सदागमायत्ततर्कः श्रेयः समाप्नुयात्‌ ।
   इति प्रोक्तो हेमचूडः प्रिययाऽत्यन्तधीरया ॥ ५९ ॥
   sadā sadāgama-āyatta-tarkaḥ śreyaḥ samāpnuyāt ।
   iti prokto hemacūḍaḥ priyayā 'tyanta-dhīrayā ॥ 59 ॥
   sadā — always; sadāgama-āyatta — dependent on true scriptures; tarkaḥ — reasoning; śreyaḥ — welfare; samāpnuyāt — would attain; iti — thus; proktaḥ — was told; hemacūḍaḥ — Hemachuda; priyayā — by his beloved; atyanta-dhīrayā — extremely wise
   Reasoning that always depends on true scriptures will attain welfare. This is what Hemachuda was told by his extremely wise beloved.
   
   Verse 60
   पुनः पप्रच्छ चात्यन्तविस्मितस्तां महाशयाम्‌ ।
   अहो प्रिये ते वैदुष्यमीदृशं नाविदं पुरा ॥ ६० ॥
   punaḥ papraccha cātyanta-vismitaḥ tāṁ mahāśayām ।
   aho priye te vaiduṣyam īdṛśaṁ nāvidaṁ purā ॥ 60 ॥
   punaḥ — again; papraccha — asked; ca — and; atyanta-vismitaḥ — extremely astonished; tāṁ — her; mahāśayām — great lady; aho — oh; priye — dear; te — your; vaiduṣyam — wisdom; īdṛśam — such; na avidam — did not know; purā — before
   Once again, extremely astonished, he asked her, "Oh dear, I was unaware of your great wisdom before."
   
   Verse 61
   धन्यासि त्वमहं चापि धन्यो यस्त्वामुपागतः ।
   ब्रवीषि श्रद्धया सर्वश्रेयःसिद्धिं हि तत्‌ कथम्‌ ॥ ६१ ॥
   dhanyāsi tvam ahaṁ cāpi dhanyo yas tvām upāgataḥ ।
   bravīṣi śraddhayā sarva-śreyaḥ-siddhiṁ hi tat katham ॥ 61 ॥
   dhanyāsi — blessed are you; tvam — you; aham — I; ca api — also; dhanyaḥ — blessed; yaḥ — who; tvām — you; upāgataḥ — has approached; bravīṣi — you say; śraddhayā — with faith; sarva-śreyaḥ-siddhim — attainment of all auspiciousness; hi — indeed; tat — that; katham — how
   Blessed are you, and blessed am I for having approached you. You say that with faith one attains all auspiciousness. How is that so?
   
   Verse 62
   कुत्र श्रद्धा विधातव्या कुत्र वा सा न शस्यते ।
   आनन्त्यादागमानां वै विरुद्धार्थसमाश्रयात्‌ ॥ ६२ ॥
   kutra śraddhā vidhātavyā kutra vā sā na śasyate ।
   ānantyād āgamānāṁ vai viruddhārtha-samāśrayāt ॥ 62 ॥
   kutra — where; śraddhā — faith; vidhātavyā — should be placed; kutra — where; vā — or; sā — it; na — not; śasyate — is recommended; ānantyāt — due to the multitude; āgamānām — of scriptures; vai — indeed; viruddha-artha-samāśrayāt — due to contradictory meanings
   Where should faith be placed, and where is it not recommended? The multitude of scriptures and their contradictory meanings make this unclear.
   
   Verse 63
   आचार्यमतभेदाच्च व्याख्यातृमतभेदतः ।
   स्वबुद्धेरनवस्थानात्‌ किमादेयं न वापि किम्‌ ॥ ६३ ॥
   ācārya-mata-bhedāc ca vyākhyātṛ-mata-bhedataḥ ।
   sva-buddheḥ anavasthānāt kim ādheyaṁ na vāpi kim ॥ 63 ॥
   ācārya-mata-bhedāt — due to differences in the opinions of teachers; ca — and; vyākhyātṛ-mata-bhedataḥ — due to differences in the interpretations of commentators; sva-buddheḥ — one's own intellect; anavasthānāt — due to instability; kim — what; ādheyaṁ — to accept; na vā api — or not
   Due to the differing opinions of teachers and commentators, and the instability of one's own intellect, what should be accepted and what should not?
   
   Verse 64
   यद्यस्याभिमतं तत्‌ स वदत्येव सुनिश्चितम्‌ ।
   अन्यच्चाप्यव्यवसितं हानिप्रदमपि प्रिये ॥ ६४ ॥
   yad yasya abhimataṁ tat sa vadati eva su-niścitam ।
   anyaṁ ca api avyavasitam hāni-pradam api priye ॥ 64 ॥
   yat — what; yasya — for whom; abhimatam — is dear; tat — that; saḥ — he; vadati — says; eva — indeed; su-niścitam — as certain; anyat — another; ca api — and also; avyavasitam — undecided; hāni-pradam — causing harm; api — even; priye — dear
   What is dear to one is declared as certain, while another's view remains undecided, causing harm, dear one.
   
   Verse 65
   तत्रैव सति नैवान्तं कश्चिदत्रापि गच्छति ।
   य: शून्यमाह तत्वं सोऽप्यशून्यं दूषयेत्‌ परम्‌ ॥ ६५ ॥
   tatra eva sati na eva antaṁ kaścit atra api gacchati ।
   yaḥ śūnyam āha tattvaṁ saḥ api aśūnyam dūṣayet param ॥ 65 ॥
   tatra — there; eva — indeed; sati — being; na eva — not at all; antam — end; kaścit — anyone; atra — here; api — even; gacchati — goes; yaḥ — who; śūnyam — emptiness; āha — says; tattvam — truth; saḥ — he; api — even; aśūnyam — non-emptiness; dūṣayet — criticizes; param — another
   No one reaches a definitive conclusion about what is true or not. He who claims that truth is emptiness criticizes another's belief in non-emptiness.
   
   Verse 66
   अश्रद्धेयं कुतो वा तत्‌ सङ्गतं चागमेन हि ।
   एतद्‌ ब्रूहि प्रिये सम्यग्‌ नह्येतत्तेऽस्त्यचिन्तितम्‌ ॥ ६६ ॥
   aśraddheyaṁ kuto vā tat saṅgataṁ ca āgamena hi ।
   etat brūhi priye samyak na hi etat te asti acintitam ॥ 66 ॥
   aśraddheyam — unbelievable; kuto vā — from where; tat — that; saṅgatam — consistent; ca — and; āgamena — with scriptures; hi — indeed; etat — this; brūhi — tell; priye — dear; samyak — correctly; na hi — not indeed; etat — this; te — your; asti — is; acintitam — unconsidered
   How can one know that something seemingly unbelievable is consistent with the scriptures? Explain this correctly, dear. Indeed, you must have considered it.


   
   इति श्रीमदितिहासोत्तमे त्रिपुरारहस्ये ज्ञानखण्डे हेमचूडोपाख्याने श्रद्धाप्रशंसनं नाम षष्ठोऽध्यायः ॥
   
   Thus ends the sixth chapter named "Praise of Faith" in the Story of Hemachuda in the Knowledge Section of the revered Tripura Rahasya.
   
   

7. DESCRIPTION OF THE NATURE OF GOD
   Verse 1
   इति पृष्टा हेमलेखा भर्त्रा प्रियतरेण सा ।
   प्रोवाच विदुषो सम्यग्‌ विज्ञातलोकसंस्थितिः ॥ १ ॥
   iti pṛṣṭā hemalekhā bhartrā priyatareṇa sā ।
   provāca viduṣo samyag vijñāta-loka-saṁsthitiḥ ॥ 1 ॥
   iti — thus; pṛṣṭā — questioned; hemalekhā — Hemalekha; bhartrā — by her husband; priyatareṇa — dearest; sā — she; provāca — replied; viduṣaḥ — wise; samyak — rightly; vijñāta-loka-saṁsthitiḥ — one who knows the state of the world
   Thus questioned by her dearest husband, Hemalekha, wise and well-acquainted with the state of the world, replied appropriately.
   
   Verse 2
   शृणु वक्ष्ये प्रियतम स्थिरस्वान्तः समादरात्‌ ।
   मनो हि मर्कटप्रायमस्थिरं सर्वदैव तत्‌ ॥ २ ॥
   śṛṇu vakṣye priyatama sthira-svāntaḥ samādarāt ।
   mano hi markaṭa-prāyam asthiraṁ sarvadaiva tat ॥ 2 ॥
   śṛṇu — listen; vakṣye — I will tell; priyatama — dearest; sthira-svāntaḥ — with a steady mind; samādarāt — with respect; manaḥ — mind; hi — indeed; markaṭa-prāyam — like a monkey; asthiram — unstable; sarvadā — always; eva — indeed; tat — it
   Listen, dearest, with a steady mind and respect, I will tell you. The mind is indeed always unstable, like a monkey.
   
   Verse 3
   यत एवं महानर्थ प्राप्तवान्‌ प्राकृतो जनः ।
   चलन्मनः सर्वदुःखनिदानं दृष्टमेव हि ॥ ३ ॥
   yata evaṁ mahān arthaṁ prāptavān prākṛto janaḥ ।
   calan-manaḥ sarva-duḥkha-nidānaṁ dṛṣṭam eva hi ॥ 3 ॥
   yataḥ — because; evaṁ — thus; mahān — great; arthaṁ — misfortune; prāptavān — has obtained; prākṛtaḥ — ordinary; janaḥ — people; calan-manaḥ — unstable mind; sarva — all; duḥkha-nidānam — cause of suffering; dṛṣṭam — seen; eva — indeed; hi — surely
   Because of this, ordinary people have experienced great misfortune. An unstable mind is recognized as the cause of all suffering.
   
   Verse 4
   यतः सुषुप्तौ चलनाभावाद्विन्दति वै सुखम्‌ ।
   तस्मान्मनः स्थिरीकृत्य शृणु यत्ते ब्रवीम्यहम्‌ ॥ ४ ॥
   yataḥ suṣuptau calana-abhāvāt vindati vai sukham ।
   tasmāt manaḥ sthirīkṛtya śṛṇu yat te bravīmy aham ॥ 4 ॥
   yataḥ — because; suṣuptau — in deep sleep; calana-abhāvāt — due to absence of movement; vindati — finds; vai — indeed; sukham — happiness; tasmāt — therefore; manaḥ — mind; sthirīkṛtya — stabilizing; śṛṇu — listen; yat — what; te — to you; bravīmi — I say; aham — I
   Because in deep sleep, the absence of movement brings happiness. Therefore, stabilize your mind and listen to what I have to say to you.
   
   Verse 5
   अनादरेण श्रुतं च भवेदश्रुतसम्मितम्‌ ।
   अफलं स्यात्तदत्यन्तं यथा चित्रतरुश्रयः ॥ ५ ॥
   anādareṇa śrutaṁ ca bhaved aśruta-saṁmitam ।
   aphalaṁ syāt tad atyantaṁ yathā citrataru-āśrayaḥ ॥ 5 ॥
   anādareṇa — with disrespect; śrutam — heard; ca — and; bhavet — becomes; aśruta-saṁmitam — as if not heard; aphalam — fruitless; syāt — may be; tad — that; atyantam — absolutely; yathā — like; citrataru-āśrayaḥ — support of a painted tree
   What is heard with disrespect is as if unheard. It is absolutely fruitless, like seeking support from a painted tree.
   
   Verse 6
   अनवस्थिततर्कत्वं तमपहाय विनाशनम्‌ ।
   सत्तर्कमाश्रित्य जन प्राप्नुयात्‌ सुफलं द्रुतम्‌ ॥ ६ ॥
   anavasthita-tarkatvaṁ tam apahāya vināśanam ।
   sat-tarkam āśritya jana prāpnuyāt su-phalaṁ drutam ॥ 6 ॥
   anavasthita-tarkatvam — unstable reasoning; tam — that; apahāya — abandoning; vināśanam — destructive; sat-tarkam — sound reasoning; āśritya — relying; jana — people; prāpnuyāt — obtain; su-phalam — good result; drutam — quickly
   By abandoning unstable reasoning, which is destructive, people who rely on sound reasoning quickly obtain good results.
   
   Verse 7
   सत्तर्कसंश्रयेणाशु साधनैकपरो भवेत्‌ ।
   सत्तर्कजनितां श्रद्धां प्राप्येह फलभाग्‌ नरः ॥ ७ ॥
   sat-tarka-saṁśrayeṇa āśu sādhanaika-paro bhavet ।
   sat-tarka-janitāṁ śraddhāṁ prāpya iha phala-bhāk naraḥ ॥ 7 ॥
   sat-tarka-saṁśrayeṇa — by relying on sound reasoning; āśu — quickly; sādhana-eka-paraḥ — dedicated to one means; bhavet — becomes; sat-tarka-janitām — generated by sound reasoning; śraddhām — faith; prāpya — having attained; iha — here; phala-bhāk — fruit-bearing; naraḥ — man
   By relying on sound reasoning, one quickly becomes dedicated to a single path. Having attained faith generated by sound reasoning, a person bears fruit here.
   
   Verse 8
   अनवस्थिततर्कं तं विहायालोकय प्रिय ।
   प्रवृत्तिमेतां जगतः श्रद्धया फलशालिनीम्‌ ॥ ८ ॥
   anavasthita-tarkaṁ tam vihāya ālokaya priya ।
   pravṛttim etāṁ jagataḥ śraddhayā phala-śālinīm ॥ 8 ॥
   anavasthita-tarkam — unstable reasoning; tam — that; vihāya — abandoning; ālokaya — see; priya — dear; pravṛttim — activity; etām — this; jagataḥ — of the world; śraddhayā — with faith; phala-śālinīm — fruitful
   Abandon that unstable reasoning and observe, dear, how this activity of the world becomes fruitful with faith.
   
   Verse 9
   सुतर्कितेन कालेन कर्षकः क्ष्मां विकर्षति ।
   श्रद्धयैव तथा रूप्यस्वर्णरत्नौषधादिकम्‌ ॥ ९ ॥
   sutarkitena kālena karṣakaḥ kṣmāṁ vikarṣati ।
   śraddhayā eva tathā rūpya-svarṇa-ratna-auṣadha-ādikam ॥ 9 ॥
   sutarkitena — with sound reasoning; kālena — over time; karṣakaḥ — farmer; kṣmām — earth; vikarṣati — tills; śraddhayā — with faith; eva — indeed; tathā — likewise; rūpya-svarṇa-ratna-auṣadha-ādikam — silver, gold, gems, and medicines
   With sound reasoning over time, a farmer tills the earth. Similarly, with faith, one obtains silver, gold, gems, and medicines.
   
   Verse 10
   व्यवस्यन्ति सुतर्केण त्यक्त्वा तर्कानवस्थितिम्‌ ।
   तस्मात्‌ सुतर्कश्रद्धाभ्यां व्यवस्य श्रेय आत्मनः ॥ १० ॥
   vyavasyanti sutarkena tyaktvā tarkān avasthitim ।
   tasmāt sutarka-śraddhābhyāṁ vyavasyet śreya ātmanaḥ ॥ 10 ॥
   vyavasyanti — decide; sutarkena — with sound reasoning; tyaktvā — abandoning; tarkān — arguments; avasthitim — stability; tasmāt — therefore; sutarka-śraddhābhyām — with sound reasoning and faith; vyavasyet — one should decide; śreyaḥ — welfare; ātmanaḥ — of oneself
   They decide with sound reasoning, abandoning unstable arguments. Therefore, one should determine their own welfare using sound reasoning and faith.
   
   Verse 11
   प्रयतेत्तत्साधनाय नहि तर्कानिवस्थितेः ।
   विरमेत्‌ पौरुषाद्‌ यत्नाच्छुङ्गानुगनरा इव ॥ ११ ॥
   prayatet tat-sādhanāya nahi tarkān avasthiteḥ ।
   viramet pauruṣād yatnāt śuṅga-anuga-narā iva ॥ 11 ॥
   prayatet — one should strive; tat-sādhanāya — for its attainment; nahi — not; tarkān — arguments; avasthiteḥ — stable; viramet — one should desist; pauruṣāt — from effort; yatnāt — from striving; śuṅga-anuga-narā iva — like the followers of Shunga
   One should strive for its attainment, not relying on unstable arguments. One should not desist from effort and perseverance, unlike the followers of Shunga.
   
   Verse 12
   श्रद्धया पौरुषपरो न विहन्येत सर्वथा ।
   दृढं पौरुषमाश्रित्य न प्राप्येत कथं फलम्‌ ॥ १२ ॥
   śraddhayā pauruṣa-paraḥ na vihanyeta sarvathā ।
   dṛḍhaṁ pauruṣam āśritya na prāpyeta kathaṁ phalam ॥ 12 ॥
   śraddhayā — with faith; pauruṣa-paraḥ — dedicated to effort; na vihanyeta — not be hindered; sarvathā — in any way; dṛḍham — firm; pauruṣam — effort; āśritya — relying on; na prāpyeta — not achieve; katham — how; phalam — result
   With faith, one dedicated to effort should not be hindered in any way. By relying on firm effort, how can one fail to achieve the desired result?
   
   Verse 13
   पौरुषात्‌ कर्षका धान्यं वणिजो धनमेव च ।
   राज्यलक्ष्मीं नृपा विप्रा विद्यां सर्वसुखाश्रयाम्‌ ॥ १३ ॥
   pauruṣāt karṣakā dhānyaṁ vaṇijo dhanam eva ca ।
   rājya-lakṣmīṁ nṛpā viprā vidyāṁ sarva-sukha-āśrayām ॥ 13 ॥
   pauruṣāt — through effort; karṣakāḥ — farmers; dhānyam — grains; vaṇijaḥ — merchants; dhanam — wealth; eva ca — and also; rājya-lakṣmīm — kingdom's wealth; nṛpāḥ — kings; viprāḥ — scholars; vidyām — knowledge; sarva-sukha-āśrayām — the foundation of all happiness
   Through effort, farmers obtain grain, merchants acquire wealth, kings secure their kingdom's riches, and scholars gain knowledge, the foundation of all happiness.
   
   Verse 14
   शूद्रा भृतिं सुधां देवास्तापसा लोकमुत्तमम्‌ ।
   प्रापुरन्येऽप्यभिमतं पौरुषेणैव कर्मणा ॥ १४ ॥
   śūdrā bhṛtiṁ sudhāṁ devāḥ tāpasāḥ lokam uttamam ।
   prāpur anye api abhimataṁ pauruṣeṇa eva karmaṇā ॥ 14 ॥
   śūdrāḥ — laborers; bhṛtim — wages; sudhām — nectar; devāḥ — gods; tāpasāḥ — ascetics; lokam uttamam — the highest world; prāpuḥ — obtained; anye — others; api — also; abhimatam — desired; pauruṣeṇa — by effort; eva — indeed; karmaṇā — through action
   Laborers obtained wages, gods acquired nectar, ascetics attained the highest world, and others achieved their desired goals through effort indeed.
   
   Verse 15
   अनवस्थिततर्केणाश्रद्धेन पुरुषेण किम्‌ ।
   कदा किञ्चित्‌ कथं प्राप्तं फलं वद विमृश्य तत्‌ ॥ १५ ॥
   anavasthita-tarkeṇa aśraddhena puruṣeṇa kim ।
   kadā kiñcit kathaṁ prāptaṁ phalaṁ vada vimṛśya tat ॥ 15 ॥
   anavasthita-tarkeṇa — with unstable reasoning; aśraddhena — without faith; puruṣeṇa — by a person; kim — what; kadā — when; kiñcit — anything; katham — how; prāptam — obtained; phalam — result; vada — tell; vimṛśya — after considering; tat — that
   With unstable reasoning and without faith, what results has anyone ever achieved? Tell me, considering that.
   
   Verse 16
   क्वचित्‌ फलविसंवादात्‌ सर्वत्राश्वासवर्जने ।
   विजानीयाद्‌ दैवहतं तं स्वात्मरिपुरूपिणम्‌ ॥ १६ ॥
   kvacit phala-visaṁvādāt sarvatra āśvāsa-varjane ।
   vijānīyāt daiva-hataṁ taṁ sva-ātma-ripu-rūpiṇam ॥ 16 ॥
   kvacit — sometimes; phala-visaṁvādāt — due to failure to achieve results; sarvatra — everywhere; āśvāsa-varjane — absence of assurance; vijānīyāt — should understand; daiva-hatam — afflicted by fate; tam — him; sva-ātma-ripu-rūpiṇam — in the form of one's own enemy
   Sometimes, due to failure to achieve results and a lack of assurance everywhere, one should recognize him as afflicted by fate, appearing as his own enemy.
   
   Verse 17
   अतः पौरुषमाश्रित्य श्रद्धासत्तर्कपोषितम्‌ ।
   श्रेयसां यन्मुख्यतमं साधनं तत्‌ समाश्रयेत्‌ ॥ १७ ॥
   ataḥ pauruṣam āśritya śraddhā-sat-tarka-poṣitam ।
   śreyasāṁ yat mukhyatamaṁ sādhanam tat samāśrayet ॥ 17 ॥
   ataḥ — therefore; pauruṣam — effort; āśritya — relying on; śraddhā-sat-tarka-poṣitam — nourished by faith and sound reasoning; śreyasām — of welfare; yat — which; mukhyatamam — the foremost; sādhanam — means; tat — that; samāśrayet — one should resort to
   Therefore, relying on effort nourished by faith and sound reasoning, one should adopt that foremost means of achieving welfare.
   
   Verse 18
   तत्र दृष्टं साधनानां वैचित्र्यं च पृथग्विधम्‌ ।
   तेषु यत्‌ सर्वथा साध्यं साधयेत्तद्धि मुख्यकम्‌ ॥ १८ ॥
   tatra dṛṣṭam sādhanānāṁ vaicitryaṁ ca pṛthag-vidham ।
   teṣu yat sarvathā sādhyam sādhayet tad dhi mukhyakam ॥ 18 ॥
   tatra — there; dṛṣṭam — observed; sādhanānām — of means; vaicitryam — diversity; ca — and; pṛthag-vidham — various kinds; teṣu — among them; yat — which; sarvathā — in every way; sādhyam — achievable; sādhayet — one should achieve; tat — that; hi — indeed; mukhyakam — principal
   There is a diversity of means that is observed, and among them, one should achieve that which is attainable in every way, as that is indeed the principal goal.
   
   Verse 19
   तत्‌ सुतर्कानुभूतिभ्यां व्यवस्याशु समारभेत्‌ ।
   तत्ते सर्व प्रवक्ष्यामि सावधानः श्रुणुष्व तत्‌ ॥ १९ ॥
   tat sutarka-anubhūtibhyāṁ vyavasya āśu samārabhet ।
   tat te sarvaṁ pravakṣyāmi sāvadhānaḥ śruṇuṣva tat ॥ 19 ॥
   tat — that; sutarka-anubhūtibhyām — through sound reasoning and experience; vyavasya — deciding; āśu — quickly; samārabhet — one should begin; tat — that; te — to you; sarvam — all; pravakṣyāmi — I will explain; sāvadhānaḥ — attentively; śruṇuṣva — listen; tat — that
   Deciding through sound reasoning and experience, one should act quickly. I will explain everything to you, so listen attentively.
   
   Verse 20
   श्रेयस्तद्धि विजानीयाद्यस्माद्‌ भूयो न शोचति ।
   शोकः सर्वत एव स्याद्‌ दृश्यते सूक्ष्मया दृशा ॥ २० ॥
   śreyas tad dhi vijānīyāt yasmād bhūyaḥ na śocati ।
   śokaḥ sarvataḥ eva syāt dṛśyate sūkṣmayā dṛśā ॥ 20 ॥
   śreyas — welfare; tat — that; hi — indeed; vijānīyāt — one should know; yasmāt — from which; bhūyaḥ — again; na śocati — does not grieve; śokaḥ — grief; sarvataḥ — everywhere; eva — indeed; syāt — may be; dṛśyate — is seen; sūkṣmayā — subtle; dṛśā — by vision
   One should recognize that true welfare is that from which one does not grieve again. Grief is seen everywhere with a subtle vision.
   
   Verse 21
   यच्छोकैरनुसंभिन्नं न तच्छ्रेयो हि सर्वथा ।
   धनं पुत्रास्तथा दारा राज्यं कोशो बलं यशः ॥ २१ ॥
   yac chokair anusaṁbhinnam na tat śreyo hi sarvathā ।
   dhanaṁ putrās tathā dārā rājyaṁ kośo balaṁ yaśaḥ ॥ 21 ॥
   yac — that which; śokaiḥ — with griefs; anusaṁbhinnam — intertwined; na — not; tat — that; śreyaḥ — welfare; hi — indeed; sarvathā — in any way; dhanam — wealth; putrāḥ — sons; tathā — as well as; dārāḥ — wives; rājyaṁ — kingdom; kośaḥ — treasury; balam — strength; yaśaḥ — fame
   That which is intertwined with griefs is not true welfare in any way: wealth, sons, wives, kingdom, treasury, strength, and fame.
   
   Verse 22
   विद्या बुद्धिर्दर्शनं च देहः सौन्दर्यसम्पदः ।
   सर्वमेतदस्थिरत्वात्‌ कालसर्पमुखस्थितम्‌ ॥ २२ ॥
   vidyā buddhir darśanaṁ ca dehaḥ saundarya-sampadaḥ ।
   sarvam etad asthiratvāt kāla-sarpa-mukha-sthitam ॥ 22 ॥
   vidyā — knowledge; buddhiḥ — intellect; darśanam — sight; ca — and; dehaḥ — body; saundarya-sampadaḥ — beauty and wealth; sarvam — all this; etat — this; asthiratvāt — due to instability; kāla-sarpa-mukha-sthitam — placed in the mouth of the serpent of time
   Knowledge, intellect, sight, body, beauty, and wealth—all these are unstable, held within the jaws of the serpent of time.
   
   Verse 23
   शोकाङ्कुरमहाशक्तिबीजात्मकतया स्थितम्‌ ।
   कुत आत्यन्तिकश्रेयःसाधनत्वं समर्हति ॥ २३ ॥
   śoka-aṅkura-mahā-śakti-bīja-ātmakatayā sthitam ।
   kutaḥ ātyantika-śreyaḥ-sādhanatvaṁ samarhati ॥ 23 ॥
   śoka-aṅkura — of the sprout of grief; mahā-śakti — great power; bīja-ātmakatayā — in the form of seed; sthitam — situated; kutaḥ — how; ātyantika-śreyaḥ — ultimate welfare; sādhanatvam — suitability; sam-arhati — is deserving
   Situated as the seed of the great power of the sprout of grief, how can it be deserving of suitability for ultimate welfare?
   
   Verse 24
   अतः परमकं श्रेय एतद्वै मुख्यतो भवेत्‌ ।
   एवं धनादिविषये यदादेयत्वविभ्रमः ॥ २४ ॥
   ataḥ paramakaṁ śreya etad vai mukhyato bhavet ।
   evaṁ dhana-ādi-viṣaye yat ādēyatva-vibhramaḥ ॥ 24 ॥
   ataḥ — therefore; paramakaṁ — highest; śreyaḥ — welfare; etad — this; vai — indeed; mukhyataḥ — primarily; bhavet — should be; evaṁ — thus; dhana-ādi-viṣaye — in the matter of wealth, etc.; yat — which; ādēyatva-vibhramaḥ — delusion of desirability
   Therefore, the highest welfare primarily lies in this; thus, in the matter of wealth and other material possessions, there is a delusion of desirability.
   
   Verse 25
   मोहादेव समुद्भूतो मोहको हि महेश्वरः ।
   यो हि सर्वजगत्कर्ता तस्मात्‌ सर्वे हि मोहिताः ॥ २५ ॥
   mohād eva samudbhūto mohako hi maheśvaraḥ ।
   yo hi sarva-jagat-kartā tasmāt sarve hi mohitāḥ ॥ 25 ॥
   mohāt — from delusion; eva — indeed; samudbhūtaḥ — arisen; mohakaḥ — deluder; hi — indeed; maheśvaraḥ — the great lord; yaḥ — who; hi — indeed; sarva-jagat-kartā — creator of all worlds; tasmāt — therefore; sarve — all; hi — indeed; mohitāḥ — deluded
   Arisen from delusion, the great lord is the deluder and the creator of all worlds; therefore, all are deluded.
   
   Verse 26
   मोहयत्यल्पकोऽपीह विद्याभागसमाश्रयात्‌ ।
   कांश्चिदेव न सर्वान्‌ स यस्माद्विद्या हि सा मिता ॥ २६ ॥
   mohayati alpa-kaḥ api iha vidyā-bhāga-samāśrayāt ।
   kāṁścid eva na sarvān saḥ yasmāt vidyā hi sā mitā ॥ 26 ॥
   mohayati — deludes; alpa-kaḥ — even a little; api — even; iha — here; vidyā-bhāga-samāśrayāt — due to a portion of knowledge; kāṁścit — some; eva — indeed; na — not; sarvān — all; saḥ — he; yasmāt — because; vidyā — knowledge; hi — indeed; sā — that; mitā — limited
   People here are deluded to some extent due to partial knowledge of some deluder; some are affected, but not all, because that knowledge is limited.
   
   Verse 27
   अल्पविद्यं मायिनं चाप्यनुत्क्रान्ता जना यतः ।
   महादेवं महामायं कः समुत्क्रान्तुमर्हति ॥ २७ ॥
   alpa-vidyaṁ māyinaṁ ca api anutkrāntā janā yataḥ ।
   mahā-devaṁ mahā-māyaṁ kaḥ samutkrāntum arhati ॥ 27 ॥
   alpa-vidyam — one with little knowledge; māyinam — deluder; ca — and; api — even; anutkrāntāḥ — surpassed; janāḥ — people; yataḥ — because; mahā-devam — the great god; mahā-māyam — great deluder; kaḥ — who; samutkrāntum — to surpass; arhati — is capable.
   Even those with little knowledge have surpassed the deluder in their delusions; then who is capable of surpassing the great god, the ultimate deluder?
   
   Verse 28
   यो हि लोकेऽल्पमायां च जानाति प्रतिविद्यया ।
   स मोहान्निर्गतः स्वस्थः सुखमाप्नोत्यनश्वरम्‌ ॥ २८ ॥
   yaḥ hi loke alpa-māyāṁ ca jānāti prati-vidyayā ।
   saḥ mohāt nirgataḥ svasthaḥ sukham āpnoti anaśvaram ॥ 28 ॥
   yaḥ — who; hi — indeed; loke — in the world; alpa-māyām — little delusion; ca — and; jānāti — knows; prati-vidyayā — by counter-knowledge; saḥ — he; mohāt — from delusion; nirgataḥ — emerged; svasthaḥ — calm; sukham — happiness; āpnoti — obtains; anaśvaram — eternal
   Who in the world, by counter-knowledge, understands the small delusion, emerges from it, remains calm, and attains eternal happiness.
   
   Verse 29
   एवंविधापि विद्या तमनाश्रित्य तु मायिनम्‌ ।
   न लभ्या सर्वथा यावदप्रसाद्य तु सर्वथा ॥ २९ ॥
   evaṁ-vidhā api vidyā tam anāśritya tu māyinam ।
   na labhyā sarvathā yāvat aprasādya tu sarvathā ॥ 29 ॥
   evaṁ-vidhā — such; api — even; vidyā — knowledge; tam — him; anāśritya — without resorting to; tu — but; māyinam — deluder; na — not; labhyā — attainable; sarvathā — in any way; yāvat — until; aprasādya — without pleasing; tu — but; sarvathā — in every way
   Even such knowledge is not attainable without resorting to the deluder, until one pleases him in every way.
   
   Verse 30
   तस्मान्महामायिनं तमप्रसाद्य कथं भवेत्‌ ।
   महामोहस्य तरणं तस्मात्तं सर्वथा श्रयेत्‌ ॥ ३० ॥
   tasmāt mahā-māyinaṁ tam aprasādya kathaṁ bhavet ।
   mahā-mohasya taraṇaṁ tasmāt taṁ sarvathā śrayet ॥ 30 ॥
   tasmāt — therefore; mahā-māyinaṁ — the great deluder; tam — him; aprasādya — without pleasing; katham — how; bhavet — can be; mahā-mohasya — of great delusion; taraṇam — crossing; tasmāt — therefore; tam — him; sarvathā — in every way; śrayet — should resort
   Therefore, without pleasing the great deluder, how can one overcome the great delusion? Thus, one should resort to him in every way.
   
   Verse 31
   यस्तं प्रसादयेत्‌ सम्यक्‌ प्राप्य तस्य प्रसादतः ।
   महाविद्यां स तन्मोहाद्‌ ध्रुवमुत्क्रान्तिमेष्यति ॥ ३१ ॥
   yaḥ tam prasādayet samyak prāpya tasya prasādataḥ ।
   mahā-vidyāṁ sa tam-mohāt dhruvam utkrāntim eṣyati ॥ 31 ॥
   yaḥ — who; tam — him; prasādayet — pleases; samyak — properly; prāpya — having attained; tasya — his; prasādataḥ — by grace; mahā-vidyām — great knowledge; saḥ — he; tam-mohāt — from that delusion; dhruvam — certainly; utkrāntim — transcendence; eṣyati — will achieve
   Whoever pleases him properly and attains his grace will certainly achieve transcendence from that delusion through great knowledge.
   
   Verse 32
   अन्येऽपि योगाः कथिताः श्रेयःसाधनकर्मणि ।
   महेश्वरप्रसादात्ते विना न स्युः फलाप्तये ॥ ३२ ॥
   anye api yogāḥ kathitāḥ śreyaḥ-sādhana-karmaṇi ।
   maheśvara-prasādāt te vinā na syuḥ phala-āptaye ॥ 32 ॥
   anye — other; api — also; yogāḥ — practices; kathitāḥ — mentioned; śreyaḥ-sādhana-karmaṇi — in acts of achieving welfare; maheśvara-prasādāt — by the grace of the great lord; te — they; vinā — without; na syuḥ — would not be; phala-āptaye — for obtaining the result
   Other practices mentioned for achieving welfare will not yield results without the grace of the great lord.
   
   Verse 33
   तस्मादाराधयेदादौ महेशं विश्वकारणम्‌ ।
   भक्त्या स साधयेदाशु योगान्मोहविनाशनान्‌ ॥ ३३ ॥
   tasmāt ārādhayet ādau maheśaṁ viśva-kāraṇam ।
   bhaktyā sa sādhayed āśu yogān moha-vināśanān ॥ 33 ॥
   tasmāt — therefore; ārādhayet — should worship; ādau — first; maheśam — the great lord; viśva-kāraṇam — cause of the universe; bhaktyā — with devotion; saḥ — he; sādhayet — should accomplish; āśu — quickly; yogān — practices; moha-vināśanān — that destroy delusion
   Therefore, one should first worship the great lord, the cause of the universe, with devotion, and then quickly undertake practices that destroy delusion.
   
   Verse 34
   एतज्जगत्‌ कार्यभूतं प्रत्यक्षं परिदृश्यते ।
   सांशमेवं पृथिव्याद्यमदृष्टारम्भमप्यलम्‌ ॥ ३४ ॥
   etaj jagat kārya-bhūtaṁ pratyakṣaṁ paridṛśyate ।
   sāṁśam evaṁ pṛthivyādyam adṛṣṭa-ārambham api alam ॥ 34 ॥
   etat — this; jagat — world; kārya-bhūtam — as an effect; pratyakṣam — directly; paridṛśyate — is seen; sāṁśam — along with parts; evam — thus; pṛthivī-ādyam — beginning with the earth; adṛṣṭa-ārambham — with an unseen cause; api — even; alam — sufficiently
   This world, along with its parts, is directly seen as an effect, beginning with the earth, even with an unseen cause, sufficiently evident.
   
   Verse 35
   कार्य स्यादिति तर्केण बह्वागमदृढेन तु ।
   व्यवस्येत्तत्र कर्तारं सर्वकर्तृ विलक्षणम्‌ ॥ ३५ ॥
   kāryaḥ syāt iti tarkeṇa bahu-āgama-dṛḍhena tu ।
   vyavasya tatra kartāraṁ sarva-kartṛ-vilakṣaṇam ॥ 35 ॥
   kāryaḥ — an effect; syāt — is; iti — thus; tarkeṇa — by reasoning; bahu-āgama-dṛḍhena — firmly established by many scriptures; tu — but; vyavasya — should ascertain; tatra — there; kartāram — a doer; sarva-kartṛ-vilakṣaṇam — distinct from all doers
   By reasoning in this way, firmly supported by many scriptures, one should ascertain a doer there, distinct from all other doers.
   
   Verse 36
   यद्यप्यकर्तृकं लोकमाह कश्चिदिहागमः ।
   तदनेकैरागमैस्तु तर्करूढैः सुबाधितम्‌ ॥ ३६ ॥
   yadyapi akartṛkaṁ lokam āha kaścit iha āgamaḥ ।
   tat anekaiḥ āgamaḥ tu tarka-rūḍhaiḥ subādhitam ॥ 36 ॥
   yadi api — although; akartṛkam — without a doer; lokam — world; āha — says; kaścit — some; iha — here; āgamaḥ — scripture; tat — that; anekaiḥ — by many; āgamaḥ — scriptures; tu — but; tarka-rūḍhaiḥ — established by reasoning; subādhitam — well refuted
   Although some scriptures claim the world is without a doer, this is well refuted by many scriptures supported by sound reasoning.
   
   Verse 37
   यत्रात्मनाश एवार्थः प्रत्यक्षैकसमाश्रयात्‌ ।
   तदागमाभासमेव न तद्धि महदाश्रयम्‌ ॥ ३७ ॥
   yatra ātma-nāśa eva arthaḥ pratyakṣa-eka-samāśrayāt ।
   tat āgama-ābhāsam eva na tat hi mahat-āśrayam ॥ 37 ॥
   yatra — where; ātma-nāśaḥ — self-destruction; eva — indeed; arthaḥ — purpose; pratyakṣa-eka-samāśrayāt — based only on perception; tat — that; āgama-ābhāsam — appearance of scripture; eva — indeed; na — not; tat — that; hi — indeed; mahat-āśrayam — a great authority
   Where the purpose is self-destruction, based solely on perception, it is merely the appearance of scripture, not a great authority.
   
   Verse 38
   शुष्कतर्कैकसंक्लृप्तं शास्त्रं तत्‌ त्याज्यमेव हि ।
   अन्यैरप्युच्यते कैश्चिद्‌ जगदेतत्‌ सनातनम्‌ ॥ ३८ ॥
   śuṣka-tarka-eka-saṁklṛptam śāstram tat tyājyam eva hi ।
   anyaiḥ api ucyate kaiścit jagat etat sanātanam ॥ 38 ॥
   śuṣka-tarka — dry logic; eka-saṁklṛptam — solely constructed; śāstram — scripture; tat — that; tyājyam — should be rejected; eva — indeed; hi — certainly; anyaiḥ — by others; api — also; ucyate — is said; kaiścit — by some; jagat — world; etat — this; sanātanam — eternal
   Scripture based solely on dry logic should indeed be rejected. Others also claim that this world is eternal.
   
   Verse 39
   अबुद्धिमत्कर्तृकं चेत्येतच्चाप्यसमञ्जसम्‌ ।
   क्रियाया बुद्धिपूर्वंत्वादबुद्धौ तददर्शनात्‌ ॥ ३९ ॥
   abuddhi-mat-kartṛkam cet etat ca api asamañjasam ।
   kriyāyāḥ buddhi-pūrvam-tvāt abuddhau tat adarśanāt ॥ 39 ॥
   abuddhi-mat — without intelligence; kartṛkam — doer; cet — if; etat — this; ca — and; api — also; asamañjasam — incongruous; kriyāyāḥ — of action; buddhi-pūrvam-tvāt — due to being preceded by intelligence; abuddhau — in the absence of intelligence; tat — that; adarśanāt — due to non-observation
   If this world is considered to be the work of one without intelligence, it is incongruous, as action is preceded by intelligence, and action is not observed in the absence of intelligence.
   
   Verse 40
   बह्वागमोपष्टम्भाच्च कर्ताऽत्र स्याद्धि बुद्धिमान्‌ ।
   बुद्धिमत्कर्तृकं कार्य सवेत्रैव हि दर्शनात्‌ ॥ ४० ॥
   bahu-āgama-upaṣṭambhāt ca kartā atra syāt hi buddhimān ।
   buddhi-mat-kartṛkam kāryam tatra eva hi darśanāt ॥ 40 ॥
   bahu-āgama — many scriptures; upaṣṭambhāt — supported by; ca — and; kartā — doer; atra — here; syāt — is; hi — indeed; buddhimān — intelligent; buddhi-mat-kartṛkam — done by an intelligent; kāryam — action; tatra — there; eva — indeed; hi — certainly; darśanāt — from observation
   Supported by many scriptures, the doer here is indeed intelligent. Action performed by an intelligent doer is certainly observed there.
   
   Verse 41
   एवं सत्तर्कागमाभ्यां जगदेतत्‌ सकर्तृकम्‌ ।
   स कर्ता लौकिकेभ्यस्तु कर्तृभ्यः स्यद्विलक्षणः ॥ ४१ ॥
   evaṁ sattarkāgamābhyāṁ jagat etat sakartṛkam ।
   sa kartā laukikebhyaḥ tu kartṛbhyaḥ syāt vilakṣaṇaḥ ॥ 41 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; sattarka-āgamābhyām — by sound reasoning and scriptures; jagat — world; etat — this; sakartṛkam — with a doer; saḥ — he; kartā — doer; laukikebhyaḥ — from worldly; tu — but; kartṛbhyaḥ — doers; syāt — would be; vilakṣaṇaḥ — distinct
   Thus, through sound reasoning and scripture, it is established that this world has a doer, but that doer is distinct from the worldly doers.
   
   Verse 42
   कार्यस्याचिन्त्यरूपत्वादचिन्त्यानन्तशक्तिकः ।
   अपरिच्छिन्नसामर्थ्यः कार्यस्यानुगुणत्वतः ॥ ४२ ॥
   kāryasya acintya-rūpatvāt acintya-ananta-śaktikaḥ ।
   aparicchinna-sāmarthyaḥ kāryasya anuguṇatvataḥ ॥ 42 ॥
   kāryasya — of the effect; acintya-rūpatvāt — due to inconceivable nature; acintya-ananta-śaktikaḥ — with inconceivable and infinite power; aparicchinna-sāmarthyaḥ — with unlimited capability; kāryasya — of the effect; anuguṇatvataḥ — due to conformity
   Due to the inconceivable nature of the effect, the doer possesses inconceivable and infinite power and unlimited capability, in accordance with the effect.
   
   Verse 43
   स प्रपन्नान्‌ समुद्धर्तु प्रभवत्येव सर्वथा ।
   अतस्तं सर्वभावेन शरणीकुरू सर्वदा ॥ ४३ ॥
   sa prapannān samuddhartu prabhavati eva sarvathā ।
   ataḥ tam sarva-bhāvena śaraṇīkuru sarvadā ॥ 43 ॥
   saḥ — he; prapannān — those who have surrendered; samuddhartu — to uplift; prabhavati — is capable; eva — indeed; sarvathā — in every way; ataḥ — therefore; tam — him; sarva-bhāvena — with all your being; śaraṇīkuru — take refuge; sarvadā — always
   He is indeed capable of uplifting those who have surrendered in every way. Therefore, always take refuge in him with all your being.
   
   Verse 44
   निदर्शनं तेऽभिधास्ये शृणु प्रत्ययकारणम्‌ ।
   मितेश्वरोऽप्यत्र लोके चाकापटयात्‌ प्रसादितः ॥ ४४ ॥
   nidarśanaṁ te abhidhāsyē śṛṇu pratyaya-kāraṇam ।
   mita-īśvaraḥ api atra loke ca akāpaṭayāt prasāditaḥ ॥ 44 ॥
   nidarśanam — example; te — to you; abhidhāsyē — will state; śṛṇu — listen; pratyaya-kāraṇam — the reason for belief; mita-īśvaraḥ — limited lord; api — even; atra — here; loke — in the world; ca — and; akāpaṭayāt — without deceit; prasāditaḥ — is pleased
   I will give you an example; listen to the reasoning with belief. Even a limited lord here in the world can be pleased without deceit.
   
   Verse 45
   सर्वात्मना योजयति स्वेष्टार्थैः श्रेयसे नरम्‌ ।
   एष लोकेश्वरो देवः सम्यग्‌ येन प्रसादितः ॥ ४५ ॥
   sarvātmanā yojayati sveṣṭārthaiḥ śreyase naram ।
   eṣa lokeśvaraḥ devaḥ samyak yena prasāditaḥ ॥ 45 ॥
   sarva-ātmanā — with all his being; yojayati — engages; sveṣṭārthaiḥ — with desired objects; śreyase — for welfare; naram — a man; eṣaḥ — this; lokeśvaraḥ — lord of the world; devaḥ — lord; samyak — properly; yena — by whom; prasāditaḥ — is pleased
   This lord of the world, when properly pleased by someone, provides a person with desired objects for their welfare.
   
   Verse 46
   तस्मै किं न दिशेद्‌ ब्रूहि भक्तलोकैकवत्सलः ।
   पुरुषा हीश्वरा लोके चानवस्था अवत्सलाः ॥ ४६ ॥
   tasmai kiṁ na diśet brūhi bhakta-loka-eka-vatsalaḥ ।
   puruṣāḥ hi īśvarā loke ca anavasthā avat-salāḥ ॥ 46 ॥
   tasmai — to him; kim — what; na diśet — would not give; brūhi — tell; bhakta-loka-eka-vatsalaḥ — the one who is the only affectionate to devotees; puruṣāḥ — men; hi — indeed; īśvarāḥ — lords; loke — in the world; ca — and; anavasthā — unstable; avat-salāḥ — not affectionate
   Tell me, what would the one who is uniquely affectionate to devotees not give to them? Indeed, worldly lords are unstable and lack true affection.
   
   Verse 47
   निर्दयाश्च कृतध्नाश्च तस्मात्‌ तत्फलमस्थिरम्‌ ।
   परमेशो दयासिन्धुः कृतज्ञः सुव्यवस्थितः ॥ ४७ ॥
   nirdayāḥ ca kṛtadhnāḥ ca tasmāt tat-phalam asthiram ।
   parama-īśaḥ dayā-sindhuḥ kṛtajñaḥ suvyavasthitaḥ ॥ 47 ॥
   nirdayāḥ — merciless; ca — and; kṛtadhnāḥ — ungrateful; ca — and; tasmāt — therefore; tat-phalam — their result; asthiram — unstable; parama-īśaḥ — the supreme lord; dayā-sindhuḥ — ocean of compassion; kṛtajñaḥ — grateful; suvyavasthitaḥ — well established
   Merciless and ungrateful, their results are therefore unstable. The supreme lord, however, is an ocean of compassion, grateful, and well established.
   
   Verse 48
   अन्यथाऽनादिसंसारे कुतोऽनिन्द्यत्वमाप्नुयात्‌ ।
   व्यवस्थिता जगद्यात्रा चापि वा स्यात्‌ कथं वद ॥ ४८ ॥
   anyathā anādi-saṁsāre kuto anindyatvam āpnuyāt ।
   vyavasthitā jagad-yātrā ca api vā syāt kathaṁ vada ॥ 48 ॥
   anyathā — otherwise; anādi-saṁsāre — in the beginningless cycle of existence; kutaḥ — how; anindyatvam — faultlessness; āpnuyāt — attain; vyavasthitā — established; jagad-yātrā — world’s course; ca — and; api vā — also; syāt — be; katham — how; vada — tell
   Otherwise, in the beginningless cycle of existence, how could one attain faultlessness? Tell me, how could the world's course be maintained?
   
   Verse 49
   अनवस्थस्य राज्यं तु नष्टमालोक्यते यतः ।
   तस्मादेष दयासिन्धुः सुव्यवस्थश्च कीर्तितः ॥ ४९ ॥
   anavasthasya rājyaṁ tu naṣṭam ālokyate yataḥ ।
   tasmāt eṣaḥ dayā-sindhuḥ suvyavasthaḥ ca kīrtitaḥ ॥ 49 ॥
   anavasthasya — of the unstable; rājyam — kingdom; tu — indeed; naṣṭam — lost; ālokyate — is seen; yataḥ — because; tasmāt — therefore; eṣaḥ — he; dayā-sindhuḥ — ocean of compassion; suvyavasthaḥ — well established; ca — and; kīrtitaḥ — described
   Because the kingdoms of the unstable are seen to be lost, he is therefore described as an ocean of compassion and well established.
   
   Verse 50
   तमेव सर्वभावेन भक्त्याशु शरणीकृरु ।
   श्रेयसि त्वां योजयेत्‌ स त्वं न तत्परतां व्रज ॥ ५० ॥
   tam eva sarva-bhāvena bhaktyā āśu śaraṇīkuru ।
   śreyasi tvām yojayet saḥ tvam na tat-paratāṁ vraja ॥ 50 ॥
   tam — him; eva — indeed; sarva-bhāvena — with all your being; bhaktyā — with devotion; āśu — quickly; śaraṇīkuru — take refuge; śreyasi — in welfare; tvām — you; yojayet — will engage; saḥ — he; tvam — you; na — not; tat-paratām — subordination; vraja — go
   Quickly take refuge in him with all your being and devotion. He will lead you to welfare; do not succumb to subordination.
   
   Verse 51
   उपासनं बहुविधमार्त्त्यार्थार्थित्वतोऽपि च ।
   निर्हेतुकं तु क्वाचित्कं तत्‌ सत्योपासनं भवेत्‌ ॥ ५१ ॥
   upāsanaṁ bahuvidham ārtārthārthitvataḥ api ca ।
   nirhetukaṁ tu kvacit kaṁ tat satyopāsanaṁ bhavet ॥ 51 ॥
   upāsanam — worship; bahuvidham — various kinds; ārta — for the distressed; arthārthitvataḥ — for wealth-seeking; api — also; ca — and; nirhetukam — causeless; tu — indeed; kvacit — somewhere; kam — it; tat — that; satya-upāsanam — true worship; bhavet — would be
   Worship comes in various forms, for the distressed and the wealth-seeking, but there is also causeless worship, and that is true worship.
   
   Verse 52
   दृष्टमेतत्‌ सर्वतो वै चार्त्तेनोपासितः प्रभुः ।
   कदाचिद्‌ दययाविष्ट आर्त्तिं तस्य विमोचयेत्‌ ॥ ५२ ॥
   dṛṣṭam etat sarvataḥ vai cārtā upāsitaḥ prabhuḥ ।
   kadācit dayayā āviṣṭaḥ ārttim tasya vimocayet ॥ 52 ॥
   dṛṣṭam — seen; etat — this; sarvataḥ — everywhere; vai — indeed; ārta — by the distressed; upāsitaḥ — worshipped; prabhuḥ — lord; kadācit — sometimes; dayayā — with compassion; āviṣṭaḥ — overcome; ārttim — distress; tasya — his; vimocayet — releases
   It is observed everywhere that when the distressed worship the lord, he sometimes, overcome with compassion, releases them from their suffering.
   
   Verse 53
   उपेक्षेत कदाचिद्वोपास्तेर्वै तारतम्यतः ।
   एवमेवार्थार्थिनोऽपि मितं चानियतं फलम्‌ ॥ ५३ ॥
   upekṣeta kadācit vā upāsteḥ vai tāratamyataḥ ।
   evam eva arthārthinaḥ api mitam ca aniyatam phalam ॥ 53 ॥
   upekṣeta — disregards; kadācit — sometimes; vā — or; upāsteḥ — worship; vai — indeed; tāratamyataḥ — due to differences; evam — thus; eva — indeed; arthārthinaḥ — wealth-seekers; api — also; mitam — limited; ca — and; aniyatam — uncertain; phalam — result
   Sometimes, he disregards worship due to differences; likewise, for wealth-seekers, the result is limited and uncertain.
   
   Verse 54
   निर्हेतुकोपासकस्य ज्ञात्वा निर्हेतुतां चिरात्‌ ।
   मितेश्वरोऽप्यव्यवस्थस्तदधीनो भवत्बलम्‌ ॥ ५४ ॥
   nirhetuka-upāsakasya jñātvā nirhetutām cirāt ।
   mitā-īśvaraḥ api avyavasthaḥ tad-adhīnaḥ bhavat balam ॥ 54 ॥
   nirhetuka-upāsakasya — of the causeless worshipper; jñātvā — knowing; nirhetutām — causelessness; cirāt — after a long time; mitā-īśvaraḥ — limited lord; api — also; avyavasthaḥ — unstable; tad-adhīnaḥ — dependent on that; bhavat — becomes; balam — strength
   Recognizing the sincerity of the causeless worshipper after a long time, even the limited and unstable lord becomes dependent on that devotion.
   
   Verse 55
   निर्हेतुकत्वज्ञानाय चिरं स्यादज्ञभावतः ।
   एष सर्वेश्वरो देवो हृदयेशोऽखिलस्य तु ॥ ५५ ॥
   nirhetukatva-jñānāya ciram syāt ajña-bhāvataḥ ।
   eṣaḥ sarveśvaraḥ devaḥ hṛdayeśaḥ akhilasya tu ॥ 55 ॥
   nirhetukatva-jñānāya — for knowing the causelessness; ciram — long time; syāt — may be; ajña-bhāvataḥ — due to ignorance; eṣaḥ — this; sarveśvaraḥ — lord of all; devaḥ — lord; hṛdayeśaḥ — lord of the heart; akhilasya — of all; tu — indeed
   Due to ignorance, it may take a long time to recognize causelessness. This lord of all is indeed the lord of the hearts of all.
   
   Verse 56
   सर्वं जानाति तत्काले फलं दद्याच्च सत्वरम्‌ ।
   आर्तमर्थार्थिनं देवस्तदर्थेनाभियोजितुम्‌ ॥ ५६ ॥
   sarvaṁ jānāti tat-kāle phalam dadyāt ca satvaram ।
   ārtam-arthārthinaṁ devaḥ tad-arthena abhiyojitum ॥ 56 ॥
   sarvam — everything; jānāti — knows; tat-kāle — at that time; phalam — result; dadyāt — gives; ca — and; satvaram — quickly; ārtam — distressed; arthārthinam — wealth-seeker; devaḥ — lord; tad-arthena — with that purpose; abhiyojitum — to engage
   The lord knows everything and quickly grants results to the distressed and the wealth-seeker, engaging them with their desired purpose.
   
   Verse 57
   स्वनियत्या कर्मपाकं प्रतीक्ष्य फलमादिशेत्‌ ।
   निर्हेतुकोपासकं स्वमनन्यशरणं विभुः ॥ ५७ ॥
   sva-niyatyā karma-pākam pratīkṣya phalam ādiśet ।
   nirhetuka-upāsakam sva-ananya-śaraṇam vibhuḥ ॥ 57 ॥
   sva-niyatyā — by his own law; karma-pākam — ripening of actions; pratīkṣya — waiting for; phalam — result; ādiśet — orders; nirhetuka-upāsakam — causeless worshipper; sva-ananya-śaraṇam — his exclusive refuge; vibhuḥ — lord
   By his own law, waiting for the ripening of actions, the lord determines the result for the causeless worshipper who takes exclusive refuge in him.
   
   Verse 58
   ज्ञात्वा सर्वात्मना तस्य योगक्षेमवहो भवेत्‌ ।
   अप्रतीक्ष्य कर्मपाकं नियतिं स्वां विधूय च ॥ ५८ ॥
   jñātvā sarvātmanaḥ tasya yoga-kṣema-vahaḥ bhavet ।
   apratīkṣya karma-pākam niyatim svām vidhūya ca ॥ 58 ॥
   jñātvā — knowing; sarvātmanaḥ — of all beings; tasya — his; yoga-kṣema-vahaḥ — provider of well-being; bhavet — becomes; apratīkṣya — without waiting; karma-pākam — ripening of actions; niyatim — law; svām — his own; vidhūya — shaking off; ca — and
   Knowing this, the lord becomes the provider of well-being for all beings, without waiting for the ripening of actions, setting aside his own law.
   
   Verse 59
   तत्साधनं सम्प्रसाध्य द्रुतं संयोजयेत्‌ फले ।
   एतदेव महेशत्वं स्वातन्त्र्यमहतं तु यत्‌ ॥ ५९ ॥
   tat-sādhanam samprasādhya drutam saṁyojayet phale ।
   etat eva maheśatvam svātantrya-mahatam tu yat ॥ 59 ॥
   tat-sādhanam — that means; samprasādhya — having accomplished; drutam — quickly; saṁyojayet — engages; phale — in the result; etat — this; eva — indeed; maheśatvam — lordship; svātantrya-mahatam — great independence; tu — but; yat — which
   Having accomplished that means, the lord quickly brings about the result; this is indeed true lordship and great independence.
   
   Verse 60
   प्रारब्धं नियतिर्वापि महेशविमुखे भवेत्‌ ।
   एतन्मृकण्डुतनयेऽत्यन्तमीश्वरतत्परे ॥ ६० ॥
   prārabdhaṁ niyatir vā api maheśa-vimukhe bhavet ।
   etat mṛkaṇḍu-tanaye atyantam īśvara-tatpare ॥ 60 ॥
   prārabdhaṁ — destined; niyatiḥ — law; vā — or; api — also; maheśa-vimukhe — opposing the lord; bhavet — becomes; etat — this; mṛkaṇḍu-tanaye — in the son of Mṛkaṇḍu; atyantam — exceedingly; īśvara-tatpare — devoted to the lord
   The lord also opposes destined law; this is seen in the case of Mṛkaṇḍu's son, who was exceedingly devoted to the lord.
   
   Verse 61
   सर्वैर्ज्ञातं महेशस्य नियत्यारब्धलङ्घनम् ।
