   iti matvā nirudhyānyabhāsanaṁ suvyavasthitaḥ ॥ 64 ॥
   asamyaḍ — incorrect; bhāsanam — perception; ca — and; anya-bhāsanasya — other perception; nimittataḥ — due to the cause; iti — thus; matvā — considering; nirudhya — stopping; anya-bhāsanam — other perceptions; suvyavasthitaḥ — well settled
   Incorrect perception arises from other perceptions. Considering this, I stopped those other perceptions and became well-settled.
   
   Verse 65
   अपश्यमन्धकारं च प्रकाशमन्यदेव च ।
   क्वचित्‌ सुखं महत्‌ प्राप्तं किमेतद्वद मे प्रिये ॥ ६५ ॥
   apaśyam-andhakāraṁ ca prakāśam-anyadeva ca ।
   kvacit sukhaṁ mahat prāptaṁ kim-etad-vad me priye ॥ 65 ॥
   apaśyam — I saw; andhakāram — darkness; ca — and; prakāśam — light; anyat — another; eva — indeed; ca — and; kvacit — sometimes; sukham — bliss; mahat — great; prāptam — obtained; kim — what; etat — this; vada — tell; me — to me; priye — dear
   I saw darkness and other time light, sometimes experiencing great bliss. What is this? Tell me, dear.
   
   Verse 66
   इदमेवात्मनो रूपमथवाऽन्यद्‌ भवेत्‌ क्वचित्‌ ।
   सम्यग्‌ विविच्य कथय यथा तमभिलक्षये ॥ ६६ ॥
   idam-evātmano rūpam-athavā'nyad bhavet kvacit ।
   samyag-vivicya kathaya yathā tam-abhilakṣaye ॥ 66 ॥
   idam — this; eva — indeed; ātmanaḥ — of the self; rūpam — form; athavā — or; anyat — another; bhavet — may be; kvacit — sometimes; samyak — properly; vivicya — discerning; kathaya — tell; yathā — as; tam — that; abhilakṣaye — I observe
   Is this truly the form of the self, or could it be something else? Properly discern it and tell me how I can observe it.
   
   Verse 67
   इत्युक्ता साऽब्रवीद्‌ हेमलेखा ज्ञातपरावरा ।
   शृणु प्रिय प्रवक्ष्यामि समाहितधियाऽखिलम्‌ ॥ ६७ ॥
   ityuktā sā'bravīd hemalekhā jñāta-parāvarā ।
   śṛṇu priya pravakṣyāmi samāhita-dhiyā'khilam ॥ 67 ॥
   iti-uktā — thus addressed; sā — she; abravīd — said; hemalekhā — Hemalekha; jñāta-parāvarā — knower of the ultimate; śṛṇu — listen; priya — dear; pravakṣyāmi — I will tell; samāhita-dhiyā — with concentrated mind; akhilam — all
   Thus addressed, Hemalekha, the knower of the ultimate, said: "Listen, dear, I will tell you everything with a concentrated mind."
   
   Verse 68
   यस्त्वया बाह्यसंरोधे व्यवसायः समेधितः ।
   स शुभः सम्मतः सर्वैः सुमुख्यश्चात्मवेदिभिः ॥ ६८ ॥
   yastvayā bāhya-saṁrodhe vyavasāyaḥ samedhitaḥ ।
   sa śubhaḥ sammataḥ sarvaiḥ sumukhyaś-cātma-vedibhiḥ ॥ 68 ॥
   yaḥ — which; tvayā — by you; bāhya-saṁrodhe — in external suppression; vyavasāyaḥ — effort; samedhitaḥ — undertaken; saḥ — that; śubhaḥ — auspicious; sammataḥ — approved; sarvaiḥ — by all; sumukhyaḥ — especially; ca — and; ātma-vedibhiḥ — by self-knowers
   The effort you made in external suppression is auspicious, approved by all, especially by those who know the self.
   
   Verse 69
   विना तेन न तत्‌ प्राप्तं केनापि कुत्रचित्‌ क्वचित्‌ ।
   न तत्‌ कारणतामेति तत्प्राप्तौ प्राप्तभावतः ॥ ६९ ॥
   vinā tena na tat prāptaṁ kenāpi kutracit kvacit ।
   na tat kāraṇatāmeti tat-prāptau prāpta-bhāvataḥ ॥ 69 ॥
   vinā — without; tena — that; na — not; tat — that; prāptam — obtained; kenāpi — by anyone; kutracit — anywhere; kvacit — anytime; na — not; tat — that; kāraṇatām — cause; eti — attains; tat-prāptau — in obtaining that; prāpta-bhāvataḥ — due to being obtained
   Without that, no one has attained it anywhere or anytime. However, it does not become a cause since it is always present.
   
   Verse 70
   अप्राप्तावात्मता न स्यादात्मत्वेऽनाप्तता कुतः ।
   अप्राप्यः सर्वथैवात्मा प्राप्तिस्तस्य न विद्यते ॥ ७० ॥
   aprāptāv-ātmatā na syād-ātmatve'nāptatā kutaḥ ।
   aprāpyaḥ sarvathaivātmā prāptis-tasya na vidyate ॥ 70 ॥
   aprāptau — in non-attainment; ātmatā — selfhood; na — not; syāt — be; ātmatve — in selfhood; anāptatā — non-attainment; kutaḥ — how; aprāpyaḥ — unattainable; sarvathā — in all ways; eva — indeed; ātmā — self; prāptiḥ — attainment; tasya — of that; na vidyate — does not exist
   If the self is not attained, selfhood cannot exist; and if selfhood exists, how can there be non-attainment? The self is unattainable by any means, as it is always present; thus, the concept of attaining it does not apply.
   
   Verse 71
   अप्राप्तस्य भवेत्‌ प्राप्तिरात्मत्वान्नाप्तिरस्त्यतः ।
   तन्निरोधोऽपि नाप्त्यर्थस्त्वत्र पश्य निदर्शनम्‌ ॥ ७१ ॥
   aprāptasya bhavet prāptir-ātmatvān-nāptir-astyataḥ ।
   tan-nirodho'pi nāptyarthas-tvatra paśya nidarśanam ॥ 71 ॥
   aprāptasya — of the unattained; bhavet — may be; prāptiḥ — attainment; ātmatvāt — due to selfhood; na — not; āptiḥ — attainment; asti — exists; ataḥ — therefore; tat-nirodhaḥ — its suppression; api — also; nāpti-arthaḥ — for the purpose of attainment; tvatra — here; paśya — see; nidarśanam — example
   For what is unattained, there can be attainment, but not for the self. Therefore, its suppression is not for the purpose of attainment. Here, consider an example.
   
   Verse 72
   अन्धकारसमाच्छन्नं किञ्चित्‌ तस्य निरोधतः ।
   दीपाद्यैराप्यते प्राप्तमिव लोके यथा तथा ॥ ७२ ॥
   andhakāra-samācchannaṁ kiñcit tasya nirodhataḥ ।
   dīpādyair-āpyate prāptam-iva loke yathā tathā ॥ 72 ॥
   andhakāra-samācchannam — covered by darkness; kiñcit — something; tasya — its; nirodhataḥ — due to suppression; dīpa-ādyaiḥ — by lamps; āpyate — is obtained; prāptam — attained; iva — as if; loke — in the world; yathā — just as; tathā — so
   Something covered by darkness is revealed when illuminated by lamps, as if it were newly attained. It is just like that.
   
   Verse 73
   यथा कश्चिद्‌ भ्रान्तचित्तः क्वचिद्विस्मृतनिष्ककः ।
   अन्यचिन्तानिरोधेन समाहिततया पुनः ॥ ७३ ॥
   yathā kaścid-bhrānta-cittaḥ kvacid-vismṛta-niṣkakaḥ ।
   anya-cintā-nirodhena samāhitatayā punaḥ ॥ 73 ॥
   yathā — just as; kaścit — someone; bhrānta-cittaḥ — with a confused mind; kvacit — somewhere; vismṛta-niṣkakaḥ — forgotten an ornament; anya-cintā-nirodhena — by suppressing other thoughts; samāhitatayā — with concentration; punaḥ — again
   Just as someone with a confused mind, having forgotten an ornament somewhere, suppresses other thoughts and, with concentration, recalls it again.
   
   Verse 74
   आसादयति तन्निष्कं नष्टं प्राप्तं यथा तथा ।
   न निरोधोऽत्र हेतुः स्यान्निष्काप्तौ तु यथा तथा ॥ ७४ ॥
   āsādayati tan-niṣkaṁ naṣṭaṁ prāptaṁ yathā tathā ।
   na nirodho'tra hetuḥ syān-niṣkāptau tu yathā tathā ॥ 74 ॥
   āsādayati — obtains; tat-niṣkam — that ornament; naṣṭam — lost; prāptam — attained; yathā — just as; tathā — so; na — not; nirodhaḥ — suppression; atra — here; hetuḥ — cause; syāt — may be; niṣkāptau — in the attainment of the ornament; tu — but; yathā — as; tathā — so
   Just as one recovers a lost ornament, it is as if it were newly found. Suppression is not the cause of its recovery; rather, it is the means to rediscover the ornament as it truly is.
   
   Verse 75
   आत्मलाभे न हेतु: स्यान्निरोधो बाह्यवस्तुनः ।
   त्वया न लक्षितः स्वात्मा तत्र व्युत्पत्तिवर्जनात्‌ ॥ ७५ ॥
   ātma-lābhe na hetuḥ syān-nirodho bāhya-vastunaḥ ।
   tvayā na lakṣitaḥ svātmā tatra vyutpatti-varjanāt ॥ 75 ॥
   ātma-lābhe — in the attainment of the self; na — not; hetuḥ — cause; syāt — may be; nirodhaḥ — suppression; bāhya-vastunaḥ — of external objects; tvayā — by you; na — not; lakṣitaḥ — perceived; svātmā — self; tatra — there; vyutpatti-varjanāt — due to lack of comprehension
   Similarly, in attaining the self, the suppression of external objects is not the cause. You have not yet perceived the self because of a lack of comprehension.
   
   Verse 76
   यथा प्रकाशेऽव्युत्पन्नो रात्रौ राजसभां गतः ।
   पश्यन्‌ सभ्यांश्च दीपांश्च न जानाति प्रकाशकम्‌ ॥ ७६ ॥
   yathā prakāśe'vyutpanno rātrau rāja-sabhāṁ gataḥ ।
   paśyan sabhyāṁśca dīpāṁśca na jānāti prakāśakam ॥ 76 ॥
   yathā — just as; prakāśe — in light; avyutpannaḥ — unlearned; rātrau — at night; rāja-sabhām — royal assembly; gataḥ — having gone; paśyan — seeing; sabhyān — courtiers; ca — and; dīpān — lamps; ca — and; na — not; jānāti — knows; prakāśakam — illuminator
   Just as an unlearned person, entering the royal assembly at night, sees the courtiers and lamps but does not recognize the real source of the illumination (the self).
   
   Verse 77
   शृणु प्रिय निरोधान्ते ह्यन्धकारो विलोकितः ।
   अन्धकारावलोकादौ शेषभावस्तव स्थितः ॥ ७७ ॥
   śṛṇu priya nirodhānte hyandhakāro vilokitaḥ ।
   andhakāra-avalokādau śeṣa-bhāvas-tava sthitaḥ ॥ 77 ॥
   śṛṇu — listen; priya — dear; nirodha-ante — at the end of suppression; hi — indeed; andhakāraḥ — darkness; vilokitaḥ — seen; andhakāra-avaloka-ādau — at the beginning of seeing darkness; śeṣa-bhāvaḥ — remaining state; tava — your; sthitaḥ — established
   Listen, dear, when suppression ends, darkness is seen. At the beginning of seeing this darkness, your true state is established.
   
   Verse 78
   तं भावं भावय सदा परमानन्ददायकम्‌ ।
   अत्र सर्वे महामोहग्रहग्रस्ताः पराग्दृशः ॥ ७८ ॥
   taṁ bhāvaṁ bhāvaya sadā paramānanda-dāyakam ।
   atra sarve mahā-moha-graha-grastāḥ parāg-dṛśaḥ ॥ 78 ॥
   tam — that; bhāvam — state; bhāvaya — contemplate; sadā — always; paramānanda-dāyakam — giving supreme bliss; atra — here; sarve — all; mahā-moha-graha-grastāḥ — seized by the great delusion; parāg-dṛśaḥ — outward-seeing
   Contemplate that state always, as it provides supreme bliss. Here in this world, all are ensnared by the great delusion of outward perception.
   
   Verse 79
   अन्विष्यान्विष्य विहता न तां प्रापुश्च भावनाम्‌ ।
   सन्ति लोके शास्त्रविदः कुशलाश्च सुतार्किकाः ॥ ७९ ॥
   anviṣyānviṣya vihatā na tāṁ prāpuśca bhāvanām ।
   santi loke śāstra-vidaḥ kuśalāśca sutārkikāḥ ॥ 79 ॥
   anviṣya-anviṣya — searching and searching; vihatāḥ — obstructed; na — not; tām — that; prāpuḥ — attained; ca — and; bhāvanām — state; santi — are; loke — in the world; śāstra-vidaḥ — scholars; kuśalāḥ — skilled; ca — and; su-tārkikāḥ — good logicians
   Searching and searching, they were obstructed and did not attain that state. In the world, there are scholars, skilled and excellent logicians.
   
   Verse 80
   अविदित्वा भावममुं शोचन्त्येव दिवानिशम्‌ ।
   शब्दार्थशिल्पमात्रेण नहि तत्पदमाप्यते ॥ ८० ॥
   aviditvā bhāvam-amuṁ śocantyeva divāniśam ।
   śabdārtha-śilpa-mātreṇa nahi tat-padam-āpyate ॥ 80 ॥
   aviditvā — not knowing; bhāvam — state; amum — that; śocanti — they grieve; eva — indeed; divā-niśam — day and night; śabda-artha-śilpa-mātreṇa — by mere word-craft; nahi — not; tat-padam — that state; āpyate — is attained
   Not knowing that state, they grieve day and night. That state cannot be attained by mere word-craft.
   
   Verse 81
   यावदन्वेषणं कुर्याद्विचारं वापि पण्डितः ।
   तावन्न प्राप्यते तद्वै यतो न ग्राह्यमेव तत्‌ ॥ ८१ ॥
   yāvad-anveṣaṇaṁ kuryād-vicāraṁ vāpi paṇḍitaḥ ।
   tāvanna prāpyate tadvai yato na grāhyameva tat ॥ 81 ॥
   yāvat — as long as; anveṣaṇam — searching; kuryāt — does; vicāram — contemplation; vā api — or even; paṇḍitaḥ — learned person; tāvat — until then; na prāpyate — is not attained; tat — that; vai — indeed; yataḥ — because; na grāhyam — not graspable; eva — certainly; tat — that
   As long as a learned person searches or contemplates, it remains unattainable because it cannot be grasped.
   
   Verse 82
   गत्वा दूरं न तत्‌ प्राप्यं स्थित्वा प्राप्तं हि सर्वदा ।
   न तद्विचार्य विज्ञेयमविचाराद्‌ विभासते ॥ ८२ ॥
   gatvā dūraṁ na tat prāpyaṁ sthitvā prāptaṁ hi sarvadā ।
   na tadvicārya vijñeyam-avicārād vibhāsate ॥ 82 ॥
   gatvā — having gone; dūram — far; na tat — not that; prāpyam — attainable; sthitvā — by staying; prāptam — attained; hi — indeed; sarvadā — always; na tat — not that; vicārya — by contemplating; vijñeyam — knowable; avicārāt — without contemplation; vibhāsate — shines
   Having gone far, it is unattainable, but by remaining still, it is always present. It cannot be known through contemplation; it shines without contemplation.
   
   Verse 83
   धावन्‌ स्वमूर्धच्छायेव न प्राप्यं क्रियया क्वचित्‌ ।
   यथा हि निर्मलादर्शे प्रतिबिम्बसहस्रकम्‌ ॥ ८३ ॥
   dhāvan svamūrdhacchāyeva na prāpyaṁ kriyayā kvacit ।
   yathā hi nirmalādarśe pratibimba-sahasrakam ॥ 83 ॥
   dhāvan — running; sva-mūrdhacchāyā iva — like one's own shadow on the head; na prāpyam — not attainable; kriyayā — by action; kvacit — anywhere; yathā — just as; hi — indeed; nirmala-ādarśe — in a clean mirror; pratibimba-sahasrakam — thousands of reflections
   Chasing it is like trying to catch one's shadow on the head; it cannot be attained through action anywhere. Just as in a clean mirror, thousands of reflections are seen (so is this world).
   
   Verse 84
   पश्यन्‌ बालोऽपि नादर्श पश्यत्येवं जनः खलु ।
   पश्यन्‌ स्वात्ममहादर्शे प्रतिबिम्बं हि जागतम्‌ ॥ ८४ ॥
   paśyan bālo'pi nādarśa paśyatyevaṁ janaḥ khalu ।
   paśyan svātma-mahā-darśe pratibimbaṁ hi jāgatam ॥ 84 ॥
   paśyan — seeing; bālaḥ — child; api — even; na adarśaḥ — not seeing; paśyati — sees; evam — thus; janaḥ — person; khalu — indeed; paśyan — seeing; sva-ātma-mahā-darśe — in the great mirror of the self; pratibimbam — reflection; hi — indeed; jāgatam — the world
   Just as a child sees reflections but does not see the mirror; likewise, a person sees the reflection of the world in the great mirror of the self.
   
   Verse 85
   स्वात्मानं न विजानाति तद्व्युत्पत्तिविवर्जनात्‌ ।
   यथा परिचिताकाशः पश्यन्नाकाशसंश्रितम्‌ ॥ ८५ ॥
   svātmānaṁ na vijānāti tad-vyutpatti-vivarjanāt ।
   yathā paricita-ākāśaḥ paśyan ākāśa-saṁśritam ॥ 85 ॥
   svātmānam — self; na vijānāti — does not know; tad-vyutpatti-vivarjanāt — due to lack of understanding; yathā — just as; paricita-ākāśaḥ — familiar with the sky; paśyan — seeing; ākāśa-saṁśritam — residing in the sky
   One does not know the self due to a lack of understanding, just as someone familiar with the sky sees it but does not fully realize what it is.
   
   Verse 86
   जगन्नावैति चाकाशं तथा स्वात्मस्वरूपकम्‌ ।
   नाथ सूक्ष्मदृशा पश्य ज्ञानज्ञेयात्मकं जगत्‌ ॥ ८६ ॥
   jagannāveti cākāśaṁ tathā svātma-svarūpakam ।
   nātha sūkṣma-dṛśā paśya jñāna-jñeyātmakam jagat ॥ 86 ॥
   jagat — the world; na aveti — does not realize; ca — and; ākāśam — sky; tathā — so; sva-ātma-svarūpakam — the nature of the self; nātha — lord; sūkṣma-dṛśā — with subtle vision; paśya — see; jñāna-jñeya-ātmakam — of the nature of knowledge and the known; jagat — the world
   The world does not realize the sky; similarly, it does not comprehend the nature of the self. Lord, with subtle vision, see the world as composed of the nature of knowledge and the known.
   
   Verse 87
   तत्र ज्ञानं स्वतः सिद्धं तदभावे न किञ्चन ।
   प्रमाणानां प्रमाणं तदप्रमाणं स्वतो भवेत्‌ ॥ ८७ ॥
   tatra jñānaṁ svataḥ siddhaṁ tad-abhāve na kiñcana ।
   pramāṇānāṁ pramāṇaṁ tad-apramāṇaṁ svato bhavet ॥ 87 ॥
   tatra — there; jñānam — knowledge; svataḥ — self-established; siddham — established; tad-abhāve — in its absence; na kiñcana — nothing; pramāṇānām — of the means of knowledge; pramāṇam — the measure; tad — that; apramāṇam — non-measure; svataḥ — self-established; bhavet — is
   Knowledge is self-established; in its absence, nothing exists. It is the measure of all means of knowledge and stands on its own.
   
   Verse 88
   यतः प्रमाणानपेक्षमादिसिद्धमतस्तु तत्‌ ।
   सिद्धिसाधकभावेन न तत्सिद्धिः कदाचन ॥ ८८ ॥
   yataḥ pramāṇān-apekṣam-ādi-siddham-ataḥ tu tat ।
   siddhi-sādhaka-bhāvena na tat-siddhiḥ kadācana ॥ 88 ॥
   yataḥ — since; pramāṇān-apekṣam — independent of means of knowledge; ādi-siddham — self-established from the beginning; ataḥ — therefore; tu — but; tat — that; siddhi-sādhaka-bhāvena — in the nature of being the means to attainment; na — not; tat-siddhiḥ — its attainment; kadācana — ever
   Since it is independent of means of knowledge and self-established from the beginning, it is not attained by the means of attainment.
   
   Verse 89
   तत्र विप्रतिपन्नस्य न प्रश्नो नापि चोत्तरम्‌ ।
   अनपह्नवनीयं तन्महादर्शतलं भवेत्‌ ॥ ८९ ॥
   tatra vipratipannasya na praśno nāpi cottaram ।
   anapahnavanīyaṁ tan-mahādarśatalaṁ bhavet ॥ 89 ॥
   tatra — there; vipratipannasya — for the confused; na praśnaḥ — no question; na api — nor; ca — and; uttaram — answer; anapahnavanīyam — not to be denied; tat — that; mahā-darśa-talam — great mirror; bhavet — is
   For the confused, there is neither question nor answer. That great mirror cannot be denied.
   
   Verse 90
   तत्र सर्व भासते वै दर्पणप्रतिबिम्बवत्‌ ।
   देशेन वापि कालेन परिच्छित्तिर्न विद्यते ॥ ९० ॥
   tatra sarva bhāsate vai darpaṇa-pratibimba-vat ।
   deśena vāpi kālena paricchittir-na vidyate ॥ 90 ॥
   tatra — there; sarva — all; bhāsate — shines; vai — indeed; darpaṇa-pratibimba-vat — like the reflection in a mirror; deśena — by space; vā api — or even; kālena — by time; paricchittiḥ — limitation; na vidyate — does not exist
   There, everything shines like a reflection in a mirror. There are no limitations of space or time.
   
   Verse 91
   तदन्तर्भासमानत्वात्‌ कथं ताभ्यां परिच्छिदिः ।
   परिच्छेदस्य भानं तु गगने वस्तुभिर्यथा ॥ ९१ ॥
   tad-antar-bhāsamānatvāt kathaṁ tābhyāṁ paricchidiḥ ।
   paricchedasya bhānaṁ tu gagane vastubhir-yathā ॥ 91 ॥
   tat — that; antar — within; bhāsamānatvāt — due to shining; katham — how; tābhyām — by them; paricchidiḥ — limitation; paricchedasya — of limitation; bhānam — appearance; tu — but; gagane — in the sky; vastubhiḥ — by objects; yathā — as
   Since it shines from within, how can there be limitations of space or time? The appearance of such limitations is like objects appearing in the sky (for the sky is unaffected by them).
   
   Verse 92
   राजपुत्र ! सूक्ष्मदृशा तल्लक्षय निजं वपुः ।
   यत्र सामान्यचैतन्ये जगदेतद्‌ विराजते ॥ ९२ ॥
   rāja-putra! sūkṣma-dṛśā tal-lakṣaya nijaṁ vapuḥ ।
   yatra sāmānya-caitanye jagad-etad virājate ॥ 92 ॥
   rāja-putra — prince; sūkṣma-dṛśā — with subtle vision; tat-lakṣaya — observe that; nijaṁ vapuḥ — own self; yatra — where; sāmānya-caitanye — in the universal consciousness; jagat — world; etad — this; virājate — shines
   Prince, with subtle vision, observe your own self in which this world shines within the universal consciousness.
   
   Verse 93
   तत्समावेशसंसिद्धया सर्वकर्तृत्वमाप्नुयात्‌ ।
   तस्योपलब्धिं वक्ष्यामि यतः प्राप्नोषि तत्पदम्‌ ॥ ९३ ॥
   tat-samāveśa-saṁsiddhayā sarva-kartṛtvam-āpnuyāt ।
   tasya-upalabdhiṁ vakṣyāmi yataḥ prāpnoṣi tat-padam ॥ 93 ॥
   tat-samāveśa-saṁsiddhayā — by the perfection of absorption in that; sarva-kartṛtvam — all-doership; āpnuyāt — attains; tasya — its; upalabdhim — realization; vakṣyāmi — I will tell; yataḥ — from which; prāpnoṣi — you attain; tat-padam — that state
   Through perfect absorption in that, one attains complete doership. I will explain the realization through which you can achieve that state.
   
   Verse 94
   निद्राजाग्रन्मध्यभागे संविद्भेदान्तरे तथा ।
   मध्ये संविद्वेद्ययोश्च सूक्ष्मबुद्धयाऽभिलक्षय ॥ ९४ ॥
   nidrā-jāgran-madhya-bhāge saṁvid-bhedāntare tathā ।
   madhye saṁvid-vedyayoś-ca sūkṣma-buddhyā'bhilakṣaya ॥ 94 ॥
   nidrā — sleep; jāgran — waking; madhya-bhāge — middle part; saṁvid-bhedāntare — between the states of consciousness; tathā — and; madhye — between; saṁvid — consciousness; vedyayoḥ — and the known; ca — and; sūkṣma-buddhyā — with subtle intellect; abhilakṣaya — observe
   Observe with subtle intellect the state between sleep and waking, between different states of consciousness, and between consciousness and the known (the world).
   
   Verse 95
   एतत्पदं निजं रूपं यत्‌ प्राप्य न विमुह्यति ।
   एतदज्ञानमात्रेण प्रवृत्तं जगदीदृशम्‌ ॥ ९५ ॥
   etat-padam nijaṁ rūpam yat prāpya na vimuhyati ।
   etat-ajñāna-mātreṇa pravṛttaṁ jagad-īdṛśam ॥ 95 ॥
   etat-padam — this state; nijaṁ rūpam — own form; yat — which; prāpya — attaining; na vimuhyati — does not become deluded; etat-ajñāna-mātreṇa — by mere ignorance of this; pravṛttam — continues; jagat — world; īdṛśam — like this
   This state is one's own true form, and upon attaining it, one is no longer deluded. The world continues in its confusion due to ignorance of this truth.
   
   Verse 96
   नात्र रूपं रसो वापि न गन्धस्पर्शशब्दनम्‌ ।
   न दुःखं न सुखं वा तु न ग्राह्यं ग्राहकं च न ॥ ९६ ॥
   nātra rūpaṁ raso vāpi na gandha-sparśa-śabdnam ।
   na duḥkhaṁ na sukhaṁ vā tu na grāhyaṁ grāhakaṁ ca na ॥ 96 ॥
   na atra — not here; rūpam — form; rasaḥ — taste; vā api — nor even; gandha — smell; sparśa — touch; śabda — sound; na duḥkham — no sorrow; na sukham — no happiness; vā tu — nor indeed; na grāhyam — nothing to be grasped; grāhakam — grasper; ca — and; na — not
   Here, there is no form, taste, smell, touch, or sound. There is no sorrow or happiness, nothing to be grasped, and no one to grasp.
   
   Verse 97
   सर्वाश्रयं सर्वरूपमपि सर्वविवर्जितम्‌ ।
   एष सर्वेश्वरो धाता विष्णुरीशः सदाशिवः ॥ ९७ ॥
   sarvāśrayaṁ sarva-rūpam-api sarva-vivarjitam ।
   eṣa sarveśvaro dhātā viṣṇur-īśaḥ sadāśivaḥ ॥ 97 ॥
   sarva-āśrayam — supporting all; sarva-rūpam — in all forms; api — even; sarva-vivarjitam — devoid of all; eṣaḥ — this; sarva-īśvaraḥ — lord of all; dhātā — sustainer; viṣṇuḥ — Vishnu; īśaḥ — Ishvara; sadā-śivaḥ — Sadashiva
   This is the supreme lord, supporting all, embodying all forms yet devoid of all, the sustainer — Vishnu, Ishvara, and Sadashiva.
   
   Verse 98
   पश्येषदन्तः संरुध्य स्वात्मानं स्वात्मना सता ।
   त्यक्त्वा बहिःप्रसरतामन्तःप्रसरणोद्यतः ॥ ९८ ॥
   paśya eṣat-antaḥ saṁrudhya svātmānaṁ svātmanā satā ।
   tyaktvā bahiḥ-prasaratām-antaḥ-prasaraṇa-udyataḥ ॥ 98 ॥
   paśya — see; eṣat — slightly; antaḥ — within; saṁrudhya — restraining; svātmānam — self; svātmanā — by the self; satā — being; tyaktvā — giving up; bahiḥ-prasaratām — external expansion; antaḥ-prasaraṇa-udyataḥ — striving for inner expansion
   See, restraining slightly within the self by the self, giving up external expansion, striving for inner expansion.
   
   Verse 99
   त्यक्त्वा पश्यामीति भावमन्धवन्निश्चलात्मना ।
   दर्शनादर्शने त्यक्त्वा योऽसि सोऽसि द्रुतं भज ॥ ९९ ॥
   tyaktvā paśyāmīti bhāvam-andha-vat-niścalātmanā ।
   darśanādarśane tyaktvā yo'asi so'asi drutaṁ bhaja ॥ 99 ॥
   tyaktvā — giving up; paśyāmi iti — the thought "I see"; andha-vat — like a blind person; niścala-ātmanā — with a steady mind; darśana-adarśane — seeing and not seeing; tyaktvā — giving up; yaḥ asi — who you are; saḥ asi — that you are; drutam — quickly; bhaja — realize
   Let go of the thought "I see", and, like a blind person with a steady mind, relinquish seeing and not seeing. Quickly realize who you are.
   
   Verse 100
   इत्युक्तः प्रियया हेमचूड आलक्ष्य तत्‌ पदम्‌ ।
   चिरं विश्रान्तिमालभ्य बहिर्विस्मरणं ययौ ॥ १०० ॥
   ity-uktaḥ priyayā hemacūḍa ālakṣya tat padam ।
   ciraṁ viśrāntim ālabhya bahir vismaraṇaṁ yayau ॥ 100 ॥
   iti uktaḥ — thus spoken; priyayā — by the beloved; hemacūḍaḥ — Hemachuda; ālakṣya — realizing; tat padam — that state; ciram — long; viśrāntim — rest; ālabhya — attaining; bahiḥ — outwardly; vismaraṇam — forgetting; yayau — went
   Thus spoken by his beloved, Hemachuda, having realized that state, attained deep rest, and forgot the outward world.


   
   इति श्रीत्रिपुरारहस्ये ज्ञानखण्डे हेमचूडविश्रान्तिर्नाम नवमोऽध्यायः ॥
   
   Thus ends the ninth chapter named "Hemachuda's Rest" in the revered Knowledge Section of Tripura Rahasya.
   
   
   

10. CONCLUSION OF HEMACHUDA’S STORY
   Verse 1
   अथाऽपश्यद्धेमलेखा प्रियं प्राप्तपरस्थितिम्‌ ।
   न चालयत्‌ परपदात्ततः सोऽपि मुहूर्ततः ॥ १ ॥
   athā'paśyad-hemalekhā priyaṁ prāpta-parasthitim ।
   na cālayat para-padāt tataḥ so'pi muhūrtataḥ ॥ 1 ॥
   atha — then; apaśyat — saw; hemalekhā — Hemalekha; priyam — beloved; prāpta — having attained; parasthitim — the state beyond; na cālayat — did not move; para-padāt — from the supreme state; tataḥ — then; saḥ — he; api — also; muhūrtataḥ — for a moment
   Then Hemalekha saw that her beloved, having attained the supreme state, remained unmoved from it even for a moment.
   
   Verse 2
   प्रबुद्ध उन्मील्य नेत्रे अपश्यत्‌ सप्रियं जगत्‌ ।
   भूयस्तत्पदविश्रान्तिमीहमानोऽतिवेगतः ॥ २ ॥
   prabuddha unmīlya netre apaśyat sa-priyaṁ jagat ।
   bhūyas-tat-pada-viśrāntim-īhamāno'ti-vegataḥ ॥ 2 ॥
   prabuddha — awakened; unmīlya — opening; netre — eyes; apaśyat — saw; sa — he; priyam — beloved; jagat — world; bhūyas — again; tat-pada — that state; viśrāntim — rest; īhamānaḥ — desiring; ati-vegataḥ — with great speed
   Awakened, he opened his eyes and saw the beloved world, but desiring to return to that state of rest with great urgency.
   
   Verse 3
   नेत्रे निन्यमीलयद्यावदब्रवीत्तावदेव सा ।
   प्रियं हस्ते समादाय सुधासुन्दरभाषिणी ॥ ३ ॥
   netre ninyamīlayad-yāvad-abravīt tāvadeva sā ।
   priyaṁ haste samādāya sudhā-sundara-bhāṣiṇī ॥ 3 ॥
   netre — eyes; ninyamīlayat — closing; yāvat — as; abravīt — spoke; tāvadeva — at that moment; sā — she; priyam — beloved; haste — in hand; samādāya — taking; sudhā-sundara-bhāṣiṇī — speaking sweetly
   As he closed his eyes, she took his hand and spoke sweetly to him.
   
   Verse 4
   नाथ किं ते व्यवसितं ब्रूहि नेत्रनिमीलनात्‌ ।
   उन्मीलनाद्वा कि स्यात्ते लाभालाभौ समीरय ॥ ४ ॥
   nātha kiṁ te vyavasitaṁ brūhi netra-nimīlanāt ।
   unmīlanād-vā ki syāt-te lābhālābhau samīraya ॥ 4 ॥
   nātha — lord; kim — what; te — your; vyavasitam — intention; brūhi — tell; netra-nimīlanāt — from closing eyes; unmīlanāt-vā — or opening; ki — what; syāt-te — happened to you; lābhālābhau — gain or loss; samīraya — consider
   Lord, what was your intention? Tell me what happened to you when you closed or opened your eyes. Reflect on your gain or loss.
   
   Verse 5
   उन्मील्य न प्राप्यते कि निमील्य प्राप्यते च किम्‌ ।
   तन्मे ब्रूहि प्रियतम श्रोतुमिच्छामि ते स्थितिम्‌ ॥ ५ ॥
   unmīlya na prāpyate ki nimīlya prāpyate ca kim ।
   tan-me brūhi priyatama śrotum-icchāmi te sthitim ॥ 5 ॥
   unmīlya — opening eyes; na prāpyate — not attained; ki — what; nimīlya — closing eyes; prāpyate ca — is attained; kim — what; tan-me — tell me; priyatama — beloved; śrotum-icchāmi — I wish to hear; te sthitim — your state
   When you open your eyes, what is not attained? And what is attained by closing them? Beloved, tell me; I wish to understand your state.
   
   Verse 6
   एवं पृष्टस्तया प्राह मदमत्त इवालसः ।
   अनिच्छन्नपि वक्तुं तामालस्यभरमन्थरः ॥ ६ ॥
   evaṁ pṛṣṭas-tayā prāha madamatta ivālasaḥ ।
   anicchann-api vaktuṁ tām ālasya-bhara-mantharaḥ ॥ 6 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; pṛṣṭaḥ — asked; tayā — by her; prāha — spoke; mada-mattaḥ — like an intoxicated person; iva — as if; ālasaḥ — lazy; anicchan — unwilling; api — even; vaktum — to speak; tām — to her; ālasya-bhara-mantharaḥ — weighed down by laziness
   Thus asked by her, he spoke as if intoxicated, lazy, and reluctant, weighed down by his laziness.
   
   Verse 7
   प्रिये विश्रान्तिमत्यन्तं प्राप्तवानस्मि वै चिरात्‌ ।
   न बाह्ये दुःखभूयिष्ठे विश्रमोऽस्ति क्वचिन्मम ॥ ७ ॥
   priye viśrāntim-atyantaṁ prāptavān-asmi vai cirāt ।
   na bāhye duḥkha-bhūyiṣṭhe viśramo'sti kvacin mama ॥ 7 ॥
   priye — beloved; viśrāntim-atyantam — utmost rest; prāptavān — I have attained; asmi — I am; vai — indeed; cirāt — after a long time; na bāhye — not in the external; duḥkha-bhūyiṣṭhe — full of sorrow; viśramaḥ — rest; asti — is; kvacin — anywhere; mama — for me
   Beloved, I have attained the deepest rest after a long time. There is no rest for me in the external world, which is full of sorrow.
   
   Verse 8
   अलमृजीषरोमन्थप्रायव्यवहृतैर्बहिः ।
   दौर्भाग्यान्धो नाद्य यावदविदं स्वात्मसत्सुखम्‌ ॥ ८ ॥
   alam-ṛjīṣa-romanthapraaya-vyavahṛtaiḥ bahiḥ ।
   daurbhāgyāndho nādya yāvad-avidam svātma-sat-sukham ॥ 8 ॥
   alam — enough; ṛjīṣa — effort; romanthapraaya — contemplation; vyavahṛtaiḥ — with activities; bahiḥ — external; daurbhāgya-andhaḥ — blinded by misfortune; na adya — not now; yāvat — until; avidam — I knew; svātma-sat-sukham — true happiness of the self
   Enough of external efforts and contemplations. Blinded by misfortune, I did not recognize the true happiness of the self until now.
   
   Verse 9
   यथा कश्चिदटन्‌ भिक्षां निवानं स्वं न वेद वै ।
   तथाऽहं स्वसुखाम्भोधिमविदित्वा पुनः पुनः ॥ ९ ॥
   yathā kaścid-aṭan bhikṣāṁ nivānaṁ svaṁ na veda vai ।
   tathā'ham sva-sukhāmbhodhim-aviditvā punaḥ punaḥ ॥ 9 ॥
   yathā — as; kaścid — someone; aṭan — wandering; bhikṣām — alms; nivānam — home; svam — his; na veda — does not know; vai — indeed; tathā — similarly; aham — I; sva-sukha-ambhodhim — ocean of own happiness; aviditvā — not knowing; punaḥ punaḥ — again and again
   Just as someone wandering for alms not knowing their own home, I did not recognize the ocean of my own happiness, again and again.
   
   Verse 10
   सुखं वैषयिकं श्रेष्ठं दुःखसंघाभिसंप्लुतम्‌ ।
   विद्युद्विलयनं मत्वा स्थिरं तत्परतावशात्‌ ॥ १० ॥
   sukhaṁ vaiṣayikaṁ śreṣṭhaṁ duḥkha-saṁghābhisamplutam ।
   vidyud-vilayanaṁ matvā sthiraṁ tat-paratāvaśāt ॥ 10 ॥
   sukham — happiness; vaiṣayikam — sensory; śreṣṭham — best; duḥkha-saṁghābhisamplutam — filled with a mass of sorrows; vidyut-vilayanam — like lightning; matvā — thinking; sthiram — stable; tat-paratā-vaśāt — due to attachment to that
   Thinking that sensory pleasure to be superior, though it is overwhelmed by a flood of sorrows and is as fleeting as lightning, I sought stability due to my attachment to it.
   
   Verse 11
   दुःखैरभिहतो नूनं विश्रान्तिं न तु लब्धवान्‌ ।
   अहो जना दुःखसुखविवेकज्ञानवर्जिताः ॥ ११ ॥
   duḥkhair-abhi-hato nūnaṁ viśrāntiṁ na tu labdhavān ।
   aho janā duḥkha-sukha-viveka-jñāna-varjitāḥ ॥ 11 ॥
   duḥkhaiḥ — by sorrows; abhihataḥ — afflicted; nūnam — surely; viśrāntim — rest; na tu — not; labdhavān — attained; aho — alas; janāḥ — people; duḥkha-sukha-viveka-jñāna-varjitāḥ — devoid of discrimination between sorrow and happiness
   Afflicted by sorrows, I did not find rest. Alas, people lack the discernment between sorrow and happiness.
   
   Verse 12
   सुखार्थिनो दुःखसंघं सञ्चिन्वन्ति मुधा सदा ।
   तदलं दुःखभोगेन स्वयत्नासादितेन वै ॥ १२ ॥
   sukhārthino duḥkha-saṁghaṁ sañcinvanti mudhā sadā ।
   tad-alaṁ duḥkha-bhogena svayatnā-sāditena vai ॥ 12 ॥
   sukhārthinaḥ — seekers of happiness; duḥkha-saṁgham — collection of sorrows; sañcinvanti — gather; mudhā — foolishly; sadā — always; tad — that; alam — enough; duḥkha-bhogena — with experiencing sorrow; svayatnā-sāditena — self-acquired; vai — indeed
   Seekers of happiness often foolishly amass a collection of sorrows. I have had enough of this self-inflicted suffering.
   
   Verse 13
   प्रिये कृपां मयि कुरु प्रार्थयामि कृताञ्जलिः ।
   विश्रान्तिमभिवाञ्छामि चिरं स्वस्मिन्‌ सुखात्मनि ॥ १३ ॥
   priye kṛpāṁ mayi kuru prārthayāmi kṛtāñjaliḥ ।
   viśrāntim-abhi-vāñchāmi ciraṁ svasmin sukhātmani ॥ 13 ॥
   priye — beloved; kṛpām — mercy; mayi — on me; kuru — do; prārthayāmi — I request; kṛtāñjaliḥ — with folded hands; viśrāntim — rest; abhi-vāñchāmi — I wish; ciram — long; svasmin — in myself; sukhātmani — in the blissful self
   Beloved, please have mercy on me. With folded hands, I request a long rest in my own blissful self.
   
   Verse 14
   अहो दैवहता भासि ज्ञात्वापि त्वमिदं पदम्‌ ।
   तद्वश्रान्तिं परित्यज्य मुधा दुःखाय चेष्टसे ॥ १४ ॥
   aho daiva-hatā bhāsi jñātvā-api tvam-idaṁ padam ।
   tad-viśrāntiṁ parityajya mudhā duḥkhāya ceṣṭase ॥ 14 ॥
   aho — alas; daiva-hatā — struck by fate; bhāsi — you appear; jñātvā-api — even knowing; tvam — you; idam — this; padam — state; tad-viśrāntim — that rest; parityajya — abandoning; mudhā — foolishly; duḥkhāya — for sorrow; ceṣṭase — you strive
   Alas, though you know this state, it seems you are struck by fate. Despite knowing it, you foolishly continue to seek sorrow.
   
   Verse 15
   इत्युक्ता सा प्रियं प्राह स्मयित्वेषन्मनोषिणी ।
   नाथ ते तन्न विदितं पदं परमपावनम्‌ ॥ १५ ॥
   ityuktā sā priyaṁ prāha smayitvā-eṣan-manoṣiṇī ।
   nātha te tan na viditaṁ padaṁ paramapāvanam ॥ 15 ॥
   iti-uktā — thus spoken; sā — she; priyam — to her beloved; prāha — spoke; smayitvā — smiling; eṣat — slightly; manoṣiṇī — lovely; nātha — lord; te — your; tat — that; na viditam — not known; padam — state; parama-pāvanam — supremely pure
   Thus spoken, she, slightly smiling, spoke to her beloved, "Lord, that supremely pure state is not known to you."
   
   Verse 16
   यत्र स्थिता न मुह्यन्ति पण्डिताः पावनाशयाः ।
   तत्पदं दूरतस्तेऽस्ति भूस्थस्येव नभस्तलम्‌ ॥ १६ ॥
   yatra sthitā na muhyanti paṇḍitāḥ pāvanāśayāḥ ।
   tat-padaṁ dūrataḥ te-asti bhūsthasya-iva nabhastalām ॥ 16 ॥
   yatra — where; sthitāḥ — situated; na muhyanti — do not delude; paṇḍitāḥ — wise; pāvana-āśayāḥ — pure-hearted; tat-padam — that state; dūrataḥ — far; te — your; asti — is; bhūsthasya — of one on the ground; iva — like; nabhastalām — sky
   That state, where the wise and pure-hearted are not deluded, remains distant for you, like the sky is for one on the ground.
   
   Verse 17
   त्वया किञ्चित्‌ सुविदितं भवेदविदितोपमम्‌ ।
   निमील्योन्मील्य वा नेत्रे तत्पदं न समीक्ष्यते ॥ १७ ॥
   tvayā kiñcit suviditam bhavet-avidita-upamam ।
   nimīlya-unmīlya vā netre tat-padam na samīkṣyate ॥ 17 ॥
   tvayā — by you; kiñcit — somewhat; suviditam — known; bhavet — may be; avidita-upamam — like the unknown; nimīlya — closing; unmīlya — opening; vā — or; netre — eyes; tat-padam — that state; na samīkṣyate — is not seen
   You may know something, but not that state. That state is not seen by the closing or opening of your eyes.
   
   Verse 18
   अकृत्वा वापि कृत्वा वा न तल्लभ्येत कर्हिचित्‌ ।
   अगत्वा चापि वा गत्वा न तदासादयेत्‌ पदम्‌ ॥ १८ ॥
   akṛtvā vā api kṛtvā vā na tat-labhyeta karhicit ।
   agatvā ca api vā gatvā na tat-āsādayet padam ॥ 18 ॥
   akṛtvā — without doing; vā — or; api — even; kṛtvā — doing; vā — or; na tat-labhyeta — it is not attained; karhicit — ever; agatvā — without going; ca — and; api — even; gatvā — going; na tat-āsādayet — not reach; padam — state
   It is never attained through action or inaction. Without moving or moving, one cannot reach that state.
   
   Verse 19
   निमील्य कृत्वा गत्वा वा प्राप्तं पूर्ण कथं भवेत्‌ ।
   यवाष्टकमितेनैव पक्ष्मणोन्मीलितेन तु ॥ १९ ॥
   nimīlya kṛtvā gatvā vā prāptaṁ pūrṇa kathaṁ bhavet ।
   yava-aṣṭaka-mitena-eva pakṣmaṇaḥ-unmīlitena tu ॥ 19 ॥
   nimīlya — closing; kṛtvā — doing; gatvā — going; vā — or; prāptaṁ — attained; pūrṇa — full; kathaṁ bhavet — how can it be; yava-aṣṭaka-mitena — measured by eight barleycorns; eva — indeed; pakṣmaṇaḥ — of eyelash; unmīlitena — opening; tu — indeed
   How can the complete state be attained through closing, doing, or going, measured by the blink of an eyelash?
   
   Verse 20
   अन्तर्हितं यदि तदा ननु पूर्णं भवेत्पदम्‌ ।
   अहो ते मोहमाहात्म्यमाश्चर्य किमहं ब्रुवे ॥ २० ॥
   antarhitaṁ yadi tadā nanu pūrṇaṁ bhavet-padam ।
   aho te moham-āhātmyam-āścarya kim-ahaṁ bruve ॥ 20 ॥
   antarhitaṁ — hidden; yadi — if; tadā — then; nanu — indeed; pūrṇaṁ — full; bhavet-padam — would be the state; aho — oh; te — your; moham-āhātmyam — grandeur of delusion; āścarya — wonder; kim-ahaṁ bruve — what can I say
   If it were hidden within, the state would always be full. Oh, the grandeur of your delusion is truly astonishing — what more can I say?
   
   Verse 21
   यस्मिन्‌ ब्रह्माण्डकोटीनां कोटयः कोणसंस्थिताः ।
   पक्ष्मणोऽङ्गुलिमानस्योन्मीलनात्तत्तिरोहितम्‌ ॥ २१ ॥
   yasmin brahmāṇḍa-koṭīnāṁ koṭayaḥ koṇa-saṁsthitāḥ ।
   pakṣmaṇaḥ aṅguli-mānasya unmīlanāt tat tirohitam ॥ 21 ॥
   yasmin — in which; brahmāṇḍa-koṭīnāṁ — of universes; koṭayaḥ — crores; koṇa-saṁsthitāḥ — positioned at angles; pakṣmaṇaḥ — of an eyelash; aṅguli-mānasya — the width of a finger; unmīlanāt — by opening; tat — that; tirohitam — hidden
   In which countless universes, positioned at different angles, is hidden within the width of an eyelash's opening?
   
   Verse 22
   शृणु राजकुमारैतत्‌ तत्त्वसारं वदामि यत्‌ ।
   यावद्‌ ग्रन्थिविभेदो न न तावत्‌ सुखमृच्छति ॥ २२ ॥
   śṛṇu rājakumāra etat tattva-sāraṁ vadāmi yat ।
   yāvad granthi-vibhedo na na tāvat sukham ṛcchati ॥ 22 ॥
   śṛṇu — listen; rājaku-māra — prince; etat — this; tattva-sāram — essence of truth; vadāmi — I say; yat — which; yāvat — until; granthi-vibhedaḥ — breaking of knots; na — not; tāvat — so much; sukham — happiness; ṛcchati — attains
   Listen, prince, I will reveal the essence of truth: until all the knots are broken, true happiness is not attained.
   
   Verse 23
   ग्रन्थयः कोटिशः सन्ति मोहरज्जुविवर्तिताः ।
   तत्र स्वरूपासंवित्तिर्मोहरज्जुरुदीरिता ॥ २३ ॥
   granthayaḥ koṭiśaḥ santi moha-rajju-vivartitāḥ ।
   tatra svarūpa-asaṁvittiḥ moha-rajjuḥ udīritā ॥ 23 ॥
   granthayaḥ — knots; koṭiśaḥ — crores; santi — are; moha-rajju-vivartitāḥ — turned into ropes of delusion; tatra — there; svarūpa-asaṁvittiḥ — lack of self-awareness; moha-rajjuḥ — rope of delusion; udīritā — is said
   There are countless knots formed into ropes of delusion. The lack of self-awareness is described as this rope of delusion.
   
   Verse 24
   यत्र ता ग्रन्थयः सन्ति विपरीतग्रहात्मत्मिकाः ।
   तत्राद्या देहमुख्येषु भवेदात्मत्वनिश्चयः ॥ २४ ॥
   yatra tā granthayaḥ santi viparīta-graha-ātmakāḥ ।
   tatra ādyā deha-mukhyeṣu bhavet-ātmatva-niścayaḥ ॥ 24 ॥
   yatra — where; tā — those; granthayaḥ — knots; santi — are; viparīta-graha-ātmakāḥ — of perverted understanding; tatra — there; ādyā — first; deha-mukhyeṣu — in the main body; bhavet — there is; ātmatva-niścayaḥ — certainty of selfhood
   Wherever there are knots of distorted understanding, the initial certainty about the self is found in the inquiry into one’s own body. (This is jiva)
   
   Verse 25
   यद्वशादेष संसार आततो दुष्प्रतिक्रियः ।
   तथा जगत्यनात्मत्वबुद्धिर्भानसमाश्रये ॥ २५ ॥
   yad-vaśād-eṣa saṁsāra ātato duṣ-pratikriyaḥ ।
   tathā jagati-anātmatva-buddhiḥ bhāna-samāśraye ॥ 25 ॥
   yad-vaśāt — under whose control; eṣaḥ — this; saṁsāraḥ — world; ātataḥ — spread out; duṣ-pratikriyaḥ — difficult to remedy; tathā — so; jagati — in the world; anātmatva-buddhiḥ — the understanding of non-self; bhāna-samāśraye — supported by perception
   This world, which spreads out and is hard to resist, is under the influence of someone. In the world, the belief in the non-self is based on perception. (This is ishvara)
   
   Verse 26
   एवं जीवेशभेदादिनिश्चया ग्रन्थयो मताः ।
   एतच्चिरात्‌ समुद्भूतं भूयः संवर्तितं च वै ॥ २६ ॥
   evaṁ jīva-īśa-bheda-ādi-niścayā granthayaḥ matāḥ ।
   etat cirāt samudbhūtam bhūyaḥ saṁvartitam ca vai ॥ 26 ॥
   evaṁ — thus, jīva-īśa-bheda-ādi-niścayāḥ — certainties of separation between the soul and God, granthayaḥ — knots, matāḥ — are considered, etat — this, cirāt — for long, samudbhūtam — arisen, bhūyaḥ — again, saṁvartitam — reformed, ca — and, vai — indeed
   Thus, the beliefs that create a sense of separation between the individual soul (jiva) and the divine (Ishvara) are considered knots. These misconceptions have existed for a long time and are continuously being reformed.
   
   Verse 27
   ग्रन्थिरूपं समापन्नं पुरुषः पाशितस्ततः ।
   तद्ग्रन्थिविस्त्रंसनतो बन्धान्मुक्तिः समीरिता ॥ २७ ॥
   granthi-rūpaṁ samāpannaṁ puruṣaḥ pāśitaḥ tataḥ ।
   tat-granthi-vistraṁsana-to bandhān-muktiḥ samīritā ॥ 27 ॥
   granthi-rūpam — in the form of knots; samāpannam — entangled; puruṣaḥ — person; pāśitaḥ — bound; tataḥ — from that; tat-granthi-vistraṁsana-to — by the loosening of those knots; bandhāt — from bondage; muktiḥ — liberation; samīritā — is declared
   A person bound by these knots is in bondage. Liberation from this bondage is achieved by loosening these knots.
   
   Verse 28
   यत्त्वं निमील्य नेत्रे स्वे पदमासादयस्यलम्‌ ।
   तत्पदं निजरूपं ते शुद्धसंविदनुत्तरम्‌ ॥ २८ ॥
   yat-tvaṁ nimīlya netre sve padam-āsādayasi alam ।
   tat-padaṁ nija-rūpaṁ te śuddha-saṁvid anuttaram ॥ 28 ॥
   yat — which; tvaṁ — you; nimīlya — closing; netre — eyes; sve — your; padam — state; āsādayasi — you attain; alam — sufficiently; tat-padam — that state; nija-rūpam — own form; te — your; śuddha-saṁvid — pure consciousness; anuttaram — supreme
   When you close your eyes and fully realize your state, you attain your own true form, which is pure and supreme consciousness.
   
   Verse 29
   तदेवाखिलसंसारचित्रादर्शतलं महत्‌ ।
   कदा क्व केन रूपेण नास्ति तन्मे निरूपय ॥ २९ ॥
   tad-eva-akhila-saṁsāra-citra-ādarśa-talaṁ mahat ।
   kadā kva kena rūpeṇa na asti tan-me nirūpaya ॥ 29 ॥
   tat-eva — that itself; akhila-saṁsāra — entire world; citra-ādarśa-talam — mirror surface; mahat — great; kadā — when; kva — where; kena — by what; rūpeṇa — form; na — not; asti — is; tan — that; me — to me; nirūpaya — explain
   That is the great mirror reflecting the entire world. Tell me, when, where, and in what form is it not so? Explain.
   
   Verse 30
   यदा यद्रूपतो यस्मिन्नेति ब्रूयाः स्वसंविदम्‌ ।
   तर्हि तत्कालदेशादेर्वन्ध्यापुत्रत्वमेव हि ॥ ३० ॥
   yadā yad-rūpataḥ yasmin-na iti brūyāḥ sva-saṁvidam ।
   tarhi tat-kāla-deśāt-ervandhyā-putratvam-eva hi ॥ 30 ॥
   yadā — when; yat-rūpataḥ — of which form; yasmin — in which; na — not; iti — thus; brūyāḥ — you say; sva-saṁvidam — own consciousness; tarhi — then; tat-kāla-deśāt — from that time and place; eva — indeed; vandhyā-putratvam — son of a barren woman; eva hi — is indeed
   When someone says that your consciousness has a specific form, it is as limited as a son of a barren woman — impossible and without basis in time and space.
   
   Verse 31
   प्रतिबिम्बो निरादर्शो यथा नाथ तथैव तत्‌ ।
   तस्मात्तत्पदसंत्यागान्नास्ति कुत्रापि किञ्चन ॥ ३१ ॥
   pratibimbo nirādarśo yathā nātha tathaiva tat ।
   tasmāt-tat-pada-saṁtyāgān-nāsti kutrāpi kiñcana ॥ 31 ॥
   pratibimbaḥ — reflection; nirādarśaḥ — without a mirror; yathā — as; nātha — lord; tathaiva — similarly; tat — that; tasmāt — therefore; tat-pada-saṁtyāgāt — renouncing that state; nāsti — there is not; kutrāpi — anywhere; kiñcana — anything
   Just as a reflection cannot exist without a mirror, so, O Lord, without that state, there is nothing anywhere.
   
   Verse 32
   तत्ते नेत्रोन्मीलनेन किमन्तरिततामियात्‌ ।
   यावदेवं विजानामीत्येवं ग्रन्थिर्दृढा भवेत्‌ ॥ ३२ ॥
   tat-te netra-unmīlanena kim-antaritatām-iyāt ।
   yāvat-evaṁ vijānāmi-iti-evaṁ granthiḥ dṛḍhā bhavet ॥ 32 ॥
   tat-te — that your; netra-unmīlanena — by opening eyes; kim-antaritatām-iyāt — what would it hide; yāvat — as long as; evam — thus; vijānāmi — I understand; iti — thus; evam — thus; granthiḥ — knot; dṛḍhā — firm; bhavet — becomes
   By opening your eyes, what would it conceal? As long as you think this way, the knot remains tightly bound.
   
   Verse 33
   तावन्न तत्पदं प्राप्तं यत्प्राप्तं स्यान्न तद्भवेत्‌ ।
   निमील्योन्मील्य वा नेत्रे यत्प्राप्तं मन्यसे पदम्‌ ॥ ३३ ॥
   tāvat-na tat-padaṁ prāptaṁ yat-prāptaṁ syāt-na tad-bhavet ।
   nimīlya-unmīlya vā netre yat-prāptaṁ manyase padam ॥ 33 ॥
   tāvat — as long; na — not; tat-padam — that state; prāptam — attained; yat-prāptam — what is attained; syāt — may be; na — not; tat-bhavet — that be; nimīlya — closing; unmīlya — opening; vā — or; netre — eyes; yat-prāptam — what is attained; manyase — you think; padam — state
   As long as that state is not attained, what you achieve is not that. Whether you close or open your eyes, what you believe you’ve attained is not that state.
   
   Verse 34
   तन्न पूर्णपदं यस्मात्‌ परिच्छेदात्‌ क्रियादितः ।
   कुत्र नाथ महासंविन्नास्ति कालानलप्रभा ॥ ३४ ॥
   tann pūrṇapadaṃ yasmāt paricchedāt kriyāditaḥ ।
   kutra nātha mahāsaṃvinnāsti kālānalaprabhā ॥ 34 ॥
   tann — that which; pūrṇapadaṃ — complete place; yasmāt — from which; paricchedāt — due to limitation; kriyāditaḥ — by actions indeed; kutra — where; nātha — protector; mahāsaṃvinnāsti — great confusion not exists; kālānalaprabhā — like the fire of time
   Therefore, that which is complete and undivided is always present, even when limited by actions. Where, O Lord, is that protector not found, like the brilliant light of the eternal flame?
   
   Verse 35
   स्वात्मीकरोति याऽनल्पकल्पनेन्धनसंचयम्‌ ।
   न ते कर्तव्यसंशेषो विज्ञाय परमं पदम्‌ ॥ ३५ ॥
   svātmī-karoti yā-an-alpa-kalpanā-indhana-saṁcayam ।
   na te kartavya-saṁśeṣaḥ vijñāya paramaṁ padam ॥ 35 ॥
   svātmī-karoti — makes one's own; yā — which; an-alpa — great; kalpanā — imagination; indhana-saṁcayam — accumulation of fuel; na — not; te — your; kartavya-saṁśeṣaḥ — remaining duty; vijñāya — knowing; paramaṁ padam — supreme state
   It reveals one's own self with profound insight, much like the buildup of fuel. Once you understand the supreme state, no further duties remain for you.
   
   Verse 36
   त्यज ग्रन्थिं सन्निरुध्य पश्यामीति हृदि स्थिताम्‌ ।
   इदं नाहमिति ग्रन्थिमुन्मूलय परां दृढाम्‌ ॥ ३६ ॥
   tyaja granthiṁ sanni-rudhya paśyāmīti hṛdi sthitām ।
   idaṁ na-aham-iti granthim-unmūlaya parāṁ dṛḍhām ॥ 36 ॥
   tyaja — abandon; granthim — knot; sanni-rudhya — controlling; paśyāmi-iti — I see; hṛdi sthitām — established in the heart; idaṁ — this; na-aham-iti — not I; granthim — knot; unmūlaya — uproot; parām — supreme; dṛḍhām — firm
   Abandon the knot of "I see," which is rooted in the heart.  
Uproot the deep, firm knot of "This is not I"
   
   Verse 37
   पश्य सर्वत्र चात्मानमखण्डानन्दबृहितम्‌ ।
   पश्यात्मन्यखिलं लोकं दर्पणप्रतिबिम्बवत्‌ ॥ ३७ ॥
   paśya sarvatra ca ātmānam akhaṇḍānanda-bṛhitam ।
   paśya ātmani akhilaṁ lokaṁ darpaṇa-pratibimba-vat ॥ 37 ॥
   paśya — see; sarvatra — everywhere; ca — and; ātmānam — self; akhaṇḍa-ānanda-bṛhitam — filled with unbroken bliss; paśya — see; ātmani — in the self; akhilam — entire; lokam — world; darpaṇa-pratibimba-vat — like a reflection in a mirror
   See the self everywhere, filled with unbroken bliss. Observe the entire world within the self, just as a reflection appears in a mirror.
   
   Verse 38
   सर्वत्राखिलमात्मानमिति भूयो न भावयन्‌ ।
   शेषमभ्युपगम्यान्तः स्वस्थो भव निजात्मना ॥ ३८ ॥
   sarvatra-akhilam-ātmānam-iti bhūyaḥ na bhāvayan ।
   śeṣam-abhyupagamya-antaḥ svasthaḥ bhava nija-ātmanā ॥ 38 ॥
   sarvatra — everywhere; akhilam — entire; ātmānam — self; iti — thus; bhūyaḥ — again; na bhāvayan — not contemplating; śeṣam — remaining; abhyupagamya — approaching; antaḥ — within; svasthaḥ — at peace; bhava — be; nija-ātmanā — with own self
   Without further contemplation, turn inward and see the entire self present everywhere. Then, find peace in being with your own self.
   
   Verse 39
   इति प्रियोदितं श्रुत्वा हेमचूडः सिताशयः ।
   विदित्वा पुर्णमात्मानं सर्वत्र भ्रान्तिविर्जितः ॥ ३९ ॥
   iti priyoditaṁ śrutvā hemacūḍaḥ sitāśayaḥ ।
   viditvā pūrṇam ātmānam sarvatra bhrānti-virjitaḥ ॥ 39 ॥
   iti — thus; priya-uditam — spoken by beloved; śrutvā — hearing; hemacūḍaḥ — Hemachuda; sitāśayaḥ — pure-hearted; viditvā — knowing; pūrṇam — complete; ātmānam — self; sarvatra — everywhere; bhrānti-virjitaḥ — free from delusion
   Hearing the words of his beloved, Hemachuda, with a pure heart, recognized his complete self everywhere and thus was freed from delusion.
   
   Verse 40
   क्रमात्‌ पूर्णसमावेशासादनात्‌ स्थिरभावनः ।
   विहरन्‌ सर्वदा हेमलेखादियुवतीगणैः ॥ ४० ॥
   kramāt pūrṇa-samāveśa-āsādanāt sthira-bhāvanaḥ ।
   viharan sarvadā hemalekha-ādi-yuvatī-gaṇaiḥ ॥ 40 ॥
   kramāt — gradually; pūrṇa-samāveśa-āsādanāt — by attaining complete immersion; sthira-bhāvanaḥ — with steady contemplation; viharan — roaming; sarvadā — always; hemalekha-ādi — Hemalekha and others; yuvatī-gaṇaiḥ — with groups of young women
   Gradually, by achieving deep immersion and steady contemplation, he remained constantly absorbed, spending his time with Hemalekha and groups of young women.
   
   Verse 41
   शासन्‌ राज्य समृद्धं स्व जित्वा शत्रुगणं रणे ।
   शास्त्राणि श्रावयन्‌ शृण्वन्नर्जयन्‌ धनसंचयम्‌ ॥ ४१ ॥
   śāsan rājyam samṛddham sva jitvā śatru-gaṇam raṇe ।
   śāstrāṇi śrāvayan śṛṇvan arjayan dhana-saṁcayam ॥ 41 ॥
   śāsan — ruling; rājyam — kingdom; samṛddham — prosperous; sva — his own; jitvā — having conquered; śatru-gaṇam — enemies; raṇe — in battle; śāstrāṇi — scriptures; śrāvayan — making others hear; śṛṇvan — hearing; arjayan — earning; dhana-saṁcayam — wealth accumulation
   Ruling his prosperous kingdom, conquering enemies in battle, imparting scriptures to others, listening to them, and accumulating wealth.
   
   Verse 42
   अश्वमेधराजसूयाद्यैर्यजन्‌ क्रतुमुख्यकैः ।
   वर्षाणामयुते द्वे वै जीवन्मुक्तो भुवि स्थितः ॥ ४२ ॥
   aśvamedha-rājasūya-adyaiḥ yajān kratumuḥyakaiḥ ।
   varṣāṇām ayute dve vai jīvanmukto bhuvi sthitaḥ ॥ 42 ॥
   aśvamedha-rājasūya-adyaiḥ — by Ashvamedha, Rajasuya, and other major sacrifices; yajān — performing; kratu-mukhya-kaiḥ — chief rituals; varṣāṇām — of years; ayute dve — twenty thousand; vai — indeed; jīvanmuktaḥ — liberated while living; bhuvi sthitaḥ — remained on earth
   By performing Ashvamedha, Rajasuya, and other major sacrifices, he remained on earth for twenty thousand years as a liberated soul.
   
   Verse 43
   जीवन्मुक्तदशासंस्थं निशाम्य तनयं नृपः ।
   मुक्ताचूडश्च तद्‌भ्राता मणिचूडोऽप्यचिन्तयत्‌ ॥ ४३ ॥
   jīvanmukta-daśā-saṁstham niśāmya tanayaṁ nṛpaḥ ।
   muktācūḍaś ca tad-bhrātā maṇicūḍaḥ api acintayat ॥ 43 ॥
   jīvanmukta-daśā-saṁstham — established in the state of liberation while living; niśāmya — observing; tanayam — son; nṛpaḥ — king; muktācūḍaḥ — Muktachuda; ca — and; tad-bhrātā — his brother; maṇicūḍaḥ — Manichuda; api — also; acintayat — thought
   Seeing his son established in the state of liberation while still living, the king, along with Muktachuda and his brother Manichuda, also reflected on this.
   
   Verse 44
   किमयं पूर्ववन्नेह लक्ष्यते सर्वथा किल ।
   सुखे न हृष्यत्यत्यन्तं दुःखे नोद्विजते तथा ॥ ४४ ॥
   kim ayam pūrvavat na iha lakṣyate sarvathā kila ।
   sukhe na hṛṣyati atyantam duḥkhe na udvijate tathā ॥ 44 ॥
   kim — why; ayam — he; pūrvavat — as before; na — not; iha — here; lakṣyate — appears; sarvathā — at all; kila — indeed; sukhe — in happiness; na — not; hṛṣyati — rejoices; atyantam — extremely; duḥkhe — in sorrow; na — not; udvijate — is disturbed; tathā — likewise
   Why does he not appear here as before, neither excessively rejoicing in happiness nor disturbed by sorrow?
   
   Verse 45
   लाभालाभौ शत्रुमित्रे साम्यात्‌ पश्यति वै कुतः ।
   करोति राजकार्याणि नटवद्‌ रङ्गमण्डले ॥ ४५ ॥
   lābha-ālābhau śatru-mitre sāmyāt paśyati vai kutaḥ ।
   karoti rājakāryāṇi naṭavat raṅga-maṇḍale ॥ 45 ॥
   lābha-ālābhau — gain and loss; śatru-mitre — enemy and friend; sāmyāt — with equanimity; paśyati — sees; vai — indeed; kutaḥ — why; karoti — does; rājakāryāṇi — royal duties; naṭavat — like an actor; raṅga-maṇḍale — on the stage
   Why does he view gain and loss, enemy and friend with equanimity, performing his royal duties as if merely acting on a stage?
   
   Verse 46
   कापिशायनपायीव सदा मत्तोऽभिलक्ष्यते ।
   सदान्यत्र गतस्वान्त इव कृत्यं करोत्यलम्‌ ॥ ४६ ॥
   kāpiśāyana-pāyīva sadā mattaḥ abhilaṣyate ।
   sadā anyatra gata-svānta iva kṛtyam karoti alam ॥ 46 ॥
   kāpiśāyana-pāyīva — like a drinker of intoxicating beverage; sadā — always; mattaḥ — intoxicated; abhilaṣyate — appears; sadā — always; anyatra — elsewhere; gata-svāntaḥ — with a mind gone; iva — as if; kṛtyam — duty; karoti — does; alam — sufficiently
   He always seems intoxicated, like someone drinking an intoxicating beverage, with his mind elsewhere, yet he performs his duties adequately, as if detached.
   
   Verse 47
   तत्केन हेतुना चेति तमासाद्य रहः क्वचित्‌ ।
   अपृच्छतां हेमचूडं कुत एवं भवानिति ॥ ४७ ॥
   tat kena hetunā ca iti tam āsādya rahaḥ kvacit ।
   apṛcchatāṁ hemacūḍaṁ kuta evaṁ bhavān iti ॥ 47 ॥
   tat — that; kena — for what; hetunā — reason; ca — and; iti — thus; tam — him; āsādya — approaching; rahaḥ — in private; kvacit — somewhere; apṛcchatāṁ — asked; hemacūḍaṁ — Hemachuda; kutaḥ — why; evaṁ — thus; bhavān — you; iti — thus
   For what reason, and approaching him privately, they asked Hemachuda, "Why are you like this?"
   
   Verse 48
   ततः स्वस्थितिमाचख्यौ हेमचूडस्तयोः क्रमात्‌ ।
   तावुभौ भ्रातृपितरौ हेमचूडेन बोधितौ ॥ ४८ ॥
   tataḥ sva-sthitim ācakhyau hemacūḍaḥ tayoḥ kramāt ।
   tau ubhau bhrātṛ-pitarau hemacūḍena bodhitau ॥ 48 ॥
   tataḥ — then; sva-sthitim — his state; ācakhyau — explained; hemacūḍaḥ — Hemachuda; tayoḥ — to them; kramāt — gradually; tau — they; ubhau — both; bhrātṛ-pitarau — brother and father; hemacūḍena — by Hemachuda; bodhitau — enlightened
   Hemachuda then gradually explained his state to them, enlightening both his brother and father.
   
   Verse 49
   आसादितपरंतत्त्वौ जीवन्मुक्तौ बभूवतुः ।
   अथ मन्त्रिगणोऽप्येवं राज्ञः श्रुत्वा जगद्‌गतिम्‌ ॥ ४९ ॥
   āsādita-param-tattvau jīvan-muktau babhūvatuḥ ।
   atha mantri-gaṇaḥ api evaṁ rājñaḥ śrutvā jagad-gatim ॥ 49 ॥
   āsādita-param-tattvau — having attained the supreme truth; jīvan-muktau — liberated while living; babhūvatuḥ — became; atha — then; mantri-gaṇaḥ — group of ministers; api — also; evam — thus; rājñaḥ — of the king; śrutvā — hearing; jagad-gatim — the world's condition
   Having attained the supreme truth, they became liberated while living. Hearing this, the ministers also understood the nature of the world.
   
   Verse 50
   विचार्य स्वात्मनो भावं ज्ञातज्ञेयोऽभवत्तदा ।
   एवं विशालनगरे क्रमेणैव परस्परम्‌ ॥ ५० ॥
   vicārya sva-ātmanaḥ bhāvam jñāta-jñeyaḥ abhavat tadā ।
   evaṁ viśāla-nagare krameṇa eva parasparam ॥ 50 ॥
   vicārya — considering; sva-ātmanaḥ — of their own self; bhāvam — nature; jñāta-jñeyaḥ — knowers of the knowable; abhavat — became; tadā — then; evaṁ — thus; viśāla-nagare — in the city of Vishala; krameṇa — gradually; eva — indeed; parasparam — mutually
   Considering the nature of their own selves, they became knowers of the knowable. Thus, in the city of Vishala, they gradually and mutually understood this.
   
   Verse 51
   उपदेशाद्‌ विदुः सर्वे तत्त्वमाबालगोपकाः ।
   नरा नार्यो बालवृद्धा दासा दासीगणा अपि ॥ ५१ ॥
   upadeśāt viduḥ sarve tattvam ābāla-gopakāḥ ।
   narāḥ nāryaḥ bāla-vṛddhāḥ dāsāḥ dāsī-gaṇāḥ api ॥ 51 ॥
   upadeśāt — from instruction; viduḥ — knew; sarve — all; tattvam — the truth; ābāla-gopakāḥ — from children to cowherds; narāḥ — men; nāryaḥ — women; bāla-vṛddhāḥ — young and old; dāsāḥ — male servants; dāsī-gaṇāḥ — female servants; api — also
   From the teachings, everyone came to understand the truth, including children, cowherds, men, women, the young and old, as well as male and female servants.
   
   Verse 52
   ज्ञातज्ञेयास्त्यक्तदेहाहंभावा अभवन्‌ खलु ।
   न तत्र कस्यचित्‌ कामः क्रोधो वा लोभ एव वा ॥ ५२ ॥
   jñāta-jñeyāḥ tyakta-deha-ahaṁ-bhāvāḥ abhavan khalu ।
   na tatra kasyacit kāmaḥ krodhaḥ vā lobhaḥ eva vā ॥ 52 ॥
   jñāta-jñeyāḥ — knowers of the knowable; tyakta-deha-ahaṁ-bhāvāḥ — having abandoned body-consciousness; abhavan — became; khalu — indeed; na — not; tatra — there; kasyacit — of anyone; kāmaḥ — desire; krodhaḥ — anger; vā — or; lobhaḥ — greed; eva — indeed; vā — or
   Having realized the ultimate truth and abandoned identification with the body, they became free from desire, anger, and greed.
   
   Verse 53
   अनाहृतोऽस्ति बालस्य स्थविरस्यापि वा क्वचित्‌ ।
   आहृतैः क्रोधकामाद्यैर्व्यवहारपरायणाः ॥ ५३ ॥
   anāhṛtaḥ asti bālasya sthavirasya api vā kvacit ।
   āhṛtaiḥ krodha-kāma-ādyaiḥ vyavahāra-parāyaṇāḥ ॥ 53 ॥
   anāhṛtaḥ — without being knowledgable; asti — is; bālasya — of a child; sthavirasya — of an elder; api — also; vā — or; kvacit — somewhere; āhṛtaiḥ — invited; krodha-kāma-ādyaiḥ — by anger, desire, and others; vyavahāra-parāyaṇāḥ — engaged in worldly affairs
   Whether a child or an elder, if one is not truly knowledgeable, they often display traits like anger and desire, remaining engaged in worldly affairs.
   
   Verse 54
   बालं माता खेलयति परतत्त्वस्य वार्तया ।
   दासा दास्यः स्वामिनं स्वं सदा परिचरन्ति वै ॥ ५४ ॥
   bālam mātā kheḷayati paratattvasya vārttayā ।
   dāsā dāsyaḥ svāminam svam sadā paricaranti vai ॥ 54 ॥
   bālam — child; mātā — mother; kheḷayati — plays; paratattvasya — of the supreme truth; vārttayā — with news; dāsāḥ — male servants; dāsyaḥ — female servants; svāminam — master; svam — their own; sadā — always; paricaranti — serve; vai — indeed
   The mother plays with the child while discussing the supreme truth. Both male and female servants consistently serve their master in the same manner.
   
   Verse 55
   परतत्त्वपरैर्वाक्यैर्व्याहरन्तः परस्परम्‌ ।
   नटा नाटयं वितन्वन्ति पात्रैस्तत्त्वप्रसङ्गजैः ॥ ५५ ॥
   paratattva-paraiḥ vākyaiḥ vyāharantaḥ parasparam ।
   naṭāḥ nāṭyam vitanvanti pātraiḥ tattva-prasaṅga-jaiḥ ॥ 55 ॥
   paratattva-paraiḥ — about the supreme truth; vākyaiḥ — with words; vyāharantaḥ — conversing; parasparam — with each other; naṭāḥ — actors; nāṭyam — drama; vitanvanti — perform; pātraiḥ — with characters; tattva-prasaṅga-jaiḥ — related to truth
   While discussing the supreme truth with words, actors perform dramas with characters embodying that truth.
   
   Verse 56
   विवेकवार्तापरमं वचो गायन्ति गायकाः ।
   विदूषका दूषयन्ति लोकव्यवहृतिं सदा ॥ ५६ ॥
   viveka-vārtā-paramam vacaḥ gāyanti gāyakāḥ ।
   vidūṣakāḥ dūṣayanti loka-vyavahṛtim sadā ॥ 56 ॥
   viveka-vārtā-paramam — focused on the news of discernment; vacaḥ — words; gāyanti — sing; gāyakāḥ — singers; vidūṣakāḥ — jesters; dūṣayanti — criticize; loka-vyavahṛtim — worldly affairs; sadā — always
   Singers deliver songs centered on the wisdom of discernment, while jesters consistently critique worldly affairs.
   
   Verse 57
   शास्त्राणि पाठयन्ति स्म विद्वांसः पाठकान्‌ जनान्‌ ।
   परतत्त्वविचारार्हैरुदाहरणमण्डलैः ॥ ५७ ॥
   śāstrāṇi pāṭhayanti sma vidvāṁsaḥ pāṭhakān janān ।
   paratattva-vicāra-arhaiḥ udāharaṇa-maṇḍalaiḥ ॥ 57 ॥
   śāstrāṇi — scriptures; pāṭhayanti — teach; sma — indeed; vidvāṁsaḥ — scholars; pāṭhakān — students; janān — people; paratattva-vicāra-arhaiḥ — suitable for the consideration of the supreme truth; udāharaṇa-maṇḍalaiḥ — with examples
   Scholars teach scriptures to students, providing examples that aid in understanding the supreme truth.
   
   Verse 58
   एवं तत्र नरा नार्यो दासा दास्यो नटा विटाः ।
   भृत्या भटा मन्त्रिणश्च शिल्पिनो वारयोषितः ॥ ५८ ॥
   evaṁ tatra narāḥ nāryaḥ dāsāḥ dāsyaḥ naṭāḥ viṭāḥ ।
   bhṛtyāḥ bhaṭāḥ mantriṇaḥ ca śilpinaḥ vāra-yoṣitaḥ ॥ 58 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; tatra — there; narāḥ — men; nāryaḥ — women; dāsāḥ — male servants; dāsyaḥ — female servants; naṭāḥ — actors; viṭāḥ — jesters; bhṛtyāḥ — attendants; bhaṭāḥ — soldiers; mantriṇaḥ — ministers; ca — and; śilpinaḥ — artisans; vāra-yoṣitaḥ — courtesans
   Thus, in that place, men and women, male and female servants, actors, jesters, attendants, soldiers, ministers, artisans, and courtesans.
   
   Verse 59
   सर्वे वेदितवेद्यास्ते विशालनगरेऽभवन्‌ ।
   प्राक्संस्कारबलेनैव व्यवहारपरायणाः ॥ ५९ ॥
   sarve veditavedyāḥ te viśāla-nagare abhavan ।
   prāk-saṁskāra-balena-eva vyavahāra-parāyaṇāḥ ॥ 59 ॥
   sarve — all; veditavedyāḥ — knowers of the knowable; te — they; viśāla-nagare — in the city of Vishala; abhavan — became; prāk-saṁskāra-balena — by the strength of previous impressions; eva — indeed; vyavahāra-parāyaṇāḥ — engaged in worldly affairs
   All of them became knowers of the knowable in the city of Vishala, while continuing their worldly affairs, influenced by the strength of their previous impressions.
   
   Verse 60
   न संस्मरति संवृत्तं शुभं वाप्यशुभं तथा ।
   भविष्यद्‌ नानुसन्धत्ते हर्षशोकादिसाधनम्‌ ॥ ६० ॥
   na saṁsmarati saṁvṛttam śubham vā api aśubham tathā ।
   bhaviṣyat na anusandhatte harṣa-śoka-ādi-sādhanam ॥ 60 ॥
   na — not; saṁsmarati — remembers; saṁvṛttam — past; śubham — good; vā — or; api — also; aśubham — bad; tathā — likewise; bhaviṣyat — future; na — not; anusandhatte — contemplates; harṣa-śoka-ādi-sādhanam — causes of joy, sorrow, etc
   They neither remember the past, whether good or bad, nor contemplate the future as causes of joy or sorrow.
   
   Verse 61
   वर्तमाने स्मयन्‌ हृष्यन्‌ खिद्यन्‌ क्रुध्यन्निवान्वहम्‌ ।
   मधुक्षीब इवात्यन्तं व्यवहारपरो जनः ॥ ६१ ॥
   vartamāne smayan hṛṣyan khidyan krudhyan nivānvaham ।
   madhu-kṣība iva atyantam vyavahāra-paraḥ janaḥ ॥ 61 ॥
   vartamāne — in the present; smayan — smiling; hṛṣyan — rejoicing; khidyan — grieving; krudhyan — getting angry; iva — as if; anvaham — always; madhu-kṣībaḥ — intoxicated with honey; iva — like; atyantam — extremely; vyavahāra-paraḥ — engaged in worldly affairs; janaḥ — person
   Situated in the present, a person, like one intoxicated with honey, smiles, rejoices, grieves, and gets angry, remaining deeply engaged in worldly affairs.
   
   Verse 62
   एवंविधं तन्नगरमृषयः सनकादयः ।
   प्रसिद्धविद्यानगरमित्याख्यमूचुरागताः ॥ ६२ ॥
   evaṁvidham tan nagaram ṛṣayaḥ sanakādayaḥ ।
   prasiddha-vidyā-nagaram iti ākhyam ūcur āgatāḥ ॥ 62 ॥
   evaṁvidham — such; tan — that; nagaram — city; ṛṣayaḥ — sages; sanakādayaḥ — like Sanaka; prasiddha-vidyā-nagaram — famous city of knowledge; iti — thus; ākhyam — named; ūcur — said; āgatāḥ — having arrived
   Such was that city which sages like Sanaka called the famous city of knowledge upon arriving.
   
   Verse 63
   यत्र कीराः पञ्जरस्था अपि वाचो वदन्ति वै ।
   चितिरूपं स्वमात्मानं भजध्वं चेत्यवर्जितम्‌ ॥ ६३ ॥
   yatra kīrāḥ pañjara-sthā api vāco vadanti vai ।
   citi-rūpaṁ svam ātmānaṁ bhajadhvaṁ ceti avarjitam ॥ 63 ॥
   yatra — where; kīrāḥ — parrots; pañjara-sthāḥ — caged; api — even; vācaḥ — words; vadanti — speak; vai — indeed; citi-rūpam — consciousness-form; svam — own; ātmānam — self; bhajadhvam — worship; ceti — thus; avarjitam — without ceasing
   Where even caged parrots continuously repeat, "Worship your own self in the form of consciousness."
   
   Verse 64
   नास्ति चेत्यं चितेरन्यद्‌ दर्पणप्रतिबिम्बवत्‌ ।
   चितिश्चेत्यं चितिरहं चितिः सर्वं चराचरम्‌ ॥ ६४ ॥
   nāsti cetyam citer anyad darpaṇa-pratibimba-vat ।
   citiḥ cetyam citiḥ aham citiḥ sarvam cara-acaram ॥ 64 ॥
   nāsti — there is not; cetyam — the known; citer — from consciousness; anyad — other; darpaṇa-pratibimba-vat — like the reflection in a mirror; citiḥ — consciousness; cetyam — the known; citiḥ — consciousness; aham — I; citiḥ — consciousness; sarvam — all; cara-acaram — moving and non-moving
   There is nothing known apart from consciousness, just like a reflection in a mirror. Consciousness is the only thing that is known; I am consciousness, and everything, both moving and stationary, is consciousness.
   
   Verse 65
   यतः सर्वं चितिमनु भाति सा तु स्वतन्त्रतः ।
   अतश्चितिं जनाः सर्वभासिनीं सर्वसंश्रयाम्‌ ॥ ६५ ॥
   yataḥ sarvam citim anu bhāti sā tu svatantrataḥ ।
   ataḥ citim janāḥ sarva-bhāsinīṁ sarva-saṁśrayām ॥ 65 ॥
   yataḥ — because; sarvam — everything; citim — consciousness; anu — following; bhāti — shines; sā — that; tu — indeed; svatantrataḥ — independently; ataḥ — therefore; citim — consciousness; janāḥ — people; sarva-bhāsinīm — illuminating all; sarva-saṁśrayām — the support of all
   Since everything shines because of consciousness, which is independent, people, revere consciousness as it illuminates and supports all.
   
   Verse 66
   भजध्वं भ्रान्तिमुत्सृज्य चितिमात्रं सुदृष्टयः ।
   तिर्यञ्चोऽप्येवमत्यन्तं यत्र वाचो वदन्ति वै ॥ ६६ ॥
   bhajadhvaṁ bhrāntim utsṛjya citimātraṁ su-dṛṣṭayaḥ ।
   tiryañcaḥ api evam atyantam yatra vācaḥ vadanti vai ॥ 66 ॥
   bhajadhvaṁ — worship; bhrāntim — illusion; utsṛjya — abandoning; citimātram — pure consciousness; su-dṛṣṭayaḥ — with clear vision; tiryañcaḥ — animals; api — even; evam — thus; atyantam — extremely; yatra — where; vācaḥ — words; vadanti — speak; vai — indeed
   Worship pure consciousness with clear vision, abandoning illusion. Even animals in such a place speak these words.
   
   Verse 67
   प्रसिद्धविद्यानगरं तदद्यापि प्रचक्षते ।
   एवं तत्र पुरा हेमलेखया खलु बोधितः ॥ ६७ ॥
   prasiddha-vidyā-nagaraṁ tad adya api pracakṣate ।
   evaṁ tatra purā hemalekhayā khalu bodhitaḥ ॥ 67 ॥
   prasiddha-vidyā-nagaram — the famous city of knowledge; tat — that; adya api — even today; pracakṣate — is called; evaṁ — thus; tatra — there; purā — formerly; hemalekhayā — by Hemalekha; khalu — indeed; bodhitaḥ — enlightened
   Even today, that place is known as the famous city of knowledge. There, Hemalekha once provided enlightenment.
   
   Verse 68
   हेमचूडोऽभवद्‌ विद्वान्‌ जीवन्मुक्तस्तथेतरे ।
   स्त्रीबालप्रमुखाः सर्वे जाता ज्ञातपरावराः ॥ ६८ ॥
   hemacūḍo abhavad vidvān jīvanmuktaḥ tathā itare ।
   strī-bāla-pramukhāḥ sarve jātā jñāta-parāvarāḥ ॥ 68 ॥
   hemacūḍaḥ — Hemachuda; abhavat — became; vidvān — wise; jīvanmuktaḥ — liberated while living; tathā — and; itare — others; strī-bāla-pramukhāḥ — women, children, and others; sarve — all; jātāḥ — became; jñāta-parāvarāḥ — knowers of the highest and lowest truths
   Hemachuda attained wisdom and liberation while still alive, and others, including women, children, and various individuals, all came to understand both the highest and lowest truths.
   
   Verse 69
   तस्माच्छ्रेयोनिदानं तु सत्सङ्गः प्रथमं भवेत्‌ ।
   तस्माच्छ्रेयोवाञ्छने तु सत्संश्रयपरो भवेत्‌ ॥ ६९ ॥
   tasmāt śreyo-nidānaṁ tu satsangaḥ prathamaṁ bhavet ।
   tasmāt śreyo-vāñchane tu sat-saṁśraya-paraḥ bhavet ॥ 69 ॥
   tasmāt — therefore; śreyaḥ-nidānam — the source of well-being; tu — indeed; satsangaḥ — association with the wise; prathamam — first; bhavet — should be; tasmāt — therefore; śreyaḥ-vāñchane — in desiring well-being; tu — indeed; sat-saṁśraya-paraḥ — taking refuge in the wise; bhavet — should be
   Therefore, the source of true well-being is association with the wise. To achieve well-being, one should first seek refuge with the wise.


   
   इति श्रीत्रिपुरारहस्ये ज्ञानखण्डे हेमचूडोपाख्यानसमाप्तिर्नाम दशमोऽध्यायः ॥
   
   Thus ends the tenth chapter named "Conclusion of Hemachuda's Story" in the revered Knowledge Section of Tripura Rahasya.
   
   

11. EXPLANATION OF THE ESSENCE OF THE WORLD
   Verse 1
   श्रुत्वैवं हेमचूडस्य कथामत्यद्भुतां तदा ।
   भार्गवः सन्दिग्धमनाः प्रष्टुं समुपचक्रमे ॥ १ ॥
   śrutvaivaṁ hemacūḍasya kathāmatyadbhutāṁ tadā ।
   bhārgavaḥ sandigdhamanāḥ praṣṭuṁ samupacakrame ॥ 1 ॥
   śrutvā — having heard; evaṁ — thus; hemacūḍasya — of Hemachuda; kathām — story; atya-adbhutām — very wonderful; tadā — then; bhārgavaḥ — Bhargava; sandigdha-manāḥ — with a doubtful mind; praṣṭuṁ — to ask; samupacakrame — began
   After hearing the remarkable story of Hemachuda, Bhargava, with a questioning mind, began to inquire.
   
   Verse 2
   भगवन्‌ श्रीगुरो यत्ते प्रोक्तं ज्ञानं महाद्भुतम्‌ ।
   भाति मे विषमं ह्येतदसाध्यं चापि सर्वतः ॥ २ ॥
   bhagavan śrīguro yatte proktaṁ jñānaṁ mahādbhutam ।
   bhāti me viṣamaṁ hyetad asādhyaṁ cāpi sarvataḥ ॥ 2 ॥
   bhagavan — O lord; śrīguro — O revered teacher; yat — what; te — by you; proktam — spoken; jñānam — knowledge; mahā-adbhutam — very wonderful; bhāti — appears; me — to me; viṣamam — difficult; hi — indeed; etad — this; asādhyam — unattainable; ca — also; api — even; sarvataḥ — in every way
   O revered teacher, the knowledge you have shared is indeed marvelous, but it seems to me difficult and unattainable in every respect.
   
   Verse 3
   कथमेतज्जगद्‌ दृश्यं चितिमात्रस्वरूपकम्‌ ।
   अदृष्टं केवलं ह्येतच्छ्रद्धोपेयं न चान्यथा ॥ ३ ॥
   katham etaj jagad dṛśyaṁ citimātra-svarūpakam ।
   adṛṣṭaṁ kevalaṁ hyetac chraddhopeyaṁ na ca anyathā ॥ 3 ॥
   katham — how; etat — this; jagat — world; dṛśyam — visible; citimātra-svarūpakam — of the nature of pure consciousness; adṛṣṭam — unseen; kevalam — only; hi — indeed; etat — this; śraddhā-upeyam — to be accepted by faith; na ca — not otherwise
   How can this visible world be of the nature of pure consciousness? It is not apparent, and indeed, this can only be accepted through faith, not otherwise.
   
   Verse 4
   चितिश्चेत्यविनिर्मुक्ता नानुभाव्या कथञ्चन ।
   नोपपन्न सर्वथैतत्‌ कथं चित्तं समारुहेत्‌ ॥ ४ ॥
   citiḥ cetyavinir muktā nānubhāvyā kathaṁcana ।
   nopapanna sarvathā etat kathaṁ cittaṁ samāruhet ॥ 4 ॥
   citiḥ — consciousness; cetya-vinirmuktā — free from objects; na — not; anubhāvyā — perceivable; kathaṁcana — in any way; na — not; upapanna — feasible; sarvathā — in any way; etat — this; katham — how; cittaṁ — mind; samāruhet — can ascend
   Consciousness, being free from objects, cannot be perceived in any way. This seems unfeasible. How can the mind even reach this understanding?
   
   Verse 5
   कृपया बोधनीयोऽहमत्र सर्वात्मना खलु ।
   इत्यापृष्टो दत्तगुरुरवदद्‌ भार्गवं प्रति ॥ ५ ॥
   kṛpayā bodhanīyo'ham atra sarvātmanā khalu ।
   itya-pṛṣṭo dattagurur avadad bhārgavaṁ prati ॥ 5 ॥
   kṛpayā — with kindness; bodhanīyaḥ — should be enlightened; aham — I; atra — in this matter; sarva-ātmanā — completely; khalu — indeed; iti — thus; apṛṣṭaḥ — asked; dattaguruḥ — Guru Dattatreya; avadat — said; bhārgavam prati — to Bhargava
   With kindness, I wish to be fully enlightened on this matter. Thus asked, Guru Dattatreya responded to Bhargava.
   
   Verse 6
   शृणु राम प्रवक्ष्यामि दुश्यतत्त्वं यथास्थितम्‌ ।
   एतद्‌ दुश्यमशेषं तु दृशिमात्रं न चेतरत्‌ ॥ ६ ॥
   śṛṇu rāma pravakṣyāmi duśya-tattvaṁ yathāsthitam ।
   etat duśyam aśeṣaṁ tu dṛśimātraṁ na cetarat ॥ 6 ॥
   śṛṇu — listen; rāma — O Rama; pravakṣyāmi — I will explain; duśya-tattvam — the nature of the visible; yathāsthitam — as it is; etat — this; duśyam — the visible; aśeṣam — entirely; tu — indeed; dṛśi-mātram — pure vision; na — not; itarat — other
   Listen, O Rama, I will explain the nature of the visible world as it truly is. The visible world is entirely pure consciousness and nothing else.
   
   Verse 7
   अत्रोपपत्तिं वक्ष्यामि शृणु सम्यक्‌ समाहितः ।
   एतद्‌ दृश्यं कार्यभूतमुत्पत्तेरुपलम्भतः ॥ ७ ॥
   atra upapattiṁ vakṣyāmi śṛṇu samyak samāhitaḥ ।
   etat dṛśyaṁ kārya-bhūtam utpatteḥ upalambhataḥ ॥ 7 ॥
   atra — here; upapattiṁ — rationale; vakṣyāmi — I will explain; śṛṇu — listen; samyak — attentively; samāhitaḥ — focused; etat — this; dṛśyam — visible; kārya-bhūtam — effect; utpatteḥ — from the cause; upalambhataḥ — perceptible
   Here, I will explain the reasoning. Listen attentively and with focus. This visible world is the effect, perceptible from its cause.
   
   Verse 8
   उत्पत्तिर्नूतनाभासः प्रतिक्षणमिदं जगत्‌ ।
   नूतनत्वेनैव भाति तत्क्षणोत्पत्तिमज्जगत्‌ ॥ ८ ॥
   utpattiḥ nūtanābhāsaḥ pratikṣaṇam idaṁ jagat ।
   nūtanatvenaiva bhāti tat-kṣaṇa-utpatti-majjagat ॥ 8 ॥
   utpattiḥ — creation; nūtanābhāsaḥ — new appearance; pratikṣaṇam — every moment; idam — this; jagat — world; nūtanatvena — with newness; eva — indeed; bhāti — shines; tat-kṣaṇa — that moment; utpatti-majjagat — emerging world
   Creation appears anew each moment. The world continuously shines with freshness, emerging afresh every instant.
   
   Verse 9
   केचित्‌ प्राहुर्जगदिदमखण्डैकक्षणोद्भवम्‌ ।
   अन्ये पदार्थसंघातमयं स्थिरचरात्मकम्‌ ॥ ९ ॥
   kecit prāhuḥ jagad idam akhaṇḍa-ekakṣaṇa-udbhavam ।
   anye padārtha-saṅghātam ayaṁ sthira-cara-ātmakam ॥ 9 ॥
   kecit — some; prāhuḥ — say; jagat — world; idam — this; akhaṇḍa-ekakṣaṇa-udbhavam — arising in a single moment; anye — others; padārtha-saṅghātam — aggregate of elements; ayam — this; sthira-cara-ātmakam — composed of moving and unmoving
   Some say this world arises in a single moment, while others view it as an aggregate of elements, consisting of both moving and unmoving components.
   
   Verse 10
   सर्वथा तु समुत्पत्तिमदित्येव विनिश्चितम्‌ ।
   तत्र स्वभाववादस्तु नोचितोऽतिप्रसङ्गतः ॥ १० ॥
   sarvathā tu samutpattimad ityeva viniścitam ।
   tatra svabhāvavādaḥ tu na ucitaḥ ati-prasaṅgataḥ ॥ 10 ॥
   sarvathā — in every way; tu — indeed; samutpattimad — arising; iti — thus; eva — indeed; viniścitam — ascertained; tatra — there; svabhāvavādaḥ — theory of nature; tu — indeed; na — not; ucitaḥ — appropriate; ati-prasaṅgataḥ — due to excessive implication
   It is established that the world arises in every possible way. Therefore, the theory of nature is deemed inappropriate due to its excessive implications.
   
   Verse 11
   अन्वयव्यतिरेकाभ्यां कार्यकारणनिश्चयात्‌ ।
   संवादतः प्रवृत्तीनां कथमाकस्मिकं भवेत्‌ ॥ ११ ॥
   anvaya-vyatirekābhyāṁ kārya-kāraṇa-niścayāt ।
   saṁvādataḥ pravṛttīnām katham ākasmikaṁ bhavet ॥ 11 ॥
   anvaya-vyatirekābhyām — by consistency and contradiction; kārya-kāraṇa-niścayāt — from the determination of cause and effect; saṁvādataḥ — by coherence; pravṛttīnām — of activities; katham — how; ākasmikam — accidental; bhavet — can be
   Given the consistency and contradiction in determining cause and effect, and the coherence of activities, how can it be considered accidental?
   
   Verse 12
   क्वचित्तु कारणेऽदृष्टेऽप्यदृष्टं कल्प्यमेव तत्‌ ।
   बहूनामनुरोधो हि न्याय्यः सर्वैरुदाहृतः ॥ १२ ॥
   kvacit tu kāraṇe adṛṣṭe api adṛṣṭaṁ kalpyam eva tat ।
   bahūnām anurodhaḥ hi nyāyyaḥ sarvaiḥ udāhṛtaḥ ॥ 12 ॥
   kvacit — sometimes; tu — indeed; kāraṇe — cause; adṛṣṭe — unseen; api — even; adṛṣṭam — unseen; kalpyam — should be assumed; eva — indeed; tat — that; bahūnām — many; anurodhaḥ — conformity; hi — indeed; nyāyyaḥ — justifiable; sarvaiḥ — by all; udāhṛtaḥ — stated
   Sometimes, even if the cause is not visible, an unseen cause should be assumed. This is justifiable, as universally acknowledged.
   
   Verse 13
   भूयो दृष्ट सपूर्व हि कार्यं क्वचिददर्शने ।
   दृष्टवत्‌ परिकल्प्यं स्यादन्यथा सार्वलौकिकी ॥ १३ ॥
   bhūyo dṛṣṭa-sapūrvaḥ hi kāryaṁ kvacit adarśane ।
   dṛṣṭavat parikalpyaṁ syāt anyathā sārlaukikī ॥ 13 ॥
   bhūyaḥ — repeatedly; dṛṣṭa-sapūrvaḥ — seen with a cause; hi — indeed; kāryam — effect; kvacit — sometimes; adarśane — when not seen; dṛṣṭavat — like the seen; parikalpyam — should be assumed; syāt — should be; anyathā — otherwise; sārlaukikī — universal experience
   Repeatedly, when an effect is observed with a cause, it should be assumed to have a cause even if it is not seen; otherwise, it would contradict universal experience.
   
   Verse 14
   सम्प्रवृत्तिर्विरुध्येत तस्मात्‌ सर्व सकारणम्‌ ।
   अत एव कार्यहेतोः किञ्चित्कारणतत्परः ॥ १४ ॥
   sampravṛttir virudhyeta tasmāt sarva sakāraṇam ।
   ata eva kārya-hetoḥ kiñcit kāraṇa-tat-paraḥ ॥ 14 ॥
   sampravṛttiḥ — activity; virudhyeta — would be contradicted; tasmāt — therefore; sarva — everything; sakāraṇam — has a cause; ataḥ — therefore; eva — indeed; kārya-hetoḥ — for the effect; kiñcit — some; kāraṇa-tat-paraḥ — due to the cause
   Activity would be contradicted; therefore, everything must have a cause. Thus, every effect must have a cause.
   
   Verse 15
   सर्वत्र दृश्यते लोकस्तस्मादेतन्न किञ्चन ।
   केचिदाहुरसत्कल्पैरणुभिः कार्यमुद्यतम्‌ ॥ १५ ॥
   sarvatra dṛśyate lokaḥ tasmāt etat na kiñcana ।
   kecid āhuḥ asat-kalpaiḥ aṇubhiḥ kāryam udyatam ॥ 15 ॥
   sarvatra — everywhere; dṛśyate — is seen; lokaḥ — the world; tasmāt — therefore; etat — this; na — not; kiñcana — anything; kecit — some; āhuḥ — say; asat-kalpaiḥ — by unreal atoms; aṇubhiḥ — atoms; kāryam — effect; udyatam — produced
   Since the world is seen everywhere, nothing exists without a cause. Some argue that effects are produced by unreal atoms.
   
   Verse 16
   तेभ्योऽत्यन्तं विभिन्नं चाप्यसदत्यन्ततो भवेत्‌ ।
   असत्सतोरेकता हि विरुद्धा न कुतो भवेत्‌ ॥ १६ ॥
   tebhyaḥ atyantam vibhinnam ca api asat atyantataḥ bhavet ।
   asat-sataḥ ekatā hi viruddhā na kuto bhavet ॥ 16 ॥
   tebhyaḥ — from them; atyantam — extremely; vibhinnam — different; ca — and; api — even; asat — non-existence; atyantataḥ — absolutely; bhavet — can be; asat-sataḥ — of non-existence and existence; ekatā — unity; hi — indeed; viruddhā — contradictory; na — not; kutaḥ — how; bhavet — can be
   For such people, the world would seem extremely different, even completely non-existent. The unity of non-existence and existence is inherently contradictory and cannot be.
   
   Verse 17
   नहि पीतमपीतं च प्रकाश चाप्रकाशकम्‌ ।
   एकं भवेद्‌ विरुद्धत्वात्‌ साङ्कर्यादिप्रसक्तितः ॥ १७ ॥
   nahi pītam apītam ca prakāśa ca aprakāśakam ।
   ekaṁ bhavet viruddhatvāt sāṅkarya-ādi-prasaktitaḥ ॥ 17 ॥
   nahi — indeed not; pītam — drunk; apītam — not drunk; ca — and; prakāśa — light; ca — and; aprakāśakam — darkness; ekaṁ — one; bhavet — can be; viruddhatvāt — due to contradiction; sāṅkarya-ādi-prasaktitaḥ — due to resulting confusion
   Indeed, being both drunk and not drunk, or light and darkness simultaneously, cannot be reconciled due to inherent contradictions and resulting confusion.
   
   Verse 18
   ईश्वरेच्छादितो वापि कथमादिक्रियोद्भवः ।
   गुणसाम्यप्रकृतिकं जगदित्यप्यसंभवि ॥ १८ ॥
   īśvarecchāditaḥ vā api katham ādikriyā-udbhavaḥ ।
   guṇa-sāmya-prakṛtikam jagat iti api asaṁbhavi ॥ 18 ॥
   īśvara-icchā-ditaḥ — due to the will of the Lord; vā — or; api — even; katham — how; ādikriyā-udbhavaḥ — origin of the first action; guṇa-sāmya-prakṛtikam — nature of equilibrium of qualities; jagat — world; iti — thus; api — even; asaṁbhavi — impossible
   Even with the will of the Lord, how could the origin of the first action arise? That is impossible for the world, which is characterized by a balance of qualities, to come into being.
   
   Verse 19
   वैषम्यहेतोर्मग्यत्वात्‌ साम्यहेतोश्च हीनतः ।
   चेतनेनानघिष्ठानाद्‌ दृष्टान्तानुपलम्भतः ॥ १९ ॥
   vaiṣamya-hetoḥ magyatvāt sāma-hetoḥ ca hīnataḥ ।
   cetaneṇa anaghiṣṭhānāt dṛṣṭāntānu-palambhataḥ ॥ 19 ॥
   vaiṣamya-hetoḥ — cause of inequality; magyatvāt — due to being; sāma-hetoḥ — cause of equality; ca — and; hīnataḥ — due to deficiency; cetaneṇa — by intelligence; anaghiṣṭhānāt — without basis; dṛṣṭānta-anu-palambhataḥ — due to lack of evidence
   This world appears because it arises from inequality and deficiency in the cause of equality, driven by baseless intelligence and a lack of evidence.
   
   Verse 20
   तस्माज्जागतकार्यस्य कारणं नोपलभ्यते ।
   अदृष्टे तु श्रुतिर्मूलं नान्यमानस्य सङ्गमः ॥ २० ॥
   tasmāj jāgata-kāryasya kāraṇaṁ na upalabhyate ।
   adṛṣṭe tu śrutiḥ mūlaṁ na anya-mānasya saṅgamaḥ ॥ 20 ॥
   tasmāt — therefore; jāgata-kāryasya — of the world's activity; kāraṇam — cause; na — not; upalabhyate — perceived; adṛṣṭe — unseen; tu — but; śrutiḥ — scripture; mūlam — basis; na — not; anya-mānasya — other consideration; saṅgamaḥ — conjunction
   Therefore, the cause of the world's activity is not perceived. The unseen is supported by scripture, not by other considerations.
   
   Verse 21
   प्रमातृणामपूर्णत्वात्‌ प्रमाणस्यानवस्थितेः ।
   कार्यकर्त्र वियोगस्य भूयोदर्शनहेतुतः ॥ २१ ॥
   pramātṛṇām apūrṇatvāt pramāṇasya anavasthiteḥ ।
   kārya-kartra viyogasya bhūyo-darśana-hetutaḥ ॥ 21 ॥
   pramātṛṇām — of the perceivers; apūrṇatvāt — due to imperfection; pramāṇasya — of the means of knowledge; anavasthiteḥ — due to instability; kārya-kartra — of the effect and the doer; viyogasya — of separation; bhūyo — repeated; darśana-hetutaḥ — cause of observation
   Due to the limitations of the perceivers and the instability of the means of knowledge, the separation of the effect from the doer is often observed.
   
   Verse 22
   सकर्तृकं जगदिदं सम्भवाच्चेतनो हि सः ।
   कार्यस्याचिन्त्यरूपस्य कर्ता साधारणः कथम्‌ ॥ २२ ॥
   sakartṛkaṁ jagad idaṁ sambhavāt cetano hi saḥ ।
   kāryasya acintya-rūpasya kartā sādhāraṇaḥ katham ॥ 22 ॥
   sakartṛkam — with a doer; jagat — world; idam — this; sambhavāt — because of existence; cetano — conscious; hi — indeed; saḥ — he; kāryasya — of the effect; acintya-rūpasya — of unimaginable form; kartā — doer; sādhāraṇaḥ — common; katham — how
   This world, having a doer, suggests that the doer is conscious. How can a doer of such an unimaginable nature be considered ordinary?
   
   Verse 23
   तस्मादचिन्त्यशव्तिः स आगमस्तद्विमर्शनम्‌ ।
   पूर्णस्य त्वप्रतिहतं प्रमाणं सर्वतोऽधिकम्‌ ॥ २३ ॥
   tasmāt acintya-śaktiḥ sa āgamaḥ tad-vimarśanam ।
   pūrṇasya tu apratihataṁ pramāṇaṁ sarvataḥ adhikam ॥ 23 ॥
