   tasmāt — therefore; acintya-śaktiḥ — of unimaginable power; saḥ — he; āgamaḥ — scripture; tad-vimarśanam — his reflection; pūrṇasya — of the complete; tu — indeed; apratihataṁ — uninterrupted; pramāṇam — means of knowledge; sarvataḥ — in all respects; adhikam — superior
   Therefore, he possesses unimaginable power, and scripture reflects this. The means of knowledge that reveals the complete truth is indeed uninterrupted and superior in every respect.
   
   Verse 24
   तत्रैकस्तु महेशानः पुरा सृष्टेरुदाहृतः ।
   स्वतन्त्रो ह्यनुपादानः स्वातन्त्र्यभरवैभवात्‌ ॥ २४ ॥
   tatra ekaḥ tu maheśānaḥ purā sṛṣṭeḥ udāhṛtaḥ ।
   svatantraḥ hi anupādānaḥ svātantrya-bhara-vaibhavāt ॥ 24 ॥
   tatra — there; ekaḥ — one; tu — indeed; maheśānaḥ — Lord Shiva; purā — in the past; sṛṣṭeḥ — of creation; udāhṛtaḥ — described; svatantraḥ — independent; hi — indeed; anupādānaḥ — without material cause; svātantrya-bhara-vaibhavāt — due to the grandeur of independence
   There, indeed, is one Lord Shiva is described in the past as independent and without a material cause, due to the grandeur of his independence.
   
   Verse 25
   स्वात्मभित्तौ जगच्चित्रं विलासायावभासयत्‌ ।
   यथा स्वप्नमनोराज्ये कल्पितं स्वेन केवलम्‌ ॥ २५ ॥
   svātma-bhittau jagat-citraṁ vilāsāya avabhāsayat ।
   yathā svapna-manorājye kalpitaṁ svena kevalam ॥ 25 ॥
   svātma-bhittau — on one's own foundation; jagat-citram — the world picture; vilāsāya — for play; avabhāsayat — reveals; yathā — as; svapna-manorājye — in the kingdom of dreams; kalpitaṁ — imagined; svena — by oneself; kevalam — alone
   The diverse and fascinating world appears as if it is illuminated by the light of one’s own inner self, just like how a dream world is created by the mind itself.
   
   Verse 26
   अहंत्वेनैव गृह्णाति देहं तद्वदयं जगत्‌ ।
   न ते रूपं यथा देहः स्वप्नव्यावृत्तिहेतुतः ॥ २६ ॥
   ahaṁtvena eva gṛhṇāti dehaṁ tadvat ayaṁ jagat ।
   na te rūpaṁ yathā dehaḥ svapna-vyāvṛtti-hetutaḥ ॥ 26 ॥
   ahaṁtvena — with the sense of 'I'; eva — indeed; gṛhṇāti — grasps; dehaṁ — the body; tadvat — likewise; ayaṁ — this; jagat — world; na — not; te — your; rūpam — form; yathā — as; dehaḥ — body; svapna-vyāvṛtti-hetutaḥ — due to the distinction in dreams
   The body is accepted as real only due to the sense of ‘I’ (ahamkara), and similarly, this world is perceived. The world is not different from the body, as the difference arises from the same cause as in dreams.
   
   Verse 27
   तथास्य न जगद्देहो व्यावृत्तेः प्रलये ननु ।
   देहादिव्यतिरिक्तस्त्वं यथा केवलचिन्मयः ॥ २७ ॥
   tathā asya na jagat-dehaḥ vyāvṛtteḥ pralaye nanu ।
   deha-ādi-vyatiriktaḥ tvaṁ yathā kevala-cinmayaḥ ॥ 27 ॥
   tathā — likewise; asya — his; na — not; jagat-dehaḥ — world body; vyāvṛtteḥ — of distinction; pralaye — in dissolution; nanu — indeed; deha-ādi-vyatiriktaḥ — separate from the body, etc.; tvaṁ — you; yathā — as; kevala-cinmayaḥ — pure consciousness
   Just as the physical body of the world does not dissolve with changes or dissolution, you, as pure consciousness, remain unaffected by these changes. You are distinct from the body and other forms.
   
   Verse 28
   एवं देवो जगच्छून्यचिदेकवपुरव्ययः ।
   तेनेदं स्वात्मनि जगच्चित्रमुन्मीलितं ननु ॥ २८ ॥
   evaṁ devo jagat-śūnya-cid-eka-vapuḥ avyayaḥ ।
   tena idaṁ svātmani jagat-citram unmilitaṁ nanu ॥ 28 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; devo — the deity; jagat-śūnya-cit-eka-vapuḥ — with the single form of the void and consciousness; avyayaḥ — immutable; tena — by him; idaṁ — this; svātmani — in oneself; jagat-citram — world picture; unmilitaṁ — revealed; nanu — indeed
   Therefore, the deity, embodying the singular essence of emptiness and consciousness, reveals the entire world within oneself, remaining unchanged and constant.
   
   Verse 29
   क्वोन्मीलयेज्जगच्चित्रं स्वान्यस्य क्वाप्यसम्भवात्‌ ।
   ऋते चिति कदाचिद्वा क्व किं भवितुमर्हति ॥ २९ ॥
   kva unmīlayet jagat-citram sva-anyasya kva api asambhavāt ।
   ṛte citi kadācit vā kva kiṁ bhavitum arhati ॥ 29 ॥
   kva — where; unmīlayet — could reveal; jagat-citram — world picture; sva — own; anyasya — of another; kva — where; api — even; asambhavāt — due to impossibility; ṛte — except; citi — consciousness; kadācit — at any time; vā — or; kva — where; kiṁ — what; bhavitum — to be; arhati — can
   Where else could the world be revealed if not within oneself? Is it possible for anyone else to reveal it? Only consciousness can exist at all times.
   
   Verse 30
   यत्राभावश्चितेर्ब्रूयात्‌ स देशो नैव सिध्यति ।
   अभावश्च चितेः केन सिध्येत्तस्माच्चितिः परा ॥ ३० ॥
   yatra abhāvaḥ citeḥ brūyāt sa deśaḥ na eva sidhyati ।
   abhāvaḥ ca citeḥ kena sidhyet tasmāt citiḥ parā ॥ 30 ॥
   yatra — where; abhāvaḥ — absence; citeḥ — of consciousness; brūyāt — one says; saḥ — that; deśaḥ — place; na — not; eva — indeed; sidhyati — exists; abhāvaḥ — absence; ca — and; citeḥ — of consciousness; kena — by what; sidhyet — is proven; tasmāt — therefore; citiḥ — consciousness; parā — supreme
   Wherever consciousness is said to be absent, that place itself does not exist. Since nothing can prove the absence of consciousness, it is clear that consciousness is supreme.
   
   Verse 31
   महासत्ता जगद्ग्रासशीला पूर्णाऽवभासते ।
   समुद्रमन्तरा भङ्गा दिवानाथं विना प्रभाः ॥ ३१ ॥
   mahā-sattā jagat-grāsa-śīlā pūrṇā avabhāsate ।
   samudram antarā bhaṅgā divā-nāthaṁ vinā prabhāḥ ॥ 31 ॥
   mahā-sattā — great existence; jagat-grāsa-śīlā — devouring the world; pūrṇā — complete; avabhāsate — appears; samudram — ocean; antarā — without; bhaṅgā — waves; divā-nāthaṁ — without the sun; vinā — without; prabhāḥ — light
   The great existence, which encompasses the world completely, appears like waves without an ocean or light without the sun.
   
   Verse 32
   यथा न सन्ति तद्वद्‌ वै सविद्रूपं विना जगत्‌ ।
   तस्मादेष महादेवः शुद्धचैतन्यविग्रहः ॥ ३२ ॥
   yathā na santi tadvat vai sa-vid-rūpaṁ vinā jagat ।
   tasmāt eṣa mahā-devaḥ śuddha-caitanya-vigrahaḥ ॥ 32 ॥
   yathā — as; na santi — do not exist; tadvat — similarly; vai — indeed; sa-vid-rūpam — with consciousness; vinā — without; jagat — the world; tasmāt — therefore; eṣa — this; mahā-devaḥ — great god; śuddha-caitanya-vigrahaḥ — with the form of pure consciousness
   Since the world cannot exist without consciousness, this great deity, Mahadeva must be in the form of pure consciousness.
   
   Verse 33
   आसीत्‌ सृष्टेः पुरा तस्मादुत्पन्नं तत्र संस्थितम्‌ ।
   तस्मिन्‌ विलीयते चान्ते जगदेतच्चराचरम्‌ ॥ ३३ ॥
   āsīt sṛṣṭeḥ purā tasmāt utpannam tatra saṁsthitam ।
   tasmin vilīyate ca ante jagat etac cara-acaram ॥ 33 ॥
   āsīt — was; sṛṣṭeḥ — of creation; purā — before; tasmāt — from him; utpannam — born; tatra — there; saṁsthitam — sustained; tasmin — in him; vilīyate — dissolves; ca — and; ante — in the end; jagat — world; etat — this; cara-acaram — moving and non-moving
   Before creation, the world originated from him, it is sustained by him, and in the end, it dissolves back into him — this world of both moving and non-moving things.
   
   Verse 34
   इत्यागमप्रसिद्धोऽर्थस्तन्न विप्रतिपद्यते ।
   अदृष्टार्थेषु संवादात्‌ प्रमाणं ह्यागमो भवेत्‌ ॥ ३४ ॥
   iti āgama-prasiddhaḥ arthaḥ tat na vipratipadyate ।
   adṛṣṭa-artheṣu saṁvādāt pramāṇam hi āgamaḥ bhavet ॥ 34 ॥
   iti — thus; āgama-prasiddhaḥ — well-known in scripture; arthaḥ — meaning; tat — that; na — not; vipratipadyate — contradicted; adṛṣṭa-artheṣu — in unseen matters; saṁvādāt — agreement; pramāṇam — evidence; hi — indeed; āgamaḥ — scripture; bhavet — is
   Thus, the well-known teachings of scripture are not contradicted. In matters that are not visible, agreement with scripture serves as evidence.
   
   Verse 35
   दृश्यन्ते मणिमन्त्रादिसिद्धयः सर्वतो यतः ।
   नाल्पप्रज्ञो विजानीयाद्‌ मणिमन्त्रमहाफलम्‌ ॥ ३५ ॥
   dṛśyante maṇi-mantra-ādi-siddhayaḥ sarvataḥ yataḥ ।
   na alpa-prajñaḥ vijānīyāt maṇi-mantra-mahā-phalam ॥ 35 ॥
   dṛśyante — seen; maṇi-mantra-ādi — jewel, mantra, etc.; siddhayaḥ — powers; sarvataḥ — everywhere; yataḥ — because; na — not; alpa-prajñaḥ — of limited understanding; vijānīyāt — understands; maṇi-mantra-mahā-phalam — great result of jewel, mantra
   Because the effects of jewels, mantras, and similar things are visible everywhere, a person with limited understanding may not grasp the full significance of their power.
   
   Verse 36
   तस्मात्‌ सर्वज्ञगदितो ह्यागमः सर्वदर्शनः ।
   तत्रोक्तो देव एवादौ सुष्टेर्जगत आस्थितः ॥ ३६ ॥
   tasmāt sarva-jña-gaditaḥ hi āgamaḥ sarva-darśanaḥ ।
   tatra uktaḥ devaḥ eva ādau sṛṣṭeḥ jagat āsthitaḥ ॥ 36 ॥
   tasmāt — therefore; sarva-jña-gaditaḥ — spoken by the omniscient; hi — indeed; āgamaḥ — scripture; sarva-darśanaḥ — all-seeing; tatra — there; uktaḥ — mentioned; devaḥ — god; eva — indeed; ādau — in the beginning; sṛṣṭeḥ — of creation; jagat — world; āsthitaḥ — situated
   Therefore, the scripture, which is spoken by the omniscient and all-seeing, describes the deity as being present at the beginning of creation.
   
   Verse 37
   निरुपादान एवादौ सृष्टवानखिलं जगत्‌ ।
   यस्माद्‌ महेश्वरः पूर्णस्वच्छस्वातन्त्र्यसंयुतः ॥ ३७ ॥
   nirupādānaḥ eva ādau sṛṣṭavān akhilaṁ jagat ।
   yasmāt maheśvaraḥ pūrṇa-svaccha-svātantrya-saṁyutaḥ ॥ 37 ॥
   nirupādānaḥ — without material cause; eva — indeed; ādau — in the beginning; sṛṣṭavān — created; akhilaṁ — entire; jagat — world; yasmāt — because; maheśvaraḥ — great god; pūrṇa-svaccha-svātantrya-saṁyutaḥ — endowed with complete, pure independence
   Without a material cause, he created the entire world at the beginning, because the great deity possesses complete and pure independence.
   
   Verse 38
   चिदात्मभित्तावखिलं चित्रमुन्मीलयेद्‌ जगत्‌ ।
   न तज्जगत्‌ सम्भवति बहिः क्वचिदवस्थितम्‌ ॥ ३८ ॥
   cid-ātma-bhittau akhilaṁ citram unmilayet jagat ।
   na tat jagat sambhavati bahiḥ kvacit avasthitam ॥ 38 ॥
   cid-ātma-bhittau — on the foundation of consciousness; akhilaṁ — entire; citram — picture; unmilayet — reveals; jagat — world; na — not; tat — that; jagat — world; sambhavati — exists; bahiḥ — outside; kvacit — anywhere; avasthitam — situated
   The entire world is revealed on the foundation of consciousness. This world does not exist anywhere outside of it.
   
   Verse 39
   पूर्णत्वादीश्वरस्येह स्थानमन्यन्न विद्यते ।
   अन्यस्थानस्थितं तच्च कथञ्चिन्नैव सिध्यति ॥ ३९ ॥
   pūrṇatvāt īśvarasya iha sthānam anyat na vidyate ।
   anya-sthāna-sthitam tat ca kathañcit na eva sidhyati ॥ 39 ॥
   pūrṇatvāt — due to completeness; īśvarasya — of the lord; iha — here; sthānam — place; anyat — other; na — not; vidyate — exists; anya-sthāna-sthitam — situated in another place; tat — that; ca — and; kathañcit — by any means; na — not; eva — indeed; sidhyati — proven
   Because of the lord's completeness, there is no other place in this world. Anything claimed to exist elsewhere is not supported by any evidence.
   
   Verse 40
   तथा च दर्पणाभोगे प्रतिबिम्बवदेव हि ।
   जगदुन्मीलितं देवे चैवं सर्व समञ्जसम्‌ ॥ ४० ॥
   tathā ca darpaṇa-abhoge pratibimba-vat eva hi ।
   jagat unmilitaṁ deve ca evaṁ sarva-samanjasam ॥ 40 ॥
   tathā — likewise; ca — and; darpaṇa-abhoge — on the mirror surface; pratibimba-vat — like a reflection; eva — indeed; hi — surely; jagat — world; unmilitaṁ — revealed; deve — in the deity; ca — and; evam — thus; sarva-samanjasam — everything consistent
   Similarly, just as a reflection appears on the surface of a mirror, the world is revealed within the deity, making everything consistent.
   
   Verse 41
   जगदादेर्हि देवस्य योगीव जगतः क्रियाः ।
   सङ्कल्पनगरप्रख्या सृष्टिर्देवस्य सम्मता ॥ ४१ ॥
   jagadāder hi devasya yogīva jagataḥ kriyāḥ ।
   saṅkalpa-nagara-prakhyā sṛṣṭir devasya sammatā ॥ 41 ॥
   jagadādeḥ — at the beginning of the world; hi — indeed; devasya — of the god; yogīva — like a yogi; jagataḥ — of the world; kriyāḥ — actions; saṅkalpa-nagara-prakhyā — resembling a city of imagination; sṛṣṭiḥ — creation; devasya — of the god; sammatā — considered
   At the beginning of the world, the actions of the deity are akin to those of a yogi, and creation is regarded as resembling a city imagined by the deity.
   
   Verse 42
   राम ते मानसी सृष्टिर्मनोमय्येव केवला ।
   अनेकमातृमेयादिप्रचुरा ह्यवभासते ॥ ४२ ॥
   rāma te mānasī sṛṣṭir manomayy eva kevalā ।
   aneka-mātṛ-meya-ādi-pracurā hy avabhāsate ॥ 42 ॥
   rāma — O Rama; te — your; mānasī — mental; sṛṣṭiḥ — creation; manomayī — mind-made; eva — only; kevalā — alone; aneka — many; mātṛ — measures; meya — measurable; ādi — etc.; pracurā — full of; hi — indeed; avabhāsate — appears
   O Rama, your mental creation is entirely mind-made, full of various measures and things that can be measured, and it indeed appears as such.
   
   Verse 43
   अनेकभेदभिन्नापि मनसोऽन्या नहि क्वचित्‌ ।
   उत्पन्ना मनसस्तत्र स्थिता तत्रैव लीयते ॥ ४३ ॥
   anekabheda-bhinnāpi manaso'nyā nahi kvacit ।
   utpannā manasas tatra sthitā tatraiva līyate ॥ 43 ॥
   aneka-bheda-bhinnā — many differentiated forms; api — although; manasaḥ — of the mind; anyā — other; nahi — not; kvacit — anywhere; utpannā — arisen; manasaḥ — from the mind; tatra — there; sthitā — remains; tatra — there; eva — indeed; līyate — merges
   Although differentiated into many forms, nothing exists apart from the mind; whatever arises from the mind remains within it and ultimately merges back into it.
   
   Verse 44
   सा केवलमनोरूपा यथा तद्वज्जगच्छिवात्‌ ।
   स शिवश्चितिमात्रैकरूपश्चितिरविग्रहा ॥ ४४ ॥
   sā kevala-manorūpā yathā tadvat jagac-chivāt ।
   sa śivaś citi-mātra-eka-rūpaḥ citiḥ avigrahā ॥ 44 ॥
   sā — that; kevala-manorūpā — purely mental form; yathā — as; tadvat — likewise; jagat — the world; śivāt — from Shiva; sa — he; śivaḥ — Shiva; citi-mātra-eka-rūpaḥ — having the form of pure consciousness; citiḥ — consciousness; avigrahā — without form
   Just as everything is purely mental creation, similarly this world is originating from Shiva, He, Shiva is pure consciousness — formless consciousness itself.
   
   Verse 45
   त्रिपुरानन्तशक्त्यैक्यरूपिणी सर्वसाक्षिणी ।
   सा चितिः सर्वतः पूर्णा परिच्छेदविवर्जनात्‌ ॥ ४५ ॥
   tripurānanta-śakti-aikya-rūpiṇī sarva-sākṣiṇī ।
   sā citiḥ sarvataḥ pūrṇā pariccheda-vivarjanāt ॥ 45 ॥
   tripurā-ananta-śakti-aikya-rūpiṇī — embodying the unity of infinite powers of Tripura; sarva-sākṣiṇī — witnessing all; sā — that; citiḥ — consciousness; sarvataḥ — entirely; pūrṇā — complete; pariccheda-vivarjanāt — devoid of division
   Endowed with the unity of the infinite powers of Tripura and witnessing everything, that consciousness is wholly complete and undivided.
   
   Verse 46
   कालो देशश्च लोकेऽस्मिन्‌ परिच्छेदकरः स्मृतः ।
   तत्राकारमयो देशः कालस्तु स्यात्‌ क्रियामय: ॥ ४६ ॥
   kālo deśaś ca loke'smin pariccheda-karaḥ smṛtaḥ ।
   tatra ākāra-mayaḥ deśaḥ kālas tu syāt kriyā-mayaḥ ॥ 46 ॥
   kālaḥ — time; deśaḥ — space; ca — and; loke'smin — in this world; pariccheda-karaḥ — causing division; smṛtaḥ — is remembered; tatra — there; ākāra-mayaḥ — formed of shapes; deśaḥ — space; kālaḥ — time; tu — but; syāt — is; kriyā-mayaḥ — formed of actions
   In this world, time and space are perceived as causing division; space is composed of shapes, while time is composed of actions.
   
   Verse 47
   यां चितिं समुपाश्रित्य स्यादाकारः क्रियापि वा ।
   तस्याः परिच्छेदकत्वमनयोः स्यात्‌ कथं वद ॥ ४७ ॥
   yāṁ citiṁ samupāśritya syād ākāraḥ kriyāpi vā ।
   tasyāḥ pariccheda-katvam anayoḥ syāt kathaṁ vada ॥ 47 ॥
   yām — which; citiṁ — consciousness; samupāśritya — based on; syāt — would be; ākāraḥ — form; kriyā — action; api vā — or; tasyāḥ — its; pariccheda-katvam — divisibility; anayoḥ — of these; syāt — would be; kathaṁ — how; vada — tell me
   Tell me, how could form or action, which are based on that consciousness, cause divisibility?
   
   Verse 48
   कस्मिन्‌ देशे च काले च चितिर्नास्तीह तद्वद ।
   यत्र न स्याच्चितिः सोऽपि कथं स्यादिति वै भवेत्‌ ॥ ४८ ॥
   kasmin deśe ca kāle ca citir nāstīha tadvada ।
   yatra na syāc citiḥ so'pi kathaṁ syād iti vai bhavet ॥ 48 ॥
   kasmin — in which; deśe — place; ca — and; kāle — time; citiḥ — consciousness; nāsti — is not; iha — here; tad — that; vada — tell; yatra — where; na — not; syāt — exists; citiḥ — consciousness; saḥ — that; api — also; kathaṁ — how; syāt — would be; iti — thus; vai — indeed; bhavet — is
   Tell me, where in space and time does consciousness not exist here? How could anything be where there is no consciousness?
   
   Verse 49
   अस्तिता हि पदार्थानां प्रकाशो नापरः खलु ।
   प्रकाशस्तु चितिः प्रोक्ता नाचितेः स्यात्‌ प्रकाशता ॥ ४९ ॥
   astitā hi padārthānāṁ prakāśo nāparaḥ khalu ।
   prakāśas tu citiḥ proktā nāciteḥ syāt prakāśatā ॥ 49 ॥
   astitā — existence; hi — indeed; padārthānāṁ — of objects; prakāśaḥ — illumination; na — not; aparaḥ — another; khalu — indeed; prakāśaḥ — illumination; tu — but; citiḥ — consciousness; proktā — said; na — not; aciteḥ — of non-consciousness; syāt — would be; prakāśatā — illumination
   The existence of objects is not a separate form of illumination. Illumination is identified with consciousness, not with non-consciousness.
   
   Verse 50
   प्रकाशस्तु सुमुख्यः स्याद्यः स्वतन्त्रः प्रकाशते ।
   जडा न स्वप्रकाशा हि चितियोगप्रकाशनात्‌ ॥ ५० ॥
   prakāśas tu sumukhyaḥ syād yaḥ svatantraḥ prakāśate ।
   jaḍā na svaprakāśā hi citi-yoga-prakāśanāt ॥ 50 ॥
   prakāśaḥ — illumination; tu — but; sumukhyaḥ — supreme; syāt — would be; yaḥ — which; svatantraḥ — independent; prakāśate — illuminates; jaḍā — insentient; na — not; svaprakāśāḥ — self-illuminating; hi — indeed; citi-yoga-prakāśanāt — by the illumination of consciousness
   However, supreme illumination is that which illuminates independently. The insentient objects do not illuminate themselves; they are illuminated by consciousness.
   
   Verse 51
   अन्यानपेक्षणेनैव चितिः स्वस्मिन्‌ प्रकाशते ।
   जडाश्चितिं समाश्रित्य प्रकाशन्ते न चान्यथा ॥ ५१ ॥
   anyān-apekṣaṇenaiva citiḥ svasmin prakāśate ।
   jaḍāś citiṁ samāśritya prakāśante na ca anyathā ॥ 51 ॥
   anyān — others; apekṣaṇena — depending on; eva — indeed; citiḥ — consciousness; svasmin — in itself; prakāśate — illuminates; jaḍāḥ — insentient; citiṁ — consciousness; samāśritya — relying on; prakāśante — illuminate; na — not; ca — and; anyathā — otherwise
   Consciousness illuminates on its own, without depending on anything else. Insentient objects are illuminated by consciousness, not by their own nature.
   
   Verse 52
   अप्रकाशेऽपि वस्तूनामस्तिता चेत्तदा शृणु ।
   अस्ति नास्तीति लोकेऽस्मिन्‌ व्यवस्था नहि सेत्स्यति ॥ ५२ ॥
   aprakāśe'pi vastūnāṁ astitā cet tadā śṛṇu ।
   asti nāsti iti loke'smin vyavasthā nahi setsyati ॥ 52 ॥
   aprakāśe — in non-illumination; api — even; vastūnāṁ — of objects; astitā — existence; cet — if; tadā — then; śṛṇu — listen; asti — exist; nāsti — not exist; iti — thus; loke'smin — in this world; vyavasthā — condition; nahi — not; setsyati — would be
   Listen, if objects exist even in the absence of illumination, then the concepts of existing and not existing would not make sense in this world.
   
   Verse 53
   तस्माद्वस्त्वस्तिता लोके चित्प्रकाशो न चापरः ।
   यथा हि प्रतिषिम्बानां सत्त्वं दर्पण एव हि ॥ ५३ ॥
   tasmād vastv-astitā loke cit-prakāśo na ca aparaḥ ।
   yathā hi pratiṣimbānāṁ sattvaṁ darpaṇa eva hi ॥ 53 ॥
   tasmāt — therefore; vastu-astitā — existence of objects; loke — in the world; cit-prakāśaḥ — illumination of consciousness; na — not; ca — and; aparaḥ — another; yathā — just as; hi — indeed; pratiṣimbānāṁ — of reflections; sattvam — existence; darpaṇa — in the mirror; eva — only; hi — indeed
   Therefore, the existence of objects in the world is the illumination of consciousness, and nothing else. It is similar to how reflections exist only in the mirror.
   
   Verse 54
   तथा चितिर्जगत्सत्ता ततः सर्वं चितिर्भवेत्‌ ।
   अधिकं भासते यत्तु॒ तन्नैर्मल्यमहित्त्वतः ॥ ५४ ॥
   tathā citir jagat-sattā tataḥ sarvaṁ citir bhavet ।
   adhikaṁ bhāsate yat tu tan nairmalyam ahittvataḥ ॥ 54 ॥
   tathā — thus; citiḥ — consciousness; jagat-sattā — the existence of the world; tataḥ — therefore; sarvam — everything; citiḥ — consciousness; bhavet — becomes; adhikaṁ — more; bhāsate — shines; yat — which; tu — but; tat — that; nairmalyam — purity; ahittvataḥ — from impurity
   Thus, consciousness is the essence of the world; therefore, everything becomes consciousness. Whatever shines represents purity, not impurity.
   
   Verse 55
   काठिन्यनिर्मलत्वाभ्यां प्रतिबिम्बावभासनम्‌ ।
   तयोस्तु तारतम्येन प्रतिबिम्बः स्फुटोऽस्फुटः ॥ ५५ ॥
   kāṭhinyanirmalatvābhyāṁ pratibimbāvabhāsanam ।
   tayoḥ tu tāratamyena pratibimbaḥ sphuṭaḥ asphuṭaḥ ॥ 55 ॥
   kāṭhinya-nirmalatvābhyām — by hardness and purity; pratibimba-avabhāsanam — reflection appears; tayoḥ — of those two; tu — but; tāratamyena — by degree; pratibimbaḥ — reflection; sphuṭaḥ — clear; asphuṭaḥ — unclear
   The clarity of a reflection depends on the hardness and purity of the reflecting surface, resulting in either a clear or unclear image (Similarly, the world is reflected due to the purity in consciousness).
   
   Verse 56
   दर्पणे च जले चापि स्पष्टमेतद्धि लक्ष्यते ।
   जडत्वाद्‌ दर्पणादेस्तु स्वातन्त्र्यपरिवर्जनात्‌ ॥ ५६ ॥
   darpaṇe ca jale ca api spaṣṭam etad dhi lakṣyate ।
   jaḍatvād darpaṇād e tu svātantrya-parivarjanāt ॥ 56 ॥
   darpaṇe — in the mirror; ca — and; jale — in water; ca — also; api — even; spaṣṭam — clear; etad — this; hi — indeed; lakṣyate — is observed; jaḍatvāt — due to insentience; darpaṇāt — of the mirror; e — this; tu — but; svātantrya-parivarjanāt — from lack of independence
   This is clearly observed in mirrors and water as well; due to their insentience, they lack independence.
   
   Verse 57
   बिम्बापेक्षा चितेः स्वच्छस्वातन्त्र्यादनपेक्षता ।
   निर्मलत्वं स्वत सिद्धं चितेर्मालिन्यवर्जनात्‌ ॥ ५७ ॥
   bimbāpekṣā citeḥ svaccha-svātantryāt anapekṣatā ।
   nirmalatvaṁ svataḥ siddhaṁ citeḥ mālinya-varjanāt ॥ 57 ॥
   bimba-apekṣā — reflection's dependence; citeḥ — of consciousness; svaccha-svātantryāt — from pure independence; anapekṣatā — non-dependence; nirmalatvaṁ — purity; svataḥ — inherently; siddham — established; citeḥ — of consciousness; mālinya-varjanāt — from absence of impurity
   The dependence of reflections is due to consciousness's pure independence and lack of dependence. Purity is inherently established in consciousness, arising from the absence of impurity.
   
   Verse 58
   अनेकरसतैव स्याद्‌ मालिन्यं तत्‌ चितेर्नहि ।
   ऐकात्म्यरूप्याच्चिच्छक्तेरखण्डत्वाच्च सर्वथा ॥ ५८ ॥
   anekarasataiva syād mālinyaṁ tat citer nahi ।
   aikātmya-rūpyāt cit-śakter akhaṇḍatvāc ca sarvathā ॥ 58 ॥
   anekarasataiva — of diverse qualities; syāt — would be; mālinyaṁ — impurity; tat — that; citeḥ — of consciousness; nahi — not; aikātmya-rūpyāt — from the nature of unity; cit-śakteḥ — of the power of consciousness; akhaṇḍatvāt — from indivisibility; ca — and; sarvathā — in all ways
   Diverse qualities seen lead to impurity, but consciousness itself is not diverse. It stems from the nature of unity, the power of consciousness, and its indivisibility in all aspects.
   
   Verse 59
   अरिक्तात्मभावहेतोर्नैर्मल्यं सर्वतोऽधिकम्‌ ।
   अस्वतो भासमानस्य भानमन्यानुषङ्गतः ॥ ५९ ॥
   ariktātma-bhāva-hetor nairmalyaṁ sarvato'dhikam ।
   asvato bhāsamānasya bhānam anyānuṣaṅgataḥ ॥ 59 ॥
   ariktātma-bhāva-hetor — from the nature of non-empty self; nairmalyam — purity; sarvataḥ-adhikam — superior in all ways; asvato — of non-self; bhāsamānasya — appearing; bhānam — illumination; anyānuṣaṅgataḥ — by the connection with others
   From the nature of the non-empty self, purity in the self is superior in all respects. The appearance of the non-self is simply the result of its illumination through its connection to others.
   
   Verse 60
   प्रतिबिम्बस्वरूपज्ञाः प्रतिबिम्बं प्रचक्षते ।
   जगदेतादृशं सर्वं सर्वैः समभिलक्षितम्‌ ॥ ६० ॥
   pratibimba-svarūpa-jñāḥ pratibimbaṁ pracakṣate ।
   jagad etādṛśaṁ sarvaṁ sarvaiḥ samabhilakṣitam ॥ 60 ॥
   pratibimba-svarūpa-jñāḥ — those who know the nature of reflections; pratibimbaṁ — reflection; pracakṣate — they declare; jagat — the world; etādṛśaṁ — like this; sarvam — all; sarvaiḥ — by all; samabhilakṣitam — observed
   Those who understand the nature of reflections recognize that the world is like a reflection; it is observed by all.
   
   Verse 61
   स्वतो न भासते क्वापि भासते च चिदाश्रयात्‌ ।
   अतो जगत्‌ स्यादादर्शप्रतिबिम्बसुसंमितम्‌ ॥ ६१ ॥
   svato na bhāsate kvāpi bhāsate ca cid-āśrayāt ।
   ato jagat syād ādarśa-pratibimba-susaṁmitam ॥ 61 ॥
   svataḥ — by itself; na — not; bhāsate — shines; kvāpi — anywhere; bhāsate — shines; ca — and; cid-āśrayāt — by the support of consciousness; ataḥ — therefore; jagat — world; syāt — is; ādarśa-pratibimba — mirror-reflection; susaṁmitam — well-measured
   By itself, it does not shine anywhere, but it shines through the support of consciousness. Therefore, the world is like a well-defined reflection in a mirror.
   
   Verse 62
   चितिर्विचित्राऽन्यभावैरुपरक्तापि भासिनी ।
   स्वरूपादप्रच्युतैवादर्शवल्लेशतोऽपि हि ॥ ६२ ॥
   citiḥ vicitrā anya-bhāvair uparaktā api bhāsinī ।
   svarūpāt apracyutā iva ādarśa-vat leśataḥ api hi ॥ 62 ॥
   citiḥ — consciousness; vicitrā — varied; anya-bhāvaiḥ — by other states; uparaktā — colored; api — even; bhāsinī — illuminating; svarūpāt — from its nature; apracyutā — not deviating; iva — as if; ādarśa-vat — like a mirror; leśataḥ — slightly; api — even; hi — indeed
   Even when colored by various states (varied reflections), consciousness illuminates without deviating from its true nature, just like a mirror.
   
   Verse 63
   दर्पणप्रतिबिम्बानां दर्पणानन्यता यथा ।
   चिदात्मप्रतिबिम्बानां चिदात्मानन्यता तथा ॥ ६३ ॥
   darpaṇa-pratibimbānāṁ darpaṇa-ananyatā yathā ।
   cid-ātma-pratibimbānāṁ cid-ātma-ananyatā tathā ॥ 63 ॥
   darpaṇa-pratibimbānāṁ — of the mirror's reflections; darpaṇa-ananyatā — non-difference from the mirror; yathā — as; cid-ātma-pratibimbānāṁ — of the reflections in consciousness; cid-ātma-ananyatā — non-difference from consciousness; tathā — similarly
   Just as reflections in a mirror are not separate from the mirror itself, similarly reflections in the consciousness are not separate from consciousness.
   
   Verse 64
   दर्पणे प्रतिबिम्बो हि बिम्बहेतुर्निरूपितः ।
   चितिः तिस्वातन्त्र्यहेतुः स्यात्‌ प्रतिबिम्बो हि जागतः ॥
   darpaṇe pratibimbo hi bimba-hetur nirūpitaḥ ।
   citiḥ ti-svātantrya-hetuḥ syāt pratibimbo hi jāgataḥ ॥ 64 ॥
   darpaṇe — in the mirror; pratibimbaḥ — reflection; hi — indeed; bimba-hetuḥ — cause of the image; nirūpitaḥ — is established; citiḥ — consciousness; ti-svātantrya-hetuḥ — cause of its independence; syāt — may be; pratibimbaḥ — reflection; hi — indeed; jāgataḥ — of the world
   The reflection in the mirror clearly causes the image we see. Similarly, consciousness can be seen as the source of the world's existence and independence, just as the reflection depends on the mirror.
   
   Verse 65
   स्वसङ्कल्पाद्राम पश्य स्वात्मनि प्रतिबिम्बितान्‌ ।
   भावान्‌ बिम्बविनाभूतान्निर्निमित्तावभासनान्‌ ॥ ६५ ॥
   sva-saṅkalpād rāma paśya svātmani pratibimbitān ।
   bhāvān bimba-vinābhūtān nirnimittāvabhāsanān ॥ 65 ॥
   sva-saṅkalpāt — by self-will; rāma — O Rama; paśya — see; svātmani — in oneself; pratibimbitān — reflected; bhāvān — states; bimba-vinābhūtān — without the image; nirnimitta-avabhāsanān — appearing without cause
   O Rama, observe how all states are reflected in oneself by one's own will, appearing without any inherent cause or original image.
   
   Verse 66
   सङ्कल्प एव स्वातन्त्र्यं चितेरुच्छूनमीर्यते ।
   असङ्कल्पदशायां सा चितिः स्वच्छैकरूपिणी ॥ ६६ ॥
   saṅkalpa eva svātantryaṁ citer uccāvaṇīryate ।
   asaṅkalpa-daśāyāṁ sā citiḥ svaccha-eka-rūpiṇī ॥ 66 ॥
   saṅkalpaḥ — will; eva — indeed; svātantryam — independence; citer — of consciousness; uccāvaṇīryate — is declared; asaṅkalpa-daśāyāṁ — in the state without will; sā — that; citiḥ — consciousness; svaccha-eka-rūpiṇī — of pure single form
   Will is considered a manifestation of consciousness's independence. In the state without will, consciousness is in its pure, singular form.
   
   Verse 67
   एवं चितेर्विशुद्धैकरूपायाः सृष्टितः पुरा ।
   बृहत्‌ स्वातन्त्र्यमभवत्‌ सङ्कल्पात्मकमेव तत्‌ ॥ ६७ ॥
   evaṁ citer viśuddha-eka-rūpāyāḥ sṛṣṭitaḥ purā ।
   bṛhat svātantryam abhavat saṅkalpātmakam eva tat ॥ 67 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; citer — of consciousness; viśuddha-eka-rūpāyāḥ — of pure single form; sṛṣṭitaḥ — from creation; purā — before; bṛhat — great; svātantryam — independence; abhavat — became; saṅkalpa-ātmakam — of the nature of will; eva — indeed; tat — that
   Thus, from the pure, singular form of consciousness, there was great independence before creation, which was indeed of the nature of will.
   
   Verse 68
   तत एतत्समाभातं प्रतिबिम्बात्मकं जगत्‌ ।
   बृहत्सङ्कल्पसुस्थैर्याच्चिरमेतद्‌ विभासते ॥ ६८ ॥
   tata etat samābhātaṁ pratibimba-ātmakam jagat ।
   bṛhat-saṅkalpa-susthairya-ciram etad vibhāsate ॥ 68 ॥
   tataḥ — from that; etat — this; samābhātam — manifests; pratibimba-ātmakam — reflection-like; jagat — world; bṛhat-saṅkalpa-susthairya — from the stability of great will; ciram — for long; etad — this; vibhāsate — shines
   From that, the world manifests like a reflection. Due to the stability of great will, it shines for a long time.
   
   Verse 69
   साधारणं जगद्‌ भाति पूर्णस्वातन्त्र्यहेतुतः ।
   अन्येषां तदपूर्णत्वाद्‌ भात्यसाधारणात्मना ॥ ६९ ॥
   sādhāraṇaṁ jagad bhāti pūrṇa-svātantrya-hetutaḥ ।
   anyeṣāṁ tad apūrṇatvād bhāti asādhāraṇa-ātmanā ॥ 69 ॥
   sādhāraṇam — common; jagat — world; bhāti — shines; pūrṇa-svātantrya-hetutaḥ — from the cause of full independence; anyeṣām — of others; tad — that; apūrṇatvāt — from incompleteness; bhāti — shines; asādhāraṇa-ātmanā — with uncommon nature
   The ordinary world shines because of its complete independence. For others, it appears unusual or complex due to their own lack of completeness (For the jiva, the world appears complex, due to their own imperfections).
   
   Verse 70
   अभ्यासान्मणिमन्त्राद्यैः स्वातन्त्र्यं तु यथा यथा ।
   त्यजेत्‌ सङ्कोचमात्मस्थं तथा तत्र हि भासनम्‌ ॥ ७० ॥
   abhyāsān maṇi-mantrādyaiḥ svātantryaṁ tu yathā yathā ।
   tyajet saṅkocam ātma-stham tathā tatra hi bhāsanam ॥ 70 ॥
   abhyāsāt — by practice; maṇi-mantra-ādyaiḥ — by jewels, mantras, etc.; svātantryam — independence; tu — indeed; yathā yathā — as much as; tyajet — leaves; saṅkocam — constraints; ātma-stham — in oneself; tathā — thus; tatra — there; hi — indeed; bhāsanam — illumination.
   Through repeated practice with jewels, mantras, and other methods, and by overcoming personal constraints, one achieves illumination.
   
   Verse 71
   पश्यैन्द्रजालिकं राम निरूपादानयोगतः ।
   भासयन्तं जगच्चित्रं सङ्कल्पादेव सर्वतः ॥ ७१ ॥
   paśya indrajālikam rāma nirūpādāna-yogataḥ ।
   bhāsayantaṁ jagat-citraṁ saṅkalpāt eva sarvataḥ ॥ 71 ॥
   paśya — see; indrajālikam — magician; rāma — O Rama; nirūpādāna-yogataḥ — without using materials; bhāsayantaṁ — illuminating; jagat-citram — world-picture; saṅkalpāt — by will; eva — indeed; sarvataḥ — everywhere
   Look, O Rama, at the magician who, by will alone and without using any materials, illuminates the entire world-picture everywhere.
   
   Verse 72
   साधारणं स्थिरं स्वार्थक्रियार्हं भूय एव तु ।
   स्वात्मन्युपसंहरेच्च जगदेवं विभासते ॥ ७२ ॥
   sādhāraṇaṁ sthiraṁ sva-artha-kriyārhaṁ bhūya eva tu ।
   svātmani upasaṁharet ca jagat evaṁ vibhāsate ॥ 72 ॥
   sādhāraṇam — common; sthiram — stable; sva-artha-kriyārham — suitable for one's purposes; bhūyaḥ — again; eva — indeed; tu — but; svātmani — in oneself; upasaṁharet — withdraws; ca — and; jagat — world; evam — thus; vibhāsate — shines
   The stable, ordinary world, which serves one's purposes, is later on, again withdrawn into oneself. Thus, the world shines.
   
   Verse 73
   योगिनः पश्य सृष्टिं तां पूर्णस्थैर्यसमावृताम्‌ ।
   योगिनस्तु मितत्वेन सृष्टिर्बाह्या विभाविता ॥ ७३ ॥
   yoginaḥ paśya sṛṣṭiṁ tāṁ pūrṇa-sthairya-samāvṛtām ।
   yoginaḥ tu mitatvena sṛṣṭiḥ bāhyā vibhāvitā ॥ 73 ॥
   yoginaḥ — yogis; paśya — see; sṛṣṭim — creation; tām — that; pūrṇa-sthairya-samāvṛtām — enveloped in full stability; yoginaḥ — yogis; tu — but; mitatvena — with limitation; sṛṣṭiḥ — creation; bāhyā — external; vibhāvitā — is considered
   The yogis clearly perceive creation as fully stable and enveloped in stability, while others see external creation through their own limitations.
   
   Verse 74
   अमितत्वात्सृष्टिरियं चिन्नाथस्यान्तरेव हि ।
   अत एव चिदात्मत्वव्यतिरेकादसत्यता ॥ ७४ ॥
   amitatvāt sṛṣṭir iyaṁ cinnāthasyāntareva hi ।
   ata eva cid-ātmatvavyatirekād asatyatā ॥ 74 ॥
   amitatvāt — due to boundlessness; sṛṣṭiḥ — creation; iyam — this; cin-nāthasya — of the Lord of Consciousness; antare — within; eva — indeed; hi — for; ata eva — therefore; cid-ātmatva — the nature of consciousness; vyatirekāt — due to the distinction; asatyatā — falsity
   Due to its boundless nature, creation exists only within the Lord of Consciousness. Therefore, because it is distinct from the nature of consciousness, it is considered false.
   
   Verse 75
   जगतः प्रतिबिम्बस्यादर्शात्मस्वं विना यथा ।
   अत एव विचारेणासत्यतां याति नान्यथा ॥ ७५ ॥
   jagataḥ pratibimbasya ādarśātma-svaṁ vinā yathā ।
   ata eva vicāreṇāsatyatāṁ yāti nānyathā ॥ 75 ॥
   jagataḥ — of the world; pratibimbasya — of the reflection; ādarśa-ātma-svam — the nature of the mirror; vinā — without; yathā — just as; ata eva — therefore; vicāreṇa — by contemplation; asatyatām — falsehood; yāti — becomes; nānyathā — not otherwise
   Just as a reflection in a mirror cannot exist without the mirror itself, the world is considered false through contemplation and cannot exist otherwise.
   
   Verse 76
   सत्यं स्वभावं नो मुञ्चेदसत्यं तं परित्यजेत्‌ ।
   जगत्पश्य भार्गवैतत्‌ स्वभावादतिचञ्चलम्‌ ॥ ७६ ॥
   satyaṁ svabhāvaṁ no muñced asatyaṁ taṁ parityajet ।
   jagat paśya bhārgavaitat svabhāvād aticancalam ॥ 76 ॥
   satyaṁ — truth; svabhāvam — the nature; na — does not; muñcet — relinquish; asatyaṁ — falsehood; tam — that; parityajet — should abandon; jagat — the world; paśya — see; bhārgava — O descendant of Bhrigu; it — this; svabhāvāt — from its nature; aticancalam — exceedingly unstable
   Truth always remains true and doesn’t give up its true nature. In contrast, observe, O descendant of Bhrigu, that the world is naturally unstable and constantly changing.
   
   Verse 77
   सत्यासत्ये विभागेन भासेते सर्वतोऽखिलम्‌ ।
   प्रतिबिम्बादर्शभानमिव तत्प्रविचारय ॥ ७७ ॥
   satyāsatye vibhāgena bhāseta sarvato ’khilam ।
   pratibimbād arśa-bhānam iva tat pravicāraya ॥ 77 ॥
   satya-asatyā — truth and falsehood; vibhāgena — by division; bhāseta — appears; sarvataḥ — everywhere; akhilam — entirely; pratibimbāt — from the reflection; arśa-bhānam — the light of the mirror; iva — like; tat — that; pravicāraya — consider
   Truth and falsehood manifest everywhere through division, much like reflections in a mirror. Reflect on this carefully.
   
   Verse 78
   आदर्शो ह्यचलस्तत्र चलं हि प्रतिबिम्बकम्‌ ।
   तथा जगच्चलं संविदचला सर्वभाविता ॥ ७८ ॥
   ādarśo hy acalas tatra calaṁ hi pratibimbakam ।
   tathā jagat calaṁ saṁvid acalā sarva-bhāvitā ॥ 78 ॥
   ādarśaḥ — mirror; hi — indeed; acalaḥ — immovable; tatra — there; calan — moving; hi — indeed; pratibimbakam — reflection; tathā — similarly; jagat — world; calan — moving; saṁvid — consciousness; acalā — immovable; sarva-bhāvitā — all-encompassing.
   The mirror itself is immovable, but the reflection it shows moves. Similarly, while the world is in constant motion, consciousness remains immovable and all-encompassing.
   
   Verse 79
   अत एव हि भावानां विचारासहरूपता ।
   तथा हि सूर्यालोको हि वस्तूनामवभासकः ॥ ७९ ॥
   ata eva hi bhāvānāṁ vicārā-saha-rūpatā ।
   tathā hi sūrya-ālokaḥ hi vastūnām avabhāsakaḥ ॥ 79 ॥
   ataḥ eva — therefore; hi — indeed; bhāvānām — of the states; vicāra-saha-rūpatā — nature of being considered; tathā — similarly; hi — indeed; sūrya-ālokaḥ — sunlight; hi — indeed; vastūnām — of objects; avabhāsakaḥ — illuminator
   Therefore, the nature of the states depends on the one who perceives them, much like how sunlight illuminates objects.
   
   Verse 80
   उलूकादिदिवान्धानां विपरीतोऽन्धकारवत्‌ ।
   प्रकाशत्वान्धकारत्वे न विविक्तेऽनयोः स्फुटे ॥ ८० ॥
   ulūka-ādi-divā-andhānāṁ viparītaḥ andhakāra-vat ।
   prakāśatva-andhakāratve na vivikte anayoḥ sphuṭe ॥ 80 ॥
   ulūka-ādi-divā-andhānām — of owls and others blind during the day; viparītaḥ — opposite; andhakāra-vat — like darkness; prakāśatva — illumination; andhakāratve — darkness; na — not; vivikte — distinct; anayoḥ — of these; sphuṭe — clearly
   Just as, for owls and similar creatures that are active at night but blind during the day, they cannot clearly distinguish between light and darkness, as it appears similar to them.
   
   Verse 81
   एवं विषं कस्यचित्‌ स्यादविषं कस्यचिद्‌ भवेत्‌ ।
   मनुष्यादेः प्रतीघातकरी भीतिर्हि लक्ष्यते ॥ ८१ ॥
   evaṁ viṣaṁ kasyacit syād aviṣaṁ kasyacid bhavet ।
   manuṣyādeḥ pratīghātakarī bhītiḥ hi lakṣyate ॥ 81 ॥
   evaṁ — thus; viṣam — poison; kasyacit — for some; syāt — may be; aviṣam — non-poison; kasyacid — for some; bhavet — may be; manuṣya-ādeḥ — for humans and others; pratīghāta-karī — harmful; bhītiḥ — fear; hi — indeed; lakṣyate — is observed
   Thus, poison may be harmful to some and not to others. For humans and similar beings, nature is often seen with fear and can be harmful.
   
   Verse 82
   योगिनां गुह्यकादीनामप्रतीघातलक्षणा ।
   कालो देशश्च दीर्घो यो मनुष्यादिप्रभावितः ॥ ८२ ॥
   yogināṁ guhyakādīnāṁ apratīghāta-lakṣaṇā ।
   kālo deśaś ca dīrgho yo manuṣya-ādi-prabhāvitaḥ ॥ 82 ॥
   yoginām — for yogis; guhyaka-ādīnāṁ — for celestial beings; apratīghāta-lakṣaṇā — of non-harmful nature; kālaḥ — time; deśaḥ — place; ca — and; dīrghaḥ — long; yaḥ — which; manuṣya-ādi-prabhāvitaḥ — influenced by humans and others
   But for yogis and celestial beings, nature is not harmful. Time and place, which seem lengthy to humans and similar beings, are experienced differently by them as well.
   
   Verse 83
   स एव विपरीतो वै देवानां योगिनामपि ।
   दर्पणे भासमानस्य दूरादेर्दूरता यथा ॥ ८३ ॥
   sa eva viparīto vai devānāṁ yoginām api ।
   darpaṇe bhāsamānasya dūrāder dūratā yathā ॥ 83 ॥
   saḥ — it; eva — indeed; viparītaḥ — opposite; vai — certainly; devānām — for gods; yoginām — for yogis; api — also; darpaṇe — in the mirror; bhāsamānasya — appearing; dūrāt — from a distance; dūratā — distance; yathā — as
   For gods and yogis, the experience (of time and place) is quite different, just as the apparent distance in a mirror differs from the actual distance.
   
   Verse 84
   तथैवास्य स्वभावोऽपि विचारे न स्थिरो भवेत्‌ ।
   अत आश्रयरूपेण विना नास्ति हि किञ्चन ॥ ८४ ॥
   tathā eva asya svabhāvaḥ api vicāre na sthiraḥ bhavet ।
   ataḥ āśraya-rūpeṇa vinā na asti hi kiñcana ॥ 84 ॥
   tathā — similarly; eva — indeed; asya — of this; svabhāvaḥ — nature; api — also; vicāre — in consideration; na sthiraḥ — not stable; bhavet — may be; ataḥ — therefore; āśraya-rūpeṇa — in the form of a support; vinā — without; na asti — does not exist; hi — indeed; kiñcana — anything
   Similarly, its nature is not stable upon examination. Therefore, nothing exists without some form of support.
   
   Verse 85
   यदस्तीति भाति तत्तु चितिरेव महेश्वरी ।
   एवं जगच्चिदेकात्मरूपं ते सम्यगीरितम्‌ ॥ ८५ ॥
   yad asti iti bhāti tat tu citir eva maheśvarī ।
   evaṁ jagat cit-eka-ātma-rūpaṁ te samyag-īritam ॥ 85 ॥
   yat — what; asti — exists; iti — thus; bhāti — shines; tat — that; tu — indeed; citiḥ — consciousness; eva — only; maheśvarī — the great goddess; evaṁ — thus; jagat — world; cit-eka-ātma-rūpaṁ — of the nature of one consciousness; te — to you; samyak-īritam — rightly said
   What truly exists and shines is only consciousness, the great goddess. Thus, the world is rightly said to be of the nature of that one consciousness.


   
   इति श्रीत्रिपुरारहस्ये ज्ञानखण्डे जगत्तत्त्वनिरूपणे एकादशोऽध्यायः ॥
   
   Thus ends the eleventh chapter named "Explanation of the Essence of the World" in the revered Knowledge Section of Tripura Rahasya.

TRIPURA RAHASYA

SOHAM HAMSO

7

EPILOGUE
